<9>PART I: THE UNION AND ITS TERRITORY <7>1. Name and territory of the Union <6>1.<5> India, that is Bharat, shall be a Union of States. <6>2.<5> The States and the territories thereof shall be as specified in the First Schedule. <6>3.<5> The territory of India shall comprise- <6>a.<5> the territories of the States; <6>b.<5> the Union territories specified in the First Schedule; and <4>• Colonies <6>c. <5>such other territories as may be acquired. <4>• Accession of territory <7>2. Admission or establishment of new States <5>Parliament may by law admit into the Union, or establish, new States on such terms <5>and conditions as it thinks fit. <7>2A. Sikkim to be associated with the Union <5>Rep. by the Constitution (Thirty-sixth Amendment) Act, 1975, s. 5(w.e.f. 26-4-1975). <7>3. Formation of new States and alteration of areas, <7>boundaries or names of existing States <5>Parliament may by law- <6>a.<5> form a new State by separation of territory from any State or by uniting two <5>or more States or parts of States or by uniting any territory to a part of any <5>State; <6>b.<5> increase the area of any State; <6>c. <5>diminish the area of any State; <6>d.<5> alter the boundaries of any State; <6>e.<5> alter the name of any State: <5>Provided that no Bill for the purpose shall be introduced in either House of <5>Parliament except on the recommendation of the President and unless, where the <5>proposal contained in the Bill affects the area, boundaries or name of any of the <5>States, the Bill has been referred by the President to the Legislature of that State for <5>expressing its views thereon within such period as may be specified in the reference <5>or within such further period as the President may allow and the period so specified <5>or allowed has expired. <7>Explanation I <5>In this article, in clauses (a) to (e), "State" includes a Union territory, but in the <5>proviso, "State" does not include a Union territory. <7>Explanation II <5>The power conferred on Parliament by clause (a) includes the power to form a new <5>State or Union territory by uniting a part of any State or Union territory to any other <5>State or Union territory. <7>4. Laws made under articles 2 and 3 to provide for the <7>amendment of the First and the Fourth Schedules and <7>supplemental, incidental and consequential matters <6>1.<5> Any law referred to in article 2 or article 3 shall contain such provisions for the <5>amendment of the First Schedule and the Fourth Schedule as may be necessary <5>to give effect to the provisions of the law and may also contain such <5>supplemental, incidental and consequential provisions (including provisions as <5>to representation in Parliament and in the Legislature or Legislatures of the <5>State or States affected by such law) as Parliament may deem necessary. <6>2.<5> No such law as aforesaid shall be deemed to be an amendment of this <5>Constitution for the purposes of article 368. <9>PART II: CITIZENSHIP <7>5. Citizenship at the commencement of the Constitution <4>• Requirements for birthright citizenship <5>At the commencement of this Constitution, every person who has his domicile in the <5>territory of India and- <6>a.<5> who was born in the territory of India; or <6>b.<5> either of whose parents was born in the territory of India; or <6>c. <5>who has been ordinarily resident in the territory of India for not less than <5>five years immediately preceding such commencement, <5>shall be a citizen of India. <7>6. Rights of citizenship of certain persons who have <4>• Requirements for birthright citizenship <7>migrated to India from Pakistan <5>Notwithstanding anything in article 5, a person who has migrated to the territory of <5>India from the territory now included in Pakistan shall be deemed to be a citizen of <5>India at the commencement of this Constitution if- <6>a.<5> he or either of his parents or any of his grand-parents was born in India as <5>defined in the Government of India Act, 1935 (as originally enacted); and <6>b. <6>i. <5>in the case where such person has so migrated before the nineteenth <5>day of July, 1948, he has been ordinarily resident in the territory of <5>India since the date of his migration, or <6>ii. <5>in the case where such person has so migrated on or after the <5>nineteenth day of July, 1948, he has been registered as a citizen of <5>India by an officer appointed in that behalf by the Government of the <5>Dominion of India on an application made by him therefor to such <5>officer before the commencement of this Constitution in the form and <5>manner prescribed by that Government: <5>Provided that no person shall be so registered unless he has been <5>resident in the territory of India for at least six months immediately <5>preceding the date of his application. <7>7. Rights of citizenship of certain migrants to Pakistan <4>• Requirements for birthright citizenship <5>Notwithstanding anything in articles 5 and 6, a person who has after the first day of <5>March, 1947, migrated from the territory of India to the territory now included in <5>Pakistan shall not be deemed to be a citizen of India: <5>Provided that nothing in this article shall apply to a person who, after having so <5>migrated to the territory now included in Pakistan, has returned to the territory of <5>India under a permit for resettlement or permanent return issued by or under the <5>authority of any law and every such person shall for the purposes of clause (b) of <5>article 6 be deemed to have migrated to the territory of India after the nineteenth <5>day of July, 1948. <7>8. Rights of citizenship of certain persons of Indian origin <4>• Requirements for birthright citizenship <7>residing outside India <5>Notwithstanding anything in article 5, any person who or either of whose parents or <5>any of whose grand-parents was born in India as defined in the Government of India <5>Act, 1935 (as originally enacted), and who is ordinarily residing in any country <5>outside India as so defined shall be deemed to be a citizen of India if he has been <5>registered as a citizen of India by the diplomatic or consular representative of India <5>in the country where he is for the time being residing on an application made by him <5>therefor to such diplomatic or consular representative, whether before or after the <5>commencement of this Constitution, in the form and manner prescribed by the <5>Government of the Dominion of India or the Government of India. <7>9. Persons voluntarily acquiring citizenship of a foreign <4>• Requirements for birthright citizenship <4>• Conditions for revoking citizenship <7>State not to be citizens <5>No person shall be a citizen of India by virtue of article 5, or be deemed to be a citizen <5>of India by virtue of article 6 or article 8, if he has voluntarily acquired the citizenship <5>of any foreign State. <7>10. Continuance of the rights of citizenship <4>• Requirements for birthright citizenship <5>Every person who is or is deemed to be a citizen of India under any of the foregoing <5>provisions of this Part shall, subject to the provisions of any law that may be made by <5>Parliament, continue to be such citizen. <7>11. Parliament to regulate the right of citizenship by law <4>• Requirements for birthright citizenship <4>• Conditions for revoking citizenship <4>• Requirements for naturalization <5>Nothing in the foregoing provisions of this Part shall derogate from the power of <5>Parliament to make any provision with respect to the acquisition and termination of <5>citizenship and all other matters relating to citizenship. <9>PART III: FUNDAMENTAL RIGHTS <7>General <7>12. Definition <5>In this Part, unless the context otherwise requires, "the State" includes the <5>Government and Parliament of India and the Government and the Legislature of <5>each of the States and all local or other authorities within the territory of India or <5>under the control of the Government of India. <7>13. Laws inconsistent with or in derogation of the <7>fundamental rights <6>1.<5> All laws in force in the territory of India immediately before the commencement <5>of this Constitution, in so far as they are inconsistent with the provisions of this <5>Part, shall, to the extent of such inconsistency, be void. <6>2.<5> The State shall not make any law which takes away or abridges the rights <5>conferred by this Part and any law made in contravention of this clause shall, to <5>the extent of the contravention, be void. <6>3.<5> In this article, unless the context otherwise requires,- <6>a.<5> "law" includes any Ordinance, order, bye-law, rule, regulation, notification, <5>custom or usage having in the territory of India the force of law; <6>b.<5> "laws in force" includes laws passed or made by a Legislature or other <5>competent authority in the territory of India before the commencement of <5>this Constitution and not previously repealed, notwithstanding that any <5>such law or any part thereof may not be then in operation either at all or in <5>particular areas. <6>4.<5> Nothing in this article shall apply to any amendment of this Constitution made <5>under article 368. <7>Right to Equality <4>• General guarantee of equality <7>14. Equality before law <5>The State shall not deny to any person equality before the law or the equal <5>protection of the laws within the territory of India. <4>• General guarantee of equality <7>15. Prohibition of discrimination on grounds of religion, <4>• Equality regardless of gender <4>• Equality regardless of origin <4>• Equality regardless of race <7>race, caste, sex or place of birth <4>• Equality regardless of religion <6>1. <5>The State shall not discriminate against any citizen on grounds only of religion, <5>race, caste, sex, place of birth or any of them. <6>2. <5>No citizen shall, on grounds only of religion, race, caste, sex, place of birth or any <5>of them, be subject to any disability, liability, restriction or condition with regard <5>to- <6>a.<5> access to shops, public restaurants, hotels and places of public <5>entertainment; or <6>b.<5> the use of wells, tanks, bathing ghats, roads and places of public resort <5>maintained wholly or partly out of State funds or dedicated to the use of <5>general public. <6>3. <5>Nothing in this article shall prevent the State from making any special provision <5>for women and children. <6>4. <5>Nothing in this article or in clause (2) of article 29 shall prevent the State from <5>making any special provision for the advancement of any socially and <5>educationally backward classes of citizens or for the Scheduled Castes and the <5>Scheduled Tribes. <6>5. <5>Nothing in this article or in sub-clause (g) of clause (1) of article 19 shall prevent <5>the State from making any special provision, by law, for the advancement of any <5>socially and educationally backward classes of citizens or for the Scheduled <5>Castes or the Scheduled Tribes in so far as such special provisions relate to their <5>admission to educational institutions including private educational institutions, <5>whether aided or unaided by the State, other than the minority educational <5>institutions referred to in clause (1) of article 30. <4>• General guarantee of equality <7>16. Equality of opportunity in matters of public <4>• Equality regardless of gender <4>• Equality regardless of origin <4>• Equality regardless of race <7>employment <4>• Equality regardless of religion <6>1. <5>There shall be equality of opportunity for all citizens in matters relating to <5>employment or appointment to any office under the State. <6>2. <5>No citizen shall, on grounds only of religion, race, caste, sex, descent, place of <5>birth, residence or any of them, be ineligible for, or discriminated against in <5>respect of, any employment or office under the State. <6>3. <5>Nothing in this article shall prevent Parliament from making any law prescribing, <5>in regard to a class or classes of employment or appointment to an office under <5>the Government of, or any local or other authority within, a State or Union <5>territory, any requirement as to residence within that State or Union territory <5>prior to such employment or appointment. <6>4. <5>Nothing in this article shall prevent the State from making any provision for the <5>reservation of appointments or posts in favour of any backward class of citizens <5>which, in the opinion of the State, is not adequately represented in the services <5>under the State. <6>4A. <5>Nothing in this article shall prevent the State from making any provision for <5>reservation in matters of promotion, with consequential seniority, to any class <5>or classes of posts in the services under the State in favour of the Scheduled <5>Castes and the Scheduled Tribes which in the opinion of the States, are not <5>adequately represented in the services under the State. <6>4B. <5>Nothing in this article shall prevent the State from considering any unfilled <5>vacancies of a year which are reserved for being filled up in that year in <5>accordance with any provision for reservation made under clause (4) or clause <5>(4A) as a separate class of vacancies to be filled up in any succeeding year or <5>years and such class of vacancies shall not be considered together with the <5>vacancies of the year in which they are being filled up for determining the ceiling <5>of fifty per cent, reservation on total number of vacancies of that year. <6>5. <5>Nothing in this article shall affect the operation of any law which provides that <5>the incumbent of an office in connection with the affairs of any religious or <5>denominational institution or any member of the governing body thereof shall <5>be a person professing a particular religion or belonging to a particular <5>denomination. <4>• Mentions of social class <7>17. Abolition of Untouchability <5>"Untouchability" is abolished and its practice in any form is forbidden. The <5>enforcement of any disability arising out of "Untouchability" shall be an offence <5>punishable in accordance with law. <4>• Mentions of social class <7>18. Abolition of titles <6>1.<5> No title, not being a military or academic distinction, shall be conferred by the <5>State. <6>2.<5> No citizen of India shall accept any title from any foreign State. <6>3.<5> No person who is not a citizen of India shall, while he holds any office of profit or <5>trust under the State, accept without the consent of the President any title from <5>any foreign State. <6>4.<5> No person holding any office of profit or trust under the State shall, without the <5>consent of the President, accept any present, emolument, or office of any kind <5>from or under any foreign State. <7>Right to Freedom <4>• Emergency provisions <7>19. Protection of certain rights regarding freedom of <7>speech, etc <6>1. <5>All citizens shall have the right- <4>• Freedom of expression <6>a.<5> to freedom of speech and expression; <4>• Freedom of assembly <6>b.<5> to assemble peaceably and without arms; <4>• Freedom of association <6>c. <5>to form associations or unions or co-operative societies; <4>• Right to join trade unions <4>• Freedom of movement <6>d.<5> to move freely throughout the territory of India; <6>e.<5> to reside and settle in any part of the territory of India; <6>f. <5>[omitted by s. 2, ibid., (w.e.f. 20-6-1979).] <4>• Right to establish a business <6>g.<5> to practise any profession, or to carry on any occupation, trade or business. <4>• Right to choose occupation <6>2. <5>Nothing in sub-clause (a) of clause (1) shall affect the operation of any existing <5>law, or prevent the State from making any law, in so far as such law imposes <5>reasonable restrictions on the exercise of the right conferred by the said <5>sub-clause in the interests of the sovereignty and integrity of India, the security <5>of the State, friendly relations with Foreign States, public order, decency or <5>morality, or in relation to contempt of court, defamation or incitement to an <5>offence. <6>3. <5>Nothing in sub-clause (b) of the said clause shall affect the operation of any <5>existing law in so far as it imposes, or prevent the State from making any law <5>imposing, in the interest of the sovereignty and integrity of India or public order, <5>reasonable restrictions on the exercise of the right conferred by the said <5>sub-clause. <6>4. <5>Nothing in sub-clause (c) of the said clause shall affect the operation of any <5>existing law in so far as it imposes, or prevent the State from making any law <5>imposing, in the interests of the sovereignty and integrity of India or public order <5>or morality, reasonable restrictions on the exercise of the right conferred by the <5>said sub-clause. <6>5. <5>Nothing in sub-clause (d) and (e) of the said clause shall affect the operation of <5>any existing law in so far as it imposes, or prevent the State from making any law <5>imposing, reasonable restrictions on the exercise of any of the rights conferred <5>by the said sub-clauses either in the interests of the general public or for the <5>protection of the interests of any Scheduled Tribe. <6>6. <5>Nothing in sub-clause (g) of the said clause shall affect the operation of any <5>existing law in so far as it imposes, or prevent the State from making any law <5>imposing, in the interests of the general public, reasonable restrictions on the <5>exercise of the right conferred by the said sub-clause; and, in particular, nothing <5>in the said sub-clause shall affect the operation of any existing law in so far as it <5>relates to, or prevent the State from making any law relating to,- <6>i. <5>the professional or technical qualifications necessary for practising any <5>profession or carrying on any occupation, trade or business, or <6>ii. <5>the carrying on by the State, or by a corporation owned or controlled by the <5>State, of any trade, business, industry or service, whether to the exclusion, <5>complete or partial, of citizens or otherwise. <7>20. Protection in respect of conviction for offences <4>• Protection from ex post facto laws <6>1.<5> No person shall be convicted of any offence except for violation of a law in force <4>• Principle of no punishment without law <5>at the time of the commission of the act charged as an offence, nor be subjected <5>to a penalty greater than that which might have been inflicted under the law in <5>force at the time of the commission of the offence. <4>• Prohibition of double jeopardy <6>2.<5> No person shall be prosecuted and punished for the same offence more than <5>once. <4>• Protection from self-incrimination <6>3.<5> No person accused of any offence shall be compelled to be a witness against <5>himself. <4>• Right to life <7>21. Protection of life and personal liberty <5>No person shall be deprived of his life or personal liberty except according to <5>procedure established by law. <4>• Compulsory education <7>21A. Right to education <4>• Free education <5>The State shall provide free and compulsory education to all children of the age of six <5>to fourteen years in such manner as the State may, by law, determine. <7>22. Protection against arrest and detention in certain cases <4>• Protection from unjustified restraint <4>• Right to counsel <6>1. <5>No person who is arrested shall be detained in custody without being informed, <5>as soon as may be, of the grounds for such arrest nor shall he be denied the right <5>to consult, and to be defended by, a legal practitioner of his choice. <6>2. <5>Every person who is arrested and detained in custody shall be produced before <5>the nearest magistrate within a period of twenty-four hours of such arrest <5>excluding the time necessary for the journey from the place of arrest to court of <5>the magistrate and no such person shall be detained in custody beyond the said <5>period without the authority of a magistrate. <6>3. <5>Nothing in clauses (1) and (2) shall apply- <6>a.<5> to any person who for the time being is an enemy alien; or <6>b.<5> to any person who is arrested or detained under any law providing for <5>preventive detention. <6>4. <5>No law providing for preventive detention shall authorise the detention of a <5>person for a longer period than three months unless- <6>a.<5> an Advisory Board consisting of persons who are, or have been, or are <5>qualified to be appointed as, Judges of a High Court has reported before <5>the expiration of the said period of three months that there is in its opinion <5>sufficient cause for such detention: <5>Provided that nothing in this sub-clause shall authorise the detention of any <5>person beyond the maximum period prescribed by any law made by <5>Parliament under sub-clause (b) of clause (7); or <6>b.<5> such person is detained in accordance with the provisions of any law made <5>by Parliament under sub-clauses (a) and (b) of clause (7). <6>5.<5> When any person is detained in pursuance of an order made under any law <5>providing for preventive detention, the authority making the order shall, as soon <5>as may be, communicate to such person the grounds on which the order has <5>been made and shall afford him the earliest opportunity of making a <5>representation against the order. <6>6.<5> Nothing in clause (5) shall require the authority making any such order as is <5>referred to in that clause to disclose facts which such authority considers to be <5>against the public interest to disclose. <6>7.<5> Parliament may by law prescribe- <6>a.<5> the circumstances under which, and the class or classes of cases in which, a <5>person may be detained for a period longer than three months under any <5>law providing for preventive detention without obtaining the opinion of an <5>Advisory Board in accordance with the provisions of sub-clause (a) of <5>clause (4); <6>b.<5> the maximum period for which any person may in any class or classes of <5>cases be detained under any law providing for preventive detention; and <6>c. <5>the procedure to be followed by an Advisory Board in an inquiry under <5>sub-clause (a) of clause (4). <7>Right against Exploitation <7>23. Prohibition of traffic in human beings and forced labour <6>1.<5> Traffic in human beings and begar and other similar forms of forced labour are <5>prohibited and any contravention of this provision shall be an offence <5>punishable in accordance with law. <6>2.<5> Nothing in this article shall prevent the State from imposing compulsory service <5>for public purposes, and in imposing such service the State shall not make any <5>discrimination on grounds only of religion, race, caste or class or any of them. <7>24. Prohibition of employment of children in factories, etc <4>• Limits on employment of children <5>No child below the age of fourteen years shall be employed to work in any factory or <5>mine or engaged in any other hazardous employment. <4>• Freedom of religion <7>Right to Freedom of Religion <7>25. Freedom of conscience and free profession, practice <7>and propagation of religion <6>1.<5> Subject to public order, morality and health and to the other provisions of this <5>Part, all persons are equally entitled to freedom of conscience and the right <5>freely to profess, practise and propagate religion. <6>2.<5> Nothing in this article shall affect the operation of any existing law or prevent <5>the State from making any law <6>a.<5> regulating or restricting any economic, financial, political or other secular <5>activity which may be associated with religious practice; <6>b.<5> providing for social welfare and reform or the throwing open of Hindu <5>religious institutions of a public character to all classes and sections of <5>Hindus. <7>Explanation I <5>The wearing and carrying of kirpans shall be deemed to be included in the profession <5>of the Sikh religion. <7>Explanation II <5>In sub-clause (b) of clause (2), the reference to Hindus shall be construed as including <5>a reference to persons professing the Sikh, Jaina or Buddhist religion, and the <5>reference to Hindu religious institutions shall be construed accordingly. <7>26. Freedom to manage religious affairs <5>Subject to public order, morality and health, every religious denomination or any <5>section thereof shall have the right- <6>a.<5> to establish and maintain institutions for religious and charitable purposes; <6>b.<5> to manage its own affairs in matters of religion; <6>c. <5>to own and acquire movable and immovable property; and <6>d.<5> to administer such property in accordance with law. <7>27. Freedom as to payment of taxes for promotion of any <7>particular religion <5>No person shall be compelled to pay any taxes, the proceeds of which are specifically <5>appropriated in payment of expenses for the promotion or maintenance of any <5>particular religion or religious denomination. <7>28. Freedom as to attendance at religious instruction or <7>religious worship in certain educational institutions <4>• Separation of church and state <6>1.<5> No religious instruction shall be provided in any educational institution wholly <5>maintained out of State funds. <6>2.<5> Nothing in clause <5>(1) shall apply to an educational institution which is <5>administered by the State but has been established under any endowment or <5>trust which requires that religious instruction shall be imparted in such <5>institution. <6>3.<5> No person attending any educational institution recognised by the State or <5>receiving aid out of State funds shall be required to take part in any religious <5>instruction that may be imparted in such institution or to attend any religious <5>worship that may be conducted in such institution or in any premises attached <5>thereto unless such person or, if such person is a minor, his guardian has given <5>his consent thereto. <7>Cultural and Educational Rights <4>• Right to culture <7>29. Protection of interests of minorities <4>• Protection of language use <6>1.<5> Any section of the citizens residing in the territory of India or any part thereof <5>having a distinct language, script or culture of its own shall have the right to <5>conserve the same. <6>2.<5> No citizen shall be denied admission into any educational institution maintained <5>by the State or receiving aid out of State funds on grounds only of religion, race, <5>caste, language or any of them. <7>30. Right of minorities to establish and administer <7>educational institutions <6>1.<5> All minorities, whether based on religion or language, shall have the right to <5>establish and administer educational institutions of their choice. <6>1A.<5> In making any law providing for the compulsory acquisition of any property of <5>an educational institution established and administered by a minority, referred <5>to in clause (1), the State shall ensure that the amount fixed by or determined <5>under such law for the acquisition of such property is such as would not restrict <5>or abrogate the right guaranteed under that clause. <6>2.<5> The State shall not, in granting aid to educational institutions, discriminate <5>against any educational institution on the ground that it is under the <5>management of a minority, whether based on religion or language. <7>31. Compulsory acquisition of property <5>Rep. by the Constitution <5>(Forty-fourth Amendment) Act, <5>1978, s. <5>6(w.e.f. <5>20-6-1979). <7>Saving of Certain Laws <7>31A. Saving of laws providing for acquisition of estates, etc <4>• Protection from expropriation <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything contained in article 13, no law providing for- <6>a.<5> the acquisition by the State of any estate or of any rights therein or the <5>extinguishment or modification of any such rights, or <6>b.<5> the taking over of the management of any property by the State for a <5>limited period either in the public interest or in order to secure the proper <5>management of the property, or <6>c. <5>the amalgamation of two or more corporations either in the public interest <5>or in order to secure the proper management of any of the corporations, or <6>d.<5> the extinguishment or modification of any rights of managing agents, <5>secretaries and treasurers, managing directors, directors or managers of <5>corporations, or of any voting rights of share-holders thereof, or <6>e.<5> the extinguishment or modification of any rights accruing by virtue of any <5>agreement, lease or licence for the purpose of searching for, or winning, any <5>mineral or mineral oil, or the premature termination or cancellation of any <5>such agreement, lease or licence, <5>shall be deemed to be void on the ground that it is inconsistent with, or takes <5>away or abridges any of the rights conferred by article 14 or article 19: <5>Provided that where such law is a law made by the Legislature of a State, the <5>provisions of this article shall not apply thereto unless such law, having been <5>reserved for the consideration of the President, has received his assent: <5>Provided further that where any law makes any provision for the acquisition by <5>the State of any estate and where any land comprised therein is held by a person <5>under his personal cultivation, it shall not be lawful for the State to acquire any <5>portion of such land as is within the ceiling limit applicable to him under any law <5>for the time being in force or any building or structure standing thereon or <5>appurtenant thereto, unless the law relating to the acquisition of such land, <5>building or structure, provides for payment of compensation at a rate which <5>shall not be less than the market value thereof. <6>2. <5>In this article,- <6>a.<5> the expression "estate" shall, in relation to any local area, have the same <5>meaning as that expression or its local equivalent has in the existing law <5>relating to land tenures in force in that area and shall also include- <6>i. <5>any jagir, inam or muafi or other similar grant and in the States of Tamil <5>Nadu and Kerala, any janmam right; <6>ii. <5>any land held under ryotwari settlement; <6>iii. <5>any land held or let for purposes of agriculture or for purposes <5>ancillary thereto, including waste land, forest land, land for pasture or <5>sites of buildings and other structures occupied by cultivators of land, <5>agricultural labourers and village artisans; <6>b.<5> the expression "rights", in relation to an estate, shall include any rights <5>vesting in a proprietor, sub-proprietor, under-proprietor, tenure-holder, <5>raiyat, under-raiyat or other intermediary and any rights or privileges in <5>respect of land revenue. <7>31B. Validation of certain Acts and Regulations <5>Without prejudice to the generality of the provisions contained in article 31A, none <5>of the Acts and Regulations specified in the Ninth Schedule nor any of the provision <5>thereof shall be deemed to be void, or ever to have become void, on the ground that <5>such Act, Regulation or provision is inconsistent with, or takes away or abridges any <5>of the rights conferred by, any provisions of this part, and notwithstanding any <5>judgment, decree or order of any court or tribunal to the contrary, each of the said <5>Acts and Regulations shall, subject to the power of any competent Legislature to <5>repeal or amend it, continue in force. <7>31C. Saving of laws giving effect to certain directive <7>principles <5>Notwithstanding anything contained in article 13, no law giving effect to the policy of <5>the State towards securing all or any of the principles laid down in Part IV shall be <5>deemed to be void on the ground that it is inconsistent with, or takes away or <5>abridges any of the rights conferred by article 14 or article 19; and no law containing <5>a declaration that it is for giving effect to such policy shall be called in question in any <5>court on the ground that it does not give effect to such policy: <5>Provided that where such law is made by the Legislature of a State, the provisions of <5>this article shall not apply thereto unless such law, having been reserved for the <5>consideration of the President, has received his assent. <7>31D. Saving of laws in respect of anti-national activities <5>Rep. by the Constitution (Forty-third Amendment) Act, 1977, s. 2(w.e.f. 13-4-1978) <7>Right to Constitutional Remedies <7>32. Remedies for enforcement of rights conferred by this <7>Part <6>1.<5> The right to move the Supreme Court by appropriate proceedings for the <5>enforcement of the rights conferred by this Part is guaranteed. <6>2.<5> The Supreme Court shall have power to issue directions or orders or writs, <5>including writs in the nature of habeas corpus, mandamus, prohibition, quo <5>warranto and certiorari, whichever may be appropriate, for the enforcement of <5>any of the rights conferred by this Part. <6>3.<5> Without prejudice to the powers conferred on the Supreme Court by clauses (1) <5>and (2), Parliament may by law empower any other court to exercise within the <5>local limits of its jurisdiction all or any of the powers exercisable by the Supreme <5>Court under clause (2). <6>4.<5> The right guaranteed by this article shall not be suspended except as otherwise <5>provided for by this Constitution. <7>32A. Constitutional validity of State laws not to be <7>considered in proceedings under article 32 <5>Rep. by the Constitution (Forty-third Amendment) Act, 1977, s. 3 (w.e.f. 13-41978). <7>33. Power of Parliament to modify the rights conferred by <4>• Restrictions on the armed forces <7>this Part in their application to Forces, etc <5>Parliament may, by law, determine to what extent any of the rights conferred by this <5>Part shall, in their application to,- <6>a.<5> the members of the Armed Forces; or <6>b.<5> the members of the Forces charged with the maintenance of public order; <5>or <6>c. <5>persons employed in any bureau or other organisation established by the <5>State for purposes of intelligence or counter intelligence; or <6>d.<5> persons employed in, or in connection with, the telecommunication <5>systems set up for the purposes of any Force, bureau or organisation <5>referred to in clauses (a) to (c), <5>be restricted or abrogated so as to ensure the proper discharge of their duties and <5>the maintenance of discipline among them. <7>34. Restriction on rights conferred by this Part while <7>martial law is in force in any area <5>Notwithstanding anything in the foregoing provisions of this Part, Parliament may by <5>law indemnify any person in the service of the Union or of a State or any other <5>person in respect of any act done by him in connection with the maintenance or <5>restoration of order in any area within the territory of India where martial law was in <5>force or validate any sentence passed, punishment inflicted, forfeiture ordered or <5>other act done under martial law in such area. <7>35. Legislation to give effect to the provisions of this Part <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,- <6>a.<5> Parliament shall have, and the Legislature of a State shall not have, power <5>to make laws- <6>i. <5>with respect to any of the matters which under clause (3) of article 16, <5>clause (3) of article 32, article 33 and article 34 may be provided for by <5>law made by Parliament; and <6>ii. <5>for prescribing punishment for those acts which are declared to be <5>offences under this part, <5>and Parliament shall, as soon as may be after the commencement of this <5>Constitution, make laws for prescribing punishment for the acts referred to <5>in sub-clause (ii); <6>b.<5> any law in force immediately before the commencement of this <5>Constitution in the territory of India with respect to any of the matters <5>referred to in sub-clause (i) of clause (a) or providing for punishment for any <5>act referred to in sub-clause (ii) of that clause shall, subject to the terms <5>thereof and to any adaptations and modifications that may be made therein <5>under article 372, continue in force until altered or repealed or amended by <5>Parliament. <7>Explanation <5>In this article, the expression "law in force" has the same meaning as in article 372. <9>PART IV: DIRECTIVE PRINCIPLES OF STATE <9>POLICY <7>36. Definition <5>In this Part, unless the context otherwise requires, "the State" has the same meaning <5>as in Part III. <7>37. Application of the principles contained in this Part <5>The provisions contained in this Part shall not be enforceable by any court, but the <5>principles therein laid down are nevertheless fundamental in the governance of the <5>country and it shall be the duty of the State to apply these principles in making laws. <7>38. State to secure a social order for the promotion of <7>welfare of the people <6>1.<5> The State shall strive to promote the welfare of the people by securing and <5>protecting as effectively as it may a social order in which justice, social, <5>economic and political, shall inform all the institutions of the national life. <6>2.<5> The State shall, in particular, strive to minimise the inequalities in income, and <5>endeavour to eliminate inequalities in status, facilities and opportunities, not <5>only amongst individuals but also amongst groups of people residing in different <5>areas or engaged in different vocations. <7>39. Certain principles of policy to be followed by the State <5>The State shall, in particular, direct its policy towards securing- <4>• Equality regardless of gender <6>a.<5> that the citizen, men and women equally, have the right to an adequate <5>means of livelihood; <6>b.<5> that the ownership and control of the material resources of the community <5>are so distributed as best to subserve the common good; <6>c. <5>that the operation of the economic system does not result in the <5>concentration of wealth and means of production to the common <5>detriment; <4>• Right to equal pay for work <6>d.<5> that there is equal pay for equal work for both men and women; <4>• Rights of children <6>e.<5> that the health and strength of workers, men and women, and the tender <4>• Limits on employment of children <5>age of children are not abused and that citizens are not forced by economic <5>necessity to enter avocations unsuited to their age or strength; <4>• Rights of children <6>f. <5>that children are given opportunities and facilities to develop in a healthy <4>• Limits on employment of children <4>• Human dignity <5>manner and in conditions of freedom and dignity and that childhood and <5>youth are protected against exploitation and against moral and material <5>abandonment. <4>• Right to counsel <7>39A. Equal justice and free legal aid <5>The State shall secure that the operation of the legal system promotes justice, on a <5>basis of equal opportunity, and shall, in particular, provide free legal aid, by suitable <5>legislation or schemes or in any other way, to ensure that opportunities for securing <5>justice are not denied to any citizen by reason of economic or other disabilities. <7>40. Organisation of village panchayats <5>The State shall take steps to organise village panchayats and endow them with such <5>powers and authority as may be necessary to enable them to function as units of <5>self-government. <4>• State support for the elderly <7>41. Right to work, to education and to public assistance in <4>• State support for the unemployed <4>• State support for the disabled <4>• Right to work <7>certain cases <5>The State shall, within the limits of its economic capacity and development, make <5>effective provision for securing the right to work, to education and to public <5>assistance in cases of unemployment, old age, sickness and disablement, and in other <5>cases of undeserved want. <7>42. Provision for just and humane conditions of work and <4>• Right to safe work environment <7>maternity relief <5>The State shall make provision for securing just and humane conditions of work and <5>for maternity relief. <7>43. Living wage, etc., for workers <4>• Right to reasonable standard of living <5>The State shall endeavour to secure, by suitable legislation or economic organisation <5>or in any other way, to all workers agricultural, industrial or otherwise, work, a living <5>wage, conditions of work ensuring a decent standard of life and full enjoyment of <5>leisure and social and cultural opportunities and, in particular, the State shall <5>endeavour to promote cottage industries on an individual or co-operative basis in <5>rural areas. <7>43A. Participation of workers in management of industries <5>The State shall take steps, by suitable legislation or in any other way, to secure the <5>participation of workers in the management of undertakings, establishments or <5>other organisation engaged in any industry. <7>43B. Promotion of co-operative societies <5>The state shall endeavour to promote voluntary formation, autonomous functioning, <5>democratic control and professional management of co-operative societies. <7>44. Uniform civil code for the citizens <5>The State shall endeavour to secure for the citizens a uniform civil code throughout <5>the territory of India. <4>• Compulsory education <7>45. Provision for early childhood care and education to <4>• Free education <7>children below the age of six years <5>The State shall endeavour to provide early childhood care and education for all <5>children until they complete the age of six years. <7>46. Promotion of educational and economic interests of <4>• Integration of ethnic communities <7>Scheduled Castes, Scheduled Tribes and other weaker <7>sections <5>The State shall promote with special care the educational and economic interests of <5>the weaker sections of the people, and in particular, of the Scheduled Castes and the <5>Scheduled Tribes, and shall protect them from social injustice and all forms of <5>exploitation. <4>• Right to health care <7>47. Duty of the State to raise the level of nutrition and the <7>standard of living and to improve public health <5>The State shall regard the raising of the level of nutrition and the standard of living of <5>its people and the improvement of public health as among its primary duties and, in <5>particular, the State shall endeavour to bring about prohibition of the consumption <5>except for medicinal purposes of intoxicating drinks and of drugs which are injurious <5>to health. <4>• Reference to science <7>48. Organisation of agriculture and animal husbandry <5>The State shall endeavour to organise agriculture and animal husbandry on modern <5>and scientific lines and shall, in particular, take steps for preserving and improving <5>the breeds, and prohibiting the slaughter, of cows and calves and other milch and <5>draught cattle. <4>• Protection of environment <7>48A. Protection and improvement of environment and <7>safeguarding of forests and wild life <5>The State shall endeavour to protect and improve the environment and to safeguard <5>the forests and wild life of the country. <4>• Reference to art <7>49. Protection of monuments and places and objects of <7>national importance <5>It shall be the obligation of the State to protect every monument or place or object of <5>artistic or historic interest, declared by or under law made by Parliament to be of <5>national importance, from spoliation, disfigurement, destruction, removal, disposal <5>or export, as the case may be. <4>• Claim of executive independence <7>50. Separation of judiciary from executive <4>• Judicial independence <5>The State shall take steps to separate the judiciary from the executive in the public <5>services of the State. <7>51. Promotion of international peace and security <5>The State shall endeavour to- <6>a.<5> promote international peace and security; <6>b.<5> maintain just and honourable relations between nations; <4>• International law <6>c. <5>foster respect for international law and treaty obligations in the dealings of <4>• Treaty ratification <5>organised people with one another; and <6>d.<5> encourage settlement of international disputes by arbitration. <9>PART IVA: FUNDAMENTAL DUTIES <7>51A. Fundamental duties <5>It shall be the duty of every citizen of India- <4>• Duty to obey the constitution <6>a. <5>to abide by the Constitution and respect its ideals and institutions, the <4>• National anthem <4>• National flag <5>National Flag and the National Anthem; <6>b. <5>to cherish and follow the noble ideals which inspired our national struggle <5>for freedom; <6>c. <5>to uphold and protect the sovereignty, unity and integrity of India; <4>• Duty to serve in the military <6>d. <5>to defend the country and render national service when called upon to do <5>so; <4>• Human dignity <6>e. <5>to promote harmony and the spirit of common brotherhood amongst all the <5>people of India transcending religious, linguistic and regional or sectional <5>diversities; to renounce practices derogatory to the dignity of women; <6>f. <5>to value and preserve the rich heritage of our composite culture; <4>• Protection of environment <6>g. <5>to protect and improve the natural environment including forests, lakes, <5>rivers and wild life, and to have compassion for living creatures; <6>h. <5>to develop the scientific temper, humanism and the spirit of inquiry and <5>reform; <6>i. <5>to safeguard public property and to abjure violence; <6>j. <5>to strive towards excellence in all spheres of individual and collective <5>activity so that the nation constantly rises to higher levels of endeavour and <5>achievement. <6>k.<5> who is a parent or guardian to provide opportunities for education to his <5>child or, as the case may be, ward between the age of six and fourteen <5>years. <9>PART V: THE UNION <7>CHAPTER I: THE EXECUTIVE <7>The President and Vice-President <4>• Name/structure of executive(s) <7>52. The President of India <5>There shall be a President of India. <4>• Name/structure of executive(s) <7>53. Executive power of the Union <6>1.<5> The executive power of the Union shall be vested in the President and shall be <5>exercised by him either directly or through officers subordinate to him in <5>accordance with this Constitution. <4>• Designation of commander in chief <6>2.<5> Without prejudice to the generality of the foregoing provision, the supreme <5>command of the Defence Forces of the Union shall be vested in the President <5>and the exercise thereof shall be regulated by law. <6>3.<5> Nothing in this article shall- <6>a.<5> be deemed to transfer to the President any functions conferred by any <5>existing law on the Government of any State or other authority; or <6>b.<5> prevent Parliament from conferring by law functions on authorities other <5>than the President. <4>• Head of state selection <7>54. Election of President <5>The President shall be elected by the members of an electoral college consisting of- <6>a.<5> the elected members of both Houses of Parliament; and <6>b.<5> the elected members of the Legislative Assemblies of the States. <7>Explanation <5>In this article and in article 55, "State" includes the National Capital Territory of <5>Delhi and the Union territory of Pondicherry. <4>• Head of state selection <7>55. Manner of election of President <6>1.<5> As far as practicable, there shall be uniformity in the scale of representation of <5>the different States at the election of the President. <6>2.<5> For the purpose of securing such uniformity among the States inter se as well as <5>parity between the States as a whole and the Union, the number of votes which <5>each elected member of Parliament and of the Legislative Assembly of each <5>State is entitled to cast at such election shall be determined in the following <5>manner:- <6>a.<5> every elected member of the Legislative Assembly of a State shall have as <5>many votes as there are multiples of one thousand in the quotient obtained <5>by dividing the population of the State by the total number of the elected <5>members of the Assembly; <6>b.<5> if, after taking the said multiples of one thousand, the remainder is not less <5>than five hundred, then the vote of each member referred to in sub-clause <5>(a) shall be further increased by one; <6>c. <5>each elected member of either House of Parliament shall have such number <5>of votes as may be obtained by dividing the total number of votes assigned <5>to the members of the Legislative Assemblies of the States under <5>sub-clauses (a) and (b) by the total number of the elected members of both <5>Houses of Parliament, fractions exceeding one-half being counted as one <5>and other fractions being disregarded. <4>• Secret ballot <6>3.<5> The election of the President shall be held in accordance with the system of <5>proportional representation by means of the single transferable vote and the <5>voting at such election shall be by secret ballot. <7>Explanation <4>• Census <5>In this article, the expression "population" means the population as ascertained at <5>the last preceding census of which the relevant figures have been published: <5>Provided that the reference in this Explanation to the last preceding census of which <5>the relevant figures have been published shall, until the relevant figures for the first <5>census taken after the year 49.1 have been published, be construed as a reference to <5>the 1971 census. <7>56. Term of office of President <4>• Head of state term length <6>1.<5> The President shall hold office for a term of five years from the date on which he <5>enters upon his office: <5>Provided that- <6>a.<5> the President may, by writing under his hand addressed to the <5>Vice-President, resign his office; <6>b.<5> the President may, for violation of the Constitution, be removed from office <5>by impeachment in the manner provided in article 61; <6>c. <5>the President shall, notwithstanding the expiration of his term, continue to <5>hold office until his successor enters upon his office. <6>2.<5> Any resignation addressed to the Vice-President under clause (a) of the proviso <5>to clause (1) shall forthwith be communicated by him to the Speaker of the <5>House of the People. <7>57. Eligibility for re-election <5>A person who holds, or who has held, office as President shall, subject to the other <5>provisions of this Constitution be eligible for re-election to that office. <4>• Eligibility for head of state <7>58. Qualifications for election as President <6>1.<5> No person shall be eligible for election as President unless he- <6>a.<5> is a citizen of India, <4>• Minimum age of head of state <6>b.<5> has completed the age of thirty-five years, and <6>c. <5>is qualified for election as a member of the House of the People <6>2.<5> A person shall not be eligible for election as President if he holds any office of <5>profit under the Government of India or the Government of any State or under <5>any local or other authority subject to the control of any of the said <5>Governments. <7>Explanation <5>For the purposes of this article, a person shall not be deemed to hold any office of <5>profit by reason only that he is the President or Vice-President of the Union or the <5>Governor of any State or is a Minister either for the Union or for any State. <7>59. Conditions of President's office <6>1.<5> The President shall not be a member of either House of Parliament or of a House <5>of the Legislature of any State, and if a member of either House of Parliament or <5>of a House of the Legislature of any State be elected President, he shall be <5>deemed to have vacated his seat in that House on the date on which he enters <5>upon his office as President. <6>2.<5> The President shall not hold any other office of profit. <6>3.<5> The President shall be entitled without payment of rent to the use of his official <5>residences and shall be also entitled to such emoluments, allowances and <5>privileges as may be determined by Parliament by law and, until provision in that <5>behalf is so made, such emoluments, allowances and privileges as are specified in <5>the Second Schedule. <6>4.<5> The emoluments and allowances of the President shall not be diminished during <5>his term of office. <7>60. Oath or affirmation by the President <4>• God or other deities <5>Every President and every person acting as President or discharging the functions of <4>• Oaths to abide by constitution <5>the President shall, before entering upon his office, make and subscribe in the <5>presence of the Chief Justice of India or, in his absence, the senior-most Judge of the <5>Supreme Court available, an oath or affirmation in the following form, that is to say- <4>• God or other deities <5>"I, A.B., do Swear in the name of God/Solemnly Affirm that I will faithfully execute <4>• Oaths to abide by constitution <5>the office of President (or discharge the functions of the President) of India and will <5>to the best of my ability preserve, protect and defend the Constitution and the law <5>and that I will devote myself to the service and well-being of the people of India." <4>• Head of state removal <7>61. Procedure for impeachment of the President <6>1.<5> When a President is to be impeached for violation of the Constitution, the <5>charge shall be preferred by either House of Parliament. <6>2.<5> No such charge shall be preferred unless- <6>a.<5> the proposal to prefer such charge is contained in a resolution which has <5>been moved after at least fourteen days' notice in writing signed by not less <5>than one-fourth of the total number of members of the House has been <5>given of their intention to move the resolution, and <6>b.<5> such resolution has been passed by a majority of not less than two-thirds of <5>the total membership of the House. <6>3.<5> When a charge has been so preferred by either House of Parliament, the other <5>House shall investigate the charge or cause the charge to be investigated and <5>the President shall have the right to appear and to be represented at such <5>investigation. <6>4.<5> If as a result of the investigation a resolution is passed by a majority of not less <5>than two-thirds of the total membership of the House by which the charge was <5>investigated or caused to be investigated, declaring that the charge preferred <5>against the President has been sustained, such resolution shall have the effect of <5>removing the President from his office as from the date on which the resolution <5>is so passed. <4>• Head of state replacement <7>62. Time of holding election to fill vacancy in the office of <7>President and the term of office of person elected to fill <7>casual vacancy <6>1.<5> An election to fill a vacancy caused by the expiration of the term of office of <5>President shall be completed before the expiration of the term. <6>2.<5> An election to fill a vacancy in the office of President occurring by reason of his <5>death, resignation or removal, or otherwise shall be held as soon as possible <5>after, and in no case later than six months from, the date of occurrence of the <5>vacancy; and the person elected to fill the vacancy shall, subject to the <5>provisions of article 56, be entitled to hold office for the full term of five years <5>from the date on which he enters upon his office. <4>• Deputy executive <7>63. The Vice-President of India <5>There shall be a Vice-President of India. <7>64. The Vice-President to be ex-officio Chairman of the <7>Council of States <4>• Deputy executive <5>The Vice-President shall be ex-officio Chairman of the Council of States and shall not <5>hold any other office of profit: <5>Provided that during any period when the Vice-President acts as President or <5>discharges the functions of the President under article 65, he shall not perform the <5>duties of the office of Chairman of the Council of States and shall not be entitled to <5>any salary or allowance payable to the Chairman of the Council of States under <5>article 97. <7>65. The Vice-President to act as President or to discharge <7>his functions during casual vacancies in the office, or <7>during the absence, of President <6>1.<5> In the event of the occurrence of any vacancy in the office of the President by <5>reason of his death, resignation or removal, or otherwise, the Vice-President <5>shall act as President until the date on which a new President elected in <5>accordance with the provisions of this Chapter to fill such vacancy enters upon <5>his office. <6>2.<5> When the President is unable to discharge his functions owing to absence, <5>illness or any other cause, the Vice-President shall discharge his functions until <5>the date on which the President resumes his duties. <6>3.<5> The Vice-President shall, during, and in respect of, the period while he is so <5>acting as, or discharging the functions of, President have all the powers and <5>immunities of the President and be entitled to such emoluments, allowances and <5>privileges as may be determined by Parliament by law and, until provision in that <5>behalf is so made, such emoluments, allowances and privileges as are specified in <5>the Second Schedule. <4>• Deputy executive <7>66. Election of Vice-President <4>• Secret ballot <6>1.<5> The Vice-President shall be elected by the members of an electoral college <5>consisting of the members of both Houses of Parliament in accordance with the <5>system of proportional representation by means of the single transferable vote <5>and the voting at such election shall be by secret ballot. <6>2.<5> The Vice-President shall not be a member of either House of Parliament or of a <5>House of the Legislature of any State, and if a member of either House of <5>Parliament or of a House of the Legislature of any State be elected <5>Vice-President, he shall be deemed to have vacated his seat in that House on the <5>date on which he enters upon his office as Vice-President. <6>3.<5> No person shall be eligible for election as Vice-President unless he- <6>a.<5> is a citizen of India; <6>b.<5> has completed the age of thirty-five years; and <6>c. <5>is qualified for election as a member of the Council of States. <6>4.<5> A person shall not be eligible for election as Vice-President if he holds any office <5>of profit under the Government of India or the Government of any State or <5>under any local or other authority subject to the control of any of the said <5>Governments. <7>Explanation <5>For the purposes of this article, a person shall not be deemed to hold any office of <5>profit by reason only that he is the President or Vice-President of the Union or the <5>Governor of any State or is a Minister either for the Union or for any State. <7>67. Term of office of Vice-President <5>The Vice-President shall hold office for a term of five years from the date on which h <5>enters upon his office: <5>Provided that- <6>a.<5> a Vice-President may, by writing under his hand addressed to the <5>President, resign his office; <6>b.<5> a Vice-President may be removed from his office by a resolution of the <5>Council of States passed by a majority of all the then members of the <5>Council and agreed to by the House of the People; but no resolution for the <5>purpose of this clause shall be moved unless at least fourteen days' notice <5>has been given of the intention to move the resolution; <6>c. <5>a Vice-President shall, notwithstanding the expiration of his term, continue <5>to hold office until his successor enters upon his office. <7>68. Time of holding election to fill vacancy in the office of <7>Vice-President and the term of office of person elected to <7>fill casual vacancy <6>1.<5> An election to fill a vacancy caused by the expiration of the term of office of <5>Vice-President shall be completed before the expiration of the term. <6>2.<5> An election to fill a vacancy in the office of Vice-President occurring by reason of <5>his death, resignation or removal, or otherwise shall be held as soon as possible <5>after the occurrence of the vacancy, and the person elected to fill the vacancy <5>shall, subject to the provisions of article 67, be entitled to hold office for the full <5>term of five years from the date on which he enters upon his office. <7>69. Oath or affirmation by the Vice-President <4>• God or other deities <5>Every Vice-President shall, before entering upon his office, make and subscribe <4>• Oaths to abide by constitution <5>before the President, or some person appointed in that behalf by him, an oath or <5>affirmation in the following form, that is to say- <4>• God or other deities <5>"I, A.B., do Swear in the name of God/Solemnly Affirm that I will bear true faith and <4>• Oaths to abide by constitution <5>allegiance to the Constitution of India as by law established and that I will faithfully <5>discharge the duty upon which I am about to enter." <7>70. Discharge of President's functions in other <7>contingencies <5>Parliament may make such provision as it thinks fit for the discharge of the functions <5>of the President in any contingency not provided for in this Chapter. <7>71. Matters relating to, or connected with, the election of a <7>President or Vice-President <6>1.<5> All doubts and disputes arising out of or in connection with the election of a <5>President or Vice-President shall be inquired into and decided by the Supreme <5>Court whose decision shall be final. <6>2.<5> If the election of a person as President or Vice-President is declared void by the <5>Supreme Court, acts done by him in the exercise and performance of the powers <5>and duties of the office of President or Vice-President, as the case may be, on or <5>before the date of the decision of the Supreme Court shall not be invalidated by <5>reason of that declaration. <6>3.<5> Subject to the provisions of this Constitution, Parliament may by law regulate <5>any matter relating to or connected with the election of a President, or <5>Vice-President. <6>4.<5> The election of a person as President or Vice-President shall not be called in <5>question on the ground of the existence of any vacancy for whatever reason <5>among the members of the electoral college electing him. <7>72. Power of President to grant pardons, etc., and to <7>suspend, remit or commute sentences in certain cases <4>• Power to pardon <6>1.<5> The President shall have the power to grant pardons, reprieves, respites or <5>remissions of punishment or to suspend, remit or commute the sentence of any <5>persons convicted of any offence- <6>a.<5> in all cases where the punishment or sentence is by a Court Martial; <6>b.<5> in all cases where the punishment or sentence is for an offence against any <5>law relating to a matter to which the executive power of the Union extends; <6>c. <5>in all cases where the sentence is a sentence of death. <6>2.<5> Nothing in sub-clause (a) of clause (1) shall affect the power conferred by law on <5>any officer of the Armed Forces of the Union to suspend, remit or commute a <5>sentence passed by a Court martial. <6>3.<5> Nothing in sub-clause (c) of clause (1) shall affect the power to suspend, remit or <5>commute a sentence of death exercisable by the Governor of a State under any <5>law for the time being in force. <4>• Head of state powers <7>73. Extent of executive power of the Union <6>1.<5> Subject to the provisions of this Constitution, the executive power of the Union <5>shall extend- <6>a.<5> to the matters with respect to which Parliament has power to make laws; <5>and <6>b.<5> to the exercise of such rights, authority and jurisdiction as are exercisable <5>by the Government of India by virtue of any treaty or agreement: <5>Provided that the executive power referred to in sub-clause (a) shall not, save as <5>expressly provided in this Constitution or in any law made by Parliament, extend <5>in any State to matters with respect to which the Legislature of the State has <5>also power to make laws. <6>2.<5> Until otherwise provided by Parliament, a State and any officer or authority of a <5>State may, notwithstanding anything in this article, continue to exercise in <5>matters with respect to which Parliament has power to make laws for that State <5>such executive power or functions as the State or officer or authority thereof <5>could exercise immediately before the commencement of this Constitution. <7>Council of Ministers <7>74. Council of Ministers to aid and advise President <4>• Establishment of cabinet/ministers <4>• Powers of cabinet <4>• Name/structure of executive(s) <6>1.<5> There shall be a Council of Ministers with the Prime Minister at the head to aid <5>and advise the President who shall, in the exercise of his functions, act in <5>accordance with such advice: <5>Provided that the President may require the Council of Ministers to reconsider <5>such advice, either generally or otherwise, and the President shall act in <5>accordance with the advice tendered after such reconsideration. <6>2.<5> The question whether any, and if so what, advice was tendered by Ministers to <5>the President shall not be inquired into in any court. <7>75. Other provisions as to Ministers <4>• Cabinet selection <6>1.<5> The Prime Minister shall be appointed by the President and the other Ministers <4>• Head of government selection <5>shall be appointed by the President on the advice of the Prime Minister. <6>1A.<5> The total number of Ministers, including the Prime Minister, in the Council of <5>Ministers shall not exceed fifteen percent of the total number of members of the <5>House of the People. <4>• Cabinet removal <6>1B.<5> A member of either House of Parliament belonging to any political party who is <5>disqualified for being a member of that House under paragraph 2 of the Tenth <5>Schedule shall also be disqualified to be appointed as a Minister under clause (1) <5>for duration of the period commencing from the date of his disqualification till <5>the date on which the term of his office as such member would expire or where <5>he contests any election to either House of Parliament before the expiry of such <5>period, till the date on which he is declared elected, whichever is earlier. <4>• Cabinet removal <6>2.<5> The Ministers shall hold office during the pleasure of the President. <4>• Head of government removal <4>• Cabinet removal <6>3.<5> The Council of Ministers shall be collectively responsible to the House of the <4>• Head of government removal <5>People. <4>• Oaths to abide by constitution <6>4.<5> Before a Minister enters upon his office, the President shall administer to him <5>the oaths of office and of secrecy according to the forms set out for the purpose <5>in the Third Schedule. <4>• Eligibility for cabinet <6>5.<5> A Minister who for any period of six consecutive months is not a member of <4>• Minimum age of head of government <4>• Head of government's role in the <5>either House of Parliament shall at the expiration of that period cease to be a <4>legislature <4>• Eligibility for head of government <5>Minister. <6>6.<5> The salaries and allowances of Ministers shall be such as Parliament may from <5>time to time by law determine and, until Parliament so determines, shall be as <5>specified in the Second Schedule. <7>The Attorney-General for India <4>• Attorney general <7>76. Attorney-General for India <6>1.<5> The President shall appoint a person who is qualified to be appointed a Judge of <5>the Supreme Court to be Attorney-General for India. <6>2.<5> It shall be the duty of the Attorney-General to give advice to the Government of <5>India upon such legal matters, and to perform such other duties of a legal <5>character, as may from time to time be referred or assigned to him by the <5>President, and to discharge the functions conferred on him by or under this <5>Constitution or any other law for the time being in force. <6>3.<5> In the performance of his duties the Attorney-General shall have right of <5>audience in all courts in the territory of India. <6>4.<5> The Attorney-General shall hold office during the pleasure of the President, and <5>shall receive such remuneration as the President may determine. <7>Conduct of Government Business <7>77. Conduct of business of the Government of India <6>1.<5> All executive action of the Government of India shall be expressed to be taken in <5>the name of the President. <6>2.<5> Orders and other instruments made and executed in the name of the President <5>shall be authenticated in such manner as may be specified in rules to be made by <5>the President, and the validity of an order or instrument which is so <5>authenticated shall not be called in question on the ground that it is not an order <5>or instrument made or executed by the President. <6>3.<5> The President shall make rules for the more convenient transaction of the <5>business of the Government of India, and for the allocation among Ministers of <5>the said business. <4>• Head of government powers <7>78. Duties of Prime Minister as respects the furnishing of <7>information to the President, etc <5>It shall be the duty of the Prime Minister- <6>a.<5> to communicate to the President all decisions of the Council of Ministers <5>relating to the administration of the affairs of the Union and proposals for <5>legislation; <6>b.<5> to furnish such information relating the administration of the affairs of the <5>Union and proposals for legislation as the President may call for; and <6>c. <5>if the President so requires, to submit for the consideration of the Council <5>of Ministers any matter on which a decision has been taken by a Minister <5>but which has not been considered by the Council. <7>CHAPTER II: PARLIAMENT <7>General <4>• Structure of legislative chamber(s) <7>79. Constitution of Parliament <5>There shall be a Parliament for the Union which shall consist of the President and <5>two Houses to be known respectively as the Council of States and the House of the <5>People. <7>80. Composition of the Council of States <4>• Structure of legislative chamber(s) <4>• Second chamber selection <4>• Size of second chamber <6>1.<5> The Council of States shall consist of- <6>a.<5> twelve members to be nominated by the President in accordance with the <5>provisions of clause (3); and <6>b.<5> not more than two hundred and thirty-eight representatives of the States <5>and of the Union territories. <6>2.<5> The allocation of seats in the Council of States to be filled by representatives of <5>the States and of the Union territories shall be in accordance with the provisions <5>in that behalf contained in the Fourth Schedule. <6>3.<5> The members to be nominated by the President under sub-clause (a) of clause <5>(1) shall consist of persons having special knowledge or practical experience in <5>respect of such matters as the following, namely:- <5>Literature, science, art and social service. <6>4.<5> The representatives of each State in the Council of States shall be elected by the <5>elected members of the Legislative Assembly of the State in accordance with the <5>system of proportional representation by means of the single transferable vote. <6>5.<5> The representatives of the Union territories in the Council of States shall be <5>chosen in such manner as Parliament may by law prescribe. <7>81. Composition of the House of the People <4>• Structure of legislative chamber(s) <4>• Size of first chamber <4>• First chamber selection <6>1. <5>Subject to the provisions of article 331,the House of the People shall consist of- <6>a.<5> not more than five hundred and thirty members chosen by direct election <5>from territorial constituencies in the States, and <6>b.<5> not more than twenty members to represent the Union territories, chosen <5>in such manner as Parliament may by law provide. <6>2. <5>For the purposes of sub-clause (a) of clause (1),- <6>a.<5> there shall be allotted to each State a number of seats in the House of the <5>People in such manner that the ratio between that number and the <5>population of the State is, so far as practicable, the same for all States; and <6>b.<5> each State shall be divided into territorial constituencies in such manner <5>that the ratio between the population of each constituency and the number <5>of seats allotted to it is, so far as practicable, the same throughout the <5>State: <5>Provided that the provisions of sub-clause (a) of this clause shall not be <5>applicable for the purpose of allotment of seats in the House of the People to <5>any State so long as the population of that State does not exceed six millions. <4>• Census <6>3. <5>In this article, the expression "population" means the population as ascertained <5>at the last preceding census of which the relevant figures have been published: <5>Provided that the reference in this clause to the last preceding census of which <5>the relevant figures have been published shall, until the relevant figures for the <5>first census taken after the year have been published, be construed,- <6>i. <5>for the purposes of sub-clause (a) of clause (2) and the proviso to that <5>clause, as a reference to the 1971 census; and <6>ii. <5>for the purposes of sub-clause (b) of clause (2) as a reference to the 2001 <5>census. <4>• Census <7>82. Readjustment after each census <4>• Electoral districts <5>Upon the completion of each census, the allocation of seats in the House of the <5>People to the States and the division of each state into territorial constituencies shall <5>be readjusted by such authority and in such manner as Parliament may by law <5>determine: <5>Provided that such readjustment shall not affect representation in the House of the <5>People until the dissolution of the then existing House: <5>Provided further that such readjustment shall take effect from such date as the <5>President may, by order, specify and until such readjustment takes effect, any <5>election to the House may be held on the basis of the territorial constituencies <5>existing before such readjustment: <5>Provided also that until the relevant figures for the first census taken after the year <5>2026 have been published, it shall not be necessary to readjust- <6>i. <5>the allocation of seats in the House of the People to the State as readjusted <5>on the basis of the 1971 census; and <6>ii. <5>the division of each State into territorial constituencies as may be <5>readjusted on the basis of the 2001 census, under this article. <7>83. Duration of Houses of Parliament <6>1.<5> The Council of States shall not be subject to dissolution, but as nearly as possible <5>one third of the members thereof shall retire as soon as may be on the <5>expiration of every second year in accordance with the provisions made in that <5>behalf by Parliament by law. <4>• Term length for first chamber <6>2.<5> The House of the People, unless sooner dissolved, shall continue for five years <5>from the date appointed for its first meeting and no longer and the expiration of <5>the said period of five years shall operate as a dissolution of the House: <4>• Emergency provisions <5>Provided that the said period may, while a Proclamation of Emergency is in <5>operation, be extended by Parliament by law for a period not exceeding one <5>year at a time and not extending in any case beyond a period of six months after <5>the Proclamation has ceased to operate. <4>• Eligibility for cabinet <7>84. Qualification for membership of Parliament <4>• Eligibility for head of government <4>• Eligibility for head of state <4>• Eligibility for first chamber <4>• Eligibility for second chamber <5>A person shall not be qualified to be chosen to fill a seat in Parliament unless he- <4>• Oaths to abide by constitution <6>a.<5> is a citizen of India, and makes and subscribes before some person <5>authorised in that behalf by the Election Commission an oath or affirmation <5>according to the form set out for the purpose in the Third Schedule; <4>• Minimum age of head of government <6>b.<5> is, in the case of a seat in the Council of States, not less than thirty years of <4>• Minimum age for first chamber <4>• Minimum age for second chamber <5>age and, in the case of a seat in the House of the People, not less than <5>twenty-five years of age; and <6>c. <5>possesses such other qualifications as may be prescribed in that behalf by <5>or under any law made by Parliament. <7>85. Sessions of Parliament, prorogation and dissolution <4>• Extraordinary legislative sessions <6>1.<5> The President shall from time to time summon each House of Parliament to <5>meet at such time and place as he thinks fit, but six months shall not intervene <5>between its last sitting in one session and the date appointed for its first sitting <5>in the next session. <6>2.<5> The President may from time to time- <6>a.<5> prorogue the Houses or either House, <4>• Dismissal of the legislature <6>b.<5> dissolve the House of the People. <7>86. Right of President to address and send messages to <7>Houses <6>1.<5> The President may address either House of Parliament or both Houses <5>assembled together, and for that purpose require the attendance of members. <6>2.<5> The President may send messages to either House of Parliament, whether with <5>respect to a Bill then pending in Parliament or otherwise, and a House to which <5>any message is so sent shall with all convenient despatch consider any matter <5>required by the message to be taken into consideration. <7>87. Special address by the President <4>• Legislative oversight of the executive <6>1.<5> At the commencement of the first session after each general election to the <5>House of the People and at the commencement of the first session of each year <5>the President shall address both Houses of Parliament assembled together and <5>inform Parliament of the causes of its summons. <6>2.<5> Provision shall be made by the rules regulating the procedure of either House <5>for the allotment of time for discussion of the matters referred to in such <5>address. <7>88. Rights of Ministers and Attorney-General as respects <7>Houses <5>Every Minister and the Attorney-General of India shall have the right to speak in, and <5>otherwise to take part in the proceeding of, either House, any joint sitting of the <5>Houses, and any committee of Parliament of which he may be named a member, but <5>shall not by virtue of this article be entitled to vote. <7>Officers of Parliament <7>89. The Chairman and Deputy Chairman of the Council of <7>States <4>• Leader of second chamber <6>1.<5> The Vice-President of India shall be ex-officio Chairman of the Council of States. <6>2.<5> The Council of States shall, as soon as may be, choose a member of the Council <5>to be Deputy Chairman thereof and, so often as the office of Deputy Chairman <5>becomes vacant, the Council shall choose another member to be Deputy <5>Chairman thereof. <7>90. Vacation and resignation of, and removal from, the <7>office of Deputy Chairman <5>A member holding office as Deputy Chairman of the Council of States- <6>a.<5> shall vacate his office if he ceases to be a member of the Council; <6>b.<5> may at any time, by writing under his hand addressed to the Chairman, <5>resign his office; and <6>c. <5>may be removed from his office by a resolution of the Council passed by a <5>majority of all the then members of the Council: <5>Provided that no resolution for the purpose of clause (c) shall be moved unless at <5>least fourteen days' notice has been given of the intention to move the resolution. <7>91.
