Power of the Deputy Chairman or other person to <7>perform the duties of the office of, or to act as, Chairman <6>1.<5> While the Office of Chairman is vacant, or during any period when the <5>Vice-President is acting as, or discharging the functions of, President, the duties <5>of the office shall be performed by the Deputy Chairman, or, if the office of <5>Deputy Chairman is also vacant, by such member of the Council of States as the <5>President may appoint for the purpose. <6>2.<5> During the absence of the Chairman from any sitting of the Council of States the <5>Deputy Chairman, or, if he is also absent, such person as may be determined by <5>the rules of procedure of the Council, or, if no such person is present, such other <5>person as may be determined by the Council, shall act as Chairman. <7>92. The Chairman or the Deputy Chairman not to preside <7>while a resolution for his removal from office is under <7>consideration <6>1.<5> At any sitting of the Council of States, while any resolution for the removal of <5>the Vice-President from his office is under consideration, the Chairman, or while <5>any resolution for the removal of the Deputy Chairman from his office is under <5>consideration, the Deputy Chairman, shall not, though he is present, preside, and <5>the provisions of clause (2) of article 91 shall apply in relation to every such <5>sitting as they apply in relation to a sitting from which the Chairman, or, as the <5>case may be, the Deputy Chairman, is absent. <6>2.<5> The Chairman shall have the right to speak in, and otherwise to take part in the <5>proceedings of, the Council of States while any resolution for the removal of the <5>Vice-President from his office is under consideration in the Council, but, <5>notwithstanding anything in article 100 shall not be entitled to vote at all on <5>such resolution or on any other matter during such proceedings. <4>• Leader of first chamber <7>93. The Speaker and Deputy Speaker of the House of the <7>People <5>The House of the People shall, as soon as may be, choose two members of the House <5>to be respectively Speaker and Deputy Speaker thereof and, so often as the office of <5>Speaker or Deputy Speaker becomes vacant, the House shall choose another <5>member to be Speaker or Deputy Speaker, as the case may be. <4>• Leader of first chamber <7>94. Vacation and resignation of, and removal from, the <7>offices of Speaker and Deputy Speaker <5>A member holding office as Speaker or Deputy Speaker of the House of the People- <6>a.<5> shall vacate his office if he ceases to be a member of the House of the <5>People; <6>b.<5> may at any time, by writing under his hand addressed, if such member is the <5>Speaker, to the Deputy Speaker, and if such member is the Deputy Speaker, <5>to the Speaker, resign his office; and <6>c. <5>may be removed from his office by a resolution of the House of the People <5>passed by a majority of all the then members of the House: <5>Provided that no resolution for the purpose of clause (c) shall be moved unless at <5>least fourteen days' notice has been given of the intention to move the resolution: <5>Provided further that, whenever the House of the People is dissolved, the Speaker <5>shall not vacate his office until immediately before the first meeting of the House of <5>the People after the dissolution. <4>• Leader of first chamber <7>95. Power of the Deputy Speaker or other person to <7>perform the duties of the office of, or to act as, Speaker <6>1.<5> While the office of Speaker is vacant, the duties of the office shall be performed <5>by the Deputy Speaker or, if the office of Deputy Speaker is also vacant, by such <5>member of the House of the People as the President may appoint for the <5>purpose. <6>2.<5> During the absence of the Speaker from any sitting of the House of the People <5>the Deputy Speaker or, if he is also absent, such person as may be determined by <5>the rules of procedure of the House, or, if no such person is present, such other <5>person as may be determined by the House, shall act as Speaker. <4>• Leader of first chamber <7>96. The Speaker or the Deputy Speaker not to preside <7>while a resolution for his removal from office is under <7>consideration <6>1.<5> At any sitting of the House of the People, while any resolution for the removal of <5>the Speaker from his office is under consideration, the Speaker, or while any <5>resolution for the removal of the Deputy Speaker from his office is under <5>consideration, the Deputy Speaker, shall not, though he is present, preside, and <5>the provisions of clause (2) of article 95 shall apply in relation to every such <5>sitting as they apply in relation to a sitting from which the Speaker, or, as the <5>case may be, the Deputy Speaker, is absent. <6>2.<5> The Speaker shall have the right to speak in, and otherwise to take part in the <5>proceedings of, the House of the People while any resolution for his removal <5>from office is under consideration in the House and shall, notwithstanding <5>anything in article 100, be entitled to vote only in the first instance on such <5>resolution or on any other matter during such proceedings but not in the case of <5>an equality of votes. <7>97. Salaries and allowances of the Chairman and Deputy <7>Chairman and the Speaker and Deputy Speaker <5>There shall be paid to the Chairman and the Deputy Chairman of the Council of <5>States, and to the Speaker and the Deputy Speaker of the House of the People, such <5>salaries and allowances as may be respectively fixed by Parliament by law and, until <5>provision in that behalf is so made, such salaries and allowances as are specified in <5>the Second Schedule. <7>98. Secretariat of Parliament <6>1.<5> Each House of Parliament shall have a separate secretarial staff: <5>Provided that nothing in this clause shall be construed as preventing the <5>creation of posts common to both Houses of Parliament. <6>2.<5> Parliament may by law regulate the recruitment and the conditions of service of <5>persons appointed, to the secretarial staff of either House of Parliament. <6>3.<5> Until provision is made by Parliament under clause (2), the President may, after <5>consultation with the Speaker of the House of the People or the Chairman of the <5>Council of States, as the case may be, make rules regulating the recruitment, and <5>the conditions of service of persons appointed, to the secretarial staff of the <5>House of the People or the Council of States, and any rules so made shall have <5>effect subject to the provisions of any law made under the said clause. <7>Conduct of Business <4>• Oaths to abide by constitution <7>99. Oath or affirmation by members <5>Every member of either House of Parliament shall, before taking his seat, make and <5>subscribe before the President, or some person appointed in that behalf by him, an <5>oath or affirmation according to the form set out for the purpose in the Third <5>Schedule. <7>100. Voting in Houses, power of Houses to act <7>notwithstanding vacancies and quorum <4>• Veto override procedure <6>1.<5> Save as otherwise provided in this Constitution, all questions at any sitting of <5>either House or joint sitting of the Houses shall be determined by a majority of <5>votes of the members present and voting, other than the Speaker or person <5>acting as Chairman or Speaker. <5>The Chairman or Speaker, or person acting as such, shall not vote in the first <5>instance, but shall have and exercise a casting vote in the case of an equality of <5>votes. <6>2.<5> Either House of Parliament shall have power to act notwithstanding any vacancy <5>in the membership thereof, and any proceedings in Parliament shall be valid <5>notwithstanding that it is discovered subsequently that some person who was <5>not entitled so to do sat or voted or otherwise took part in the proceedings. <4>• Quorum for legislative sessions <6>3.<5> Until Parliament by law otherwise provides, the quorum to constitute a meeting <5>of either House of Parliament shall be one-tenth of the total number of <5>members of the House. <6>4.<5> If at any time during a meeting of a House there is no quorum, it shall be the duty <5>of the Chairman or Speaker, or person acting as such, either to adjourn the <5>House or to suspend the meeting until there is a quorum. <7>Disqualifications of Members <7>101. Vacation of seats <6>1. <5>No person shall be a member of both Houses of Parliament and provision shall <5>be made by Parliament by law for the vacation by a person who is chosen a <5>member of both Houses of his seat in one House or the other. <6>2. <5>No person shall be a member both of Parliament and of a House of the <5>Legislature of a State, and if a person is chosen a member both of Parliament and <5>of a House of the Legislature of a State, then, at the expiration of such period as <5>may be specified in rules made by the President, that person's seat in Parliament <5>shall become vacant, unless he has previously resigned his seat in the Legislature <5>of the State. <6>3. <5>If a member of either House of Parliament- <6>a.<5> becomes subject to any of the disqualifications mentioned in clause (1) or <5>clause (2) of article 102; or <6>b.<5> resigns his seat by writing under his hand addressed to the Chairman or the <5>Speaker, as the case may be, and his resignation is accepted by the <5>Chairman or the Speaker, as the case may be, <5>his seat shall thereupon become vacant: <5>Provided that in the case of any resignation referred to in sub-clause (b), if from <5>information received or otherwise and after making such inquiry as he thinks fit, <5>the Chairman or the Speaker, as the case may be, is satisfied that such <5>resignation is not voluntary or genuine, he shall not accept such resignation. <4>• Attendance by legislators <6>4. <5>If for a period of sixty days a member of either House of Parliament is without <4>• Removal of individual legislators <5>permission of the House absent from all meetings thereof, the House may <5>declare his seat vacant: <5>Provided that in computing the said period of sixty days no account shall be <5>taken of any period during which the House is prorogued or is adjourned for <5>more than four consecutive days. <4>• Eligibility for cabinet <7>102. Disqualifications for membership <4>• Eligibility for head of government <4>• Eligibility for head of state <4>• Eligibility for first chamber <6>1.<5> A person shall be disqualified for being chosen as, and for being, a member of <4>• Removal of individual legislators <4>• Eligibility for second chamber <5>either House of Parliament- <4>• Outside professions of legislators <6>a.<5> if he holds any office of profit under the Government of India or the <5>Government of any State, other than an office declared by Parliament by <5>law not to disqualify its holder; <6>b.<5> if he is of unsound mind and stands so declared by a competent court; <6>c. <5>if he is an undischarged insolvent; <6>d.<5> if he is not a citizen of India, or has voluntarily acquired the citizenship of a <5>foreign State, or is under any acknowledgment of allegiance or adherence <5>to a foreign State; <6>e.<5> if he is so disqualified by or under any law made by Parliament. <7>Explanation <5>For the purposes of this clause a person shall not be deemed to hold an office of <5>profit under the Government of India or the Government of any State by reason only <5>that he is a Minister either for the Union or for such State. <6>2.<5> A person shall be disqualified for being a member of either House of Parliament <5>if he is so disqualified under the Tenth Schedule. <7>103. Decision on questions as to disqualifications of <4>• Removal of individual legislators <7>members <6>1.<5> If any question arises as to whether a member of either House of Parliament has <5>become subject to any of the disqualifications mentioned in clause (1) of article <5>102, the question shall be referred for the decision of the President and his <5>decision shall be final. <6>2.<5> Before giving any decision on any such question, the President shall obtain the <5>opinion of the Election Commission and shall act according to such opinion. <7>104. Penalty for sitting and voting before making oath or <7>affirmation under article 99 or when not qualified or when <7>disqualified <5>If a person sits or votes as a member of either House of Parliament before he has <5>complied with the requirements of article 99, or when he knows that he is not <5>qualified or that he is disqualified for membership thereof, or that he is prohibited <5>from so doing by the provisions of any law made by Parliament, he shall be liable in <5>respect of each day on which he so sits or votes to a penalty of five hundred rupees <5>to be recovered as a debt due to the Union. <7>Powers Privileges and Immunities of Parliament and its <7>Members <4>• Legislative committees <7>105. Powers, Privileges, etc., of the Houses of Parliament <7>and of the members and committees thereof <6>1.<5> Subject to the provisions of this Constitution and to the rules and standing <5>orders regulating the procedure of Parliament, there shall be freedom of speech <5>in Parliament. <6>2.<5> No member of Parliament shall be liable to any proceedings in any court in <5>respect of anything said or any vote given by him in Parliament or any <5>committee thereof, and no person shall be so liable in respect of the publication <5>by or under the authority of either House of Parliament of any report, paper, <5>votes or proceedings. <6>3.<5> In other respects, the powers, privileges and immunities of each House of <5>Parliament, and of the members and the committees of each House, shall be <5>such as may from time to time be defined by Parliament by law, and, until so <5>defined, shall be those of that House and of its members and committees <5>immediately before the coming into force of section 15 of the Constitution <5>(Forty-fourth Amendment) Act, 1978. <6>4.<5> The provisions of clauses (1), (2) and (3) shall apply in relation to persons who by <5>virtue of this Constitution have the right to speak in, and otherwise to take part <5>in the proceedings of, a House of Parliament or any committee thereof as they <5>apply in relation to members of Parliament. <4>• Compensation of legislators <7>106. Salaries and allowances of members <5>Members of either House of Parliament shall be entitled to receive such salaries and <5>allowances as may from time to time be determined by Parliament by law and, until <5>provision in that respect is so made, allowances at such rates and upon such <5>conditions as were immediately before the commencement of this Constitution <5>applicable in the case of members of the Constituent Assembly of the Dominion of <5>India. <7>Legislative Procedure <7>107. Provisions as to introduction and passing of Bills <4>• Division of labor between chambers <4>• Initiation of general legislation <6>1.<5> Subject to the provisions of articles 109 and 117 with respect to Money Bills and <5>other financial Bills, a Bill may originate in either House of Parliament. <6>2.<5> Subject to the provisions of articles 108 and 109, a Bill shall not be deemed to <5>have been passed by the Houses of Parliament unless it has been agreed to by <5>both Houses, either without amendment or with such amendments only as are <5>agreed to by both Houses. <6>3.<5> A Bill pending in Parliament shall not lapse by reason of the prorogation of the <5>Houses. <6>4.<5> A Bill pending in the Council of States which has not been passed by the House <5>of the People shall not lapse on a dissolution of the House of the People. <6>5.<5> A Bill which is pending in the House of the People, or which having been passed <5>by the House of the People is pending in the Council of States, shall, subject to <5>the provisions of article 108, lapse on a dissolution of the House of the People. <7>108. Joint sitting of both Houses in certain cases <4>• Joint meetings of legislative chambers <6>1.<5> If after a Bill has been passed by one House and transmitted to the other House- <6>a.<5> the Bill is rejected by the other House; or <6>b.<5> the Houses have finally disagreed as to the amendments to be made in the <5>Bill; or <6>c. <5>more than six months elapse from the date of the reception of the Bill by <5>the other House without the Bill being passed by it, <5>the President may, unless the Bill has elapsed by reason of a dissolution of the <5>House of the People, notify to the Houses by message if they are sitting or by <5>public notification if they are not sitting, his intention to summon them to meet <5>in a joint sitting for the purpose of deliberating and voting on the Bill: <5>Provided that nothing in this clause shall apply to a Money Bill. <6>2.<5> In reckoning any such period of six months as is referred to in clause (1) no <5>account shall be taken of any period during which the House referred to in <5>sub-clause (c) of that clause is prorogued or adjourned for more than four <5>consecutive days. <6>3. <5>Where the President has under clause (1) notified his intention of summoning <5>the Houses to meet in a joint sitting, neither House shall proceed further with <5>the Bill, but the President may at any time after the date of his notification <5>summon the Houses to meet in a joint sitting for the purpose specified in the <5>notification and, if he does so, the Houses shall meet accordingly. <6>4. <5>If at the joint sitting of the two Houses the Bill, with such amendments, if any, as <5>are agreed to in joint sitting, is passed by a majority of the total number of <5>members of both Houses present and voting, it shall be deemed for the purposes <5>of this Constitution to have been passed by both Houses: <5>Provided that at a joint sitting- <6>a.<5> if the Bill, having been passed by one House, has not been passed by the <5>other House with amendments and returned to the House in which it <5>originated, no amendment shall be proposed to the Bill other than such <5>amendments (if any) as are made necessary by the delay in the passage of <5>the Bill; <6>b.<5> if the Bill has been so passed and returned, only such amendments as <5>aforesaid shall be proposed to the Bill and such other amendments as are <5>relevant to the matters with respect to which the Houses have not agreed, <5>and the decision of the person presiding as to the amendments which are <5>admissible under this clause shall be final. <6>5. <5>A joint sitting may be held under this article and a Bill passed thereat, <5>notwithstanding that a dissolution of the House of the People has intervened <5>since the President notified his intention to summon the Houses to meet <5>therein. <4>• Budget bills <7>109. Special procedure in respect of Money Bills <4>• Finance bills <4>• First chamber reserved policy areas <4>• Spending bills <6>1.<5> A Money Bill shall not be introduced in the Council of States. <4>• Tax bills <6>2.<5> After a Money Bill has been passed by the House of the People it shall be <5>transmitted to the Council of States for its recommendations and the Council of <5>States shall within a period of fourteen days from the date of its receipt of the <5>Bill return the Bill to the House of the People with its recommendations and the <5>House of the People may thereupon either accept or reject all or any of the <5>recommendations of the Council of States. <6>3.<5> If the House of the People accepts any of the recommendations of the Council of <5>States, the Money Bill shall be deemed to have been passed by both Houses with <5>the amendments recommended by the Council of States and accepted by the <5>House of the People. <6>4.<5> If the House of the People does not accept any of the recommendations of the <5>Council of States, the Money Bill shall be deemed to have been passed by both <5>Houses in the form in which it was passed by the House of the People without <5>any of the amendments recommended by the Council of States. <6>5.<5> If a Money Bill passed by the House of the People and transmitted to the Council <5>of States for its recommendations is not returned to the House of the People <5>within the said period of fourteen days, it shall be deemed to have been passed <5>by both Houses at the expiration of the said period in the form in which it was <5>passed by the House of the People. <7>110. Definition of "Money Bills <6>1. <5>For the purposes of this Chapter, a Bill shall be deemed to be a Money Bill if it <5>contains only provisions dealing with all or any of the following matters, <5>namely:- <4>• Tax bills <6>a.<5> the imposition, abolition, remission, alteration or regulation of any tax; <6>b.<5> the regulation of the borrowing of money or the giving of any guarantee by <5>the Government of India, or the amendment of the law with respect to any <5>financial obligations undertaken or to be undertaken by the Government of <5>India; <6>c. <5>the custody of the Consolidated Fund or the Contingency Fund of India, the <5>payment of moneys into or the withdrawal of moneys from any such Fund; <6>d.<5> the appropriation of moneys out of the Consolidated Fund of India; <6>e.<5> the declaring of any expenditure to be expenditure charged on the <5>Consolidated Fund of India or the increasing of the amount of any such <5>expenditure; <6>f. <5>the receipt of money on account of the Consolidated Fund of India or the <5>public account of India or the custody or issue of such money or the audit of <5>the accounts of the Union or of a State; or <6>g.<5> any matter incidental to any of the matters specified in sub-clauses (a)to (f). <6>2. <5>A Bill shall not be deemed to be a Money Bill by reason only that it provides for <5>the imposition of fines or other pecuniary penalties, or for the demand or <5>payment of fees for licences or fees for services rendered, or by reason that it <5>provides for the imposition, abolition, remission, alteration or regulation of any <5>tax by any local authority or body for local purposes. <6>3. <5>If any question arises whether a Bill is a Money Bill or not, the decision of the <5>Speaker of the House of the People thereon shall be final. <6>4. <5>There shall be endorsed on every Money Bill when it is transmitted to the <5>Council of States under article 109, and when it is presented to the President for <5>assent under article 111, the certificate of the Speaker of the House of the <5>People signed by him that it is a Money Bill. <4>• Approval of general legislation <7>111. Assent to Bills <5>When a Bill has been passed by the Houses of Parliament, it shall be presented to the <5>President, and the President shall declare either that he assents to the Bill, or that he <5>withholds assent therefrom: <4>• Veto override procedure <5>Provided that the President may, as soon as possible after the presentation to him of <5>a Bill for assent, return the Bill if it is not a Money Bill to the Houses with a message <5>requesting that they will reconsider the Bill or any specified provisions thereof and, <5>in particular, will consider the desirability of introducing any such amendments as he <5>may recommend in his message, and when a Bill is so returned, the Houses shall <5>reconsider the Bill accordingly, and if the Bill is passed again by the Houses with or <5>without amendment and presented to the President for assent, the President shall <5>not withhold assent therefrom. <7>Procedure in Financial Matters <4>• Budget bills <7>112. Annual financial statement <6>1. <5>The President shall in respect of every financial year cause to be laid before both <5>the Houses of Parliament a statement of the estimated receipts and expenditure <5>of the Government of India for that year, in this Part referred to as the "annual <5>financial statement". <6>2. <5>The estimates of expenditure embodied in the annual financial statement shall <5>show separately- <6>a.<5> the sums required to meet expenditure described by this Constitution as <5>expenditure charged upon the Consolidated Fund of India; and <6>b.<5> the sums required to meet other expenditure proposed to be made from <5>the Consolidated Fund of India, <5>and shall distinguish expenditure on revenue account from other expenditure. <6>3. <5>The following expenditure shall be expenditure charged on the Consolidated <5>Fund of India- <6>a. <5>the emoluments and allowances of the President and other expenditure <5>relating to his office; <6>b. <5>the salaries and allowances of the Chairman and the Deputy Chairman of <5>the Council of States and the Speaker and the Deputy Speaker of the House <5>of the People; <6>c. <5>debt charges for which the Government of India is liable including interest, <5>sinking fund charges and redemption charges, and other expenditure <5>relating to the raising of loans and the service and redemption of debt; <6>d. <6>i. <5>the salaries, allowances and pensions payable to or in respect of <5>Judges of the Supreme Court: <6>ii. <5>the pensions payable to or in respect of Judges of the Federal Court; <6>iii. <5>the pensions payable to or in respect of Judges of any High Court <5>which exercises jurisdiction in relation to any area included in the <5>territory of India or which at any time before the commencement of <5>this Constitution exercised jurisdiction in relation to any area included <5>in a Governor's Province of the Dominion of India; <6>e. <5>the salary, allowances and pension payable to or in respect of the <5>Comptroller and Auditor-General of India; <6>f. <5>any sums required to satisfy any judgment, decree or award of any court or <5>arbitral tribunal; <6>g. <5>any other expenditure declared by this Constitution or by Parliament by <5>law to be so charged. <7>113. Procedure in Parliament with respect to estimates <6>1.<5> So much of the estimates as relates to expenditure charged upon the <5>Consolidated Fund of India shall not be submitted to the vote of Parliament, but <5>nothing in this clause shall be construed as preventing the discussion in either <5>House of Parliament of any of those estimates. <6>2.<5> So much of the said estimates as relates to other expenditure shall be submitted <5>in the form of demands for grants to the House of the People, and the House of <5>the People shall have power to assent, or to refuse to assent, to any demand, or <5>to assent to any demand subject to a reduction of the amount specified therein. <6>3.<5> No demand for a grant shall be made except on the recommendation of the <5>President. <4>• Spending bills <7>114. Appropriation Bills <6>1.<5> As soon as may be after the grants under article 113 have been made by the <5>House of the People, there shall be introduced a Bill to provide for the <5>appropriation out of the Consolidated Fund of India of all moneys required to <5>meet- <6>a.<5> the grants so made by the House of the People; and <6>b.<5> the expenditure charged on the Consolidated Fund of India but not <5>exceeding in any case the amount shown in the statement previously laid <5>before Parliament. <6>2.<5> No amendment shall be proposed to any such Bill in either House of Parliament <5>which will have the effect of varying the amount or altering the destination of <5>any grant so made or of varying the amount of any expenditure charged on the <5>Consolidated Fund of India, and the decision of the person presiding as to <5>whether an amendment is inadmissible under this clause shall be final. <6>3.<5> Subject to the provisions of articles 115 and 116, no money shall be withdrawn <5>from the Consolidated Fund of India except under appropriation made by law <5>passed in accordance with the provisions of this article. <7>115. Supplementary, additional or excess grants <6>1.<5> The President shall- <6>a.<5> if the amount authorised by any law made in accordance with the <5>provisions of article 114 to be expended for a particular service for the <5>current financial year is found to be insufficient for the purposes of that <5>year or when a need has arisen during the current financial year for <5>supplementary or additional expenditure upon some new service not <5>contemplated in the annual financial statement for that year, or <6>b.<5> if any money has been spent on any service during a financial year in excess <5>of the amount granted for that service and for that year, <5>cause to be laid before both the Houses of Parliament another statement <5>showing the estimated amount of that expenditure or cause to be presented to <5>the House of the People a demand for such excess, as the case may be. <6>2.<5> The provisions of articles 112, 113 and 114 shall have effect in relation to any <5>such statement and expenditure or demand and also to any law to be made <5>authorising the appropriation of moneys out of the Consolidated Fund of India <5>to meet such expenditure or the grant in respect of such demand as they have <5>effect in relation to the annual financial statement and the expenditure <5>mentioned therein or to a demand for a grant and the law to be made for the <5>authorisation of appropriation of moneys out of the Consolidated Fund of India <5>to meet such expenditure or grant. <7>116. Votes on account, votes of credit and exceptional <7>grants <6>1. <5>Notwithstanding anything in the foregoing provisions of this Chapter, the House <5>of the People shall have power- <6>a.<5> to make any grant in advance in respect of the estimated expenditure for a <5>part of any financial year pending the completion of the procedure <5>prescribed in article 113 for the voting of such grant and the passing of the <5>law in accordance with the provisions of article 114 in relation to that <5>expenditure; <6>b.<5> to make a grant for meeting an unexpected demand upon the resources of <5>India when on account of the magnitude or the indefinite character of the <5>service the demand cannot be stated with the details ordinarily given in an <5>annual financial statement; <6>c. <5>to make an exceptional grant which forms no part of the current service of <5>any financial year, <5>and Parliament shall have power to authorise by law the withdrawal of moneys <5>from the Consolidated Fund of India for the purposes for which the said grants <5>are made. <6>2. <5>The provisions of articles 113 and 114 shall have effect in relation to the making <5>of any grant under clause (1) and to any law to be made under that clause as they <5>have effect in relation to the making of a grant with regard to any expenditure <5>mentioned in the annual financial statement and the law to be made for the <5>authorisation of appropriation of moneys out of the Consolidated Fund of India <5>to meet such expenditure. <4>• Finance bills <7>117. Special provisions as to financial Bills <4>• Spending bills <4>• Tax bills <6>1.<5> A Bill or amendment making provision for any of the matters specified in <5>sub-clauses (a) to (f) of clause (1) of article 110 shall not be introduced or moved <5>except on the recommendation of the President and a Bill making such provision <5>shall not be introduced in the Council of States: <5>Provided that no recommendation shall be required under this clause for the <5>moving of an amendment making provision for the reduction or abolition of any <5>tax. <6>2.<5> A Bill or amendment shall not be deemed to make provision for any of the <5>matters aforesaid by reason only that it provides for the imposition of fines or <5>other pecuniary penalties, or for the demand or payment of fees for licences or <5>fees for services rendered, or by reason that it provides for the imposition, <5>abolition, remission, alteration or regulation of any tax by any local authority or <5>body for local purposes. <6>3.<5> A Bill which, if enacted and brought into operation, would involve expenditure <5>from the Consolidated Fund of India shall not be passed by either House of <5>Parliament unless the President has recommended to that House the <5>consideration of the Bill. <7>Procedure Generally <7>118. Rules of procedure <6>1.<5> Each House of Parliament may make rules for regulating, subject to the <5>provisions of this Constitution, its procedure and the conduct of its business. <6>2.<5> Until rules are made under clause (1), the rules of procedure and standing orders <5>in force immediately before the commencement of this Constitution with <5>respect to the Legislature of the Dominion of India shall have effect in relation to <5>Parliament subject to such modifications and adaptations as may be made <5>therein by the Chairman of the Council of States or the Speaker of the House of <5>the People, as the case may be. <6>3.<5> The President, after consultation with the Chairman of the Council of States and <5>the Speaker of the House of the People, may make rules as to the procedure <5>with respect to joint sittings of, and communications between, the two Houses. <6>4.<5> At a joint sitting of the two Houses the Speaker of the House of People, or in his <5>absence such person as may be determined by rules of procedure made under <5>clause (3), shall preside. <7>119. Regulation by law of procedure in Parliament in <7>relation to financial business <5>Parliament may, for the purpose of the timely completion of financial business, <5>regulate by law the procedure of, and the conduct of business in, each House of <5>Parliament in relation to any financial matter or to any Bill for the appropriation of <5>moneys out of the Consolidated Fund of India, and, if and so far as any provision of <5>any law so made is inconsistent with any rule made by a House of Parliament under <5>clause (1) of article 118 or with any rule or standing order having effect in relation to <5>Parliament under clause (2) of that article, such provision shall prevail. <7>120. Language to be used in Parliament <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in Part XVII, but subject to the provisions of article <5>348, business in Parliament shall be transacted in Hindi or in English: <5>Provided that the Chairman of the Council of States or Speaker of the House of <5>the People, or person acting as such, as the case may be, may permit any <5>member who cannot adequately express himself in Hindi or in English to address <5>the House in his mother tongue. <6>2.<5> Unless Parliament by law otherwise provides, this article shall, after the <5>expiration of a period of fifteen years from the commencement of this <5>Constitution, have effect as if the words "or in English" were omitted therefrom. <7>121. Restriction on discussion in Parliament <5>No discussion shall take place in Parliament with respect to the conduct of any Judge <5>of the Supreme Court or of a High Court in the discharge of his duties except upon a <5>motion for presenting an address to the President praying for the removal of the <5>Judge as hereinafter provided. <7>122. Courts not to inquire into proceedings of Parliament <6>1.<5> The validity of any proceedings in Parliament shall not be called in question on <5>the ground of any alleged irregularity of procedure. <6>2.<5> No officer or member of Parliament in whom powers are vested by or under this <5>Constitution for regulating procedure or the conduct of business, or for <5>maintaining order, in Parliament shall be subject to the jurisdiction of any court <5>in respect of the exercise by him of those powers. <7>CHAPTER III: LEGISLATIVE POWERS OF THE PRESIDENT <4>• Head of state decree power <7>123. Power of President to promulgate Ordinances during <7>recess of Parliament <6>1.<5> If at any time, except when both Houses of Parliament are in session, the <5>President is satisfied that circumstances exist which render it necessary for him <5>to take immediate action, he may promulgate such Ordinances as the <5>circumstances appear to him to require. <6>2.<5> An Ordinance promulgated under this article shall have the same force and <5>effect as an Act of Parliament, but every such Ordinance- <6>a.<5> shall be laid before both Houses of Parliament and shall cease to operate at <5>the expiration of six weeks from the reassembly of Parliament, or, if before <5>the expiration of that period resolutions disapproving it are passed by both <5>Houses, upon the passing of the second of those resolutions; and <6>b.<5> may be withdrawn at any time by the President. <7>Explanation <5>Where the Houses of Parliament are summoned to reassemble on different dates, <5>the period of six weeks shall be reckoned from the later of those dates for the <5>purposes of this clause. <6>3.<5> If and so far as an Ordinance under this article makes any provision which <5>Parliament would not under this Constitution be competent to enact, it shall be <5>void. <7>CHAPTER IV: THE UNION JUDICIARY <7>124. Establishment and Constitution of Supreme Court <4>• Structure of the courts <6>1.<5> There shall be a Supreme Court of India consisting of a Chief Justice of India and, <5>until Parliament by law prescribes a larger number, of not more than seven <5>other Judges. <4>• Supreme court selection <6>2.<5> Every Judge of the Supreme Court shall be appointed by the President by <4>• Supreme court term length <4>• Mandatory retirement age for judges <5>warrant under his hand and seal on the recommendation of the National Judicial <5>Appointments Commission referred to in article 124A and shall hold office until <5>he attains the age of sixty-five years: <5>[omitted by the Constitution (Ninety-ninth Amendment) Act, 2014] <5>Provided that- <6>a.<5> a Judge may, by writing under his hand addressed to the President, resign <5>his office; <6>b.<5> a judge may be removed from his office in the manner provided in clause <5>(4). <4>• Minimum age of supreme court judges <6>2A.<5> The age of a Judge of the Supreme Court shall be determined by such authority <5>and in such manner as Parliament may by law provide. <4>• Eligibility for supreme court judges <6>3.<5> A person shall not be qualified for appointment as a Judge of the Supreme Court <5>unless he is a citizen of India and- <6>a.<5> has been for at least five years a Judge of a High Court or of two or more <5>such Courts in succession; or <6>b.<5> has been for at least ten years an advocate of a High Court or of two or <5>more such Courts in succession; or <6>c. <5>is, in the opinion of the President, a distinguished jurist. <7>Explanation I <5>In this clause "High Court" means a High Court which exercises, or which at any time <5>before the commencement of this Constitution exercised, jurisdiction in any part of <5>the territory of India. <7>Explanation II <5>In computing for the purpose of this clause the period during which a person has <5>been an advocate, any period during which a person has held judicial office not <5>inferior to that of a district judge after he became an advocate shall be included. <4>• Supreme/ordinary court judge removal <6>4.<5> A Judge of the Supreme Court shall not be removed from his office except by an <5>order of the President passed after an address by each House of Parliament <5>supported by a majority of the total membership of that House and by a majority <5>of not less than two thirds of the members of that House present and voting has <5>been presented to the President in the same session for such removal on the <5>ground of proved misbehaviour or incapacity. <4>• Supreme/ordinary court judge removal <6>5.<5> Parliament may by law regulate the procedure for the presentation of an <5>address and for the investigation and proof of the misbehaviour or incapacity of <5>a Judge under clause (4). <4>• Oaths to abide by constitution <6>6.<5> Every person appointed to be a Judge of the Supreme Court shall, before he <5>enters upon his office, make and subscribe before the President, or some person <5>appointed in that behalf by him, an oath or affirmation according to the form set <5>out for the purpose in the Third Schedule. <6>7.<5> No person who has held office as a Judge of the Supreme Court shall plead or act <5>in any court or before any authority within the territory of India. <4>• Establishment of judicial council <7>124A. National Judicial Appointments Commission <6>1. <5>There shall be a Commission to be known as the National Judicial Appointments <5>Commission consisting of the following, namely:- <6>a.<5> the Chief Justice of India, Chairperson, ex officio; <6>b.<5> two other senior Judges of the Supreme Court next to the Chief Justice of <5>India - Members, ex officio; <6>c. <5>the Union Minister in charge of Law and Justice - Member, ex officio; <6>d.<5> two eminent persons to be nominated by the committee consisting of the <5>Prime Minister, the Chief Justice of India and the Leader of Opposition in <5>the House of the People or where there is no such Leader of Opposition, <5>then, the Leader of single largest Opposition Party in the House of the <5>People - Members: <4>• Mentions of social class <5>Provided that one of the eminent person shall be nominated from amongst <5>the persons belonging to the Scheduled Castes, the Scheduled Tribes, <5>Other Backward Classes, Minorities or Women: <5>Provided further that an eminent person shall be nominated for a period of <5>three years and shall not be eligible for renomination. <6>2. <5>No act or proceedings of the National Judicial Appointments Commission shall <5>be questioned or be invalidated merely on the ground of the existence of any <5>vacancy or defect in the constitution of the Commission. <4>• Establishment of judicial council <7>124B. Functions of Commission <5>It shall be the duty of the National Judicial Appointments Commission to- <4>• Supreme court selection <6>a.<5> recommend persons for appointment as Chief Justice of India, Judges of <4>• Ordinary court selection <5>the Supreme Court, Chief Justices of High Courts and other Judges of High <5>Courts; <6>b.<5> recommend transfer of Chief Justices and other Judges of High Courts <5>from one High Court to any other High Court; and <6>c. <5>ensure that the person recommended is of ability and integrity. <7>124C. Power of Parliament to make law <5>Parliament may, by law, regulate the procedure for the appointment of Chief Justice <5>of India and other Judges of the Supreme Court and Chief Justices and other Judges <5>of High Courts and empower the Commission to lay down by regulations the <5>procedure for the discharge of its functions, the manner of selection of persons for <5>appointment and such other matters as may be considered necessary by it. <7>125. Salaries, etc., of Judges <6>1.<5> There shall be paid to the Judges of the Supreme Court such salaries as may be <5>determined by Parliament by law and, until provision in that behalf is so made, <5>such salaries as are specified in the Second Schedule. <4>• Protection of judges' salaries <6>2.<5> Every Judge shall be entitled to such privileges and allowances and to such <5>rights in respect of leave of absence and pension as may from time to time be <5>determined by or under law made by Parliament and, until so determined, to <5>such privileges, allowances and rights as are specified in the Second Schedule: <5>Provided that neither the privileges nor the allowances of a Judge nor his rights <5>in respect of leave of absence or pension shall be varied to his disadvantage <5>after his appointment. <7>126. Appointment of acting Chief Justice <5>When the office of Chief Justice of India is vacant or when the Chief Justice is, by <5>reason of absence or otherwise, unable to perform the duties of his office, the duties <5>of the office shall be performed by such one of the other Judges of the Court as the <5>President may appoint for the purpose. <7>127. Appointment of ad hoc Judges <4>• Establishment of judicial council <6>1.<5> If at any time there should not be a quorum of the Judges of the Supreme Court <5>available to hold or continue any session of the Court, the National Judicial <5>Appointments Commission on a reference made to it by the Chief Justice of <5>India, may with the previous consent of the President and after consultation <5>with the Chief Justice of the High Court concerned, request in writing the <5>attendance at the sittings of the Court, as an ad hoc Judge, for such period as <5>may be necessary, of a Judge of a High Court duly qualified for appointment as a <5>Judge of the Supreme Court to be designated by the Chief Justice of India. <6>2.<5> It shall be the duty of the Judge who has been so designated, in priority to other <5>duties of his office to attend the sittings of the Supreme Court at the time and <5>for the period for which his attendance is required, and while so attending he <5>shall have all the jurisdiction, powers and privileges, and shall discharge the <5>duties, of a Judge of the Supreme Court. <7>128. Attendance of retired Judges at sittings of the <4>• Establishment of judicial council <7>Supreme Court <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Chapter, the National Judicial Appointments <5>Commission may at any time, with the previous consent of the President, request <5>any person who has held the office of a Judge of the Supreme Court or of the Federal <5>Court or who has held the office of a Judge of a High Court and is duly qualified for <5>appointment as a Judge of the Supreme Court to sit and act as a Judge of the <5>Supreme Court, and every such person so requested shall, while so sitting and acting, <5>be entitled to such allowances as the President may by order determine and have all <5>the jurisdiction, powers and privileges of, but shall not otherwise be deemed to be, a <5>Judge of that Court: <5>Provided that nothing in this article shall be deemed to require any such person as <5>aforesaid to sit and act as a Judge of that Court unless he consents so to do. <7>129. Supreme Court to be a court of record <5>The Supreme Court shall be a court of record and shall have all the powers of such a <5>court including the power to punish for contempt of itself. <7>130. Seat of Supreme Court <5>The Supreme Court shall sit in Delhi or in such other place or places, as the Chief <5>Justice of India may, with the approval of the President, from time to time, appoint. <4>• Supreme court powers <7>131. Original jurisdiction of the Supreme Court <5>Subject to the provisions of this Constitution, the Supreme Court shall, to the <5>exclusion of any other court, have original jurisdiction in any dispute- <6>a.<5> between the Government of India and one or more States; or <6>b.<5> between the Government of India and any State or States on one side and <5>one or more other States on the other; or <6>c. <5>between two or more States, <5>if and in so far as the dispute involves any question (whether of law or fact) on which <5>the existence or extent of a legal right depends: <5>Provided that the said jurisdiction shall not extend to a dispute arising out of any <5>treaty, agreement, covenant, engagement, sanad or other similar instrument which, <5>having been entered into or executed before the commencement of this <5>Constitution, continues in operation after such commencement, or which provides <5>that the said jurisdiction shall not extend to such a dispute. <7>131A. Executive jurisdiction of the Supreme Court in <7>regard to questions as to constitutional validity of Central <7>laws <5>Rep. by the Constitution (Forty-third Amendment) Act, 1977, s. 4(w.e.f. 13-4-1978). <7>132. Appellate jurisdiction of Supreme Court in appeals <4>• Right to appeal judicial decisions <7>from High Courts in certain cases <4>• Constitutional interpretation <6>1.<5> An appeal shall lie to the Supreme Court from any judgment, decree or final <5>order of a High Court in the territory of India, whether in a civil, criminal or other <5>proceeding, if the High Court certifies under article 134A that the case involves <5>a substantial question of law as to the interpretation of this Constitution. <6>2. <5>[omitted by s. 17, ibid. (w.e.f. 1-8-1979).] <6>3.<5> Where such a certificate is given, any party in the case may appeal to the <5>Supreme Court on the ground that any such question as aforesaid has been <5>wrongly decided. <7>Explanation <5>For the purposes of this article, the expression "final order" includes an order <5>deciding an issue which, if decided in favour of the appellant, would be sufficient for <5>the final disposal of the case. <7>133. Appellate jurisdiction of Supreme Court in appeals <4>• Right to appeal judicial decisions <7>from High Courts in regard to civil matters <6>1.<5> An appeal shall lie to the Supreme Court from any judgment, decree or final <5>order in a civil proceeding of a High Court in the territory of India if the High <5>Court certifies under article 134A- <6>a.<5> that the case involves a substantial question of law of general importance; <5>and <6>b.<5> that in the opinion of the High Court the said question needs to be decided <5>by the Supreme Court. <6>2.<5> Notwithstanding anything in article 132, any party appealing to the Supreme <5>Court under clause (1) may urge as one of the grounds in such appeal that a <5>substantial question of law as to the interpretation of this Constitution has been <5>wrongly decided. <6>3.<5> Notwithstanding anything in this article, no appeal shall, unless Parliament by <5>law otherwise provides, lie to the Supreme Court from the judgment, decree or <5>final order of one Judge of a High Court. <7>134. Appellate jurisdiction of Supreme Court in regard to <4>• Right to appeal judicial decisions <7>criminal matters <6>1.<5> An appeal shall lie to the Supreme Court from any judgment, final order or <5>sentence in a criminal proceeding of a High Court in the territory of India if the <5>High Court- <6>a.<5> has on appeal reversed an order of acquittal of an accused person and <5>sentenced him to death; or <6>b.<5> has withdrawn for trial before itself any case from any court subordinate to <5>its authority and has in such trial convicted the accused person and <5>sentenced him to death; or <6>c. <5>certifies under article 134A that the case is a fit one for appeal to the <5>Supreme Court: <5>Provided that an appeal under sub-clause (c) shall lie subject to such provisions <5>as may be made in that behalf under clause (1) of article 145 and to such <5>conditions as the High Court may establish or require. <6>2.<5> Parliament may by law confer on the Supreme Court any further powers to <5>entertain and hear appeals from any judgment, final order or sentence in a <5>criminal proceeding of a High Court in the territory of India subject to such <5>conditions and limitations as may be specified in such law. <7>134A. Certificate for appeal to the Supreme Court <5>Every High Court, passing or making a judgment, decree, final order, or sentence, <5>referred to in clause (1) of article 132 or clause (1) of article 133, or clause (1) of <5>article 134,- <6>a.<5> may, if it deems fit so to do, on its own motion; and <6>b.<5> shall, if an oral application is made, by or on behalf of the party aggrieved, <5>immediately after the passing or making of such judgment, decree, final <5>order or sentence, <5>determine, as soon as may be after such passing or making, the question whether a <5>certificate of the nature referred to in clause (1) of article 132, or clause (1) of article <5>133 or, as the case may be, sub-clause (c) of clause (1) of article 134, may be given in <5>respect of that case. <4>• Supreme court powers <7>135. Jurisdiction and powers of the Federal Court under <7>existing law to be exercisable by the Supreme Court <5>Until Parliament by law otherwise provides, the Supreme Court shall also have <5>jurisdiction and powers with respect to any matter to which the provisions of article <5>133 or article 134 do not apply if jurisdiction and powers in relation to that matter <5>were exercisable by the Federal Court immediately before the commencement of <5>this Constitution under any existing law. <4>• Supreme court powers <7>136. Special leave to appeal by the Supreme Court <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in this Chapter, the Supreme Court may, in its <5>discretion, grant special leave to appeal from any judgment, decree, <5>determination, sentence or order in any cause or matter passed or made by any <5>court or tribunal in the territory of India. <4>• Establishment of administrative courts <6>2.<5> Nothing in clause (1) shall apply to any judgment, determination, sentence or <4>• Establishment of military courts <5>order passed or made by any court or tribunal constituted by or under any law <5>relating to the Armed Forces. <4>• Supreme court powers <7>137. Review of judgments or orders by the Supreme Court <5>Subject to the provisions of any law made by Parliament or any rules made under <5>article <5>145, the Supreme Court shall have power to review any judgment <5>pronounced or order made by it. <4>• Supreme court powers <7>138. Enlargement of the jurisdiction of the Supreme Court <6>1.<5> The Supreme Court shall have such further jurisdiction and powers with respect <5>to any of the matters in the Union List as Parliament may by law confer. <6>2.<5> The Supreme Court shall have such further jurisdiction and powers with respect <5>to any matter as the Government of India and the Government of any State may <5>by special agreement confer; if Parliament by law provides for the exercise of <5>such jurisdiction and powers by the Supreme Court. <4>• Supreme court powers <7>139. Conferment on the Supreme Court of powers to issue <7>certain writs <5>Parliament may by law confer on the Supreme Court power to issue directions, <5>orders or writs, including writs in the nature of habeas corpus, mandamus, <5>prohibition, quo warranto and certiorari, or any of them, for any purposes other than <5>those mentioned in clause (2) of article 32. <7>139A. Transfer of certain cases <6>1.<5> Where cases involving the same or substantially the same questions of law are <5>pending before the Supreme Court and one or more High Courts or before two <5>or more High Courts and the Supreme Court is satisfied on its own motion or on <5>an application made by the Attorney-General of India or by a party to any such <5>case that such questions are substantial questions of general importance, the <5>Supreme Court may withdraw the case or cases pending before the High Court <5>or the High Courts and dispose of all the cases itself: <5>Provided that the Supreme Court may after determining the said questions of <5>law return any case so withdrawn together with a copy of its judgment on such <5>questions to the High Court from which the case has been withdrawn, and the <5>High Court shall on receipt thereof, proceed to dispose of the case in conformity <5>with such judgment. <6>2.<5> The Supreme Court may, if it deems it expedient so to do for the ends of justice, <5>transfer any case, appeal or other proceedings pending before any High Court to <5>any other High Court. <4>• Supreme court powers <7>140. Ancillary powers of Supreme Court <5>Parliament may by law make provision for conferring upon the Supreme Court such <5>supplemental powers not inconsistent with any of the provisions of this Constitution <5>as may appear to be necessary or desirable for the purpose of enabling the Court <5>more effectively to exercise the jurisdiction conferred upon it by or under this <5>Constitution. <4>• National vs subnational laws <7>141. Law declared by Supreme Court to be binding on all <7>courts <5>The law declared by the Supreme Court shall be binding on all courts within the <5>territory of India. <7>142. Enforcement of decrees and orders of Supreme Court <7>and orders as to discovery, etc <6>1.<5> The Supreme Court in the exercise of its jurisdiction may pass such decree or <5>make such order as is necessary for doing complete justice in any cause or <5>matter pending before it, and any decree so passed or order so made shall be <5>enforceable throughout the territory of India in such manner as may be <5>prescribed by or under any law made by Parliament and, until provision in that <5>behalf is so made, in such manner as the President may by order prescribe. <6>2.<5> Subject to the provisions of any law made in this behalf by Parliament, the <5>Supreme Court shall, as respects the whole of the territory of India, have all and <5>every power to make any order for the purpose of securing the attendance of <5>any person, the discovery or production of any documents, or the investigation <5>or punishment of any contempt of itself. <7>143. Power of President to consult Supreme Court <6>1.<5> If at any time it appears to the President that a question of law or fact has arisen, <5>or is likely to arise, which is of such a nature and of such public importance that it <5>is expedient to obtain the opinion of the Supreme Court upon it, he may refer <5>the question to that Court for consideration and the Court may, after such <5>hearing as it thinks fit, report to the President its opinion thereon. <6>2.<5> The President may, notwithstanding anything in the proviso to article 131, refer <5>a dispute of the kind mentioned in the said proviso to the Supreme Court for <5>opinion and the Supreme Court shall, after such hearing as it thinks fit, report to <5>the President its opinion thereon. <7>144. Civil and judicial authorities to act in aid of the <7>Supreme Court <5>All authorities, civil and judicial, in the territory of India shall act in aid of the <5>Supreme Court. <7>144A. Special provisions as to disposal of questions <7>relating to constitutional validity of laws <5>Rep. by the Constitution (Forty-third Amendment) Act, 1977, s. 5(w.e.f. 13-4-1978). <7>145. Rules of Court, etc <6>1. <5>Subject to the provisions of any law made by Parliament, the Supreme Court <5>may from time to time, with the approval of the President, make rules for <5>regulating generally the practice and procedure of the Court including- <6>a. <5>rules as to the persons practising before the Court; <6>b. <5>rules as to the procedure for hearing appeals and other matters pertaining <5>to appeals including the time within which appeals to the Court are to be <5>entered; <6>c. <5>rules as to the proceedings in the Court for the enforcement of any of the <5>rights conferred by Part III; <6>cc. <5>rules as to the proceedings in the Court under article 139A: <6>d. <5>rules as to the entertainment of appeals under sub-clause (c) of clause (1) of <5>article 134; <6>e. <5>rules as to the conditions subject to which any judgment pronounced or <5>order made by the Court may be reviewed and the procedure for such <5>review including the time within which applications to the Court for such <5>review are to be entered; <6>f. <5>rules as to the costs of and incidental to any proceedings in the Court and as <5>to the fees to be charged in respect of proceedings therein; <4>• Right to pre-trial release <6>g. <5>rules as to the granting of bail; <6>h. <5>rules as to stay of proceedings; <6>i. <5>rules providing for the summary determination of any appeal which <5>appears to the Court to be frivolous or vexatious or brought for the <5>purpose of delay; <6>j. <5>rules as to the procedure for inquiries referred to in clause (1) of article <5>317. <6>2.<5> Subject to the provisions of clause(3), rules made under this article may fix the <5>minimum number of Judges who are to sit for any purpose, and may provide for <5>the powers of single Judges and Division Courts. <6>3.<5> The minimum number of Judges who are to sit for the purpose of deciding any <5>case involving a substantial question of law as to the interpretation of this <5>Constitution or for the purpose of hearing any reference under article 143 shall <5>be five: <5>Provided that, where the Court hearing an appeal under any of the provisions of <5>this Chapter other than article 132 consists of less than five Judges and in the <5>course of the hearing of the appeal the Court is satisfied that the appeal involves <5>a substantial question of law as to the interpretation of this Constitution the <5>determination of which is necessary for the disposal of the appeal, such Court <5>shall refer the question for opinion to a Court constituted as required by this <5>clause for the purpose of deciding any case involving such a question and shall <5>on receipt of the opinion dispose of the appeal in conformity with such opinion. <6>4.<5> No judgment shall be delivered by the Supreme Court save in open Court, and <5>no report shall be made under article 143 save in accordance with an opinion <5>also delivered in open Court. <4>• Supreme court opinions <6>5.<5> No judgment and no such opinion shall be delivered by the Supreme Court save <4>• Constitutionality of legislation <5>with the concurrence of a majority of the Judges present at the hearing of the <5>case, but nothing in this clause shall be deemed to prevent a Judge who does not <5>concur from delivering a dissenting judgment or opinion. <7>146. Officers and servants and the expenses of the <7>Supreme Court <6>1.<5> Appointments of officers and servants of the Supreme Court shall be made by <5>the Chief Justice of India or such other Judge or officer of the Court as he may <5>direct: <5>Provided that the President may by rule require that in such cases as may be <5>specified in the rule, no person not already attached to the Court shall be <5>appointed to any office connected with the Court, save after consultation with <5>the Union Public Service Commission. <6>2.<5> Subject to the provisions of any law made by Parliament, the conditions of <5>service of officers and servants of the Supreme Court shall be such as may be <5>prescribed by rules made by the Chief Justice of India or by some other Judge or <5>officer of the Court authorised by the Chief Justice of India to make rules for the <5>purpose: <5>Provided that the rules made under this clause shall, so far as they relate to <5>salaries, allowances, leave or pensions, require the approval of the President. <6>3.<5> The administrative expenses of the Supreme Court, including all salaries, <5>allowances and pensions payable to or in respect of the officers and servants of <5>the Court, shall be charged upon the Consolidated Fund of India, and any fees or <5>other moneys taken by the Court shall form part of that Fund. <7>147. Interpretation <5>In this Chapter and in Chapter V of Part VI, references to any substantial question of <5>law as to the interpretation of this Constitution shall be construed as including <5>references to any substantial question of law as to the interpretation of the <5>Government of India Act, <5>1935 <5>(including any enactment amending or <5>supplementing that Act), or of any Order in Council or order made thereunder, or of <5>the Indian Independence Act, 1947, or of any order made thereunder. <7>CHAPTER V: COMPTROLLER AND AUDITOR-GENERAL <7>OF INDIA <7>148. Comptroller and Auditor-General of India <6>1. <5>There shall be a Comptroller and Auditor-General of India who shall be <5>appointed by the President by warrant under his hand and seal and shall only be <5>removed from office in like manner and on the like grounds as a Judge of the <5>Supreme Court. <4>• God or other deities <6>2. <5>Every person appointed to be the Comptroller and Auditor-General of India <4>• Oaths to abide by constitution <5>shall, before he enters upon his office, make and subscribe before the President, <5>or some person appointed in that behalf by him, an oath or affirmation according <5>to the form set out for the purpose in the Third Schedule. <6>3. <5>The salary and other conditions of service of the Comptroller and <5>Auditor-General shall be such as may be determined by Parliament by law and, <5>until they are so determined, shall be as specified in the Second Schedule: <5>Provided that neither the salary of a Comptroller and Auditor-General nor his <5>rights in respect of leave of absence, pension or age of retirement shall be varied <5>to his disadvantage after his appointment. <6>4. <5>The Comptroller and Auditor-General shall not be eligible for further office <5>either under the Government of India or under the Government of any State <5>after he has ceased to hold his office. <6>5. <5>Subject to the provisions of this Constitution and of any law made by <5>Parliament, the conditions of service of persons serving in the Indian Audit and <5>Accounts Department and the administrative powers of the Comptroller and <5>Auditor-General shall be such as may be prescribed by rules made by the <5>President after consultation with the Comptroller and Auditor-General. <6>6. <5>The administrative expenses of the office of the Comptroller and <5>Auditor-General, including all salaries, allowances and pensions payable to or in <5>respect of persons serving in that office, shall be charged upon the Consolidated <5>Fund of India. <7>149. Duties and powers of the Comptroller and <7>Auditor-General <5>The Comptroller and Auditor-General shall perform such duties and exercise such <5>powers in relation to the accounts of the Union and of the States and of any other <5>authority or body as may be prescribed by or under any law made by Parliament and, <5>until provision in that behalf is so made, shall perform such duties and exercise such <5>powers in relation to the accounts of the Union and of the States as were conferred <5>on or exercisable by the Auditor-General of India immediately before the <5>commencement of this Constitution in relation to the accounts of the Dominion of <5>India and of the Provinces respectively. <7>150. Form of accounts of the Union and of the States <5>The accounts of the Union and of the States shall be kept in such form as the <5>President may, on the advice of the Comptroller and Auditor-General of India, <5>prescribe. <7>151. Audit reports <6>1.<5> The reports of the Comptroller and Auditor-General of India relating to the <5>accounts of the Union shall be submitted to the President, who shall cause them <5>to be laid before each House of Parliament. <6>2.<5> The reports of the Comptroller and Auditor-General of India relating to the <5>accounts of a State shall be submitted to the Governor of the State, who shall <5>cause them to be laid before the Legislature of the State. <9>PART VI: THE STATES <4>• Subsidiary unit government <7>CHAPTER I: GENERAL <7>152. Definition <5>In this Part, unless the context otherwise requires, the expression "State" does not <5>include the State of Jammu and Kashmir. <4>• Subsidiary unit government <7>CHAPTER II: THE EXECUTIVE <7>The Governor <7>153. Governors of States <5>There shall be a Governor for each State: <5>Provided that nothing in this article shall prevent the appointment of the same <5>person as Governor for two or more States. <7>154. Executive power of State <6>1.<5> The executive power of the State shall be vested in the Governor and shall be <5>exercised by him either directly or through officers subordinate to him in <5>accordance with this Constitution. <6>2.<5> Nothing in this article shall- <6>a.<5> be deemed to transfer to the Governor any functions conferred by any <5>existing law on any other authority; or <6>b.<5> prevent Parliament or the Legislature of the State from conferring by law <5>functions on any authority subordinate to the Governor. <7>155. Appointment of Governor <5>The Governor of a State shall be appointed by the President by warrant under his <5>hand and seal. <7>156. Term of office of Governor <6>1.<5> The Governor shall hold office during the pleasure of the President. <6>2.<5> The Governor may, by writing under his hand addressed to the President, resign <5>his office. <6>3.<5> Subject to the foregoing provisions of this article, a Governor shall hold office <5>for a term of five years from the date on which he enters upon his office: <5>Provided that a Governor shall, notwithstanding the expiration of his term, <5>continue to hold office until his successor enters upon his office. <7>157. Qualifications for appointment as Governor <5>No person shall be eligible for appointment as Governor unless he is a citizen of India <5>and has completed the age of thirty-five years. <7>158. Conditions of Governor's office <6>1.<5> The Governor shall not be a member of either House of Parliament or of a House <5>of the Legislature of any State specified in the First Schedule, and if a member of <5>either House of Parliament or of a House of the Legislature of any such State be <5>appointed Governor, he shall be deemed to have vacated his seat in that House <5>on the date on which he enters upon his office as Governor. <6>2.<5> The Governor shall not hold any other office of profit <6>3.<5> The Governor shall be entitled without payment of rent to the use of his official <5>residences and shall be also entitled to such emoluments, allowances and <5>privileges as may be determined by Parliament by law and, until provision in that <5>behalf is so made, such emoluments, allowances and privileges as are specified in <5>the Second Schedule. <6>3A.<5> Where the same person is appointed as Governor of two or more States, the <5>emoluments and allowances payable to the Governor shall be allocated among <5>the States in such proportion as the President may by order determine. <6>4.<5> The emoluments and allowances of the Governor shall not be diminished during <5>his term of office. <7>159. Oath or affirmation by the Governor <5>Every Governor and every person discharging the functions of the Governor shall, <5>before entering upon his office, make and subscribe in the presence of the Chief <5>Justice of the High Court exercising jurisdiction in relation to the State, or, in his <5>absence, the senior most Judge of that Court available, an oath or affirmation in the <5>following form, that is to say- <5>"I, A.B., do Swear in the name of God/Solemnly Affirm that I will faithfully execute <5>the office of Governor (or discharge the functions of the Governor) of (name of the <5>State) and will to the best of my ability preserve, protect and defend the Constitution <5>and the law and that I will devote myself to the service and well-being of the people <5>of (name of the State)." <7>160. Discharge of the functions of the Governor in certain <7>contingencies <5>The President may make such provision as he thinks fit for the discharge of the <5>functions of the Governor of a State in any contingency not provided for in this <5>Chapter. <7>161. Power of Governor to grant pardons, etc., and to <7>suspend, remit or commute sentences in certain cases <5>The Governor of a State shall have the power to grant pardons, reprieves, respites or <5>remissions of punishment or to suspend, remit or commute the sentence of any <5>person convicted of any offence against any law relating to a matter to which the <5>executive power of the State extends. <7>162. Extent of executive power of State <5>Subject to the provisions of this Constitution, the executive power of a State shall <5>extend to the matters with respect to which the Legislature of the State has power to <5>make laws: <5>Provided that in any matter with respect to which the Legislature of a State and <5>Parliament have power to make laws, the executive power of the State shall be <5>subject to, and limited by, the executive power expressly conferred by this <5>Constitution or by any law made by Parliament upon the Union or authorities <5>thereof. <7>Council of Ministers <7>163. Council of Ministers to aid and advise Governor <6>1.<5> There shall be a Council of Ministers with the Chief Minister at the head to aid <5>and advise the Governor in the exercise of his function, except in so far as he is <5>by or under this Constitution required to exercise his functions or any of them in <5>his discretion. <6>2.<5> If any question arises whether any matter is or is not a matter as respects which <5>the Governor is by or under this Constitution required to act in his discretion, <5>the decision of the Governor in his discretion shall be final, and the validity of <5>anything done by the Governor shall not be called in question on the ground that <5>he ought or ought not to have acted in his discretion. <6>3.<5> The question whether any, and if so what, advice was tendered by Ministers to <5>the Governor shall not be inquired into in any court. <7>164. Other provisions as to Ministers <6>1.<5> The Chief Minister shall be appointed by the Governor and the other Ministers <5>shall be appointed by the Governor on the advice of the Chief Minister, and the <5>Ministers shall hold office during the pleasure of the Governor: <5>Provided that in the States of Chhattisgarh, Jharkhand, Madhya Pradesh and <5>Orissa, there shall be a Minister in charge of tribal welfare who may in addition <5>be in charge of the welfare of the Scheduled Castes and backward classes or any <5>other work. <6>1A. <5>The total number of Ministers, including the Chief Minister, in the Council of <5>Ministers in a State shall not exceed fifteen percent of the total number of <5>members of the Legislative Assembly of that State: <5>Provided that the number of Ministers, including Chief Minister in a State shall <5>not be less than twelve: <5>Provided further that where the total number of Ministers including the Chief <5>Minister in the Council of Ministers in any State at the commencement of the <5>Constitution (Ninety-first Amendment) Act, 2003 exceeds the said fifteen per <5>cent. or the number specified in the first proviso, as the case may be, then, the <5>total number of Ministers in that State shall be brought in conformity with the <5>provisions of this clause within six months from such date as the President may <5>by public notification appoint. <6>1B. <5>A member of Legislative Assembly of a State or either House of the Legislature <5>of a State having Legislative Council belonging to any political party who is <5>disqualified for being a member of that House under paragraph 2 of the Tenth <5>Schedule shall also be disqualified to be appointed as a Minister under clause (1) <5>for duration of the period commencing from the date of his disqualification till <5>the date on which the term of his office as such member would expire or where <5>he contests any election to the Legislative Assembly of a State or either House <5>of the Legislature of a State having Legislative Council, as the case may be, <5>before the expiry of such period, till the date on which he is declared elected, <5>whichever is earlier. <6>2. <5>The Council of Ministers shall be collectively responsible to the Legislative <5>Assembly of the State. <4>• Oaths to abide by constitution <6>3. <5>Before a Minister enters upon his office, the Governor shall administer to him <5>the oaths of office and of secrecy according to the forms set out for the purpose <5>in the Third Schedule. <6>4. <5>A Minister who for any period of six consecutive months is not a member of the <5>Legislature of the State shall at the expiration of that period cease to be a <5>Minister. <6>5. <5>The salaries and allowances of Ministers shall be such as the Legislature of the <5>State may from time to time by law determine and, until the Legislature of the <5>State so determines, shall be as specified in the Second Schedule. <7>The Advocate-General for the State <7>165. Advocate-General for the State <6>1.<5> The Governor of each State shall appoint a person who is qualified to be <5>appointed a Judge of a High Court to be Advocate-General for the State. <6>2.<5> It shall be the duty of the Advocate-General to give advice to the Government of <5>the State upon such legal matters, and to perform such other duties of a legal <5>character, as may from time to time be referred or assigned to him by the <5>Governor, and to discharge the functions conferred on him by or under this <5>Constitution or any other law for the time being in force. <6>3.<5> The Advocate-General shall hold office during the pleasure of the Governor, and <5>shall receive such remuneration as the Governor may determine. <7>Conduct of Government Business <7>166. Conduct of business of the Government of a State <6>1.<5> All executive action of the Government of a State shall be expressed to be taken <5>in the name of the Governor. <6>2.<5> Orders and other instruments made and executed in the name of the Governor <5>shall be authenticated in such manner as may be specified in rules to be made by <5>the Governor, and the validity of an order or instrument which is so <5>authenticated shall not be called in question on the ground that it is not an order <5>or instrument made or executed by the Governor. <6>3.<5> The Governor shall make rules for the more convenient transaction of the <5>business of the Government of the State, and for the allocation among Ministers <5>of the said business in so far as it is not business with respect to which the <5>Governor is by or under this Constitution required to act in his discretion. <7>167. Duties of Chief Minister as respects the furnishing of <7>information to Governor, etc <5>It shall be the duty of the Chief Minister of each State- <6>a.<5> to communicate to the Governor of the State all decisions of the Council of <5>Ministers relating to the administration of the affairs of the State and <5>proposals for legislation; <6>b.<5> to furnish such information relating to the administration of the affairs of <5>the State and proposals for legislation as the Governor may call for; and <6>c. <5>if the Governor so requires, to submit for the consideration of the Council <5>of Ministers any matter on which a decision has been taken by a Minister <5>but which has not been considered by the Council. <4>• Subsidiary unit government <7>CHAPTER III: THE STATE LEGISLATURE <7>General <7>168. Constitution of Legislatures in States <6>1.<5> For every State there shall be a Legislature which shall consist of the Governor, <5>and- <6>a.<5> in the States of, Bihar, Maharashtra, Karnataka, and Uttar Pradesh, two <5>Houses; <6>b.<5> in other States, one House. <6>2.<5> Where there are two Houses of the Legislature of a State, one shall be known as <5>the Legislative Council and the other as the Legislative Assembly, and where <5>there is only one House, it shall be known as the Legislative Assembly. <7>169. Abolition or creation of Legislative Councils in States <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in article 168, Parliament may by law provide for the <5>abolition of the Legislative Council of a State having such a Council or for the <5>creation of such a Council in a State having no such Council, if the Legislative <5>Assembly of the State passes a resolution to that effect by a majority of the total <5>membership of the Assembly and by a majority of not less than two-thirds of the <5>members of the Assembly present and voting. <6>2.<5> Any law referred to in clause <5>(1) shall contain such provisions for the <5>amendment of this Constitution as may be necessary to give effect to the <5>provisions of the law and may also contain such supplemental, incidental and <5>consequential provisions as Parliament may deem necessary. <6>3.<5> No such law as aforesaid shall be deemed to be an amendment of this <5>Constitution for the purposes of article 368. <7>170. Composition of the Legislative Assemblies <6>1.<5> Subject to the provisions of article 333, the Legislative Assembly of each State <5>shall consist of not more than five hundred, and not less than sixty, members <5>chosen by direct election from territorial constituencies in the State. <6>2.<5> For the purposes of clause (1), each State shall be divided into territorial <5>constituencies in such manner that the ratio between the population of each <5>constituency and the number of seats allotted to it shall, so far as practicable, be <5>the same throughout the State. <7>Explanation <5>In
