this clause, the expression "population" means the population as ascertained at <5>the last preceding census of which the relevant figures have been published: <5>Provided that the reference in this Explanation to the last preceding census of which <5>the relevant figures have been published shall, until the relevant figures for the first <5>census taken after the year 2026 have been published, be construed as a reference <5>to the 2001 census. <4>• Census <6>3.<5> Upon the completion of each census, the total number of seats in the Legislative <5>Assembly of each State and the division of each State into territorial <5>constituencies shall be readjusted by such authority and in such manner as <5>Parliament may by law determine: <5>Provided that such readjustment shall not affect representation in the <5>Legislative Assembly until the dissolution of the then existing Assembly: <5>Provided further that such readjustment shall take effect from such date as the <5>President may, by order, specify and until such readjustment takes effect, any <5>election to the Legislative Assembly may be held on the basis of the territorial <5>constituencies existing before such readjustment: <5>Provided also that until the relevant figures for the first census taken after the <5>year 2026 have been published, it shall not be necessary to readjust- <6>i. <5>the total number of seats in the Legislative Assembly of each State as <5>readjusted on the basis of the 1971 census; and <6>ii. <5>the division of such State into territorial constituencies as may be <5>readjusted on the basis of the 2001 census, <5>under this clause. <7>171. Composition of the Legislative Councils <6>1. <5>The total number of members in the Legislative Council of a State having such a <5>Council shall not exceed one-third of the total number of members in the <5>Legislative Assembly of that State: <5>Provided that the total number of members in the Legislative Council of a State <5>shall in no case be less than forty. <6>2. <5>Until Parliament by law otherwise provides, the composition of the Legislative <5>Council of a State shall be as provided in clause (3). <6>3. <5>Of the total number of members of the Legislative Council of a State- <6>a.<5> as nearly as may be, one-third shall be elected by electorates consisting of <5>members of municipalities, district boards and such other local authorities <5>in the State as Parliament may by law specify; <6>b.<5> as nearly as may be, one-twelfth shall be elected by electorates consisting <5>of persons residing in the State who have been for at least three years <5>graduates of any university in the territory of India or have been for at least <5>three years in possession of qualifications prescribed by or under any law <5>made by Parliament as equivalent to that of a graduate of any such <5>university; <6>c. <5>as nearly as may be, one-twelfth shall be elected by electorates consisting <5>of persons who have been for at least three years engaged in teaching in <5>such educational institutions within the State, not lower in standard than <5>that of a secondary school, as may be prescribed by or under any law made <5>by Parliament; <6>d.<5> as nearly as may be, one-third shall be elected by the members of the <5>Legislative Assembly of the State from amongst persons who are not <5>members of the Assembly; <6>e.<5> the remainder shall be nominated by the Governor in accordance with the <5>provisions of clause (5). <6>4. <5>The members to be elected under sub-clauses (a), (b) and (c) of clause (3) shall be <5>chosen in such territorial constituencies as may be prescribed by or under any <5>law made by Parliament, and the elections under the said sub-clauses and under <5>sub-clause (d) of the said clause shall be held in accordance with the system of <5>proportional representation by means of the single transferable vote. <6>5. <5>The members to be nominated by the Governor under sub-clause (c) of clause <5>(3) shall consist of persons having special knowledge or practical experience in <5>respect of such matters as the following, namely:- <5>Literature, science, art, co-operative movement and social service. <7>172. Duration of State Legislatures <6>1.<5> Every Legislative Assembly of every State, unless sooner dissolved, shall <5>continue for five years from the date appointed for its first meeting and no <5>longer and the expiration of the said period of five years shall operate as a <5>dissolution of the Assembly: <5>Provided that the said period may, while a Proclamation of Emergency is in <5>operation, be extended by Parliament by law for a period not exceeding one <5>year at a time and not extending in any case beyond a period of six months after <5>the Proclamation has ceased to operate. <6>2.<5> The Legislative Council of a State shall not be subject to dissolution, but as <5>nearly as possible one-third of the members thereof shall retire as soon as may <5>be on the expiration of every second year in accordance with the provisions <5>made in that behalf by Parliament by law. <7>173. Qualification for membership of the State Legislature <5>A person shall not be qualified to be chosen to fill a seat in the Legislature of a State <5>unless he- <4>• Oaths to abide by constitution <6>a.<5> is a citizen of India, and makes and subscribes before some person <5>authorised in that behalf by the Election Commission an oath or affirmation <5>according to the form set out for the purpose in the Third Schedule; <6>b.<5> is, in the case of a seat in the Legislative Assembly, not less than twenty-five <5>years of age and, in the case of a seat in the Legislative Council, not less <5>than thirty years of age; and <6>c. <5>possesses such other qualifications as may be prescribed in that behalf by <5>or under any law made by Parliament. <7>174. Sessions of the State Legislature, prorogation and <7>dissolution <6>1.<5> The Governor shall from time to time summon the House or each House of the <5>Legislature of the State to meet at such time and place as he thinks fit, but six <5>months shall not intervene between its last sitting in one session and the date <5>appointed for its first sitting in the next session. <6>2.<5> The Governor may from time to time- <6>a.<5> prorogue the House or either House; <6>b.<5> dissolve the Legislative Assembly. <7>175. Right of Governor to address and send messages to <7>the House or Houses <6>1.<5> The Governor may address the Legislative Assembly or, in the case of a State <5>having a Legislative Council, either House of the Legislature of the State, or both <5>Houses assembled together, and may for that purpose require the attendance of <5>members. <6>2.<5> The Governor may send messages to the House or Houses of the Legislature of <5>the State, whether with respect to a Bill then pending in the Legislature or <5>otherwise, and a House to which any message is so sent shall with all convenient <5>despatch consider any matter required by the message to be taken into <5>consideration. <7>176. Special address by the Governor <6>1.<5> At the commencement of the first session after each general election to the <5>Legislative Assembly and at the commencement of the first session of each year, <5>the Governor shall address the Legislative Assembly or, in the case of a State <5>having a Legislative Council, both Houses assembled together and inform the <5>Legislature of the causes of its summons. <6>2.<5> Provision shall be made by the rules regulating the procedure of the House or <5>either House for the allotment of time for discussion of the matters referred to <5>in such address. <7>177. Rights of Ministers and Advocate-General as respects <7>the Houses <5>Every Minister and the Advocate-General for a State shall have the right to speak in, <5>and otherwise to take part in the proceedings of, the Legislative Assembly of the <5>State or, in the case of a State having a Legislative Council, both Houses, and to speak <5>in, and otherwise to take part in the proceedings of, any committee of the Legislature <5>of which he may be named a member, but shall not, by virtue of this article, be <5>entitled to vote. <7>Officers of the State Legislature <7>178. The Speaker and Deputy Speaker of the Legislative <7>Assembly <5>Every Legislative Assembly of a State shall, as soon as may be, choose two members <5>of the Assembly to be respectively Speaker and Deputy Speaker thereof and, so <5>often as the office of Speaker or Deputy Speaker becomes vacant, the Assembly shall <5>choose another member to be Speaker or Deputy Speaker, as the case may be. <7>179. Vacation and resignation of, and removal from, the <7>offices of Speaker and Deputy Speaker <5>A member holding office as Speaker or Deputy Speaker of an Assembly- <6>a.<5> shall vacate his office if he ceases to be a member of the Assembly; <6>b.<5> may at any time by writing under his hand addressed, if such member is the <5>Speaker, to the Deputy Speaker, and if such member is the Deputy Speaker, <5>to the Speaker, resign his office; and <6>c. <5>may be removed from his office by a resolution of the Assembly passed by a <5>majority of all the then members of the Assembly: <5>Provided that no resolution for the purpose of clause (c) shall be moved unless at <5>least fourteen days' notice has been given of the intention to move the resolution: <5>Provided further that, whenever the Assembly is dissolved, the Speaker shall not <5>vacate his office until immediately before the first meeting of the Assembly after the <5>dissolution. <7>180. Power of the Deputy Speaker or other person to <7>perform the duties of the office of, or to act as, Speaker <6>1.<5> While the office of Speaker is vacant, the duties of the office shall be performed <5>by the Deputy Speaker or, if the office of Deputy speaker is also vacant, by such <5>member of the Assembly as the Governor may appoint for the purpose. <6>2.<5> During the absence of the Speaker from any sitting of the Assembly the Deputy <5>Speaker or, if he is also absent, such person as may be determined by the rules of <5>procedure of the Assembly, or, if no such person is present, such other person as <5>may be determined by the Assembly, shall act as Speaker. <7>181. The Speaker or the Deputy Speaker not to preside <7>while a resolution for his removal from office is under <7>consideration <6>1.<5> At any sitting of the Legislative Assembly, while any resolution for the removal <5>of the Speaker from his office is under consideration, the Speaker, or while any <5>resolution for the removal of the Deputy Speaker from his office is under <5>consideration, the Deputy Speaker, shall not, though he is present, preside, and <5>the provisions of clause (2) of article 180 shall apply in relation to every such <5>sitting as they apply in relation to a sitting from which the Speaker or, as the case <5>may be, the Deputy Speaker, is absent <6>2.<5> The Speaker shall have the right to speak in, and otherwise to take part in the <5>proceedings of, the Legislative Assembly while any resolution for his removal <5>from office is under consideration in the Assembly and shall, notwithstanding <5>anything in article 189, be entitled to vote only in the first instance on such <5>resolution or on any other matter during such proceedings but not in the case of <5>an equality of votes. <7>182. The Chairman and Deputy Chairman of the Legislative <7>Council <5>The Legislative Council of every State having such Council shall, as soon as may be, <5>choose two members of the Council to be respectively Chairman and Deputy <5>Chairman thereof and, so often as the office of Chairman or Deputy Chairman <5>becomes vacant, the Council shall choose another member to be Chairman or <5>Deputy Chairman, as the case may be. <7>183. Vacation and resignation of, and removal from, the <7>offices of Chairman and Deputy Chairman <5>A member holding office as Chairman or Deputy Chairman of a Legislative Council- <6>a.<5> shall vacate his office if he ceases to be a member of the Council; <6>b.<5> may at any time by writing under his hand addressed, if such member is the <5>Chairman, to the Deputy Chairman, and if such member is the Deputy <5>Chairman, to the Chairman, resign his office; and <6>c. <5>may be removed from his office by a resolution of the Council passed by a <5>majority of all the then members of the Council: <5>Provided that no resolution for the purpose of clause (c) shall be moved unless at <5>least fourteen days' notice has been given of the intention to move the resolution. <7>184. Power of the Deputy Chairman or other person to <7>perform the duties of the office of, or to act as, Chairman <6>1.<5> While the office of Chairman is vacant, the duties of the office shall be <5>performed by the Deputy Chairman or, if the office of Deputy Chairman is also <5>vacant, by such member of the Council as the Governor may appoint for the <5>purpose. <6>2.<5> During the absence of the Chairman from any sitting of the Council the Deputy <5>Chairman or, if he is also absent, such person as may be determined by the rules <5>of procedure of the Council, or, if no such person is present, such other person as <5>may be determined by the Council, shall act as Chairman. <7>185. The Chairman or the Deputy Chairman not to preside <7>while a resolution for his removal from office is under <7>consideration <6>1.<5> At any sitting of the Legislative Council, while any resolution for the removal of <5>the Chairman from his office is under consideration, the Chairman, or while any <5>resolution for the removal of the Deputy Chairman from his office is under <5>consideration, the Deputy Chairman, shall not, though he is present, preside, and <5>the provisions of clause (2) of article 184 shall apply in relation to every such <5>sitting as they apply in relation to a sitting from which the Chairman or, as the <5>case may be, the Deputy Chairman is absent. <6>2.<5> The Chairman shall have the right to speak in, and otherwise to take part in the <5>proceedings of, the Legislative Council while any resolution for his removal from <5>office is under consideration in the Council and shall notwithstanding anything <5>in article 189, be entitled to vote only in the first instance on such resolution or <5>on any other matter during such proceedings but not in the case of an equality of <5>votes. <7>186. Salaries and allowances of the Speaker and Deputy <7>Speaker and the Chairman and Deputy Chairman <5>There shall be paid to the Speaker and the Deputy Speaker of the Legislative <5>Assembly, and to the Chairman and the Deputy Chairman of the Legislative Council, <5>such salaries and allowances as may be respectively fixed by the Legislature of the <5>State by law and, until provision in that behalf is so made, such salaries and <5>allowances as are specified in the Second Schedule. <7>187. Secretariat of State Legislature <6>1.<5> The House or each House of the Legislature of a state shall have a separate <5>secretarial staff: <5>Provided that nothing in this clause shall, in the case of the Legislature of a State <5>having a Legislative Council, be construed as preventing the creation of posts <5>common to both Houses of such Legislature. <6>2.<5> The Legislature of a State may by law regulate the recruitment, and the <5>conditions of service of persons appointed, to the secretarial staff of the House <5>or Houses of the Legislature of the State. <6>3.<5> Until provision is made by the Legislature of the State under clause (2), the <5>Governor may, after consultation with the Speaker of the Legislative Assembly <5>or the Chairman of the Legislative Council, as the case may be, make rules <5>regulating the recruitment, and the conditions of service of persons appointed, <5>to the secretarial staff of the Assembly or the Council, and any rules so made <5>shall have effect subject to the provisions of any law made under the said clause. <7>Conduct of Business <7>188. Oath or affirmation by members <5>Every member of the Legislative Assembly or the Legislative Council of a State shall, <5>before taking his seat, make and subscribe before the Governor, or some person <5>appointed in that behalf by him, an oath or affirmation according to the form set out <5>for the purpose in the Third Schedule. <7>189. Voting in Houses, power of Houses to act <7>notwithstanding vacancies and quorum <6>1.<5> Save as otherwise provided in this Constitution, all questions at any sitting of a <5>House of the Legislature of a State shall be determined by a majority of votes of <5>the members present and voting, other than the Speaker or Chairman, or person <5>acting as such. <5>The Speaker or Chairman, or person acting as such, shall not vote in the first <5>instance, but shall have and exercise a casting vote in the case of an equality of <5>votes. <6>2.<5> A House of the Legislature of a State shall have power to act notwithstanding <5>any vacancy in the membership thereof, and any proceedings in the Legislature <5>of a State shall be valid notwithstanding that it is discovered subsequently that <5>some person who was not entitled so to do sat or voted or otherwise took part in <5>the proceedings. <6>3.<5> Until the Legislature of the State by law otherwise provides, the quorum to <5>constitute a meeting of a House of the Legislature of a State shall be ten <5>members or one-tenth of the total number of members of the House, whichever <5>is greater. <6>4.<5> If at any time during a meeting of the Legislative Assembly or the Legislative <5>Council of a State there is no quorum, it shall be the duty of the Speaker or <5>Chairman, or person acting as such, either to adjourn the House or to suspend <5>the meeting until there is a quorum. <7>Disqualifications of Members <7>190. Vacation of seats <6>1.<5> No person shall be a member of both Houses of the Legislature of a State and <5>provision shall be made by the Legislature of the State by law for the vacation by <5>a person who is chosen a member of both Houses of his seat in one House or the <5>other. <6>2. <5>No person shall be a member of the Legislatures of two or more States specified <5>in the First Schedule and if a person is chosen a member of the Legislatures of <5>two or more such States, then, at the expiration of such period as may be <5>specified in rules made by the President, that person's seat in the Legislatures of <5>all such States shall become vacant, unless he has previously resigned his seat in <5>the Legislatures of all but one of the States. <6>3. <5>If a member of a House of the Legislature of a State- <6>a.<5> becomes subject to any of the disqualifications mentioned in clause (1) or <5>clause (2) of article 191; or <6>b.<5> resigns his seat by writing under his hand addressed to the Speaker or the <5>Chairman, as the case may be, and his resignation is accepted by the <5>Speaker or the Chairman, as the case may be, <5>his seat shall thereupon become vacant: <5>Provided that in the case of any resignation referred to in sub-clause (b), if from <5>information received or otherwise and after making such inquiry as he thinks fit, <5>the Speaker or the Chairman, as the case may be, is satisfied that such <5>resignation is not voluntary or genuine, he shall not accept such resignation. <6>4. <5>If for a period of sixty days a member of a House of the Legislature of a State is <5>without permission of the House absent from all meetings thereof, the House <5>may declare his seat vacant: <5>Provided that in computing the said period of sixty days no account shall be <5>taken of any period during which the House is prorogued or is adjourned for <5>more than four consecutive days. <7>191. Disqualifications for membership <6>1.<5> A person shall be disqualified for being chosen as, and for being, a member of the <5>Legislative Assembly or Legislative Council of a State- <6>a.<5> if he holds any office of profit under the Government of India or the <5>Government of any State specified in the First Schedule, other than an <5>office declared by the Legislature of the State by law not to disqualify its <5>holder; <6>b.<5> if he is of unsound mind and stands so declared by a competent court; <6>c. <5>if he is an undischarged insolvent; <6>d.<5> if he is not a citizen of India, or has voluntarily acquired the citizenship of a <5>foreign State, or is under any acknowledgment of allegiance or adherence <5>to a foreign State; <6>e.<5> if he is so disqualified by or under any law made by Parliament. <7>Explanation <5>For the purposes of this clause, a person shall not be deemed to hold an office of <5>profit under the Government of India or the Government of any State specified in <5>the First Schedule by reason only that he is a Minister either for the Union or for <5>such State. <6>2.<5> A person shall be disqualified for being a member of the Legislative Assembly or <5>Legislative Council of a State if he is so disqualified under the Tenth Schedule. <7>192. Decision on questions as to disqualifications of <7>members <6>1.<5> If any question arises as to whether a member of a House of the Legislature of a <5>State has become subject to any of the disqualifications mentioned in clause (1) <5>of article 191, the question shall be referred for the decision of the Governor <5>and his decision shall be final. <6>2.<5> Before giving any decision on any such question, the Governor shall obtain the <5>opinion of the Election Commission and shall act according to such opinion. <7>193. Penalty for sitting and voting before making oath or <7>affirmation under article 188 or when not qualified or <7>when disqualified <5>If a person sits or votes as a member of the Legislative Assembly or the Legislative <5>Council of a State before he has complied with the requirements of article 188, or <5>when he knows that he is not qualified or that he is disqualified for membership <5>thereof, or that he is prohibited from so doing by the provisions of any law made by <5>Parliament or the Legislature of the State, he shall be liable in respect of each day on <5>which he so sits or votes to a penalty of five hundred rupees to be recovered as a <5>debt due to the State. <7>Powers Privileges and Immunities of State Legislatures and <7>their Members <7>194. Powers, privileges, etc., of the Houses of Legislatures <7>and of the members and committees thereof <6>1.<5> Subject to the provisions of this Constitution and to the rules and standing <5>orders regulating the procedure of the Legislature, there shall be freedom of <5>speech in the Legislature of every State. <6>2.<5> No member of the Legislature of a State shall be liable to any proceedings in any <5>court in respect of anything said or any vote given by him in the Legislature or <5>any committee thereof, and no person shall be so liable in respect of the <5>publication by or under the authority of a House of Such a Legislature of any <5>report, paper, votes or proceedings. <6>3.<5> In other respects, the powers, privileges and immunities of a House of the <5>Legislature of a State, and of the members and the committees of a House of <5>such Legislature, shall be such as may from time to time be defined by the <5>Legislature by law, and, until so defined, shall be those of that House and of its <5>members and committees immediately before the coming into force of section <5>26 of the Constitution (Forty-fourth Amendment) Act, 1978. <6>4.<5> The provisions of clauses (1), (2) and (3) shall apply in relation to persons who by <5>virtue of this Constitution have the right to speak in, and otherwise to take part <5>in the proceedings of, a House of the Legislature of a State or any committee <5>thereof as they apply in relation to members of that Legislature. <7>195. Salaries and allowances of members <5>Members of the Legislative Assembly and the Legislative Council of a State shall be <5>entitled to receive such salaries and allowances as may from time to time be <5>determined, by the Legislature of the State by law and, until provision in that respect <5>is so made, salaries and allowances at such rates and upon such conditions as were <5>immediately before the commencement of this Constitution applicable in the case of <5>members of the Legislative Assembly of the corresponding province. <7>Legislative Procedure <7>196. Provisions as to introduction and passing of Bills <6>1.<5> Subject to the provisions of article 198 and 207 with respect to Money Bills and <5>other financial Bills, a Bill may originate in either House of the Legislature of a <5>State which has a Legislative Council. <6>2.<5> Subject to the provisions of articles 197 and 198, a Bill shall not be deemed to <5>have been passed by the Houses of the Legislature of a State having a Legislative <5>Council unless it has been agreed to by both Houses, either without amendment <5>or with such amendments only as are agreed to by both Houses. <6>3.<5> A Bill pending in the Legislature of a State shall not lapse by reason of the <5>prorogation of the House or Houses thereof. <6>4.<5> A Bill pending in the Legislative Council of a State which has not been passed by <5>the Legislative Assembly shall not lapse on a dissolution of the Assembly. <6>5.<5> A Bill which is pending in the Legislative Assembly of a State, or which having <5>been passed by the Legislative Assembly is pending in the Legislative Council, <5>shall lapse on a dissolution of the Assembly. <7>197. Restriction on powers of Legislative Council as to Bills <7>other than Money Bills <6>1.<5> If after a Bill has been passed by the Legislative Assembly of a State having a <5>Legislative Council and transmitted to the Legislative Council- <6>a.<5> the Bill is rejected by the Council; or <6>b.<5> more than three months elapse from the date on which the Bill is laid <5>before the Council without the Bill being passed by it; or <6>c. <5>the Bill is passed by the Council with amendments to which the Legislative <5>Assembly does not agree, <5>the Legislative Assembly may, subject to the rules regulating its procedure, pass <5>the Bill again in the same or in any subsequent session with or without such <5>amendments, if any, as have been made, suggested or agreed to by the <5>Legislative Council and then transmit the Bill as so passed to the Legislative <5>Council. <6>2.<5> If after a Bill has been so passed for the second time by the Legislative Assembly <5>and transmitted to the Legislative Council- <6>a.<5> the Bill is rejected by the Council; or <6>b.<5> more than one month elapses from the date on which the Bill is laid before <5>the Council without the Bill being passed by it; or <6>c. <5>the Bill is passed by the Council with amendments to which the Legislative <5>Assembly does not agree, <5>the Bill shall be deemed to have been passed by the Houses of the Legislature of <5>the State in the form in which it was passed by the Legislative Assembly for the <5>second time with such amendments, if any, as have been made or suggested by <5>the Legislative Council and agreed to by the Legislative Assembly. <6>3.<5> Nothing in this article shall apply to a Money Bill. <7>198. Special procedure in respect of Money Bills <6>1.<5> A Money Bill shall not be introduced in a Legislative Council. <6>2.<5> After a Money Bill has been passed by the Legislative Assembly of a State having <5>a Legislative Council, it shall be transmitted to the Legislative Council for its <5>recommendations, and the Legislative Council shall within a period of fourteen <5>days from the date of its receipt of the Bill return the Bill to the Legislative <5>Assembly with its recommendations, and the Legislative Assembly may <5>thereupon either accept or reject all or any of the recommendations of the <5>Legislative Council. <6>3.<5> If the Legislative Assembly accepts any of the recommendations of the <5>Legislative Council, the Money Bill shall be deemed to have been passed by both <5>Houses with the amendments recommended by the Legislative Council and <5>accepted by the Legislative Assembly. <6>4.<5> If the Legislative Assembly does not accept any of the recommendations of the <5>Legislative Council, the Money Bill shall be deemed to have been passed by both <5>Houses in the form in which it was passed by the Legislative Assembly without <5>any of the amendments recommended by the Legislative Council. <6>5.<5> If a Money Bill passed by the Legislative Assembly and transmitted to the <5>Legislative Council for its recommendations is not returned to the Legislative <5>Assembly within the said period of fourteen days, it shall be deemed to have <5>been passed by both Houses at the expiration of the said period in the form in <5>which it was passed by the Legislative Assembly. <7>199. Definition of "Money Bills <6>1.<5> For the purposes of this Chapter, a Bill shall be deemed to be a Money Bill if it <5>contains only provisions dealing with all or any of the following matters, <5>namely:- <6>a.<5> the imposition, abolition, remission, alteration or regulation of any tax; <6>b.<5> the regulation of the borrowing of money or the giving of any guarantee by <5>the State, or the amendment of the law with respect to any financial <5>obligations undertaken or to be undertaken by the State; <6>c. <5>the custody of the Consolidated Fund or the Contingency Fund of the State, <5>the payment of moneys into or the withdrawal of moneys from any such <5>Fund; <6>d.<5> the appropriation of moneys out of the Consolidated Fund of the State; <6>e.<5> the declaring of any expenditure to be expenditure charged on the <5>Consolidated Fund of the State, or the increasing of the amount of any such <5>expenditure; <6>f. <5>the receipt of money on account of the Consolidated Fund of the State or <5>the public account of the State or the custody or issue of such money; or <6>g.<5> any matter incidental to any of the matters specified in sub-clauses (a)to (f). <6>2.<5> A Bill shall not be deemed to be a Money Bill by reason only that it provides for <5>the imposition of fines or other pecuniary penalties, or for the demand or <5>payment of fees for licences or fees for services rendered, or by reason that it <5>provides for the imposition, abolition, remission, alteration or regulation of any <5>tax by any local authority or body for local purposes. <6>3.<5> If any question arises whether a Bill introduced in the Legislature of a State <5>which has a Legislative Council is a Money Bill or not, the decision of the Speaker <5>of the Legislative Assembly of such State thereon shall be final. <6>4.<5> There shall be endorsed on every Money Bill when it is transmitted to the <5>Legislative Council under article 198, and when it is presented to the Governor <5>for assent under article 200, the certificate of the Speaker of the Legislative <5>Assembly signed by him that it is a Money Bill. <7>200. Assent to Bills <5>When a Bill has been passed by the Legislative Assembly of a State or, in the case of a <5>State having a Legislative Council, has been passed by both Houses of the Legislature <5>of the State, it shall be presented to the Governor and the Governor shall declare <5>either that he assents to the Bill or that he withholds assent therefrom or that he <5>reserves the Bill for the consideration of the President: <5>Provided that the Governor may, as soon as possible after the presentation to him of <5>the Bill for assent, return the Bill if it is not a Money Bill together with a message <5>requesting that the House or Houses will reconsider the Bill or any specified <5>provisions thereof and, in particular, will consider the desirability of introducing any <5>such amendments as he may recommend in his message and, when a Bill is so <5>returned, the House or Houses shall reconsider the Bill accordingly, and if the Bill is <5>passed again by the House or Houses with or without amendment and presented to <5>the Governor for assent, the Governor shall not withhold assent therefrom: <5>Provided further that the Governor shall not assent to, but shall reserve for the <5>consideration of the President, any Bill which in the opinion of the Governor would, <5>if it became law, so derogate from the powers of the High Court as to endanger the <5>position which that Court is by this Constitution designed to fill. <7>201. Bills reserved for consideration <5>When a Bill is reserved by a Governor for the consideration of the President, the <5>President shall declare either that he assents to the Bill or that he withholds assent <5>therefrom: <5>Provided that, where the Bill is not a Money Bill, the President may direct the <5>Governor to return the Bill to the House or, as the case may be, the Houses of the <5>Legislature of the State together with such a message as is mentioned in the first <5>proviso to article 200 and, when a Bill is so returned, the House or Houses shall <5>reconsider it accordingly within a period of six months from the date of receipt of <5>such message and, if it is again passed by the House or Houses with or without <5>amendment, it shall be presented again to the President for his consideration. <7>Procedure in Financial Matters <7>202. Annual financial statement <6>1. <5>The Governor shall in respect of every financial year cause to be laid before the <5>House or Houses of the Legislature of the State a statement of the estimated <5>receipts and expenditure of the State for that year, in this Part referred to as the <5>"annual financial statement". <6>2. <5>The estimates of expenditure embodied in the annual financial statement shall <5>show separately- <6>a.<5> the sums required to meet expenditure described by this Constitution as <5>expenditure charged upon the Consolidated Fund of the State; and <6>b.<5> the sums required to meet other expenditure proposed to be made from <5>the Consolidated Fund of the State, <5>and shall distinguish expenditure on revenue account from other expenditure. <6>3. <5>The following expenditure shall be expenditure charged on the Consolidated <5>Fund of each State- <6>a.<5> the emoluments and allowances of the Governor and other expenditure <5>relating to his office; <6>b.<5> the salaries and allowances of the Speaker and the Deputy Speaker of the <5>Legislative Assembly and, in the case of State having a Legislative Council, <5>also of the Chairman and the Deputy Chairman of the Legislative Council; <6>c. <5>debt charges for which the State is liable including interest, sinking fund <5>charges and redemption charges, and other expenditure relating to the <5>raising of loans and the service and redemption of debt; <6>d.<5> expenditure in respect of the salaries and allowances of Judges of any High <5>Court; <6>e.<5> any sums required to satisfy any judgment, decree or award of any court or <5>arbitral tribunal; <6>f. <5>any other expenditure declared by this Constitution, or by the Legislature <5>of the State by law, to be so charged. <7>203. Procedure in Legislature with respect to estimates <6>1.<5> So much of the estimates as relates to expenditure charged upon the <5>Consolidated Fund of a State shall not be submitted to the vote of the <5>Legislative Assembly, but nothing in this clause shall be construed as preventing <5>the discussion in the Legislature of any of those estimates. <6>2.<5> So much of the said estimates as relates to other expenditure shall be submitted <5>in the form of demands for grants to the Legislative Assembly, and the <5>Legislative Assembly shall have power to assent, or to refuse to assent, to any <5>demand, or to assent to any demand subject to a reduction of the amount <5>specified therein. <6>3.<5> No demand for a grant shall be made except on the recommendation of the <5>Governor. <7>204. Appropriation Bills <6>1.<5> As soon as may be after the grants under article 203 have been made by the <5>Assembly, there shall be introduced a Bill to provide for the appropriation out of <5>the Consolidated Fund of the State of all moneys required to meet- <6>a.<5> the grants so made by the Assembly; and <6>b.<5> the expenditure charged on the Consolidated Fund of the State but not <5>exceeding in any case the amount shown in the statement previously laid <5>before the House or Houses. <6>2.<5> No amendment shall be proposed to any such Bill in the House or either House <5>of the Legislature of the State which will have the effect of varying the amount <5>or altering the destination of any grant so made or of varying the amount of any <5>expenditure charged on the Consolidated Fund of the State, and the decision of <5>the person presiding as to whether an amendment is inadmissible under this <5>clause shall be final. <6>3.<5> Subject to the provisions of articles 205 and 206, no money shall be withdrawn <5>from the Consolidated Fund of the State except under appropriation made by <5>law passed in accordance with the provisions of this article. <7>205. Supplementary, additional or excess grants <6>1.<5> The Governor shall- <6>a.<5> if the amount authorised by any law made in accordance with the <5>provisions of article 204 to be expended for a particular service for the <5>current financial year is found to be insufficient for the purposes of that <5>year or when a need has arisen during the current financial year for <5>supplementary or additional expenditure upon some new service not <5>contemplated in the annual financial statement for that year, or <6>b.<5> if any money has been spent on any service during a financial year in excess <5>of the amount granted for that service and for that year, <5>cause to be laid before the House or the Houses of the Legislature of the State <5>another statement showing the estimated amount of that expenditure or cause <5>to be presented to the Legislative Assembly of the State a demand for such <5>excess, as the case may be. <6>2.<5> The provisions of articles 202, 203 and 204 shall have effect in relation to any <5>such statement and expenditure or demand and also to any law to be made <5>authorising the appropriation of moneys out of the Consolidated Fund of the <5>State to meet such expenditure or the grant in respect of such demand as they <5>have effect in relation to the annual financial statement and the expenditure <5>mentioned therein or to a demand for a grant and the law to be made for the <5>authorisation of appropriation of moneys out of the Consolidated Fund of the <5>State to meet such expenditure or grant. <7>206. Votes on account, votes of credit and exceptional <7>grants <6>1. <5>Notwithstanding anything in the foregoing provisions of this Chapter, the <5>Legislative Assembly of a State shall have power- <6>a.<5> to make any grant in advance in respect of the estimated expenditure for a <5>part of any financial year pending the completion of the procedure <5>prescribed in article 203 for the voting of such grant and the passing of the <5>law in accordance with the provisions of article 204 in relation to that <5>expenditure; <6>b.<5> to make a grant for meeting an unexpected demand upon the resources of <5>the State when on account of the magnitude or the indefinite character of <5>the service the demand cannot be stated with the details ordinarily given in <5>an annual financial statement; <6>c. <5>to make an exceptional grant which forms no part of the current service of <5>any financial year, <5>and the Legislature of the State shall have power to authorise by law the <5>withdrawal of moneys from the Consolidated Fund of the State for the purposes <5>for which the said grants are made. <6>2. <5>The provisions of articles 203 and 204 shall have effect in relation to the making <5>of any grant under clause (1) and to any law to be made under that clause as they <5>have effect in relation to the making of a grant with regard to any expenditure <5>mentioned in the annual financial statement and the law to be made for the <5>authorisation of appropriation of moneys out of the Consolidated Fund of the <5>state to meet such expenditure. <7>207. Special provisions as to financial Bills <6>1.<5> A Bill or amendment making provision for any of the matters specified in <5>sub-clauses (a) to (f) of clause (1) of article 199 shall not be introduced or moved <5>except on the recommendation of the Governor, and a Bill making such <5>provision shall not be introduced in a Legislative Council: <5>Provided that no recommendation shall be required under this clause for the <5>moving of an amendment making provision for the reduction or abolition of any <5>tax. <6>2.<5> A Bill or amendment shall not be deemed to make provision for any of the <5>matters aforesaid by reason only that it provides for the imposition of fines or <5>other pecuniary penalties, or for the demand or payment of fees for licences or <5>fees for services rendered, or by reason that it provides for the imposition, <5>abolition, remission, alteration or regulation of any tax by any local authority or <5>body for local purposes. <6>3.<5> A Bill which, if enacted and brought into operation, would involve expenditure <5>from the Consolidated Fund of a State shall not be passed by a House of the <5>Legislature of the State unless the Governor has recommended to that House <5>the consideration of the Bill. <7>Procedure Generally <7>208. Rules of procedure <6>1.<5> A House of the Legislature of a State may make rules for regulating, subject to <5>the provisions of this Constitution, its procedure and the conduct of its business. <6>2.<5> Until rules are made under clause (1), the rules of procedure and standing orders <5>in force immediately before the commencement of this Constitution with <5>respect to the Legislature for the corresponding Province shall have effect in <5>relation to the Legislature of the State subject to such modifications and <5>adaptations as may be made therein by the Speaker of the Legislative Assembly, <5>or the Chairman of the Legislative Council, as the case may be. <6>3.<5> In a State having a Legislative Council the Governor, after consultation with the <5>Speaker of the Legislative Assembly and the Chairman of the Legislative <5>Council, may make rules as to the procedure with respect to communications <5>between the two Houses. <7>209. Regulation by law of procedure in the Legislature of <7>the State in relation to financial business <5>The Legislature of a State may, for the purpose of the timely completion of financial <5>business, regulate by law the procedure of, and the conduct of business in, the House <5>or Houses of the Legislature of the State in relation to any financial matter or to any <5>Bill for the appropriation of moneys out of the Consolidated Fund of the State, and, if <5>and so far as any provision of any law so made is inconsistent with any rule made by <5>the House or either House of the Legislature of the State under clause (1) of article <5>208 or with any rule or standing order having effect in relation to the Legislature of <5>the State under clause (2) of that article, such provision shall prevail. <7>210. Language to be used in the Legislature <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in Part XVII, but subject to the provisions of article <5>348, business in the Legislature of a State shall be transacted in the official <5>language or languages of the State or in Hindi or in English: <5>Provided that the Speaker of the Legislative Assembly or Chairman of the <5>Legislative Council, or person acting as such, as the case may be, may permit any <5>member who cannot adequately express himself in any of the languages <5>aforesaid to address the House in his mother-tongue. <6>2.<5> Unless the Legislature of the State by law otherwise provides, this article shall, <5>after the expiration of a period of fifteen years from the commencement of this <5>Constitution, have effect as if the words "or in English" were omitted therefrom: <5>Provided that in relation to the Legislatures of the States of Himachal Pradesh, <5>Manipur, Meghalaya and Tripura this clause shall have effect as if for the words <5>"fifteen years" occurring therein, the words "twenty-five years" were <5>substituted: <5>Provided further that in relation to the Legislature of the States of Arunachal <5>Pradesh, Goa and Mizoram, this clause shall have effect as if for the words <5>"fifteen years" occurring therein, the words "forty years" were substituted. <7>211. Restriction on discussion in the Legislature <5>No discussion shall take place in the Legislature of a State with respect to the <5>conduct of any Judge of the Supreme Court or of a High Court in the discharge of his <5>duties. <7>212. Courts not to inquire into proceedings of the <7>Legislature <6>1.<5> The validity of any proceedings in the Legislature of a State shall not be called in <5>question on the ground of any alleged irregularity of procedure. <6>2.<5> No officer or member of the Legislature of a State in whom powers are vested by <5>or under this Constitution for regulating procedure or the conduct of business, <5>or for maintaining order, in the Legislature shall be subject to the jurisdiction of <5>any court in respect of the exercise by him of those powers. <4>• Subsidiary unit government <7>CHAPTER IV: LEGISLATIVE POWER OF THE GOVERNOR <7>213. Power of Governor to promulgate Ordinances during <7>recess of Legislature <6>1. <5>If at any time, except when the Legislative Assembly of a State is in session, or <5>where there is a Legislative Council in a State, except when both Houses of the <5>Legislature are in session, the Governor is satisfied that circumstances exist <5>which render it necessary for him to take immediate action, he may promulgate <5>such Ordinances as the circumstances appear to him to require: <5>Provided that the Governor shall not, without instructions from the President, <5>promulgate any such Ordinance if- <6>a.<5> a Bill containing the same provisions would under this Constitution have <5>required the previous sanction of the President for the introduction <5>thereof into the Legislature; or <6>b.<5> he would have deemed it necessary to reserve a Bill containing the same <5>provisions for the consideration of the President; or <6>c. <5>an Act of the Legislature of the State containing the same provisions would <5>under this Constitution have been invalid unless, having been reserved for <5>the consideration of the President, it had received the assent of the <5>President. <6>2. <5>An Ordinance promulgated under this article shall have the same force and <5>effect as an Act of the Legislature of the state assented to by the Governor, but <5>every such Ordinance- <6>a.<5> shall be laid before the Legislative Assembly of the State, or where there is <5>a Legislative Council in the State, before both the Houses, and shall cease to <5>operate at the expiration of six weeks from the reassembly of the <5>Legislature, or if before the expiration of that period a resolution <5>disapproving it is passed by the Legislative Assembly and agreed to by the <5>Legislative Council, if any, upon the passing of the resolution or, as the case <5>may be, on the resolution being agreed to by the Council; and <6>b.<5> may be withdrawn at any time by the Governor. <7>Explanation <5>Where the Houses of the Legislature of a State having a Legislative Council are <5>summoned to reassemble on different dates, the period of six weeks shall be <5>reckoned from the later of those dates for the purposes of this clause. <6>3.<5> If and so far as an Ordinance under this article makes any provision which would <5>not be valid if enacted in an Act of the Legislature of the State assented to by the <5>Governor, it shall be void: <5>Provided that, for the purposes of the provisions of this Constitution relating to <5>the effect of an Act of the Legislature of a State which is repugnant to an Act of <5>Parliament or an existing law with respect to a matter enumerated in the <5>Concurrent List, an Ordinance promulgated under this article in pursuance of <5>instructions from the President shall be deemed to be an Act of the Legislature <5>of the State which has been reserved for the consideration of the President and <5>assented to by him. <7>CHAPTER V: THE HIGH COURTS IN THE STATES <4>• Structure of the courts <7>214. High Courts for States <5>There shall be a High Court for each State. <7>215. High Courts to be courts of record <5>Every High Court shall be a court of record and shall have all the powers of such a <5>court including the power to punish for contempt of itself. <7>216. Constitution of High Courts <5>Every High Court shall consist of a Chief Justice and such other Judges as the <5>President may from time to time deem it necessary to appoint. <7>217. Appointment and conditions of the office of a Judge of <4>• Supreme/ordinary court judge removal <4>• Ordinary court selection <7>a High Court <4>• Mandatory retirement age for judges <6>1.<5> Every Judge of a High Court shall be appointed by the President by warrant <4>• Ordinary court term length <5>under his hand and seal on the recommendation of the National Judicial <5>Appointments Commission referred to in article 124A, and shall hold office, in <5>the case of an additional or acting Judge, as provided in article 224, and in any <5>other case, until he attains the age of sixty-two years: <5>Provided that- <6>a.<5> a Judge may, by writing under his hand addressed to the President, resign <5>his office; <6>b.<5> a Judge may be removed from his office by the President in the manner <5>provided in clause (4) of article 124 for the removal of a Judge of the <5>Supreme Court; <6>c. <5>the office of a Judge shall be vacated by his being appointed by the <5>President to be a Judge of the Supreme Court or by his being transferred by <5>the President to any other High Court within the territory of India. <4>• Eligibility for ordinary court judges <6>2.<5> A person shall not be qualified for appointment as a Judge of a High Court unless <5>he is a citizen of India and- <6>a.<5> has for at least ten years held a judicial office in the territory of India; or <6>b.<5> has for at least ten years been an advocate of a High Court or of two or <5>more such Courts in succession; <7>Explanation <5>For the purposes of this clause- <6>a.<5> in computing the period during which a person has held judicial office in the <5>territory of India, there shall be included any period, after he has held any <5>judicial office, during which the person has been an advocate of a High <5>Court or has held the office of a member of a tribunal or any post, under the <5>Union or a State, requiring special knowledge of law; <6>aa.<5> in computing the period during which a person has been an advocate of a <5>High Court, there shall be included any period during which the person has <5>held judicial office or the office of a member of a tribunal or any post, under <5>the Union or a State, requiring special knowledge of law after he became an <5>advocate; <6>b.<5> in computing the period during which a person has held judicial office in the <5>territory of India or been an advocate of a High Court, there shall be <5>included any period before the commencement of this Constitution during <5>which he has held judicial office in any area which was comprised before <5>the fifteenth day of August, <5>1947, within India as defined by the <5>Government of India Act, 1935, or has been an advocate of any High Court <5>in any such area, as the case may be. <6>3.<5> If any question arises as to the age of a Judge of a High Court, the question shall <5>be decided by the President after consultation with the Chief Justice of India <5>and the decision of the President shall be final. <7>218. Application of certain provisions relating to Supreme <7>Court to High Courts <5>The provisions of clauses (4) and (5) of article 124 shall apply in relation to a High <5>Court as they apply in relation to the Supreme Court with the substitution of <5>references to the High Court for references to the Supreme Court. <4>• Oaths to abide by constitution <7>219. Oath or affirmation by Judges of High Courts <5>Every person appointed to be a Judge of a High Court shall, before he enters upon <5>his office, make and subscribe before the Governor of the State, or some person <5>appointed in that behalf by him, an oath or affirmation according to the form set out <5>for the purpose in the Third Schedule. <7>220. Restriction on practice after being a permanent Judge <5>No person who, after the commencement of this Constitution, has held office as a <5>permanent Judge of a High Court shall plead or act in any court or before any <5>authority in India except the Supreme Court and the other High Courts. <7>Explanation <5>In this article, the expression "High Court" does not include a High Court for a State <5>specified in Part B of the First Schedule as it existed before the commencement of <5>the Constitution (Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956. <4>• Protection of judges' salaries <7>221. Salaries, etc., of Judges <6>1.<5> There shall be paid to the Judges of each High Court such salaries as may be <5>determined by Parliament by law and, until provision in that behalf is so made, <5>such salaries as are specified in the Second Schedule. <6>2.<5> Every Judge shall be entitled to such allowances and to such rights in respect of <5>leave of absence and pension as may from time to time be determined by or <5>under law made by Parliament and, until so determined, to such allowances and <5>rights as are specified in the Second Schedule: <5>Provided that neither the allowances of a Judge nor his rights in respect of leave <5>of absence or pension shall be varied to his disadvantage after his appointment. <7>222. Transfer of a Judge from one High Court to another <6>1.<5> The President may, on the recommendation of the National Judicial <5>Appointments Commission referred to in article 124A, transfer a Judge from <5>one High Court to any other High Court. <6>2.<5> When a Judge has been or is so transferred, he shall, during the period he serves, <5>after the commencement of the Constitution (Fifteenth Amendment) Act, 1963, <5>as a Judge of the other High Court, be entitled to receive in addition to his salary <5>such compensatory allowance as may be determined by Parliament by law and, <5>until so determined, such compensatory allowance as the President may by <5>order fix. <7>223. Appointment of acting Chief Justice <5>When the office of Chief Justice of a High Court is vacant or when any such Chief <5>Justice is by reason of absence or otherwise, unable to perform the duties of his <5>office, the duties of the office shall be performed by such one of the other Judges of <5>the Court as the President may appoint for the purpose. <4>• Ordinary court selection <7>224. Appointment of additional and acting Judges <6>1.<5> If by reason of any temporary increase in the business of a High Court or by <5>reason of arrears of work therein, it appears to the President that the number of <5>the Judges of that Court should be for the time being increased, the President <5>may, in consultation with the National Judicial Appointments Commission, <5>appoint duly qualified persons to be additional Judges of the Court for such <5>period not exceeding two years as he may specify. <6>2.<5> When any Judge of a High Court other than the Chief Justice is by reason of <5>absence or for any other reason unable to perform the duties of his office or is <5>appointed to act temporarily as Chief Justice, the President may, in consultation <5>with the National Judicial Appointments Commission, appoint a duly qualified <5>person to act as a Judge of that Court until the permanent Judge has resumed <5>his duties. <6>3.<5> No person appointed as an additional or acting Judge of a High Court shall hold <5>office after attaining the age of sixty-two years. <7>224A. Appointment of retired Judges at sittings of High <4>• Establishment of judicial council <7>Courts <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Chapter, the National Judicial Appointments <5>Commission on a reference made to it by the Chief Justice of a High Court for any <5>State, may with the previous consent of the President, request any person who has <5>held the office of a Judge of that Court or of any other High Court to sit and act as a <5>Judge of the High Court for that State, and every such person so requested shall, <5>while so sitting and acting, be entitled to such allowances as the President may by <5>order determine and have all the jurisdiction, powers and privileges of, but shall not <5>otherwise be deemed to be, a Judge of that High Court: <5>Provided that nothing in this article shall be deemed to require any such person as <5>aforesaid to sit and act as a Judge of that High Court unless he consents so to do. <7>225. Jurisdiction of existing High Courts <5>Subject to the provisions of this Constitution and to the provisions of any law of the <5>appropriate Legislature made by virtue of powers conferred on that Legislature by <5>this Constitution, the jurisdiction of, and the law administered in, any existing High <5>Court, and the respective powers of the Judges thereof in relation to the <5>administration of justice in the Court, including any power to make rules of Court <5>and to regulate the sittings of the Court and of members thereof sitting alone or in <5>Division Courts, shall be the same as immediately before the commencement of this <5>Constitution: <5>Provided that any restriction to which the exercise of original jurisdiction by any of <5>the High Courts with respect to any matter concerning the revenue or concerning <5>any act ordered or done in the collection thereof was subject immediately before the <5>commencement of this Constitution shall no longer apply to the exercise of such <5>jurisdiction. <7>226. Power of High Courts to issue certain writs <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in article 32, every High Court shall have power, <5>throughout the territories in relation to which it exercises jurisdiction, to issue <5>to any person or authority, including in appropriate cases, any Government, <5>within those territories directions, orders or writs, including writs in the nature <5>of habeas corpus, mandamus, prohibition, quo warranto and certiorari, or any of <5>them, for the enforcement of any of the rights conferred by Part III and for any <5>other purpose. <6>2.<5> The power conferred by clause (1) to issue directions, orders or writs to any <5>Government, authority or person may also be exercised by any High Court <5>exercising jurisdiction in relation to the territories within which the cause of <5>action, wholly or in part, arises for the exercise of such power, notwithstanding <5>that the seat of such Government or authority or the residence of such person is <5>not within those territories. <6>3.<5> Where any party against whom an interim order, whether by way of injunction <5>or stay or in any other manner, is made on, or in any proceedings relating to, a <5>petition under clause (1), without- <6>a.<5> furnishing to such party copies of such petition and all documents in <5>support of the plea for such interim order; and <6>b.<5> giving such party an opportunity of being heard, <5>makes an application to the High Court for the vacation of such order and <5>furnishes a copy of such application to the party in whose favour such order has <5>been made or the counsel of such party, the High Court shall dispose of the <5>application within a period of two weeks from the date on which it is received or <5>from the date on which the copy of such application is so furnished, whichever is <5>later, or where the High Court is closed on the last day of that period, before the <5>expiry of the next day afterwards on which the High Court is open; and if the <5>application is not so disposed of, the interim order shall, on the expiry of that <5>period, or, as the case may be, the expiry of the said next day, stand vacated. <6>4.<5> The power conferred on a High Court by this article shall not be in derogation of <5>the power conferred on the Supreme Court by clause (2) of article 32. <7>226A. Constitutional validity of Central laws not to be <7>considered in proceedings under article 226 <5>Rep. by the Constitution (Forty-third Amendment) Act, 1977, s.8 (w.e.f. 13-4-1978). <7>227. Power of superintendence over all courts by the High <7>Court <6>1.<5> Every High Court shall have superintendence over all courts and tribunals <5>throughout the territories in relation to which it exercises jurisdiction. <6>2.<5> Without prejudice to the generality of the foregoing provision, the High Court <5>may- <6>a.<5> call for returns from such courts; <6>b.<5> make and issue general rules and prescribe forms for regulating the <5>practice and proceedings of such courts; and <6>c. <5>prescribe forms in which books, entries and accounts shall be kept by the <5>officers of any such courts. <6>3.<5> The High Court may also settle tables of fees to be allowed to the sheriff and all <5>clerks and officers of such courts and to attorneys, advocates and pleaders <5>practising therein: <5>Provided that any rules made, forms prescribed or tables settled under clause <5>(2) or clause <6>3.<5> shall not be inconsistent with the provision of any law for the time being in force, <5>and shall require the previous approval of the Governor. <4>• Establishment of administrative courts <6>4.<5> Nothing in this article shall be deemed to confer on a High Court powers of <4>• Establishment of military courts <5>superintendence over any court or tribunal constituted by or under any law <5>relating to the Armed Forces. <7>228. Transfer of certain cases to High Court <5>If the High Court is satisfied that a case pending in a court subordinate to it involves <5>a substantial question of law as to the interpretation of this Constitution the <5>determination of which is necessary for the disposal of the case, it shall withdraw the <5>case and may- <6>a.<5> either dispose of the case itself, or <6>b.<5> determine the said question of law and return the case to the court from <5>which the case has been so withdrawn together with a copy of its judgment <5>on such question, and the said court shall on receipt thereof proceed to <5>dispose of the case in conformity with such judgment. <7>228A. Special provisions as to disposal of questions <7>relating to constitutional validity of State laws <5>Rep. by the Constitution <5>(Forty-third Amendment) Act, <5>1977, s. <5>10 (w.e.f. <5>13-4-1978). <7>229. Officers and servants and the expenses of High Courts <6>1.<5> Appointments of officers and servants of a High Court shall be made by the <5>Chief Justice of the Court or such other Judge or officer of the Court as he may <5>direct: <5>Provided that the Governor of the State may by rule require that in such cases <5>as may be specified in the rule no person not already attached to the Court shall <5>be appointed to any office connected with the Court save after consultation <5>with the State Public Service Commission. <6>2.<5> Subject to the provisions of any law made by the Legislature of the State, the <5>conditions of service of officers and servants of a High Court shall be such as <5>may be prescribed by rules made by the Chief Justice of the Court or by some <5>other Judge or officer of the Court authorised by the Chief Justice to make rules <5>for the purpose: <5>Provided that the rules made under this clause shall, so far as they relate to <5>salaries, allowances, leave or pensions, require the approval of the Governor of <5>the State. <6>3.<5> The administrative expenses of a High Court, including all salaries, allowances <5>and pensions payable to or in respect of the officers and servants of the Court, <5>shall be charged upon the Consolidated Fund of the State, and any fees or other <5>moneys taken by the Court shall form part of that Fund. <7>230. Extension of jurisdiction of High Courts to Union <7>territories <6>1.<5> Parliament may by law extend the jurisdiction of a High Court to, or exclude the <5>jurisdiction of a High Court from, any Union territory. <6>2.<5> Where the High Court of a State exercises jurisdiction in relation to a Union <5>territory,- <6>a.<5> nothing in this Constitution shall be construed as empowering the <5>Legislature of the State to increase, restrict or abolish that jurisdiction; and <6>b.<5> the reference in article 227 to the Governor shall, in relation to any rules, <5>forms or tables for subordinate courts in that territory, be construed as a <5>reference to the president. <7>231. Establishment of a common High Court for two or <7>more States <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything contained in the preceding provisions of this Chapter, <5>Parliament may by law establish a common High Court for two or more States or <5>for two or more States and a Union territory. <6>2.<5> In relation to any such High Court,- <6>a. <5>[omitted by the Constitution (Ninety-ninth Amendment) Act, 2014] <6>b.<5> the reference in article 227 to the Governor shall, in relation to any rules, <5>forms or tables for subordinate courts, be construed as a reference to the <5>Governor of the State in which the subordinate courts are situate; and <6>c. <5>the references in articles 219 and 229 to the State shall be construed as a <5>reference to the State in which the High Court has its principal seat: <5>Provided that if such principal seat is in a Union territory, the references in <5>articles <5>219 and 229 to the Governor, Public Service Commission, <5>Legislature and Consolidated Fund of the State shall be construed <5>respectively as references to the President, Union Public Service <5>Commission, Parliament and Consolidated Fund of India. <7>CHAPTER VI: SUBORDINATE COURTS <4>• Structure of the courts <7>233. Appointment of district judges <4>• Ordinary court selection <6>1.<5> Appointments of persons to be, and the posting and promotion of, district judges <5>in any State shall be made by the Governor of the State in consultation with the <5>High Court exercising jurisdiction in relation to such State. <4>• Eligibility for ordinary court judges <6>2.<5> A person not already in the service of the Union or of the State shall only be <5>eligible to be appointed a district judge if he has been for not less than seven <5>years an advocate or a pleader and is recommended by the High Court for <5>appointment. <7>233A. Validation of appointments of, and judgments, etc., <7>delivered by, certain district judges <5>Notwithstanding any judgment, decree or order of any court,- <6>a. <6>i. <5>no appointment of any person already in the judicial service of a State <5>or of any person who has been for not less than seven years an <5>advocate or a pleader, to be a district judge in that State, and <6>ii. <5>no posting, promotion or transfer of any such person as a district judge, <5>made at any time before the commencement of the Constitution <5>(Twentieth Amendment) Act, 1966, otherwise than in accordance with <5>the provisions of article 233 or article 235 shall be deemed to be illegal <5>or void or ever to have become illegal or void by reason only of the fact <5>that such appointment, posting, promotion or transfer was not made in <5>accordance with the said provisions: <6>b.<5> no jurisdiction exercised, no judgment, decree, sentence or order passed or <5>made, and no other act or proceeding done or taken, before the <5>commencement of the Constitution (Twentieth Amendment) Act, 1966 by, <5>or before, any person appointed, posted, promoted or transferred as a <5>district judge in any State otherwise than in accordance with the provisions <5>of article 233 or article 235 shall be deemed to be illegal or invalid or ever <5>to have become illegal or invalid by reason only of the fact that such <5>appointment, posting, promotion or transfer was not made in accordance <5>with the said provisions. <7>234. Recruitment of persons other than district judges to <7>the judicial service <5>Appointments of persons other than district judges to the judicial service of a State <5>shall be made by the Governor of the State in accordance with rules made by him in <5>that behalf after consultation with the State Public Service Commission and with the <5>High Court exercising jurisdiction in relation to such State. <4>• Structure of the courts <7>235. Control over subordinate courts <5>The control over district courts and courts subordinate thereto including the posting <5>and promotion of, and the grant of leave to, persons belonging to the judicial service <5>of a State and holding any post inferior to the post of district judge shall be vested in <5>the High Court, but nothing in this article shall be construed as taking away from any <5>such person any right of appeal which he may have under the law regulating the <5>conditions of his service or as authorising the High Court to deal with him otherwise <5>than in accordance with the conditions of his service prescribed under such law. <7>236. Interpretation <5>In this Chapter- <6>a.<5> the expression "district judge" includes judge of a city civil court, additional <5>district judge, joint district judge, assistant district judge, chief judge of a <5>small cause court, chief presidency magistrate, additional chief presidency <5>magistrate, sessions judge, additional sessions judge and assistant sessions <5>judge; <6>b.<5> the expression "judicial service" means a service consisting exclusively of <5>persons intended to fill the post of district judge and other civil judicial <5>posts inferior to the post of district judge. <7>237. Application of the provisions of this Chapter to <7>certain class or classes of magistrates <5>The Governor may by public notification direct that the foregoing provisions of this <5>Chapter and any rules made thereunder shall with effect from such date as may be <5>fixed by him in that behalf apply in relation to any class or classes of magistrates in <5>the State as they apply in relation to persons appointed to the judicial service of the <5>State subject to such exceptions and modifications as may be specified in the <5>notification. <9>PART VII: The States in Part B of the First <9>Schedule <5>Rep. by the Constitution (Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956, s. 29 and Sch. <9>PART VIII: THE UNION TERRITORIES <7>239. Administration of Union territories <6>1.<5> Save as otherwise provided by Parliament by law, every Union territory shall be <5>administered by the President acting, to such extent as he thinks fit, through an <5>administrator to be appointed by him with such designation as he may specify. <6>2.<5> Notwithstanding anything contained in Part VI, the President may appoint the <5>Governor of a State as the administrator of an adjoining Union territory, and <5>where a Governor is so appointed, he shall exercise his functions as such <5>administrator independently of his Council of Ministers. <7>239A. Creation of local Legislatures or Council of Ministers <7>or both for certain Union territories <6>1.<5> Parliament may by law create for the Union territory of Pondicherry- <6>a.<5> a body, whether elected or partly nominated and partly elected, to function <5>as a Legislature for the Union territory, or <6>b.<5> a Council of Ministers, <5>or both with such constitution, powers and functions, in each case, as may be <5>specified in the law. <6>2.<5> Any such law as is referred to in clause (1) shall not be deemed to be an <5>amendment of this Constitution for the purposes of article 368 notwithstanding <5>that it contains any provision which amends or has the effect of amending this <5>Constitution. <4>• National capital <7>239AA. Special provisions with respect to Delhi <6>1. <5>As from the date of commencement of the Constitution <5>(Sixty-ninth <5>Amendment) Act, 1991, the Union territory of Delhi shall be called the National <5>Capital Territory of Delhi (hereafter in this Part referred to as the National <5>Capital Territory) and the administrator thereof appointed under article 239 <5>shall be designated as the Lieutenant Governor. <6>2. <6>a. <5>There shall be a Legislative Assembly for the National Capital Territory and <5>the seats in such Assembly shall be filled by members chosen by direct <5>election from territorial constituencies in the National Capital Territory. <6>b. <5>The total number of seats in the Legislative Assembly, the number of seats <5>reserved for Scheduled Castes, the division of the National Capital <5>Territory into territorial constituencies <5>(including the basis for such <5>division) and all other matters relating to the functioning of the Legislative <5>Assembly shall be regulated by law made by Parliament. <6>c. <5>The provisions of articles 324 to 327 and 329 shall apply in relation to the <5>National Capital Territory, the Legislative Assembly of the National Capital <5>Territory and the members thereof as they apply, in relation to a State, the <5>Legislative Assembly of a State and the members thereof respectively; and <5>any reference in articles 326 and 329 to "appropriate Legislature" shall be <5>deemed to be a reference to Parliament. <6>3. <6>a. <5>Subject to the provisions of this Constitution, the Legislative Assembly shall <5>have power to make laws for the whole or any part of the National Capital <5>Territory with respect to any of the matters enumerated in the State List or <5>in the Concurrent List in so far as any such matter is applicable to Union <5>territories except matters with respect to Entries 1, 2 and 18 of the State <5>List and Entries 64,65 and 66 of that List in so far as they relate to the said <5>Entries 1, 2, and 18. <6>b. <5>Nothing in sub-clause (a) shall derogate from the powers of Parliament <5>under this Constitution to make laws with respect to any matter for a Union <5>territory or any part thereof. <6>c. <5>If any provision of a law made by the Legislative Assembly with respect to <5>any matter is repugnant to any provision of a law made by Parliament with <5>respect to that matter, whether passed before or after the law made by the <5>Legislative Assembly, or of an earlier law, other than a law made by the <5>Legislative Assembly, then, in either case, the law made by Parliament, or, <5>as the case may be, such earlier law, shall prevail and the law made by the <5>Legislative Assembly shall, to the extent of the repugnancy, be void: <5>Provided that if any such law made by the Legislative Assembly has been <5>reserved for the consideration of the President and has received his assent, <5>such law shall prevail in the National Capital Territory: <5>Provided further that nothing in this sub-clause shall prevent Parliament <5>from enacting at any time any law with respect to the same matter <5>including a law adding to, amending, varying or repealing the law so made <5>by the Legislative Assembly. <6>4. <5>There shall be a Council of Ministers consisting of not more than ten per cent, of <5>the total number of members in the Legislative Assembly, with the Chief <5>Minister at the head to aid and advise the Lieutenant Governor in the exercise of <5>his functions in relation to matters with respect to which the Legislative <5>Assembly has power to make laws, except in so far as he is, by or under any law, <5>required to act in his discretion: <5>Provided that in the case of difference of opinion between the Lieutenant <5>Governor and his Ministers on any matter, the Lieutenant Governor shall refer it <5>to the President for decision and act according to the decision given thereon by <5>the President and pending such decision it shall be competent for the Lieutenant <5>Governor in any case where the matter, in his opinion, is so urgent that it is <5>necessary for him to take immediate action, to take such action or to give such <5>direction in the matter as he deems necessary. <6>5. <5>The Chief Minister shall be appointed by the President and the other Ministers <5>shall be appointed by the President on the advice of the Chief Minister and the <5>Ministers shall hold office during the pleasure of the President. <6>6. <5>The Council of Ministers shall be collectively responsible to the Legislative <5>Assembly. <6>7. <6>a.<5> Parliament may, by law, make provisions for giving effect to, or <5>supplementing the provisions contained in the foregoing clauses and for all <5>matters incidental or consequential thereto. <6>b.<5> Any such law as is referred to in sub-clause (a) shall not be deemed to be an <5>amendment of this Constitution for the purposes of article <5>368 <5>notwithstanding that it contains any provision which amends or has the <5>effect of amending, this Constitution. <6>8. <5>The provisions of article 239B shall, so far as may be, apply in relation to the <5>National Capital Territory, the Lieutenant Governor and the Legislative <5>Assembly, as they apply in relation to the Union territory of Pondicherry, the <5>administrator and its Legislature, respectively; and any reference in that article <5>to "clause (1) of article 239A" shall be deemed to be a reference to this article or <5>article 239AB, as the case may be. <7>239AB. Provisions in case of failure of constitutional <7>machinery <5>If the President, on receipt of a report from the Lieutenant Governor or otherwise, is <5>satisfied- <6>a.<5> that a situation has arisen in which the administration of the National <5>Capital Territory cannot be carried on in accordance with the provisions of <5>article 239AA or of any law made in pursuance of that article; or <6>b.<5> that for the proper administration of the National Capital Territory it is <5>necessary or expedient so to do, <5>the President may by order suspend the operation of any provision of article 239AA <5>or of all or any of the provisions of any law made in pursuance of that article for such <5>period and subject to such conditions as may be specified in such law and make such <5>incidental and consequential provisions as may appear to him to be necessary or <5>expedient for administering the National Capital Territory in accordance with the <5>provisions of article 239 and article 239AA. <7>239B. Power of administrator to promulgate Ordinances <7>during recess of Legislature <6>1. <5>If at any time, except when the Legislature of the Union territory of Pondicherry <5>is in session, the administrator thereof is satisfied that circumstances exist <5>which render it necessary for him to take immediate action, he may promulgate <5>such Ordinances as the circumstances appear to him to require: <5>Provided that no such Ordinance shall be promulgated by the administrator <5>except after obtaining instructions from the President in that behalf: <5>Provided further that whenever the said Legislature is dissolved, or its <5>functioning remains suspended on account of any action taken under any such <5>law as is referred to in clause (1) of article 239A, the administrator shall not <5>promulgate any Ordinance during the period of such dissolution or suspension. <6>2. <5>An Ordinance promulgated under this article in pursuance of instructions from <5>the President shall be deemed to be an Act of the Legislature of the Union <5>territory which has been duly enacted after complying with the provisions in <5>that behalf contained in any such law as is referred to in clause (1) of article <5>239A, but every such Ordinance- <6>a.<5> shall be laid before the Legislature of the Union territory and shall cease to <5>operate at the expiration of six weeks from the reassembly of the <5>Legislature or if, before the expiration of that period, a resolution <5>disapproving it is passed by the Legislature, upon the passing of the <5>resolution;
