and <6>b.<5> may be withdrawn at any time by the administrator after obtaining <5>instructions from the President in that behalf. <6>3. <5>If and so far as an Ordinance under this article makes any provision which would <5>not be valid if enacted in an Act of the Legislature of the Union territory made <5>after complying with the provisions in that behalf contained in any such law as is <5>referred to in clause (1) of article 239A, it shall be void. <7>240. Power of President to make regulations for certain <7>Union territories <6>1.<5> The President may make regulations for the peace, progress and good <5>government of the Union territory of- <6>a.<5> the Andaman and Nicobar Islands; <6>b.<5> Lakshadweep; <6>c. <5>Dadra and Nagar Haveli; <6>d.<5> Daman and Diu; <6>e.<5> Pondicherry; <5>Provided that when any body is created under article 239A to function as a <5>Legislature for the Union territory of Pondicherry, the President shall not make <5>any regulation for the peace, progress and good government of that Union <5>territory with effect from the date appointed for the first meeting of the <5>Legislature: <5>Provided further that when ever the body functioning as Legislature for the <5>Union territory of Pondicherry is dissolved, or the functioning of that body as <5>such Legislature remains suspended on account of any action taken under any <5>such law is referred to in clause (1) of article 239A, the President may, during the <5>period of such dissolution or suspension, make regulations for the peace, <5>progress and good government of that Union territory. <6>2.<5> Any regulation so made may repeal or amend any Act made by Parliament or any <5>other law, which is for the time being applicable to the Union territory and, when <5>promulgated by the President, shall have the same force and effect as an Act of <5>Parliament which applies to that territory. <7>241. High Courts for Union territories <6>1.<5> Parliament may by law constitute a High Court for a Union territory or declare <5>any court in any such territory to be a High Court for all or any of the purposes <5>of this Constitution. <6>2.<5> The provisions of Chapter V of Part VI shall apply in relation to every High Court <5>referred to in clause (1) as they apply in relation to a High Court referred to in <5>article 214 subject to such modifications or exceptions as Parliament may by law <5>provide. <6>3.<5> Subject to the provisions of this Constitution and to the provisions of any law of <5>the appropriate Legislature made by virtue of powers conferred on that <5>Legislature by or under this Constitution, every High Court exercising <5>jurisdiction immediately before the commencement of the Constitution <5>(Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956, in relation to any Union territory shall <5>continue to exercise such jurisdiction in relation to that territory after such <5>commencement. <6>4.<5> Nothing in this article derogates from the power of Parliament to extend or <5>exclude the jurisdiction of a High Court for a State to, or from, any Union <5>territory or part thereof. <7>242. Coorg <5>Rep. by the Constitution (Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956, s. 29 and Sch. <9>PART IX: THE PANCHAYATS <4>• Municipal government <7>243. Definitions <5>In this Part, unless the context otherwise requires,- <6>a.<5> "district" means a district in a State; <6>b.<5> "Gram Sabha" means a body consisting of persons registered in the <5>electoral rolls relating to a village comprised within the area of Panchayat <5>at the village level; <6>c. <5>"intermediate level" means a level between the village and district levels <5>specified by the Governor of a State by public notification to be the <5>intermediate level for the purposes of this Part; <6>d.<5> "Panchayat" means an institution <5>(by whatever name called) of <5>self-government constituted under article 243B, for the rural areas; <6>e.<5> "Panchayat area" means the territorial area of a Panchayat; <6>f. <5>"population" means the population as ascertained at the last preceding <5>census of which the relevant figures have been published; <6>g.<5> "village" means a village specified by the Governor by public notification to <5>be a village for the purposes of this Part and includes a group of villages so <5>specified. <4>• Municipal government <7>243A. Gram Sabha <5>A Gram Sabha may exercise such powers and perform such functions at the village <5>level as the Legislature of a State may, by law, provide. <4>• Municipal government <7>243B. Constitution of Panchayats <6>1.<5> There shall be constituted in every State, Panchayats at the village, intermediate <5>and district levels in accordance with the provisions of this Part. <6>2.<5> Notwithstanding anything in clause (1), Panchayats at the intermediate level <5>may not be constituted in a State having a population not exceeding twenty <5>lakhs. <4>• Municipal government <7>243C. Composition of Panchayats <6>1. <5>Subject to the provisions of this Part, the Legislature of a State may, by law, <5>make provisions with respect to the composition of Panchayats: <5>Provided that the ratio between the population of the territorial area of a <5>Panchayat at any level and the number of seats in such Panchayat to be filled by <5>election shall, so far as practicable, be the same throughout the State. <6>2. <5>All the seats in a Panchayat shall be filled by persons chosen by direct election <5>from territorial constituencies in the Panchayat area and, for this purpose each <5>Panchayat area shall be divided into territorial constituencies in such manner <5>that the ratio between the population of each constituency and the number of <5>seats allotted to it shall, so far as practicable, be the same throughout the <5>Panchayat area. <6>3. <5>The Legislature of a State may, by law, provide for the representation- <6>a.<5> of the Chairpersons of the Panchayats at the village level, in the Panchayats <5>at the intermediate level or, in the case of a State not having Panchayats at <5>the intermediate level, in the Panchayats at the district level; <6>b.<5> of the Chairpersons of the Panchayats at the intermediate level, in the <5>Panchayats at the district level; <6>c. <5>of the members of the House of the People and the members of the <5>Legislative Assembly of the State representing constituencies which <5>comprise wholly or partly a Panchayat area at a level other than the village <5>level, in such Panchayat; <6>d.<5> of the members of the Council of States and the members of the Legislative <5>Council of the State, where they are registered as electors within- <6>i. <5>a Panchayat area at the intermediate level, in Panchayat at the <5>intermediate level; <6>ii. <5>a Panchayat area at the district level, in Panchayat at the district level. <6>4.<5> The Chairperson of a Panchayat and other members of a Panchayat whether or <5>not chosen by direct election from territorial constituencies in the Panchayat <5>area shall have the right to vote in the meetings of the Panchayats. <6>5.<5> The Chairperson of- <6>a.<5> a Panchayat at the village level shall be elected in such manner as the <5>Legislature of a State may, by law, provide, and <6>b.<5> a Panchayat at the intermediate level or district level shall be elected by, <5>and from amongst, the elected members thereof. <7>243D. Reservation of seats <6>1. <5>Seats shall be reserved for- <6>a.<5> the Scheduled Castes; and <6>b.<5> the Scheduled Tribes, <5>in every Panchayat and the number of seats so reserved shall bear, as nearly as <5>may be, the same proportion to the total number of seats to be filled by direct <5>election in that Panchayat as the population of the Scheduled Castes in that <5>Panchayat area or of the Scheduled Tribes in that Panchayat area bears to the <5>total population of that area and such seats may be allotted by rotation to <5>different constituencies in a Panchayat. <6>2. <5>Not less than one-third of the total number of seats reserved under clause (1) <5>shall be reserved for women belonging to the Scheduled Castes or, as the case <5>may be, the Scheduled Tribes. <6>3. <5>Not less than one-third (including the number of seats reserved for women <5>belonging to the Scheduled Castes and the Scheduled Tribes) of the total <5>number of seats to be filled by direct election in every Panchayat shall be <5>reserved for women and such seats may be allotted by rotation to different <5>constituencies in a Panchayat. <6>4. <5>The offices of the Chairpersons in the Panchayats at the village or any other <5>level shall be reserved for the Scheduled Castes, the Scheduled Tribes and <5>women in such manner as the Legislature of a State may, by law, provide: <5>Provided that the number of offices of Chairpersons reserved for the Scheduled <5>Castes and the Scheduled Tribes in the Panchayats at each level in any State <5>shall bear, as nearly as may be, the same proportion to the total number of such <5>offices in the Panchayats at each level as the population of the Scheduled Castes <5>in the State or of the Scheduled Tribes in the State bears to the total population <5>of the State: <5>Provided further that not less than one-third of the total number of offices of <5>Chairpersons in the Panchayats at each level shall be reserved for women: <5>Provided also that the number of offices reserved under this clause shall be <5>allotted by rotation to different Panchayats at each level. <6>5.<5> The reservation of seats under clauses (1) and (2) and the reservation of offices <5>of Chairpersons (other than the reservation for women) under clause (4) shall <5>cease to have effect on the expiration of the period specified in article 334. <6>6.<5> Nothing in this Part shall prevent the Legislature of a State from making any <5>provision for reservation of seats in any Panchayat or offices of Chairpersons in <5>the Panchayats at any level in favour of backward class of citizens. <7>243E. Duration of Panchayats etc <6>1.<5> Every Panchayat, unless sooner dissolved under any law for the time being in <5>force, shall continue for five years from the date appointed for its first meeting <5>and no longer. <6>2.<5> No amendment of any law for the time being in force shall have the effect of <5>causing dissolution of a Panchayat at any level, which is functioning immediately <5>before such amendment, till the expiration of its duration specified in clause (1). <6>3.<5> An election to constitute a Panchayat shall be completed- <6>a.<5> before the expiry of its duration specified in clause (1) <6>b.<5> before the expiration of a period of six months from the date of its <5>dissolution: <5>Provided that where the remainder of the period for which the dissolved <5>Panchayat would have continued is less than six months, it shall not be <5>necessary to hold any election under this clause for constituting the <5>Panchayat for such period. <6>4.<5> A Panchayat constituted upon the dissolution of a Panchayat before the <5>expiration of its duration shall continue only for the remainder of the period for <5>which the dissolved Panchayat would have continued under clause (1) had it not <5>been so dissolved. <7>243F. Disqualifications for membership <6>1.<5> A person shall be disqualified for being chosen as, and for being, a member of a <5>Panchayat- <6>a.<5> if he is so disqualified by or under any law for the time being in force for the <5>purposes of elections to the Legislature of the State concerned: <5>Provided that no person shall be disqualified on the ground that he is less <5>than twenty-five years of age, if he has attained the age of twenty-one <5>years; <6>b.<5> if he is so disqualified by or under any law made by the Legislature of the <5>State. <6>2.<5> If any question arises as to whether a member of a Panchayat has become <5>subject to any of the disqualifications mentioned in clause (1), the question shall <5>be referred for the decision of such authority and in such manner as the <5>Legislature of a State may, by law, provide. <4>• Municipal government <7>243G. Powers, authority and responsibilities of Panchayat <5>Subject to the provisions of the Constitution, the Legislature of a State may, by law, <5>endow the Panchayats with such powers and authority as may be necessary to <5>enable them to function as institutions of self-government and such law may contain <5>provisions for the devolution of powers and responsibilities upon Panchayats at the <5>appropriate level, subject to such conditions as may be specified therein, with <5>respect to- <6>a.<5> the preparation of plans for economic development and social justice; <6>b.<5> the implementation of schemes for economic development and social <5>justice as may be entrusted to them including those in relation to the <5>matters listed in the Eleventh Schedule. <4>• Municipal government <7>243H. Powers to impose taxes by, and Funds of, the <7>Panchayats <5>The Legislature of a State may, by law- <6>a.<5> authorise a Panchayat to levy, collect and appropriate such taxes, duties, <5>tolls and fees in accordance with such procedure and subject to such limits; <6>b.<5> assign to a Panchayat such taxes, duties, tolls and fees levied and collected <5>by the State Government for such purposes and subject to such conditions <5>and limits; <6>c. <5>provide for making such grants-in-aid to the Panchayats from the <5>Consolidated Fund of the State; and <6>d.<5> provide for constitution of such Funds for crediting all moneys received, <5>respectively, by or on behalf of the Panchayats and also for the withdrawal <5>of such moneys therefrom, <5>as may be specified in the law. <4>• Municipal government <7>243I. Constitution of Finance Commission to review <7>financial position <6>1.<5> The Governor of a State shall, as soon as may be within one year from the <5>commencement of the Constitution (Seventy-third Amendment) Act, 1992, and <5>thereafter at the expiration of every fifth year, constitute a Finance Commission <5>to review the financial position of the Panchayats and to make <5>recommendations to the Governor as to- <6>a.<5> the principles which should govern- <6>i. <5>the distribution between the State and the Panchayats of the net <5>proceeds of the taxes, duties, tolls and fees leviable by the State, which <5>may the divided between them under this Part and the allocation <5>between the panchayats at all levels of their respective shares of such <5>proceeds; <6>ii. <5>the determination of the taxes, duties, tolls and fees which may be <5>assigned to, or appropriated by, the Panchayats; <6>iii. <5>the grants-in-aid to the Panchayats from the Consolidated Fund of the <5>State; <6>b.<5> the measures needed to improve the financial position of the Panchayats; <6>c. <5>any other matter referred to the Finance Commission by the Governor in <5>the interests of sound finance of the Panchayats. <6>2.<5> The Legislature of a State may, by law, provide for the composition of the <5>Commission, the qualifications which shall be requisite for appointment as <5>members thereof and the manner in which they shall be selected. <6>3.<5> The Commission shall determine their procedure and shall have such powers in <5>the performance of their functions as the Legislature of the State may, by law, <5>confer on them. <6>4.<5> The Governor shall cause every recommendation made by the Commission <5>under this article together with as explanatory memorandum as to the action <5>taken thereon to be laid before the Legislature of the State. <7>243J. Audit of accounts of Panchayats <5>The Legislature of a State may, by law, make provisions with respect to the <5>maintenance of accounts by the Panchayats and the auditing of such accounts. <4>• Municipal government <7>243K. Elections to the Panchayats <6>1.<5> The superintendence, direction and control of the preparation of electoral rolls <5>for, and the conduct of, all elections to the Panchayats shall be vested in a State <5>Election Commission consisting of a State Election Commissioner to be <5>appointed by the Governor. <6>2.<5> Subject to the provisions of any law made by the Legislature of a State, the <5>conditions of service and tenure of office of the State Election Commissioner <5>shall be such as the Governor may by rule determine: <5>Provided that the State Election. Commissioner shall not be removed from his <5>office except in like manner and on the like grounds as a Judge of a High Court <5>and the conditions of service of the State Election Commissioner shall not be <5>varied to his disadvantage after his appointment. <6>3.<5> The Governor of a State shall, when so requested by the State Election <5>Commission, make available to the State Election Commission such staff as may <5>be necessary for the discharge of the functions conferred on the State Election <5>Commission by clause (1). <6>4.<5> Subject to the provisions of this Constitution, the Legislature of a State may, by <5>law, make provision with respect to all matters relating to, or in connection with, <5>elections to the Panchayats. <7>243L. Application to Union territories <5>The provisions of this Part shall apply to the Union territories and shall, in their <5>application to a Union territory, have effect as if the references to the Governor of a <5>State were reference to the Administrator of the Union territory appointed under <5>article 239 and references to the Legislature or the Legislative Assembly of a State <5>were references, in relation to a Union territory having a Legislative Assembly, to <5>that Legislative Assembly: <5>Provided that the President may, by public notification, direct that the provisions of <5>this Part shall apply to any Union territory or part thereof subject to such exceptions <5>and modifications as he may specify in the notification. <7>243M. Part not to apply to certain areas <6>1. <5>Nothing in this part shall apply to the Scheduled Areas referred to in clause (1), <5>and the tribal areas referred to in clause (2), of article 244. <6>2. <5>Nothing in this Part shall apply to- <6>a.<5> the States of Nagaland, Meghalaya and Mizoram; <6>b.<5> the Hill Areas in the State of Manipur for which District Councils exist <5>under any law for the time being in force. <6>3. <5>Nothing in this part- <6>a.<5> relating to Panchayats at the district level shall apply to the hill areas of the <5>District of Darjeeling in the State of West Bengal for which Darjeeling <5>Gorkha Hill Council exists under any law for the time being in force; <6>b.<5> Shall be construed to affect the functions and powers of the Darjeeling <5>Gorkha Hill Council constituted under such law. <6>3A. <5>Nothing in article 243D, relating to reservation of seats for the Scheduled <5>Castes, shall apply to the State of Arunachal Pradesh. <6>4. <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,- <6>a.<5> the Legislature of a State referred to in sub-clause (a) of clause (2) may, by <5>law, extend this Part to that State, except the areas, if any, referred to in <5>clause (1), if the Legislative Assembly of that State passes a resolution to <5>that effect by a majority of the total membership of that House and by a <5>majority of not less than two-thirds of the members of that House present <5>and voting; <6>b.<5> Parliament may, by law extend the provisions of this Part to the Scheduled <5>Areas and the Tribal Areas referred to in clause (1) subject to such <5>exceptions and modifications as may be specified in such law, and no such <5>law shall be deemed to be an amendment of this Constitution for the <5>purposes of article 368. <7>243N. Continuance of existing laws and Panchayats <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Part, any provision of any law relating to <5>Panchayats in force in a State immediately before the commencement of the <5>Constitution (Seventy-third Amendment) Act, 1992, which is inconsistent with the <5>provisions of this Part, shall continue to be in force until amended or repealed by a <5>competent Legislature or other competent authority or until the expiration of one <5>year from such commencement, whichever is earlier: <5>Provided that all the Panchayats existing immediately before such commencement <5>shall continue till the expiration of their duration, unless sooner dissolved by a <5>resolution passed to that effect by the Legislative Assembly of that State or, in the <5>case of a State having a Legislative Council, by each House of the Legislature of that <5>State. <7>243O. Bar to interference by courts in electoral matters <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,- <6>a.<5> the validity of any law relating to the delimitation of constituencies or the <5>allotment of seats to such constituencies, made or purporting to be made <5>under article 243K, shall not be called in question in any court; <6>b.<5> no election to any Panchayat shall be called in question except by an <5>election petition presented to such authority and in such manner as is <5>provided for by or under any law made by the Legislature of a State. <9>PART IXA: THE MUNICIPALITIES <7>243P. Definitions <5>In this Part, unless the context otherwise requires,- <6>a.<5> "Committee" means a Committee constituted under article 243S; <6>b.<5> "district" means a district in a State; <6>c. <5>"Metropolitan area" means an area having a population of ten lakhs or <5>more, comprised in one or more districts and consisting of two or more <5>Municipalities or Panchayats or other contiguous areas, specified by the <5>Governor by public notification to be a Metropolitan area for the purposes <5>of this Part; <6>d.<5> "Municipal area" means the territorial area of a Municipality as is notified <5>by the Governor; <6>e.<5> "Municipality" means an institution of self-government constituted under <5>article 243Q; <6>f. <5>"Panchayat" means a Panchayat constituted under article 243B; <6>g.<5> "population" means the population as ascertained at the last preceding <5>census of which the relevant figures have been published. <4>• Municipal government <7>243Q. Constitution of Municipalities <6>1.<5> There shall be constituted in every State,- <6>a.<5> A Nagar Panchayat (by whatever name called) for transitional area, that is <5>to say, an area in transition from a rural area to an urban area; <6>b.<5> a Municipal Council for a smaller urban area; and <6>c. <5>a Municipal Corporation for a larger urban area, <5>in accordance with the provisions of this Part: <5>Provided that a Municipality under this clause may not be constituted in such <5>urban area or part thereof as the Governor may, having regard to the size of the <5>area and the municipal services being provided or proposed to be provided by an <5>industrial establishment in that area and such other factors as he may deem fit, <5>by public notification, specify to be an industrial township. <6>2.<5> In this article, "a transitional area", "a smaller urban area" or "a larger urban <5>area" means such area as the Governor may, having regard to the population of <5>the area, the density of the population therein, the revenue generated for local <5>administration, the percentage of employment in non-agricultural activities, the <5>economic importance or such other factors as he may deem fit, specify by public <5>notification for the purposes of this Part. <4>• Municipal government <7>243R. Composition of Municipalities <6>1.<5> Save as provided in clause (2), all the seats in a Municipality shall be filled by <5>persons chosen by direct election from the territorial constituencies in the <5>Municipal area and for this purpose each Municipal area shall be divided into <5>territorial constituencies to be known as wards. <6>2.<5> The Legislature of a State may, by law, provide- <6>a.<5> for the representation in a Municipality of- <6>i. <5>persons having special knowledge or experience in Municipal <5>administration; <6>ii. <5>the members of the House of the People and the members of the <5>Legislative Assembly of the State representing constituencies which <5>comprise wholly or partly the Municipal area; <6>iii. <5>the members of the Council of States and the members of the <5>Legislative Council of the State registered as electors within the <5>Municipal area; <6>iv.<5> the Chairpersons of the Committees constituted under clause (5) of <5>article 243S: <5>Provided that the persons referred to in paragraph (i) shall not have the <5>right to vote in the meetings of the Municipality; <6>b.<5> the manner of election of the Chairperson of a Municipality. <7>243S. Constitution and composition of Wards Committees, <7>etc <6>1.<5> There shall be constituted Wards Committees, consisting of one or more wards, <5>within the territorial area of a Municipality having a population of three lakhs or <5>more. <6>2.<5> The Legislature of a State may, by law, make provision with respect to- <6>a.<5> the composition and the territorial area of a Wards Committee; <6>b.<5> the manner in which the seats in a Wards Committee shall be filled. <6>3.<5> A member of a Municipality representing a ward within the territorial area of <5>the Wards Committee shall be a member of that Committee. <6>4.<5> Where a Wards Committee consists of- <6>a.<5> One ward, the member representing that ward in the Municipality; or <6>b.<5> two or more wards, one of the members representing such wards in the <5>Municipality elected by the members of the Wards Committee. <5>Shall be the Chairperson of that Committee. <6>5.<5> Nothing in this article shall be deemed to prevent the Legislature of a State from <5>making provision for the constitution of Committees in addition to the Wards <5>Committees. <7>243T. Reservation of seats <6>1.<5> Seats shall be reserved for the Scheduled Castes and the Scheduled Tribes in <5>every Municipality and the number of seats so reserved shall bear, as nearly as <5>may be, the same proportion to the total number of seats to be filed by direct <5>election in that Municipality as the population of the Scheduled Castes in the <5>Municipal area or of the Scheduled Tribes in the Municipal area bears to the <5>total population in that area and such seats may be allotted by rotation to <5>different constituencies in a municipality. <6>2.<5> Not less than one-third of the total number of seats reserved under clause (1) <5>shall be reserved for women belonging to the Scheduled Castes or, as the case <5>may be, the Scheduled Tribes. <6>3.<5> Not less than one-third (including the number of seats reserved for women <5>belonging to the Scheduled Castes and the Scheduled Tribes) of the total <5>number of seats to be filled by direct election in every Municipality shall be <5>reserved for women and such seats may be allotted by rotation to different <5>constituencies in a Municipality. <6>4.<5> The offices of Chairpersons in the Municipalities shall be reserved for the <5>Scheduled Castes, the Scheduled Tribes and women in such manner as the <5>Legislature of a State may, by law, provide. <6>5.<5> The reservation of seats under clauses (1) and (2) and the reservation of offices <5>of Chairpersons (other than the reservation for women) under clause (4) shall <5>cease to have effect on the expiration of the period specified in article 334. <6>6.<5> Nothing in this Part shall prevent the Legislature of a State from making any <5>provision for reservation of seats in any Municipality or offices of Chairpersons <5>in the Municipalities in favour of backward class of citizens. <4>• Municipal government <7>243U. Duration of Municipalities, etc <6>1.<5> Every Municipality, unless sooner dissolved under any law for the time being in <5>force, shall continue for five years from the date appointed for its first meeting <5>and no longer: <5>Provided that a Municipality shall be given a reasonable opportunity of being <5>heard before its dissolution. <6>2.<5> No amendment of any law for the time being in force shall have the effect of <5>causing dissolution of a Municipality at any level, which is functioning <5>immediately before such amendment, till the expiration of its duration specified <5>in clause (1). <6>3.<5> An election to constitute a Municipality shall be completed,- <6>a.<5> before the expiry of its duration specified in clause (1); <6>b.<5> before the expiration of a period of six months from the date of its <5>dissolution: <5>Provided that where the remainder of the period for which the dissolved <5>Municipality would have continued is less than six months, it shall not be <5>necessary to hold any election under this clause for constituting the <5>Municipality for such period. <6>4.<5> A Municipality constituted upon the dissolution of a Municipality before the <5>expiration of its duration shall continue only for the remainder of the period for <5>which the dissolved Municipality would have continued under clause (1) had it <5>not been so dissolved. <7>243V. Disqualifications for membership <6>1.<5> A persons shall be disqualified for being chosen as, and for being, a member of a <5>Municipality- <6>a.<5> if he is so disqualified by or under any law for the time being in force for the <5>purposes of elections to the Legislature of the State concerned: <5>Provided that no person shall be disqualified on the ground that he is less <5>than twenty-five years of age, if he has attained the age of twenty-one <5>years; <6>b.<5> if he is so disqualified by or under any law made by the Legislature of the <5>State. <6>2.<5> If any question arises as to whether a member of a Municipality has become <5>subject to any of the disqualifications mentioned in clause (1), the question shall <5>be referred for the decision of such authority and in such manner as the <5>Legislature of a State may, by law, provide. <4>• Municipal government <7>243W. Powers, authority and responsibilities of <7>Municipalities, etc <5>Subject to the provisions of this Constitution, the Legislature of a State may, by law, <5>endow- <6>a.<5> the Municipalities with such powers and authority as may be necessary to <5>enable them to function as institutions of self-government and such law <5>may contain provisions for the devolution of powers and responsibilities <5>upon Municipalities, subject to such conditions as may be specified therein, <5>with respect to- <6>i. <5>the preparation of plans for economic development and social justice; <6>ii. <5>the performance of functions and the implementation of schemes as <5>may be entrusted to them including those in relation to the matters <5>listed in the Twelfth Schedule; <6>b.<5> the Committees with such powers and authority as may be necessary to <5>enable them to carry out the responsibilities conferred upon them including <5>those in relation to the matters listed in the Twelfth Schedule. <4>• Municipal government <7>243X. Power to impose taxes by, and Funds of, the <7>Municipalities <6>1.<5> The Legislature of a State may, by law- <6>a.<5> authorise a Municipality to levy, collect and appropriate such taxes, duties, <5>tolls and fees in accordance with such procedure and subject to such limits; <6>b.<5> assign to a Municipality such taxes, duties, tolls and fees levied and <5>collected by the State Government for such purposes and subject to such <5>conditions and limits; <6>c. <5>provide for making such grants-in-aid to the Municipalities from the <5>Consolidated Fund of the State; and <6>d.<5> provide for constitution of such Funds for crediting all moneys received, <5>respectively, by or on behalf of the Municipalities and also for the <5>withdrawal of such moneys therefrom, <5>as may be specified in the law. <6>2.<5> The Legislature of a State may, by law, make provision with respect to- <6>a.<5> the composition of the District Planning Committees; <6>b.<5> the manner in which the seats in such Committees shall be filled: <5>Provided that not less than four-fifths of the total number of members of <5>such Committee shall be elected by, and from amongst, the elected <5>members of the Panchayat at the district level and of the Municipalities in <5>the district in proportion to the ratio between the population of the rural <5>areas and of the urban areas in the district; <6>c. <5>the functions relating to district planning which may be assigned to such <5>Committees; <6>d.<5> the manner in which the Chairpersons of such Committees shall be chosen. <6>3. <5>Every District Planning Committee shall, in preparing the draft development <5>plan,- <6>a.<5> have regard to- <6>i. <5>matters of common interest between the Panchayats and the <5>Municipalities including spatial planning, sharing of water and other <5>physical and natural resources, the integrated development of <5>infrastructure and environmental conservation; <6>ii. <5>the extent and type of available resources whether financial or <5>otherwise; <6>b.<5> consult such institutions and organisations as the Governor may, by order, <5>specify. <6>4. <5>The Chairperson of every District Planning Committee shall forward the <5>development plan, as recommended by such Committee, to the Government of <5>the State. <7>243ZE. Committee for Metropolitan planning <6>1.<5> There shall be constituted in every Metropolitan area a Metropolitan Planning <5>Committee to prepare a draft development plan for the Metropolitan area as a <5>whole. <6>2.<5> The Legislature of a State may, by law, make provision with respect to- <6>a.<5> the composition of the Metropolitan Planning Committees; <6>b.<5> the manner in which the seats in such Committees shall be filled: <5>Provided that not less than two-thirds of the members of such Committee <5>shall be elected by, and from amongst, the elected members of the <5>Municipalities and Chairpersons of the Panchayats in the Metropolitan <5>area in proportion to the ratio between the population of the Municipalities <5>and of the Panchayats in that area; <6>c. <5>the representation in such Committees of the Government of India and the <5>Government of the State and of such organisations and institutions as may <5>be deemed necessary for carrying out the functions assigned to such <5>Committees; <6>d.<5> the functions relating to planning and co-ordination for the Metropolitan <5>area which may be assigned to such Committees; <6>e.<5> the manner in which the Chairpersons of such Committees shall be chosen. <6>3. <5>Every Metropolitan Planning Committee shall, in preparing the draft <5>development plan,- <6>a.<5> have regard to- <6>i. <5>the plans prepared by the Municipalities and the Panchayats in the <5>Metropolitan area; <6>ii. <5>matters of common interest between the Municipalities and the <5>Panchayats, including co-ordinated spatial planning of the area, <5>sharing of water and other physical and natural resources, the <5>integrated development of infrastructure and environmental <5>conservation; <6>iii. <5>the overall objectives and priorities set by the Government of India <5>and the Government of the State; <6>iv.<5> the extent and nature of investments likely to be made in the <5>Metropolitan area by agencies of the Government of India and of the <5>Government of the State and other available resources whether <5>financial or otherwise; <6>b.<5> consult such institutions and organisations as the Governor may, by order, <5>specify. <6>4. <5>The Chairperson of every Metropolitan Planning Committee shall forward the <5>development plan, as recommended by such Committee, to the Government of <5>the State. <7>243ZF. Continuance of existing laws and Municipalities <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Part, any provision of any law relating to <5>Municipalities in force in a State immediately before the commencement of the <5>Constitution (Seventy-fourth Amendment) Act, 1992, which is inconsistent with the <5>provisions of this Part, shall continue to be in force until amended or repealed by a <5>competent Legislature or other competent authority or until the expiration of one <5>year from such commencement, whichever is earlier: <5>Provided that all the Municipalities existing immediately before such <5>commencement shall continue till the expiration of their duration, unless sooner <5>dissolved by a resolution passed to that effect by the Legislative Assembly of that <5>State or, in the case of a State having a Legislative Council, by each House of the <5>Legislature of that State. <7>243ZG. Bar to interference by courts in electoral matters <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,- <6>a.<5> the validity of any law relating to the delimitation of constituencies or the <5>allotment of seats to such constituencies, made or purporting to be made <5>under article 243ZF shall not be called in question in any court; <6>b.<5> no election to any Municipality shall be called in question except by an <5>election petition presented to such authority and in such manner as is <5>provided for by or under any law made by the Legislature of a State. <9>Part IXB: The Co-Operative Societies <7>243ZH. Definitions <5>In this Part, unless the context otherwise requires,- <6>a. <5>“authorised person” means a person referred to as such in article 243ZQ; <6>b. <5>“board” means the board of directors or the governing body of a <5>co-operative society, by whatever name called, to which the direction and <5>control of the management of the affairs of a society is entrusted to; <6>c. <5>“co-operative society” means a society registered or deemed to be <5>registered under any law relating to co-operative societies for the time <5>being in force in any State; <6>d. <5>“multi-State co-operative society” means a society with objects not <5>confined to one State and registered or deemed to be registered under any <5>law for the time being in force relating to such co-operatives; <6>e. <5>“office bearer” means a President, Vice-President, Chairperson, <5>Vice-Chairperson, Secretary or Treasurer of a co-operative society and <5>includes any other person to be elected by the board of any co-operative <5>society; <6>f. <5>“Registrar” means the Central Registrar appointed by the Central <5>Government in relation to the multi-State co-operative societies and the <5>Registrar for co-operative societies appointed by the State Government <5>under the law made by the Legislature of a State in relation to co-operative <5>societies; <6>g. <5>“State Act” means any law made by the Legislature of a State; <6>h. <5>“State level co-operative society” means a co-operative society having its <5>area of operation extending to the whole of a State and defined as such in <5>any law made by the Legislature of a State. <7>243ZI. Incorporation of co-operative societies <5>Subject to the provisions of this Part, the Legislature of a State may, by law, make <5>provisions with respect to the incorporation, regulation and winding-up of <5>co-operative societies based on the principles of voluntary formation, democratic <5>member-control, member-economic participation and autonomous functioning. <7>243ZJ. Number and term of members of board and its <7>office bearers <6>1. <5>The board shall consist of such number of directors as may be provided by the <5>Legislature of a State, by law: <5>Provided that the maximum number of directors of a co-operative society shall <5>not exceed twenty-one: <5>Provided further that the Legislature of a State shall, by law, provide for the <5>reservation of one seat for the Scheduled Castes or the Scheduled Tribes and <5>two seats for women on board of every co-operative society consisting of <5>individuals as members and having members from such class or category of <5>persons. <6>2. <5>The term of office of elected members of the board and its office bearers shall be <5>five years from the date of election and the term of office bearers shall be <5>coterminous with the term of the board: <5>Provided that the board may fill a casual vacancy on the board by nomination <5>out of the same class of members in respect of which the casual vacancy has <5>arisen, if the term of office of the board is less than half of its original term. <6>3. <5>The Legislature of a State shall, by law, make provisions for co-option of persons <5>to be members of the board having experience in the field of banking, <5>management, finance or specialisation in any other field relating to the objects <5>and activities undertaken by the co-operative society, as members of the board <5>of such society: <5>Provided that the number of such co-opted members shall not exceed two in <5>addition to twenty-one directors specified in the first proviso to clause (1): <5>Provided further that such co-opted members shall not have the right to vote in <5>any election of the co-operative society in their capacity as such member or to <5>be eligible to be elected as office bearers of the board: <5>Provided also that the functional directors of a co-operative society shall also be <5>the members of the board and such members shall be excluded for the purpose <5>of counting the total number of directors specified in the first proviso to clause <5>(1). <7>243ZK. Election of members of board <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything contained in any law made by the Legislature of a <5>State, the election of a board shall be conducted before the expiry of the term of <5>the board so as to ensure that the newly elected members of the board assume <5>office immediately on the expiry of the term of the office of members of the <5>outgoing board. <6>2.<5> The superintendence, direction and control of the preparation of electoral rolls <5>for, and the conduct of, all elections to a co-operative society shall vest in such <5>an authority or body, as may be provided by the Legislature of a State, by law: <5>Provided that the Legislature of a State may, by law, provide for the procedure <5>and guidelines for the conduct of such elections. <7>243ZL. Supersession and suspension of board and interim <7>management <6>1. <5>Notwithstanding anything contained in any law for the time being in force, no <5>board shall be superseded or kept under suspension for a period exceeding six <5>months: <5>Provided that the board may be superseded or kept under suspension in case- <6>i. <5>of its persistent default; or <6>ii. <5>of negligence in the performance of its duties; or <6>iii. <5>the board has committed any act prejudicial to the interests of the <5>co-operative society or its members; or <6>iv.<5> there is a stalemate in the constitution or functions of the board; or <6>v.<5> the authority or body as provided by the Legislature of a State, by law, <5>under clause (2) of article 243ZK, has failed to conduct elections in <5>accordance with the provisions of the State Act: <5>Provided further that the board of any such co-operative society shall not be <5>superseded or kept under suspension where there is no Government <5>shareholding or loan or financial assistance or any guarantee by the <5>Government: <5>Provided also that in case of a co-operative society carrying on the business of <5>banking, the provisions of the Banking Regulation Act, 1949 shall also apply: <5>Provided also that in case of a co-operative society, other than a multi-State <5>co-operative society, carrying on the business of banking, the provisions of this <5>clause shall have the effect as if for the words “six months”, the words “one year” <5>had been substituted. <6>2. <5>In case of supersession of a board, the administrator appointed to manage the <5>affairs of such co-operative society shall arrange for conduct of elections within <5>the period specified in clause (1) and handover the management to the elected <5>board. <6>3. <5>The Legislature of a State may, by law, make provisions for the conditions of <5>service of the administrator. <7>243ZM. Audit of accounts of co-operative societies <6>1.<5> The Legislature of a State may, by law, make provisions with respect to the <5>maintenance of accounts by the co-operative societies and the auditing of such <5>accounts at least once in each financial year. <6>2.<5> The Legislature of a State shall, by law, lay down the minimum qualifications and <5>experience of auditors and auditing firms that shall be eligible for auditing <5>accounts of the co-operative societies. <6>3.<5> Every co-operative society shall cause to be audited by an auditor or auditing <5>firms referred to in clause (2) appointed by the general body of the co-operative <5>society: <5>Provided that such auditors or auditing firms shall be appointed from a panel <5>approved by a State Government or any authority authorised by the State <5>Government in this behalf. <6>4.<5> The accounts of every co-operative society shall be audited within six months of <5>the close of the financial year to which such accounts relate. <6>5.<5> The audit report of the accounts of an apex co-operative society, as may be <5>defined by the State Act, shall be laid before the State Legislature in the manner <5>as may be provided by the State Legislature, by law. <7>243ZN. Convening of general body meetings <5>The Legislature of a State may, by law, make provisions that the annual general body <5>meeting of every co-operative society shall be convened within a period of six <5>months of close of the financial year to transact the business as may be provided in <5>such law. <7>243ZO. Right of a member to get information <6>1.<5> The Legislature of a State may, by law, provide for access to every member of a <5>co-operative society to the books, information and accounts of the co-operative <5>society kept in regular transaction of its business with such member. <6>2.<5> The Legislature of a State may, by law, make provisions to ensure the <5>participation of members in the management of the co-operative society <5>providing minimum requirement of attending meetings by the members and <5>utilising the minimum level of services as may be provided in such law. <6>3.<5> The Legislature of a State may, by law, provide for co-operative education and <5>training for its members. <7>243ZP. Returns <5>Every co-operative society shall file returns, within six months of the close of every <5>financial year, to the authority designated by the State Government including the <5>following matters, namely:- <6>a.<5> annual report of its activities; <6>b.<5> its audited statements of accounts; <6>c. <5>plan for surplus disposal as approved by the general body of the <5>co-operative society; <6>d.<5> list of amendments to the bye-laws of the co-operative society, if any; <6>e.<5> declaration regarding date of holding of its general body meeting and <5>conduct of elections when due; and <6>f. <5>any other information required by the Registrar in pursuance of any of the <5>provisions of the State Act. <7>243ZQ. Offences and penalties <6>1.<5> The Legislature of a State may, by law, make provisions for the offences relating <5>to the co-operative societies and penalties for such offences. <6>2.<5> A law made by the Legislature of a State under clause (1) shall include the <5>commission of the following act or omission as offences, namely:- <6>a.<5> a co-operative society or an officer or member thereof wilfully makes a <5>false return or furnishes false information, or any person willfully not <5>furnishes any information required from him by a person authorised in this <5>behalf under the provisions of the State Act; <6>b.<5> any person wilfully or without any reasonable excuse disobeys any <5>summons, requisition or lawful written order issued under the provisions of <5>the State Act; <6>c. <5>any employer who, without sufficient cause, fails to pay to a co-operative <5>society amount deducted by him from its employee within a period of <5>fourteen days from the date on which such deduction is made; <6>d.<5> any officer or custodian who wilfully fails to handover custody of books, <5>accounts, documents, records, cash, security and other property belonging <5>to a co-operative society of which he is an officer or custodian, to an <5>authorised person; and <6>e.<5> whoever, before, during or after the election of members of the board or <5>office bearers, adopts any corrupt practice. <7>243ZR. Application to multi-State co-operative societies <5>The provisions of this Part shall apply to the multi-State co-operative societies <5>subject to the modification that any reference to “Legislature of a State”, “State Act” <5>or “State Government” shall be construed as a reference to “Parliament”, “Central <5>Act” or “the Central Government” respectively. <7>243ZS. Application to Union territories <5>The provisions of this Part shall apply to the Union territories and shall, in their <5>application to a Union territory, having no Legislative Assembly as if the references <5>to the Legislature of a State were a reference to the administrator thereof appointed <5>under article 239 and, in relation to a Union territory having a Legislative Assembly, <5>to that Legislative Assembly: <5>Provided that the President may, by notification in the Official Gazette, direct that <5>the provisions of this Part shall not apply to any Union territory or part thereof as he <5>may specify in the notification. <7>243ZT. Continuance of existing laws <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Part, any provision of any law relating to <5>co-operative societies in force in a State immediately before the commencement of <5>the Constitution (Ninety-seventh Amendment) Act, 2011, which is inconsistent with <5>the provisions of this Part, shall continue to be in force until amended or repealed by <5>a competent Legislature or other competent authority or until the expiration of one <5>year from such commencement, whichever is less. <9>PART X: THE SCHEDULED AND TRIBAL <9>AREAS <7>244. Administration of Scheduled Areas and Tribal Areas <6>1.<5> The provisions of the Fifth Schedule shall apply to the administration and <5>control of the Scheduled Areas and Scheduled Tribes in any State other than the <5>States of Assam , Meghalaya, Tripura and Mizoram. <6>2.<5> The provisions of the Sixth Schedule shall apply to the administration of the <5>tribal areas in the States of Assam , Meghalaya, Tripura and Mizoram. <7>244A. Formation of an autonomous State comprising <7>certain tribal areas in Assam and creation of local <7>Legislature or Council of Ministers or both therefor <6>1. <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, Parliament may, by law, form <5>within the State of Assam an autonomous State comprising (whether wholly or <5>in part) all or any of the tribal areas specified in Part I of the table appended to <5>paragraph 20 of the Sixth Schedule and create therefor- <6>a.<5> a body, whether elected or partly nominated and partly elected, to function <5>as a Legislature for the autonomous State, or <6>b.<5> a Council of Ministers, <5>or both with such constitution, powers and functions, in each case, as may be <5>specified in the law. <6>2. <5>Any such law as is referred to in clause (1) may, in particular,- <6>a.<5> specify the matters enumerated in the State List or the Concurrent List <5>with respect to which the Legislature of the autonomous State shall have <5>power to make laws for the whole or any part thereof, whether to the <5>exclusion of the Legislature of the State of Assam or otherwise; <6>b.<5> define the matters with respect to which the executive power of the <5>autonomous State shall extend; <6>c. <5>provide that any tax levied by the State of Assam shall be assigned to the <5>autonomous State in so far as the proceeds thereof are attributable to the <5>autonomous State; <6>d.<5> provide that any reference to a State in any article of this Constitution shall <5>be construed as including a reference to the autonomous State; and <6>e.<5> make such supplemental, incidental and consequential provisions as may be <5>deemed necessary. <6>3. <5>An amendment of any such law as aforesaid in so far as such amendment relates <5>to any of the matters specified in sub-clause (a) or sub-clause (b) of clause (2) <5>shall have no effect unless the amendment is passed in each House of <5>Parliament by not less than two thirds of the members present and voting. <6>4.<5> Any such law as is referred to in this article shall not be deemed to be an <5>amendment of this Constitution for the purposes of article 368 notwithstanding <5>that it contains any provision which amends or has the effect of amending this <5>Constitution. <9>PART XI: RELATIONS BETWEEN THE UNION <9>AND THE STATES <7>CHAPTER I: LEGISLATIVE RELATIONS <7>Distribution of Legislative Powers <7>245. Extent of laws made by Parliament and by the <7>Legislatures of States <6>1.<5> Subject to the provisions of this Constitution, Parliament may make laws for the <5>whole or any part of the territory of India, and the Legislature of a State may <5>make laws for the whole or any part of the State. <6>2.<5> No law made by Parliament shall be deemed to be invalid on the ground that it <5>would have extra-territorial operation. <7>246. Subject-matter of laws made by Parliament and by the <7>Legislatures of States <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in clauses (2) and (3), Parliament has exclusive power <5>to make laws with respect to any of the matters enumerated in List I in the <5>Seventh Schedule (in this Constitution referred to as the "Union List"). <6>2.<5> Notwithstanding anything in clause (3), Parliament, and, subject to clause (1), <5>the Legislature of any State also, have power to make laws with respect to any of <5>the matters enumerated in List III in the Seventh Schedule (in this Constitution <5>referred to as the "Concurrent List"). <6>3.<5> Subject to clauses (1) and (2), the Legislature of any State has exclusive power to <5>make laws for such State or any part thereof with respect to any of the matters <5>enumerated in List II in the Seventh Schedule (in this Constitution referred to as <5>the "State List"). <6>4.<5> Parliament has power to make laws with respect to any matter for any part of <5>the territory of India not included in a State notwithstanding that such matter is <5>a matter enumerated in the State List. <7>247. Power of Parliament to provide for the establishment <7>of certain additional courts <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Chapter, Parliament may by law provide for the <5>establishment of any additional courts for the better administration of laws made by <5>Parliament or of any existing law with respect to a matter enumerated in the Union <5>List. <4>• National vs subnational laws <7>248. Residuary powers of legislation <6>1.<5> Parliament has exclusive power to make any law with respect to any matter not <5>enumerated in the Concurrent List or State List. <6>2.<5> Such power shall include the power of making any law imposing a tax not <5>mentioned in either of those Lists. <4>• National vs subnational laws <7>249. Power of Parliament to legislate with respect to a <7>matter in the State List in the national interest <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in the foregoing provisions of this Chapter, if the <5>Council of States has declared by resolution supported by not less than <5>two-thirds of the members present and voting that it is necessary or expedient <5>in the national interest that Parliament should make laws with respect to any <5>matter enumerated in the State List specified in the resolution, it shall be lawful <5>for Parliament to make laws for the whole or any part of the territory of India <5>with respect to that matter while the resolution remains in force. <6>2.<5> A resolution passed under clause (1) shall remain in force for such period not <5>exceeding one year as may be specified therein: <5>Provided that, if and so often as a resolution approving the continuance in force <5>of any such resolution is passed in the manner provided in clause (1), such <5>resolution shall continue in force for a further period of one year from the date <5>on which under this clause it would otherwise have ceased to be in force. <6>3.<5> A law made by Parliament which Parliament would not but for the passing of a <5>resolution under clause (1) have been competent to make shall, to the extent of <5>the incompetency, cease to have effect on the expiration of a period of six <5>months after the resolution has ceased to be in force, except as respects things <5>done or omitted to be done before the expiration of the said period. <4>• Emergency provisions <7>250. Power of Parliament to legislate with respect to any <7>matter in the State List if a Proclamation of Emergency is in <7>operation <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in this Chapter, Parliament shall, while a <5>Proclamation of Emergency is in operation, have power to make laws for the <5>whole or any part of the territory of India with respect to any of the matters <5>enumerated in the State List. <6>2.<5> A law made by Parliament which Parliament would not but for the issue of a <5>Proclamation of Emergency have been competent to make shall, to the extent of <5>the incompetency, cease to have effect on the expiration of a period of six <5>months after the Proclamation has ceased to operate, except as respects things <5>done or omitted to be done before the expiration of the said period. <7>251. Inconsistency between laws made by Parliament <7>under articles 249 and 250 and laws made by the <7>legislatures of States <5>Nothing in articles 249 and 250 shall restrict the power of the Legislature of a State <5>to make any law which under this Constitution it has power to make, but if any <5>provision of a law made by the Legislature of a State is repugnant to any provision of <5>a law made by Parliament which Parliament has under either of the said articles <5>power to make, the law made by Parliament, whether passed before or after the law <5>made by the Legislature of the State, shall prevail, and the law made by the <5>Legislature of the State shall to the extent of the repugnancy, but so long only as the <5>law made by Parliament continues to have effect, be inoperative. <7>252. Power of Parliament to legislate for two or more <7>States by consent and adoption of such legislation by any <7>other State <6>1.<5> If it appears to the Legislatures of two or more States to be desirable that any of <5>the matters with respect to which Parliament has no power to make laws for the <5>States except as provided in articles 249 and 250 should be regulated in such <5>States by Parliament by law, and if resolutions to that effect are passed by all the <5>Houses of the Legislatures of those States, it shall be lawful for Parliament to <5>pass an Act for regulating that matter accordingly, and any Act so passed shall <5>apply to such States and to any other State by which it is adopted afterwards by <5>resolution passed in that behalf by the House or, where there are two Houses, <5>by each of the Houses of the Legislature of that State. <6>2.<5> Any Act so passed by Parliament may be amended or repealed by an Act of <5>Parliament passed or adopted in like manner but shall not, as respects any State <5>to which it applies, be amended or repealed by an Act of the Legislature of that <5>State. <4>• Treaty ratification <7>253. Legislation for giving effect to international <4>• Legal status of treaties <7>agreements <5>Notwithstanding anything in the foregoing provisions of this Chapter, Parliament <5>has power to make any law for the whole or any part of the territory of India for <5>implementing any treaty, agreement or convention with any other country or <5>countries or any decision made at any international conference, association or other <5>body. <7>254. Inconsistency between laws made by Parliament and <7>laws made by the Legislatures of States <6>1.<5> If any provision of a law made by the Legislature of a State is repugnant to any <5>provision of a law made by Parliament which Parliament is competent to enact, <5>or to any provision of an existing law with respect to one of the matters <5>enumerated in the Concurrent List, then, subject to the provisions of clause (2), <5>the law made by Parliament, whether passed before or after the law made by the <5>Legislature of such State, or, as the case may be, the existing law, shall prevail <5>and the law made by the Legislature of the State shall, to the extent of the <5>repugnancy, be void. <6>2.<5> Where a law made by the legislature of a State with respect to one of the <5>matters enumerated in the Concurrent List contains any provision repugnant to <5>the provisions of an earlier law made by Parliament or an existing law with <5>respect to that matter, then, the law so made by the Legislature of such State <5>shall, if it has been reserved for the consideration of the President and has <5>received his assent, prevail in that State: <5>Provided that nothing in this clause shall prevent Parliament from enacting at <5>any time any law with respect to the same matter including a law adding to, <5>amending, varying or repealing the law so made by the Legislature of the State. <7>255. Requirements as to recommendations and previous <7>sanctions to be regarded as matters of procedure only <5>No Act of Parliament or of the Legislature of a State, and no provision in any such <5>Act, shall be invalid by reason only that some recommendation or previous sanction <5>required by this Constitution was not given, if assent to that Act was given- <6>a.<5> where the recommendation required was that of the Governor, either by <5>the Governor or by the President; <6>b.<5> where the recommendation required was that of the Rajpramukh, either by <5>the Rajpramukh or by the President; <6>c. <5>where the recommendation or previous sanction required was that of the <5>President, by the President. <7>CHAPTER II: ADMINISTRATIVE RELATIONS <7>General <7>256. Obligation of States and the Union <5>The executive power of every State shall be so exercised as to ensure compliance <5>with the laws made by Parliament and any existing laws which apply in that State, <5>and the executive power of the Union shall extend to the giving of such directions to <5>a State as may, appear to the Government of India to be necessary for that purpose. <7>257. Control of the Union over States in certain cases <6>1.<5> The executive power of every State shall be so exercised as not to impede or <5>prejudice the exercise of the executive power of the Union, and the executive <5>power of the Union shall extend to the giving of such directions to a State as may <5>appear to the Government of India to be necessary for that purpose. <6>2.<5> The executive power of the Union shall also extend to the giving of directions to <5>a State as to the construction and maintenance of means of communication <5>declared in the direction to be of national or military importance: <5>Provided that nothing in this clause shall be taken as restricting the power of <5>Parliament to declare highways or waterways to be national highways or <5>national waterways or the power of the Union with respect to the highways or <5>waterways so declared or the power of the Union to construct and maintain <5>means of communication as part of its functions with respect to naval, military <5>and air force works. <6>3.<5> The executive power of the Union shall also extend to the giving of directions to <5>a State as to the measures to be taken for the protection of the railways within <5>the State. <6>4.<5> Where in carrying out any direction given to a State under clause (2) as to the <5>construction or maintenance of any means of communication or under clause (3) <5>as to the measures to be taken for the protection of any railway, costs have been <5>incurred in excess of those which would have been incurred in the discharge of <5>the normal duties of the State if such direction had not been given, there shall be <5>paid by the Government of India to the State such sum as may be agreed, or, in <5>default of agreement, as may be determined by an arbitrator appointed by the <5>Chief Justice of India, in respect of the extra costs so incurred by the State. <7>257A. Assistance to States by deployment of armed forces <7>or other forces of the Union <5>Rep. by the Constitution <5>(Forty-fourth Amendment) Act, <5>1978, s. <5>33 (w.e.f. <5>20-61979). <7>258. Power of the Union to confer powers, etc., on States in <7>certain cases <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, the President may, with the <5>consent of the Government of a State, entrust either conditionally or <5>unconditionally to that Government or to its officers functions in relation to any <5>matter to which the executive power of the Union extends. <6>2.<5> A law made by Parliament which applies in any State may, notwithstanding that <5>it relates to a matter with respect to which the Legislature of the State has no <5>power to make laws, confer powers and impose duties, or authorise the <5>conferring of powers and the imposition of duties, upon the State or officers and <5>authorities thereof. <6>3.<5> Where by virtue of this article powers and duties have been conferred or <5>imposed upon a State or officers or authorities thereof, there shall be paid by the <5>Government of India to the State such sum as may be agreed, or, in default of <5>agreement, as may be determined by an arbitrator appointed by the Chief <5>Justice of India, in respect of any extra costs of administration incurred by the <5>State in connection with the exercise of those powers and duties. <7>258A. Power of the States to entrust functions to the <7>Union <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, the Governor of a State may, with the <5>consent of the Government of India, entrust either conditionally or unconditionally <5>to that Government or to its officers functions in relation to any matter to which the <5>exclusive power of the State extends. <7>259. Armed Forces in States in Part B of the First Schedule <5>Rep. by the Constitution (Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956 s. 29 and Sch. <7>260. Jurisdiction of the Union in relation to territories <7>outside India <5>The Government of India may by agreement with the Government of any territory <5>not being part of the territory of India undertake any executive, legislative or judicial <5>functions vested in the Government of such territory, but every such agreement <5>shall be subject to, and governed by, any law relating to the exercise of foreign <5>jurisdiction for the time being in force. <7>261. Public acts, records and judicial proceedings <6>1.<5> Full faith and credit shall be given throughout the territory of India to public <5>acts, records and judicial proceedings of the Union and of every State. <6>2.<5> The manner in which and the conditions under which the acts, records and <5>proceedings referred to in clause (1) shall be proved and the effect thereof <5>determined shall be as provided by law made by Parliament. <6>3.<5> Final judgments or orders delivered or passed by civil courts in any part of the <5>territory of India shall be capable of execution anywhere within that territory <5>according to law. <7>Disputes relating to Waters <7>262. Adjudication of disputes relating to waters of <7>inter-State rivers or river valleys <6>1.<5> Parliament may by law provide for the adjudication of any dispute or complaint <5>with respect to the use, distribution or control of the waters of, or in, any <5>inter-State river or river valley. <6>2.<5> Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, Parliament may by law provide <5>that neither the Supreme Court nor any other court shall exercise jurisdiction in <5>respect of any such dispute or complaint as is referred to in clause (1). <7>Co-ordination between States <7>263. Provisions with respect to an inter-State Council <5>If at any time it appears to the President that the public interests would be served by <5>the establishment of a Council charged with the duty of- <6>a.<5> inquiring into and advising upon disputes which may have arisen between <5>States; <6>b.<5> investigating and discussing subjects in which some or all of the States, or <5>the Union and one or more of the States, have a common interest; or <6>c. <5>making recommendations upon any such subject and, in particular, <5>recommendations for the better co-ordination of policy and action with <5>respect to that subject, <5>it shall be lawful for the President by order to establish such a Council, and to define <5>the nature of the duties to be performed by it and its organisation and procedure. <9>PART XII: FINANCE, PROPERTY, <9>CONTRACTS AND SUITS <7>CHAPTER I: FINANCE <7>General <7>264. Interpretation <5>In this Part, "Finance Commission" means a Finance Commission constituted under <5>article 280. <4>• Tax bills <7>265. Taxes not to be imposed save by authority of law <5>No tax shall be levied or collected except by authority of law. <7>266. Consolidated Funds and public accounts of India and <7>of the States <6>1.<5> Subject to the provisions of article 267 and to the provisions of this Chapter <5>with respect to the assignment of the whole or part of the net proceeds of <5>certain taxes and duties to States, all revenues received by the Government of <5>India, all loans raised by that Government by the issue of treasury bills, loans or <5>ways and means advances and all moneys received by that Government in <5>repayment of loans shall form one consolidated fund to be entitled "the <5>Consolidated Fund of India", and all revenues received by the Government of a <5>State, all loans raised by that Government by the issue of treasury bills, loans or <5>ways and means advances and all moneys received by that Government in <5>repayment of loans shall form one consolidated fund to be entitled "the <5>Consolidated Fund of the State" <6>2.<5> All other public moneys received by or on behalf of the Government of India or <5>the Government of a State shall be credited to the public account of India or the <5>public account of the State, as the case may be. <6>3.<5> No moneys out of the Consolidated Fund of India or the Consolidated Fund of a <5>State shall be appropriated except in accordance with law and for the purposes <5>and in the manner provided in this Constitution. <7>267. Contingency Fund <6>1.<5> Parliament may by law establish a Contingency Fund in the nature of an imprest <5>to be entitled "the Contingency Fund of India" into which shall be paid from time <5>to time such sums as may be determined by such law, and the said Fund shall be <5>placed at the disposal of the President to enable advances to be made by him out <5>of such Fund for the purposes of meeting unforeseen expenditure pending <5>authorisation of such expenditure by Parliament by law under article 115 or <5>article 116. <6>2.<5> The Legislature of a State may by law establish a Contingency Fund in the nature <5>of an imprest to be entitled "the Contingency Fund of the State" into which shall <5>be paid from time to time such sums as may be determined by such law, and the <5>said Fund shall be placed at the disposal of the Governor of the State to enable <5>advances to be made by him out of such Fund for the purposes of meeting <5>unforeseen expenditure pending authorisation of such expenditure by the <5>Legislature of the State by law under article 205 or article 206. <7>Distribution of Revenues between the Union and the <7>States <7>268. Duties levied by the Union but collected and <7>appropriated by the States <6>1.<5> Such stamp duties and such duties of excise on medicinal and toilet preparations <5>as are mentioned in the Union List shall be levied by the Government of India <5>but shall be collected- <6>a.<5> in the case where such duties are leviable within any Union territory, by the <5>Government of India, and <6>b.<5> in other cases, by the States within which such duties are respectively <5>leviable. <6>2.<5> The proceeds in any financial year of any such duty leviable within any State <5>shall not form part of the Consolidated Fund of India, but shall be assigned to <5>that State. <7>268A. Service tax levied by Union and collected and <7>appropriated by the Union and the States [NOT YET IN <7>FORCE] <6>1.<5> Taxes on services shall be levied by the Government of India and such tax shall <5>be collected and appropriated by the Government of India and the States in the <5>manner provided in clause (2). <4>• Tax bills <6>2.<5> The proceeds in any financial year of any such tax levied in accordance with the <5>provisions of clause (1) shall be- <6>a.<5> collected by the Government of India and the States; <6>b.<5> appropriated by the Government of India and the States, <5>in accordance with such principles of collection and appropriation as may be <5>formulated by Parliament by law. <7>269. Taxes levied and collected by the Union but assigned <7>to the States <6>1.<5> Taxes on the sale or purchase of goods and taxes on the consignment of goods <5>shall be levied and collected by the Government of India but shall be assigned <5>and shall be deemed to have been assigned to the States on or after the 1st day <5>of April, 1996 in the manner provided in clause (2). <7>Explanation <5>For the purposes of this clause,- <6>a.<5> the expression "taxes on the sale or purchase of goods" shall mean taxes on <5>sale or purchase of goods other than newspapers, where such sale or <5>purchase takes place in the course of inter-State trade or commerce; <6>b.<5> the expression "taxes on the consignment of goods" shall mean taxes on the <5>consignment of goods (whether the consignment is to the person making it <5>or to any other person), where such consignment takes place in the course <5>of inter-State trade or commerce. <6>2.<5> The net proceeds in any financial year of any such tax, except in so far as those <5>proceeds represent proceeds attributable to Union territories, shall not form <5>part of the Consolidated Fund of India, but shall be assigned to the States within <5>which that tax is leviable in that year, and shall be distributed among those <5>States in accordance with such principles of distribution as may be formulated <5>by Parliament by law. <6>3.<5> Parliament may by law formulate principles for determining when a sale or <5>purchase of, or consignment of, goods takes place in the course of inter-State <5>trade or commerce. <7>270. Taxes levied and distributed between the Union and <7>the States <6>1.<5> All taxes and duties referred to in the Union List, except the duties and taxes <5>referred to in articles 268, 268A and 269, respectively, surcharge on taxes and <5>duties referred to in article 271 and any cess levied for specific purposes under <5>any law made by Parliament shall be levied and collected by the Government of <5>India and shall be distributed between the Union and the States in the manner <5>provided in clause (2). <6>2.<5> Such percentage, as may be prescribed, of the net proceeds of any such tax or <5>duty in any financial year shall not form part of the Consolidated Fund of India, <5>but shall be assigned to the States within which that tax or duty is leviable in that <5>year, and shall be distributed among those States in such manner and from such <5>time as may be prescribed in the manner provided in clause (3). <6>3.<5> In this article, "prescribed" means,- <6>i. <5>until a Finance Commission has been constituted, prescribed by the <5>President by order, and <6>ii. <5>after a Finance Commission has been constituted, prescribed by the <5>President by order after considering the recommendations of the Finance <5>Commission. <7>271. Surcharge on certain duties and taxes for purposes of <7>the Union <5>Notwithstanding anything in articles 269 and 270, Parliament may at any time <5>increase any of the duties or taxes referred to in those articles by a surcharge for <5>purposes of the Union and the whole proceeds of any such surcharge shall form part <5>of the Consolidated Fund of India. <7>272. Taxes which are levied and collected by the Union and <7>may be distributed between the Union and the States <5>Omitted by the Constitution (Eightieth Amendment) Act, 2000, s. 4. <7>273. Grants in lieu of export duty on jute and jute products <6>1.<5> There shall be charged on the Consolidated Fund of India in each year as <5>grants-in-aid of the revenues of the States of Assam, Bihar, Orissa and West <5>Bengal, in lieu of assignment of any share of the net proceeds in each year of <5>export duty on jute and jute products to those States, such sums as may be <5>prescribed. <6>2.<5> The sums so prescribed shall continue to be charged on the Consolidated Fund <5>of India so long as any export duty on jute or jute products continues to be levied <5>by the Government of India or until the expiration of ten years from the <5>commencement of this Constitution, whichever is earlier. <6>3.<5> In this article, the expression "prescribed" has the same meaning as in article <5>270. <7>274. Prior recommendation of President require to Bills <7>affecting taxation in which States are interested <6>1.<5> No Bill or amendment which imposes or varies any tax or duty in which States <5>are interested, or which varies the meaning of the expression "agricultural <5>income" as defined for the purposes of the enactments relating to Indian <5>income-tax, or which affects the principles on which under any of the foregoing <5>provisions of this Chapter moneys are or may be distributable to States, or <5>which imposes any such surcharge for the purposes of the Union as is mentioned <5>in the foregoing provisions of this Chapter, shall be introduced or moved in <5>either House of Parliament except on the recommendation of the President. <6>2.<5> In this article, the expression "tax or duty in which States are interested" means- <6>a.<5> a tax or duty the whole or part of the net proceeds whereof are assigned to <5>any State; or <6>b.<5> a tax or duty by reference to the net proceeds whereof sums are for the <5>time being payable out of the Consolidated Fund of India to any State. <7>275. Grants from the Union to certain States <6>1. <5>Such sums as Parliament may by law provide shall be charged on the <5>Consolidated Fund of India in each year as grants-in-aid of the revenues of such <5>States as Parliament may determine to be in need of assistance, and different <5>sums may be fixed for different States: <5>Provided that there shall be paid out of the Consolidated Fund of India as <5>grants-in-aid of the revenues of a State such capital and recurring sums as may <5>be necessary to enable that State to meet the costs of such schemes of <5>development as may be undertaken by the State with the approval of the <5>Government of India for the purpose of promoting the welfare of the Scheduled <5>Tribes in that State or raising the level of administration of the Scheduled Areas <5>therein to that of the administration of the rest of the areas of that State: <5>Provided further that there shall be paid out of the Consolidated Fund of India <5>as grants in-aid of the revenues of the State of Assam sums, capital and <5>recurring, equivalent to- <6>a.<5> the average excess of expenditure over the revenues during the two years <5>immediately preceding the commencement of this Constitution in respect <5>of the administration of the tribal areas specified in Part I of the table <5>appended to paragraph 20 of the Sixth Schedule;
