and <6>b.<5> the costs of such schemes of development as may be undertaken by that <5>State with the approval of the Government of India for the purpose of <5>raising the level of administration of the said areas to that of the <5>administration of the rest of the areas of that State. <6>1A. <5>On and from the formation of the autonomous State under article 244A,- <6>i. <5>any sums payable under clause (a) of the second proviso to clause (1) shall, <5>if the autonomous State comprises all the tribal areas referred to therein, <5>be paid to the autonomous State, and, if the autonomous State comprises <5>only some of those tribal areas, be apportioned between the State of Assam <5>and the autonomous State as the President may, by order, specify; <6>ii. <5>there shall be paid out of the Consolidated Fund of India as grants-in-aid of <5>the revenues of the autonomous State sums, capital and recurring, <5>equivalent to the costs of such schemes of development as may be <5>undertaken by the autonomous State with the approval of the Government <5>of India for the purpose of raising the level of Administration of that State <5>to that of the administration of the rest of the State of Assam. <6>2. <5>Until provision is made by Parliament under clause (1), the powers conferred on <5>Parliament under that clause shall be exercisable by the President by order and <5>any order made by the President under this clause shall have effect subject to <5>any provision so made by Parliament: <5>Provided that after a Finance Commission has been constituted no order shall <5>be made under this clause by the President except after considering the <5>recommendations of the Finance Commission. <7>276. Taxes on professions, trades, callings and <7>employments <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in article 246, no law of the Legislature of a State <5>relating to taxes for the benefit of the State or of a municipality, district board, <5>local board or other local authority therein in respect of professions, trades, <5>callings or employments shall be invalid on the ground that it relates to a tax on <5>income. <6>2.<5> The total amount payable in respect of any one person to the State or to any one <5>municipality, district board, local board or other local authority in the State by <5>way of taxes on professions, trades, callings and employments shall not exceed <5>two thousand and five hundred rupees per annum. <6>3.<5> The power of the Legislature of a State to make laws as aforesaid with respect to <5>taxes on professions, trades, callings and employments shall not be construed as <5>limiting in any way the power of Parliament to make laws with respect to taxes <5>on income accruing from or arising out of professions, trades, callings and <5>employments. <7>277. Savings <5>Any taxes, duties, cesses or fees which, immediately before the commencement of <5>this Constitution, were being lawfully levied by the Government of any State or by <5>any municipality or other local authority or body for the purposes of the State, <5>municipality, district or other local area may, notwithstanding that those taxes, <5>duties, cesses or fees are mentioned in the Union List, continue to be levied and to be <5>applied to the same purposes until provision to the contrary is made by Parliament <5>by law. <7>278. Agreement with States in Part B of the First Schedule <7>with regard to certain financial matters <5>Rep. by the Constitution (Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956, s. 29 and Sch. <7>279. Calculation of "net proceeds", etc <6>1.<5> In the foregoing provisions of this Chapter, "net proceeds" means in relation to <5>any tax or duty the proceeds thereof reduced by the cost of collection, and for <5>the purposes of those provisions the net proceeds of any tax or duty, or of any <5>part of any tax or duty, in or attributable to any area shall be ascertained and <5>certified by the Comptroller and Auditor-General of India, whose certificate <5>shall be final. <6>2.<5> Subject as aforesaid, and to any other express provision of this Chapter, a law <5>made by Parliament or an order of the President may, in any case where under <5>this Part the proceeds of any duty or tax are, or may be, assigned to any State, <5>provide for the manner in which the proceeds are to be calculated, for the time <5>from or at which and the manner in which any payments are to be made, for the <5>making of adjustments between one financial year and another, and for any <5>other incidental or ancillary matters. <7>280. Finance Commission <6>1. <5>The President shall, within two years from the commencement of this <5>Constitution and thereafter at the expiration of every fifth year or at such <5>earlier time as the President considers necessary, by order constitute a Finance <5>Commission which shall consist of a Chairman and four other members to be <5>appointed by the President. <6>2. <5>Parliament may by law determine the qualifications which shall be requisite for <5>appointment as members of the Commission and the manner in which they shall <5>be selected. <6>3. <5>It shall be the duty of the Commission to make recommendations to the <5>President as to- <6>a.<5> the distribution between the Union and the States of the net proceeds of <5>taxes which are to be, or may be, divided between them under this Chapter <5>and the allocation between the States of the respective shares of such <5>proceeds; <6>b.<5> the principles which should govern the grants-in-aid of the revenues of the <5>States out of the Consolidated Fund of India; <6>bb.<5> the measures needed to augment the Consolidated Fund of a State to <5>supplement the resources of the Panchayats in the State on the basis of the <5>recommendations made by the Finance Commission of the State; <6>c. <5>the measures needed to augment the Consolidated Fund of a State to <5>supplement the resources of the Municipalities in the State on the basis of <5>the recommendations made by the Finance Commission of the State; <6>d.<5> any other matter referred to the Commission by the President in the <5>interests of sound finance. <6>4. <5>The Commission shall determine their procedure and shall have such powers in <5>the performance of their functions as Parliament may by law confer on them. <7>281. Recommendations of the Finance Commission <5>The President shall cause every recommendation made by the Finance Commission <5>under the provisions of this Constitution together with an explanatory <5>memorandum as to the action taken thereon to be laid before each House of <5>Parliament. <7>Miscellaneous Financial Provisions <7>282. Expenditure defrayable by the Union or a State out of <7>its revenues <5>The Union or a State may make any grants for any public purpose, notwithstanding <5>that the purpose is not one with respect to which Parliament or the Legislature of <5>the State, as the case may be, may make laws. <7>283. Custody, etc., of Consolidated Funds, Contingency <7>Funds and moneys credited to the public accounts <6>1.<5> The custody of the Consolidated Fund of India and the Contingency Fund of <5>India, the payment of moneys into such Funds, the withdrawal of moneys <5>therefrom, the custody of public moneys other than those credited to such <5>Funds received by or on behalf of the Government of India, their payment into <5>the public account of India and the withdrawal of moneys from such account and <5>all other matters connected with or ancillary to matters aforesaid shall be <5>regulated by law made by Parliament, and, until provision in that behalf is so <5>made, shall be regulated by rules made by the President. <6>2.<5> The custody of the Consolidated Fund of a State and the Contingency Fund of a <5>State, the payment of moneys into such Funds, the withdrawal of moneys <5>therefrom, the custody of public moneys other than those credited to such <5>Funds received by or on behalf of the Government of the State, their payment <5>into the public account of the State and the withdrawal of moneys from such <5>account and all other matters connected with or ancillary to matters aforesaid <5>shall be regulated by law made by the Legislature of the State, and, until <5>provision in that behalf is so made, shall be regulated by rules made by the <5>Governor of the State. <7>284. Custody of suitors- deposits and other moneys <7>received by public servants and courts <5>All moneys received by or deposited with- <6>a.<5> any officer employed in connection with the affairs of the Union or of a <5>State in his capacity as such, other than revenues or public moneys raised <5>or received by the Government of India or the Government of the State, as <5>the case may be, or <6>b.<5> any court within the territory of India to the credit of any cause, matter, <5>account or persons, <5>shall be paid into the public account of India or the public account of State, as the <5>case may be. <7>285. Exemption of property of the Union from State <7>taxation <6>1.<5> The property of the Union shall, save in so far as Parliament may by law <5>otherwise provide, be exempt from all taxes imposed by a State or by any <5>authority within a State. <6>2.<5> Nothing in clause (1) shall, until Parliament by law otherwise provides, prevent <5>any authority within a State from levying any tax on any property of the Union <5>to which such property was immediately before the commencement of this <5>Constitution liable or treated as liable, so long as that tax continues to be levied <5>in that State. <7>286. Restrictions as to imposition of tax on the sale or <7>purchase of goods <6>1.<5> No Law of a State shall impose, or authorise the imposition of, a tax on the sale <5>or purchase of goods where such sale or purchase takes place- <6>a.<5> outside the State; or <6>b.<5> in the course of the import of the goods into, or export of the goods out of, <5>the territory of India. <6>2.<5> Parliament may by law formulate principles for determining when a sale or <5>purchase of goods takes place in any of the ways mentioned in clause (1). <6>3.<5> Any law of a State shall, in so far as it imposes, or authorises the imposition of,- <6>a.<5> a tax on the sale or purchase of goods declared by Parliament by law to be <5>of special importance in inter-State trade or commerce; or <6>b.<5> a tax on the sale or purchase of goods, being a tax of the nature referred to <5>in sub-clause (b), sub-clause (c) or sub-clause (d) of clause (29A) of article <5>366, <5>be subject to such restrictions and conditions in regard to the system of levy, <5>rates and other incidents of the tax as Parliament may by law specify. <7>287. Exemption from taxes on electricity <5>Save in so far as Parliament may by law otherwise provide, no law of a State shall <5>impose, or authorise the imposition of, a tax on the consumption or sale of electricity <5>(whether produced by a Government or other persons) which is- <6>a.<5> consumed by the Government of India, or sold to the Government of India <5>for consumption by that Government; or <6>b.<5> consumed in the construction, maintenance or operation of any railway by <5>the Government of India or a railway company operating that railway, or <5>sold to that Government or any such railway company for consumption in <5>the construction, maintenance or operation of any railway, <5>and any such law imposing, or authorising the imposition of, a tax on the sale of <5>electricity shall secure that the price of electricity sold to the Government of India <5>for consumption by that Government, or to any such railway company as aforesaid <5>for consumption in the construction, maintenance or operation of any railway, shall <5>be less by the amount of the tax than the price charged to other consumers of a <5>substantial quantity of electricity. <7>288. Exemption from taxation by States in respect of water <7>or electricity in certain cases <6>1.<5> Save in so far as the President may by order otherwise provide, no law of a State <5>in force immediately before the commencement of this Constitution shall <5>impose, or authorise the imposition of, a tax in respect of any water or electricity <5>stored, generated, consumed, distributed or sold by any authority established by <5>any existing law or any law made by Parliament for regulating or developing any <5>inter-State river or river-valley. <7>Explanation <5>The expression "law of a State in force" in this clause shall include a law of a State <5>passed or made before the commencement of this Constitution and not previously <5>repealed, notwithstanding that it or parts of it may not be then in operation either at <5>all or in particular areas. <6>2.<5> The Legislature of a State may by law impose, or authorise the imposition of, any <5>such tax as is mentioned in clause (1), but no such law shall have any effect <5>unless it has, after having been reserved for the consideration of the President, <5>received his assent; and if any such law provides for the fixation of the rates and <5>other incidents of such tax by means of rules or orders to be made under the law <5>by any authority, the law shall provide for the previous consent of the President <5>being obtained to the making of any such rule or order. <7>289. Exemption of property and income of a State from <7>Union taxation <6>1.<5> The property and income of a State shall be exempt from Union taxation. <6>2.<5> Nothing in clause (1) shall prevent the Union from imposing, or authorising the <5>imposition of, any tax to such extent, if any, as Parliament may by law provide in <5>respect of a trade or business of any kind carried on by, or on behalf of, the <5>Government of a State, or any operations connected therewith, or any property <5>used or occupied for the purposes of such trade or business, or any income <5>accruing or arising in connection therewith. <6>3.<5> Nothing in clause (2) shall apply to any trade or business, or to any class of trade <5>or business, which Parliament may by law declare to be incidental to the <5>ordinary functions of Government. <7>290. Adjustment in respect of certain expenses and <7>pensions <5>Where under the provisions of this Constitution the expenses of any Court or <5>Commission, or the pension payable to or in respect of a person who has served <5>before the commencement of this Constitution under the Crown in India or after <5>such commencement in connection with the affairs of the Union or of a State, are <5>charged on the Consolidated Fund of India or the Consolidated Fund of a State, then, <5>if- <6>a.<5> in the case of a charge on the Consolidated Fund of India, the court or <5>Commission serves any of the separate needs of a State, or the person has <5>served wholly or in part in connection with the affairs of a State; or <6>b.<5> in the case of a charge on the Consolidated Fund of a State, the court or <5>Commission serves any of the separate needs of the Union or another <5>State, or the person has served wholly or in part in connection with the <5>affairs of the Union or another State, <5>there shall be charged on and paid out of the Consolidated Fund of the State or, as <5>the case may be, the Consolidated Fund of India or the Consolidated Fund of the <5>other State, such contribution in respect of the expenses or pension as may be <5>agreed, or as may in default of agreement be determined by an arbitrator to be <5>appointed by the Chief Justice of India. <7>290A. Annual payment to certain Devaswom Funds <5>A sum of forty-six lakhs and fifty thousand rupees shall be charged on, and paid out <5>of the Consolidated Fund of the State of Kerala every year to the Travancore <5>Devaswom Fund; and a sum of thirteen lakhs and fifty thousand rupees shall be <5>charged on, and paid out of the Consolidated Fund of the State of Tamil Nadu, every <5>year to the Devaswom Fund established in that State for the maintenance of Hindu <5>temples and shrines in the territories transferred to that State on the 1st day of <5>November, 1956, from the State of Travancore-Cochin. <7>291. Privy purse sums of Rulers <5>Rep. by the Constitution (Twenty-sixth Amendment) Act, 1971 s. 2. <7>CHAPTER II: BORROWING <7>292. Borrowing by the Government of India <5>The executive power of the Union extends to borrowing upon the security of the <5>Consolidated Fund of India within such limits, if any, as may from time to time be <5>fixed by Parliament by law and to the giving of guarantees within such limits, if any, <5>as may be so fixed <7>293. Borrowing by States <6>1.<5> Subject to the provisions of this article, the executive power of a State extends <5>to borrowing within the territory of India upon the security of the Consolidated <5>Fund of the State within such limits, if any, as may from time to time be fixed by <5>the Legislature of such State by law and to the giving of guarantees within such <5>limits, if any, as may be so fixed. <6>2.<5> The Government of India may, subject to such conditions as may be laid down by <5>or under any law made by Parliament, make loans to any State or, so long as any <5>limits fixed under article 292 are not exceeded, give guarantees in respect of <5>loans raised by any State, and any sums required for the purpose of making such <5>loans shall be charged on the Consolidated Fund of India. <6>3.<5> A State may not without the consent of the Government of India raise any loan if <5>there is still outstanding any part of a loan which has been made to the State by <5>the Government of India or by its predecessor Government, or in respect of <5>which a guarantee has been given by the Government of India or by its <5>predecessor Government. <6>4.<5> A consent under clause (3) may be granted subject to such conditions, if any, as <5>the Government of India may think fit to impose. <7>CHAPTER III: PROPERTY, CONTRACTS, RIGHTS, <7>LIABILITIES, OBLIGATIONS AND SUITS <7>294. Succession to property, assets, rights, liabilities and <7>obligations in certain cases <5>As from the commencement of this Constitution- <6>a.<5> all property and assets which immediately before such commencement <5>were vested in His Majesty for the purposes of the Government of the <5>Dominion of India and all property and assets which immediately before <5>such commencement were vested in His Majesty for the purposes of the <5>Government of each Governor's Province shall vest respectively in the <5>Union and the corresponding State, and <6>b.<5> all rights, liabilities and obligations of the Government of the Dominion of <5>India and of the Government of each Governor's Province, whether arising <5>out of any contract or otherwise, shall be the rights, liabilities and <5>obligations respectively of the Government of India and the Government of <5>each corresponding State, <5>subject to any adjustment made or to be made by reason of the creation before the <5>commencement of this Constitution of the Dominion of Pakistan or of the Provinces <5>of West Bengal, East Bengal, West Punjab and East Punjab. <7>295. Succession to property, assets, rights, liabilities and <7>obligations in other cases <6>1.<5> As from the commencement of this Constitution- <6>a.<5> all property and assets which immediately before such commencement <5>were vested in any Indian State corresponding to a State specified in Part B <5>of the First Schedule shall vest in the Union, if the purposes for which such <5>property and assets were held immediately before such commencement <5>will thereafter be purposes of the Union relating to any of the matters <5>enumerated in the Union List, and <6>b.<5> all rights, liabilities and obligations of the Government of any Indian State <5>corresponding to a State specified in Part B of the First Schedule, whether <5>arising out of any contract or otherwise, shall be the rights, liabilities and <5>obligations of the Government of India, if the purposes for which such <5>rights were acquired or liabilities or obligations were incurred before such <5>commencement will thereafter be purposes of the Government of India <5>relating to any of the matters enumerated in the Union List, <5>subject to any agreement entered into in that behalf by the Government of India <5>with the Government of that State. <6>2.<5> Subject as aforesaid, the Government of each State specified in Part B of the <5>First Schedule shall, as from the commencement of this Constitution, be the <5>successor of the Government of the corresponding Indian State as regards all <5>property and assets and all rights, liabilities and obligations, whether arising out <5>of any contract or otherwise, other than those referred to in clause (1). <7>296. Property accruing by escheat or lapse or as Bona <7>vacantia <5>Subject as hereinafter provided, any property in the territory of India which, if this <5>Constitution had not come into operation, would have accrued to His Majesty or, as <5>the case may be, to the Ruler of an Indian State by escheat or lapse, or as bona <5>vacantia for want of a rightful owner, shall, if it is property situate in a State, vest in <5>such State, and shall, in any other case, vest in the Union: <5>Provided that any property which at the date when it would have so accrued to His <5>Majesty or to the Ruler of an Indian State was in the possession or under the control <5>of the Government of India or the Government of a State shall, according as the <5>purposes for which it was then used or held were purposes of the Union or of a State, <5>vest in the Union or in that State. <7>Explanation <5>In this article, the expressions "Rulers" and "Indian State" have the same meanings as <5>in article 363. <4>• Ownership of natural resources <7>297. Things of value within territorial waters or <7>continental shelf and resources of the exclusive economic <7>zone to vest in the Union <6>1.<5> All lands, minerals and other things of value underlying the ocean within the <5>territorial waters, or the continental shelf, or the exclusive economic zone, of <5>India shall vest in the Union and be held for the purposes of the Union. <6>2.<5> All other resources of the exclusive economic zone of India shall also vest in the <5>Union and be held for the purposes of the Union. <6>3.<5> The limits of the territorial waters, the continental shelf, the exclusive economic <5>zone, and other maritime zones, of India shall be such as may be specified, from <5>time to time, by or under any law made by Parliament. <7>298. Power to carry on trade, etc <5>The executive power of the Union and of each State shall extend to the carrying on of <5>any trade or business and to the acquisition, holding and disposal of property and the <5>making of contracts for any purpose: <5>Provided that- <6>a.<5> the said executive power of the Union shall, in so far as such trade or <5>business or such purpose is not one with respect to which Parliament may <5>make laws, be subject in each State to legislation by the State; and <6>b.<5> the said executive power of each State shall, in so far as such trade or <5>business or such purpose is not one with respect to which the State <5>Legislature may make laws, be subject to legislation by Parliament. <7>299. Contracts <6>1.<5> All contracts made in the exercise of the executive power of the Union or of a <5>State shall be expressed to be made by the President, or by the Governor of the <5>State, as the case may be, and all such contracts and all assurances of property <5>made in the exercise of that power shall be executed on behalf of the President <5>or the Governor by such persons and in such manner as he may direct or <5>authorise. <6>2.<5> Neither the President nor the Governor shall be personally liable in respect of <5>any contract or assurance made or executed for the purposes of this <5>Constitution, or for the purposes of any enactment relating to the Government <5>of India heretofore in force, nor shall any person making or executing any such <5>contract or assurance on behalf of any of them be personally liable in respect <5>thereof. <7>300. Suits and proceedings <6>1.<5> The Government of India may sue or be sued by the name of the Union of India <5>and the Government of a State may sue or be sued by the name of the State and <5>may, subject to any provisions which may be made by Act of Parliament or of the <5>Legislature of such State enacted by virtue of powers conferred by this <5>Constitution, sue or be sued in relation to their respective affairs in the like <5>cases as the Dominion of India and the corresponding Provinces or the <5>corresponding Indian States might have sued or been sued if this Constitution <5>had not been enacted. <6>2.<5> If at the commencement of this Constitution- <6>a.<5> any legal proceedings are pending to which the Dominion of India is a party, <5>the Union of India shall be deemed to be substituted for the Dominion in <5>those proceedings; and <6>b.<5> any legal proceedings are pending to which a Province or an Indian State is <5>a party, the corresponding State shall be deemed to be substituted for the <5>Province or the Indian State in those proceedings. <7>CHAPTER IV: RIGHT TO PROPERTY <4>• Protection from expropriation <7>300A. Persons not to be deprived of property save by <4>• Right to own property <7>authority of law <5>No person shall be deprived of his property save by authority of law. <9>PART XIII: TRADE, COMMERCE AND <9>INTERCOURSE WITHIN THE TERRITORY OF <9>INDIA <7>301. Freedom of trade, commerce and intercourse <5>Subject to the other provisions of this Part, trade, commerce and intercourse <5>throughout the territory of India shall be free. <7>302. Power of Parliament to impose restrictions on trade, <7>commerce and intercourse <5>Parliament may by law impose such restrictions on the freedom of trade, commerce <5>or intercourse between one State and another or within any part of the territory of <5>India as may be required in the public interest. <7>303. Restrictions on the legislative powers of the Union <7>and of the States with regard to trade and commerce <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in article 302, neither Parliament nor the Legislature <5>of a State shall have power to make any law giving, or authorising the giving of, <5>any preference to one State over another, or making, or authorising the making <5>of, any discrimination between one State and another, by virtue of any entry <5>relating to trade and commerce in any of the Lists in the Seventh Schedule. <6>2.<5> Nothing in clause (1) shall prevent Parliament from making any law giving, or <5>authorising the giving of, any preference or making, or authorising the making <5>of, any discrimination if it is declared by such law that it is necessary to do so for <5>the purpose of dealing with a situation arising from scarcity of goods in any part <5>of the territory of India. <7>304. Restrictions on trade, commerce and intercourse <7>among States <5>Notwithstanding anything in article 301 or article 303, the Legislature of a State may <5>by law- <6>a.<5> impose on goods imported from other States or the Union territories any <5>tax to which similar goods manufactured or produced in that State are <5>subject, so, however, as not to discriminate between goods so imported and <5>goods so manufactured or produced; and <6>b.<5> impose such reasonable restrictions on the freedom of trade, commerce or <5>intercourse with or within that State as may be required in the public <5>interest: <5>Provided that no Bill or amendment for the purposes of clause (b) shall be introduced <5>or moved in the Legislature of a State without the previous sanction of the President. <7>305. Saving of existing laws and laws providing for State <7>monopolies <5>Nothing in articles 301 and 303 shall affect the provisions of any existing law except <5>in so far as the President may by order otherwise direct; and nothing in article 301 <5>shall affect the operation of any law made before the commencement of the <5>Constitution (Fourth Amendment) Act, 1955, in so far as it relates to, or prevent <5>Parliament or the Legislature of a State from making any law relating to, any such <5>matter as is referred to in sub-clause (ii) of clause (6) of article 19. <7>306. Power of certain States in Part B of the First Schedule <7>to impose restrictions on trade and commerce <5>Rep. by the Constitution (Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956, s. 29 and Sch. <7>307. Appointment of authority for carrying out the <7>purposes of articles 301 to 304 <5>Parliament may by law appoint such authority as it considers appropriate for <5>carrying out the purposes of articles 301, 302, 303 and 304, and confer on the <5>authority so appointed such powers and such duties as it thinks necessary. <9>PART XIV: SERVICES UNDER THE UNION <9>AND THE STATES <7>CHAPTER I: SERVICES <7>308. Interpretation <5>In this Part, unless the context otherwise requires, the expression "State" does not <5>include the State of Jammu and Kashmir. <7>309. Recruitment and conditions of service of persons <7>serving the Union or a State <5>Subject to the provisions of this Constitution, Acts of the appropriate Legislature <5>may regulate the recruitment, and conditions of service of persons appointed, to <5>public services and posts in connection with the affairs of the Union or of any State: <5>Provided that it shall be competent for the President or such person as he may direct <5>in the case of services and posts in connection with the affairs of the Union, and for <5>the Governor of a State or such person as he may direct in the case of services and <5>posts in connection with the affairs of the State, to make rules regulating the <5>recruitment, and the conditions of service of persons appointed, to such services and <5>posts until provision in that behalf is made by or under an Act of the appropriate <5>Legislature under this article, and any rules so made shall have effect subject to the <5>provisions of any such Act. <7>310. Tenure of office of persons serving the Union or a <7>State <6>1.<5> Except as expressly provided by this Constitution, every person who is a <5>member of a defence service or of a civil service of the Union or of an all-India <5>service or holds any post connected with defence or any civil post under the <5>Union holds office during the pleasure of the President, and every person who is <5>a member of a civil service of a State or holds any civil post under a State holds <5>office during the pleasure of the Governor of the State. <6>2.<5> Notwithstanding that a person holding a civil post under the Union or a State <5>holds office during the pleasure of the President or, as the case may be, of the <5>Governor of the State, any contract under which a person, not being a member <5>of a defence service or of an all-India service or of a civil service of the Union or a <5>State, is appointed under this Constitution to hold such a post may, if the <5>President or the Governor, as the case may be, deems it necessary in order to <5>secure the services of a person having special qualifications, provide for the <5>payment to him of compensation, if before the expiration of an agreed period <5>that post is abolished or he is, for reasons not connected with any misconduct on <5>his part, required to vacate that post. <7>311. Dismissal, removal or reduction in rank of persons <7>employed in civil capacities under the Union or a State <6>1. <5>No person who is a member of a civil service of the Union or an all-India service <5>or a civil service of a State or holds a civil post under the Union or a State shall be <5>dismissed or removed by an authority subordinate to that by which he was <5>appointed. <6>2. <5>No such person as aforesaid shall be dismissed or removed or reduced in rank <5>except after an inquiry in which he has been informed of the charges against him <5>and given a reasonable opportunity of being heard in respect of those charges: <5>Provided that where it is proposed after such inquiry, to impose upon him any <5>such penalty, such penalty may be imposed on the basis of the evidence adduced <5>during such inquiry and it shall not be necessary to give such person any <5>opportunity of making representation on the penalty proposed: <5>Provided further that this clause shall not apply- <6>a.<5> where a person is dismissed or removed or reduced in rank on the ground <5>of conduct which has led to his conviction on a criminal charge; or <6>b.<5> where the authority empowered to dismiss or remove a person or to <5>reduce him in rank is satisfied that for some reason, to be recorded by that <5>authority in writing, it is not reasonably practicable to hold such inquiry; or <6>c. <5>where the President or the Governor, as the case may be, is satisfied that in <5>the interest of the security of the State it is not expedient to hold such <5>inquiry. <6>3. <5>If, in respect of any such person as aforesaid, a question arises whether it is <5>reasonably practicable to hold such inquiry as is referred to in clause (2), the <5>decision thereon of the authority empowered to dismiss or remove such person <5>or to reduce him in rank shall be final. <7>312. All-India services <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in Chapter VI of Part VI or Part XI, if the Council of <5>States has declared by resolution supported by not less than two-thirds of the <5>members present and voting that it is necessary or expedient in the national <5>interest so to do, Parliament may by law provide for the creation of one or more <5>all-India services (including an all-India judicial service) common to the Union <5>and the States, and, subject to the other provisions of this Chapter, regulate the <5>recruitment, and the conditions of service of persons appointed, to any such <5>service. <6>2.<5> The services known at the commencement of this Constitution as the Indian <5>Administrative Service and the Indian Police Service shall be deemed to be <5>services created by Parliament under this article. <6>3.<5> The all-India judicial service referred to in clause (1) shall not include any post <5>inferior to that of a district judge as defined in article 236. <6>4.<5> The law providing for the creation of the all-India judicial service aforesaid may <5>contain such provisions for the amendment of Chapter VI of Part VI as may be <5>necessary for giving effect to the provisions of that law and no such law shall be <5>deemed to be an amendment of this Constitution for the purposes of article 368. <7>312A. Power of Parliament to vary or revoke conditions of <7>service of officers of certain services <6>1. <5>Parliament may by law- <6>a.<5> vary or revoke, whether prospectively or retrospectively, the conditions of <5>service as respects remuneration, leave and pension and the rights as <5>respects disciplinary matters of persons who, having been appointed by the <5>Secretary of State or Secretary of State in Council to a civil service of the <5>Crown in India before the commencement of this Constitution, continue on <5>and after the commencement of the Constitution <5>(Twenty-eighth <5>Amendment) Act, 1972, to serve under the Government of India or of a <5>State in any service or post; <6>b.<5> vary or revoke, whether prospectively or retrospectively, the conditions of <5>service as respects pension of persons who, having been appointed by the <5>Secretary of State or Secretary of State in Council to a civil service of the <5>Crown in India before the commencement of this Constitution, retired or <5>otherwise ceased to be in service at any time before the commencement of <5>the Constitution (Twenty-eighth Amendment) Act, 1972: <5>Provided that in the case of any such person who is holding or has held the office <5>of the Chief Justice or other Judge of the Supreme Court or a High Court, the <5>Comptroller and Auditor-General of India, the Chairman or other member of the <5>Union or a State Public Service Commission or the Chief Election Commissioner, <5>nothing in sub-clause (a) or sub-clause (b) shall be construed as empowering <5>Parliament to vary or revoke, after his appointment to such post, the conditions <5>of his service to his disadvantage except in so far as such conditions of service <5>are applicable to him by reason of his being a person appointed by the Secretary <5>of State or Secretary of State in Council to a civil service of the Crown in India. <6>2. <5>Except to the extent provided for by Parliament by law under this article, <5>nothing in this article shall affect the power of any legislature or other authority <5>under any other provision of this Constitution to regulate the conditions of <5>service of persons referred to in clause (1). <6>3.<5> Neither the Supreme Court nor any other court shall have jurisdiction in- <6>a.<5> any dispute arising out of any provision of, or any endorsement on, any <5>covenant, agreement or other similar instrument which was entered into or <5>executed by any person referred to in clause (1), or arising out of any letter <5>issued to such person, in relation to his appointment to any civil service of <5>the Crown in India or his continuance in service under the Government of <5>the Dominion of India or a Province thereof; <6>b.<5> any dispute in respect of any right, liability or obligation under article 314 <5>as originally enacted. <6>4.<5> The provisions of this article shall have effect notwithstanding anything in <5>article 314 as originally enacted or in any other provision of this Constitution. <4>• Transitional provisions <7>313. Transitional provisions <5>Until other provision is made in this behalf under this Constitution, all the laws in <5>force immediately before the commencement of this Constitution and applicable to <5>any public service or any post which continues to exist after the commencement of <5>this Constitution, as an all-India service or as service or post under the Union or a <5>State shall continue in force so far as consistent with the provisions of this <5>Constitution. <7>314. Provision for protection of existing officers of certain <7>services <5>Rep. by the Constitution <5>(Twenty-eighth Amendment) Act, 1972, s. <5>3, w.e.f. <5>29-8-1972. <7>CHAPTER II: PUBLIC SERVICE COMMISSIONS <7>315. Public Service Commissions for the Union and for the <7>States <6>1.<5> Subject to the provisions of this article, there shall be a Public Service <5>Commission for the Union and a Public Service Commission for each State. <6>2.<5> Two or more States may agree that there shall be one Public Service <5>Commission for that group of States, and if a resolution to that effect is passed <5>by the House or, where there are two Houses, by each House of the Legislature <5>of each of those States, Parliament may by law provide for the appointment of a <5>Joint State Public Service Commission (referred to in this Chapter as Joint <5>Commission) to serve the needs of those States. <6>3.<5> Any such law as aforesaid may contain such incidental and consequential <5>provisions as may be necessary or desirable for giving effect to the purposes of <5>the law. <6>4.<5> The Public Service Commission for the Union, if requested so to do by the <5>Governor of a State, may, with the approval of the President, agree to serve all <5>or any of the needs of the State. <6>5.<5> References in this Constitution to the Union Public Service Commission or a <5>State Public Service Commission shall, unless the context otherwise requires, be <5>construed as references to the Commission serving the needs of the Union or, as <5>the case may be, the State as respects the particular matter in question. <7>316. Appointment and term of office of members <6>1. <5>The Chairman and other members of a Public Service Commission shall be <5>appointed, in the case of the Union Commission or a Joint Commission, by the <5>President, and in the case of a State Commission, by the Governor of the State: <5>Provided that as nearly as may be one-half of the members of every Public <5>Service Commission shall be persons who at the dates of their respective <5>appointments have held office for at least ten years either under the <5>Government of India or under the Government of a State, and in computing the <5>said period of ten years any period before the commencement of this <5>Constitution during which a person has held office under the Crown in India or <5>under the Government of an Indian State shall be included. <6>1A. <5>If the office of the Chairman of the Commission becomes vacant or if any such <5>Chairman is by reason of absence or for any other reason unable to perform the <5>duties of his office, those duties shall, until some person appointed under clause <5>(1) to the vacant office has entered on the duties thereof or, as the case may be, <5>until the Chairman has resumed his duties, be performed by such one of the <5>other members of the Commission as the President, in the case of the Union <5>Commission or a Joint Commission, and the Governor of the State in the case of <5>a State Commission, may appoint for the purpose. <6>2. <5>A member of a Public Service Commission shall hold office for a term of six years <5>from the date on which he enters upon his office or until he attains, in the case of <5>the Union Commission, the age of sixty-five years, and in the case of a State <5>Commission or a Joint Commission, the age of sixty-two years, whichever is <5>earlier: <5>Provided that- <6>a.<5> a member of a Public Service Commission may, by writing under his hand <5>addressed, in the case of the Union Commission or a Joint Commission, to <5>the President, and in the case of a State Commission, to the Governor of the <5>State, resign his office; <6>b.<5> a member of a Public Service Commission may be removed from his office <5>in the manner provided in clause (1) or clause (3) of article 317. <6>3. <5>A person who holds office as a member of a Public Service Commission shall, on <5>the expiration of his term of office, be ineligible for re-appointment to that <5>office. <7>317. Removal and suspension of a member of a Public <7>Service Commission <6>1.<5> Subject to the provisions of clause (3), the Chairman or any other member of a <5>Public Service Commission shall only be removed from his office by order of the <5>President on the ground of misbehaviour after the Supreme Court, on reference <5>being made to it by the President, has, on inquiry held in accordance with the <5>procedure prescribed in that behalf under article 145, reported that the <5>Chairman or such other member, as the case may be, ought on any such ground <5>to be removed. <6>2.<5> The President, in the case of the Union Commission or a Joint Commission, and <5>the Governor in the case of a State Commission, may suspend from office the <5>Chairman or any other member of the Commission in respect of whom a <5>reference has been made to the Supreme Court under clause (1) until the <5>President has passed orders on receipt of the report of the Supreme Court on <5>such reference. <6>3.<5> Notwithstanding anything in clause (1), the President may by order remove from <5>office the Chairman or any other member of a Public Service Commission if the <5>Chairman or such other member, as the case may be,- <6>a.<5> is adjudged an insolvent; or <6>b.<5> engages during his term of office in any paid employment outside the duties <5>of his office; or <6>c. <5>is, in the opinion of the President, unfit to continue in office by reason of <5>infirmity of mind or body. <6>4.<5> If the Chairman or any other member of a Public Service Commission is or <5>becomes in any way concerned or interested in any contract or agreement made <5>by or on behalf of the Government of India or the Government of a State or <5>participates in any way in the profit thereof or in any benefit or emolument <5>arising therefrom otherwise than as a member and in common with the other <5>members of an incorporated company, he shall, for the purposes of clause (1), be <5>deemed to be guilty of misbehaviour. <7>318. Power to make regulations as to conditions of service <7>of members and staff of the Commission <5>In the case of the Union Commission or a Joint Commission, the President and, in the <5>case of a State Commission, the Governor of the State may by regulations- <6>a.<5> determine the number of members of the Commission and their conditions <5>of service; and <6>b.<5> make provision with respect to the number of members of the staff of the <5>Commission and their conditions of service: <5>Provided that the conditions of service of a member of a Public Service Commission <5>shall not be varied to his disadvantage after his appointment. <7>319. Prohibition as to the holding of offices by members of <7>Commission on ceasing to be such members <5>On ceasing to hold office- <6>a.<5> the Chairman of the Union Public Service Commission shall be ineligible for <5>further employment either under the Government of India or under the <5>Government of a State; <6>b.<5> the Chairman of a State Public Service Commission shall be eligible for <5>appointment as the Chairman or any other member of the Union Public <5>Service Commission or as the Chairman of any other State Public Service <5>Commission, but not for any other employment either under the <5>Government of India or under the Government of a State; <6>c. <5>a member other than the Chairman of the Union Public Service Commission <5>shall be eligible for appointment as the Chairman of the Union Public <5>Service Commission or as the Chairman of a State Public Service <5>Commission, but not for any other employment either under the <5>Government of India or under the Government of a State; <6>d.<5> a member other than the Chairman of a State Public Service Commission <5>shall be eligible for appointment as the Chairman or any other member of <5>the Union Public Service Commission or as the Chairman of that or any <5>other State Public Service Commission, but not for any other employment <5>either under the Government of India or under the Government of a State. <7>320. Functions of Public Service Commissions <4>• Civil service recruitment <6>1. <5>It shall be the duty of the Union and the State Public Service Commissions to <5>conduct examinations for appointment to the services of the Union and the <5>services of the State respectively. <6>2. <5>It shall also be the duty of the Union Public Service Commission, if requested by <5>any two or more States so to do, to assist those States in framing and operating <5>schemes of joint recruitment for any services for which candidates possessing <5>special qualifications are required. <6>3. <5>The Union Public Service Commission or the State Public Service Commission, <5>as the case may be, shall be consulted- <6>a.<5> on all matters relating to methods of recruitment to civil services and for <5>civil posts; <6>b.<5> on the principles to be followed in making appointments to civil services <5>and posts and in making promotions and transfers from one service to <5>another and on the suitability of candidates for such appointments, <5>promotions or transfers; <6>c. <5>on all disciplinary matters affecting a person serving under the Government <5>of India or the Government of a State in a civil capacity, including <5>memorials or petitions relating to such matters; <6>d.<5> on any claim by or in respect of a person who is serving or has served under <5>the Government of India or the Government of a State or under the Crown <5>in India or under the Government of an Indian State, in a civil capacity, that <5>any costs incurred by him in defending legal proceedings instituted against <5>him in respect of acts done or purporting to be done in the execution of his <5>duty should be paid out of the Consolidated Fund of India, or, as the case <5>may be, out of the Consolidated Fund of the State; <6>e.<5> on any claim for the award of a pension in respect of injuries sustained by a <5>person while serving under the Government of India or the Government of <5>a State or under the Crown in India or under the Government of an Indian <5>State, in a civil capacity, and any question as to the amount of any such <5>award, <5>and it shall be the duty of a Public Service Commission to advise on any matter <5>so referred to them and on any other matter which the President, or, as the case <5>may be, the Governor of the State, may refer to them: <5>Provided that the President as respects the all-India services and also as <5>respects other services and posts in connection with the affairs of the Union, <5>and the Governor, as respects other services and posts in connection with the <5>affairs of a State, may make regulations specifying the matters in which either <5>generally, or in any particular class of case or in any particular circumstances, it <5>shall not be necessary for a Public Service Commission to be consulted. <6>4.<5> Nothing in clause (3) shall require a Public Service Commission to be consulted <5>as respects the manner in which any provision referred to in clause (4) of article <5>16 may be made or as respects the manner in which effect may be given to the <5>provisions of article 335. <6>5.<5> All regulations made under the proviso to clause (3) by the President or the <5>Governor of a State shall be laid for not less than fourteen days before each <5>House of Parliament or the House or each House of the Legislature of the State, <5>as the case may be, as soon as possible after they are made, and shall be subject <5>to such modifications, whether by way of repeal or amendment, as both Houses <5>of Parliament or the House or both Houses of the Legislature of the State may <5>make during the session in which they are so laid. <7>321. Power to extend functions of Public Service <7>Commissions <5>An Act made by Parliament or, as the case may be, the Legislature of a State may <5>provide for the exercise of additional functions by the Union Public Service <5>Commission or the State Public Service Commission as respects the services of the <5>Union or the State and also as respects the services of any local authority or other <5>body corporate constituted by law or of any public institution. <7>322. Expenses of Public Service Commissions <5>The expenses of the Union or a State Public Service Commission, including any <5>salaries, allowances and pensions payable to or in respect of the members or staff of <5>the Commission, shall be charged on the Consolidated Fund of India or, as the case <5>may be, the Consolidated Fund of the State. <7>323. Reports of Public Service Commissions <6>1.<5> It shall be the duty of the Union Commission to present annually to the <5>President a report as to the work done by the Commission and on receipt of <5>such report the President shall cause a copy thereof together with a <5>memorandum explaining, as respects the cases, if any, where the advice of the <5>Commission was not accepted, the reasons for such non-acceptance to be laid <5>before each House of Parliament. <6>2.<5> It shall be the duty of a State Commission to present annually to the Governor of <5>the State a report as to the work done by the Commission, and it shall be the <5>duty of a Joint Commission to present annually to the Governor of each of the <5>States the needs of which are served by the Joint Commission a report as to the <5>work done by the Commission in relation to that State, and in either case the <5>Governor, shall, on receipt of such report, cause a copy thereof together with a <5>memorandum explaining, as respects the cases, if any, where the advice of the <5>Commission was not accepted, the reasons for such non-acceptance to be laid <5>before the Legislature of the State. <9>PART XIVA: TRIBUNALS <7>323A. Administrative tribunals <6>1. <5>Parliament may, by law, provide for the adjudication or trial by administrative <5>tribunals of disputes and complaints with respect to recruitment and conditions <5>of service of persons appointed to public services and posts in connection with <5>the affairs of the Union or of any State or of any local or other authority within <5>the territory of India or under the control of the Government of India or of any <5>corporation owned or controlled by the Government. <6>2. <5>A law made under clause (1) may- <6>a. <5>provide for the establishment of an administrative tribunal for the Union <5>and a separate administrative tribunal for each State or for two or more <5>States; <6>b. <5>specify the jurisdiction, powers <5>(including the power to punish for <5>contempt) and authority which may be exercised by each of the said <5>tribunals; <6>c. <5>provide for the procedure (including provisions as to limitation and rules of <5>evidence) to be followed by the said tribunals; <6>d. <5>exclude the jurisdiction of all courts, except the jurisdiction of the Supreme <5>Court under article 136, with respect to the disputes or complaints <5>referred to in clause (1); <6>e. <5>provide for the transfer to each such administrative tribunal of any cases <5>pending before any court or other authority immediately before the <5>establishment of such tribunal as would have been within the jurisdiction of <5>such tribunal if the causes of action on which such suits or proceedings are <5>based had arisen after such establishment; <6>f. <5>repeal or amend any order made by the President under clause (3) of article <5>371D; <6>g. <5>contain such supplemental, incidental and consequential provisions <5>(including provisions as to fees) as Parliament may deem necessary for the <5>effective functioning of, and for the speedy disposal of cases by, and the <5>enforcement of the orders of, such tribunals. <6>3. <5>The provisions of this article shall have effect notwithstanding anything in any <5>other provision of this Constitution or in any other law for the time being in <5>force. <7>323B. Tribunals for other matters <6>1.<5> The appropriate Legislature may, by law, provide for the adjudication or trial by <5>tribunals of any disputes, complaints, or offences with respect to all or any of the <5>matters specified in clause (2) with respect to which such Legislature has power <5>to make laws. <6>2. <5>The matters referred to in clause (1) are the following, namely:- <6>a. <5>levy, assessment, collection and enforcement of any tax; <6>b. <5>foreign exchange, import and export across customs frontiers; <6>c. <5>industrial and labour disputes; <6>d. <5>land reforms by way of acquisition by the State of any estate as defined in <5>article 31A or of any rights therein or the extinguishment or modification of <5>any such rights or by way of ceiling on agricultural land or in any other way; <6>e. <5>ceiling on urban property; <6>f. <5>elections to either House of Parliament or the House or either House of the <5>Legislature of a State, but excluding the matters referred to in article 329 <5>and article 329A; <6>g. <5>production, procurement, supply and distribution of food-stuffs (including <5>edible oilseeds and oils) and such other goods as the President may, by <5>public notification, declare to be essential goods for the purpose of this <5>article and control of prices of such goods; <6>h. <5>rent, its regulation and control and tenancy issues including the right, title <5>and interest of landlords and tenants; <6>i. <5>offences against laws with respect to any of the matters specified in <5>sub-clauses (a) to (h) and fees in respect of any of those matters; <6>j. <5>any matter incidental to any of the matters specified in sub-clauses (a) to (i). <6>3. <5>A law made under clause (1) may- <6>a.<5> provide for the establishment of a hierarchy of tribunals; <6>b.<5> specify the jurisdiction, powers <5>(including the power to punish for <5>contempt) and authority which may be exercised by each of the said <5>tribunals; <6>c. <5>provide for the procedure (including provisions as to limitation and rules of <5>evidence) to be followed by the said tribunals; <6>d.<5> exclude the jurisdiction of all courts, except the jurisdiction of the Supreme <5>Court under article 136, with respect to all or any of the matters falling <5>within the jurisdiction of the said tribunals; <6>e.<5> provide for the transfer to each such tribunal of any cases pending before <5>any court or any other authority immediately before the establishment of <5>such tribunal as would have been within the jurisdiction of such tribunal if <5>the causes of action on which such suits or proceedings are based had <5>arisen after such establishment; <6>f. <5>contain such supplemental, incidental and consequential provisions <5>(including provisions as to fees) as the appropriate Legislature may deem <5>necessary for the effective functioning of, and for the speedy disposal of <5>cases by, and the enforcement of the orders of, such tribunals. <6>4.<5> The provisions of this article shall have effect notwithstanding anything in any <5>other provision of this Constitution or in any other law for the time being in <5>force. <7>Explanation <5>In this article, "appropriate Legislature", in relation to any matter, means Parliament <5>or, as the case may be, a State Legislature competent to make laws with respect to <5>such matter in accordance with the provisions of Part XI. <9>PART XV: ELECTIONS <4>• Electoral commission <7>324. Superintendence, direction and control of elections to <7>be vested in an Election Commission <6>1. <5>The superintendence, direction and control of the preparation of the electoral <5>rolls for, and the conduct of, all elections to Parliament and to the Legislature of <5>every State and of elections to the offices of President and Vice-President held <5>under this Constitution shall be vested in a Commission (referred to in this <5>Constitution as the Election Commission). <6>2. <5>The Election Commission shall consist of the Chief Election Commissioner and <5>such number of other Election Commissioners, if any, as the President may from <5>time to time fix and the appointment of the Chief Election Commissioner and <5>other Election Commissioners shall, subject to the provisions of any law made in <5>that behalf by Parliament, be made by the President. <6>3. <5>When any other Election Commissioner is so appointed the Chief Election <5>Commissioner shall act as the Chairman of the Election Commission. <6>4. <5>Before each general election to the House of the People and to the Legislative <5>Assembly of each State, and before the first general election and thereafter <5>before each biennial election to the Legislative Council of each State having such <5>Council, the President may also appoint after consultation with the Election <5>Commission such Regional Commissioners as he may consider necessary to <5>assist the Election Commission in the performance of the functions conferred on <5>the Commission by clause (1). <6>5. <5>Subject to the provisions of any law made by Parliament, the conditions of <5>service and tenure of office of the Election Commissioners and the Regional <5>Commissioners shall be such as the President may by rule determine: <5>Provided that the Chief Election Commissioner shall not be removed from his <5>office except in like manner and on the like grounds as a Judge of the Supreme <5>Court and the conditions of service of the Chief Election Commissioner shall not <5>be varied to his disadvantage after his appointment: <5>Provided further that any other Election Commissioner or a Regional <5>Commissioner shall not be removed from office except on the recommendation <5>of the Chief Election Commissioner. <6>6.<5> The President, or the Governor of a State, shall, when so requested by the <5>Election Commission, make available to the Election Commission or to a <5>Regional Commissioner such staff as may be necessary for the discharge of the <5>functions conferred on the Election Commission by clause (1). <7>325. No person to be ineligible for inclusion in, or to claim <7>to be included in a special, electoral roll on grounds of <7>religion, race, caste or sex <5>There shall be one general electoral roll for every territorial constituency for <5>election to either House of Parliament or to the House or either House of the <5>Legislature of a State and no person shall be ineligible for inclusion in any such roll or <5>claim to be included in any special electoral roll for any such constituency on grounds <5>only of religion, race, caste, sex or any of them. <4>• Restrictions on voting <7>326. Elections to the House of the People and to the <4>• Claim of universal suffrage <7>Legislative Assemblies of States to be on the basis of adult <7>suffrage <5>The elections to the House of the People and to the Legislative Assembly of every <5>State shall be on the basis of adult suffrage; that is to say, every person who is a <5>citizen of India and who is not less than eighteen years of age on such date as may be <5>fixed in that behalf by or under any law made by the appropriate Legislature and is <5>not otherwise disqualified under this Constitution or any law made by the <5>appropriate Legislature on the ground of non-residence, unsoundness of mind, crime <5>or corrupt or illegal practice, shall be entitled to be registered as a voter at any such <5>election. <4>• Electoral districts <7>327. Power of Parliament to make provision with respect <7>to elections to Legislatures <5>Subject to the provisions of this Constitution, Parliament may from time to time by <5>law make provision with respect to all matters relating to, or in connection with, <5>elections to either House of Parliament or to the House or either House of the <5>Legislature of a State including the preparation of electoral rolls, the delimitation of <5>constituencies and all other matters necessary for securing the due constitution of <5>such House or Houses. <7>328. Power of Legislature of a State to make provision with <7>respect to elections to such Legislature <5>Subject to the provisions of this Constitution and in so far as provision in that behalf <5>is not made by Parliament, the Legislature of a State may from time to time by law <5>make provision with respect to all matters relating to, or in connection with, the <5>elections to the House or either House of the Legislature of the State including the <5>preparation of electoral rolls and all other matters necessary for securing the due <5>constitution of such House or Houses. <7>329. Bar to interference by courts in electoral matters <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution- <6>a.<5> the validity of any law relating to the delimitation of constituencies or the <5>allotment of seats to such constituencies, made or purporting to be made <5>under article 327 or article 328, shall not be called in question in any court; <6>b.<5> no election to either House of Parliament or to the House or either House <5>of the Legislature of a State shall be called in question except by an election <5>petition presented to such authority and in such manner as may be <5>provided for by or under any law made by the appropriate Legislature. <7>329A. Special provision as to elections to Parliament in the <7>case of Prime Minister and Speaker <5>Rep. by the Constitution <5>(Forty-fourth Amendment) Act, <5>1978, s. <5>36 (w.e.f. <5>20-6-1979). <9>PART XVI: SPECIAL PROVISIONS RELATING <9>TO CERTAIN CLASSES <7>330. Reservation of seats for Scheduled Castes and <4>• First chamber representation quotas <7>Scheduled Tribes in the House of the People <6>1.<5> Seats shall be reserved in the House of the People for- <6>a.<5> the Scheduled Castes; <6>b.<5> the Scheduled Tribes except the Scheduled Tribes in the autonomous <5>districts of Assam; and <6>c. <5>the Scheduled Tribes in the autonomous districts of Assam. <6>2.<5> The number of seats reserved in any State or Union territory for the Scheduled <5>Castes or the Scheduled Tribes under clause (1) shall bear, as nearly as may be, <5>the same proportion to the total number of seats allotted to that State or Union <5>territory in the House of the People as the population of the Scheduled Castes in <5>the State or Union territory or of the Scheduled Tribes in the State or Union <5>territory or part of the State or Union territory, as the case may be, in respect of <5>which seats are so reserved, bears to the total population of the State or Union <5>territory. <6>3.<5> Notwithstanding anything contained in clause (2), the number of seats reserved <5>in the House of the People for the Scheduled Tribes in the autonomous districts <5>of Assam shall bear to the total number of seats allotted to that State a <5>proportion not less than the population of the Scheduled Tribes in the said <5>autonomous districts bears to the total population of the State. <7>Explanation <5>In this article and in article 332, the expression "population" means the population as <5>ascertained at the last preceding census of which the relevant figures have been <5>published: <5>Provided that the reference in this Explanation to the last preceding census of which <5>the relevant figures have been published shall, until the relevant figures for the first <5>census taken after the year 2026 have been published, be construed as a reference <5>to the 2001 census. <7>331. Representation of the Anglo-Indian community in the <4>• First chamber representation quotas <7>House of the People <5>Notwithstanding anything in article 81, the President may, if he is of opinion that the <5>Anglo-Indian community is not adequately represented in the House of the People, <5>nominate not more than two members of that community to the House of the <5>People. <7>332. Reservation of seats for Scheduled Castes and <4>• First chamber representation quotas <7>Scheduled Tribes in the Legislative Assemblies of the <7>States <6>1. <5>Seats shall be reserved for the Scheduled Castes and the Scheduled Tribes, <5>except the Scheduled Tribes in the autonomous districts of Assam, in the <5>Legislative Assembly of every State. <6>2. <5>Seats shall be reserved also for the autonomous districts in the Legislative <5>Assembly of the State of Assam. <6>3. <5>The number of seats reserved for the Scheduled Castes or the Scheduled Tribes <5>in the Legislative Assembly of any State under clause (1) shall bear, as nearly as <5>may be, the same proportion to the total number of seats in the Assembly as the <5>population of the Scheduled Castes in the State or of the Scheduled Tribes in the <5>State or part of the State, as the case may be, in respect of which seats are so <5>reserved, bears to the total population of the State. <6>3A. <5>Notwithstanding anything contained in clause (3), until the taking effect, under <5>article 170, of the re-adjustment, on the basis of the first census after the year <5>2026, of the number of seats in the Legislative Assemblies of the States of <5>Arunachal Pradesh, Meghalaya, Mizoram and Nagaland, the seats which shall be <5>reserved for the Scheduled Tribes in the Legislative Assembly of any such State <5>shall be,- <6>a.<5> if all the seats in the Legislative Assembly of such State in existence on the <5>date of coming into force of the Constitution (Fifty-seventh Amendment) <5>Act, 1987 (hereafter in this clause referred to as the existing Assembly) are <5>held by member of the Scheduled Tribes, all the seats except one; <6>b.<5> in any other case, such number of seats as bears to the total number of <5>seats, a proportion not less than the number (as on the said date) of <5>members belonging to the Scheduled Tribes in the existing Assembly bears <5>to the total number of seats in the existing Assembly. <6>3B.<5> Notwithstanding anything contained in clause (3), until the re-adjustment, <5>under article 170, takes effect on the basis of the first census after the year <5>320.1 , of the number of seats in the Legislative Assembly of the State of Tripura, <5>the seats which shall be reserved for the Scheduled Tribes in the Legislative <5>Assembly shall be, such number of seats as bears to the total number of seats, a <5>proportion not less than the number, as on the date of coming into force of the <5>Constitution (Seventy-second Amendment) Act, 1992, of members belonging to <5>the Scheduled Tribes in the Legislative Assembly in existence on the said date <5>bears to the total number of seats in that Assembly. <6>4.<5> The number of seats reserved for an autonomous district in the Legislative <5>Assembly of the State of Assam shall bear to the total number of seats in that <5>Assembly a proportion not less than the population of the district bears to the <5>total population of the State. <6>5.<5> The constituencies for the seats reserved for any autonomous district of Assam <5>shall not comprise any area outside that district. <6>6.<5> No person who is not a member of a Scheduled Tribe of any autonomous district <5>of the State of Assam shall be eligible for election to the Legislative Assembly of <5>the State from any constituency of that district. <5>Provided that for elections to the Legislative Assembly of the State of Assam, <5>the representation of the Scheduled Tribes and non-Scheduled Tribes in the <5>constituencies included in the Bodoland Territorial Areas District, so notified, <5>and existing prior to the constitution of the Bodoland Territorial Areas District, <5>shall be maintained. <7>333. Representation of the Anglo-Indian community in the <4>• First chamber representation quotas <7>Legislative Assemblies of the States <5>Notwithstanding anything in article 170, the Governor of a State may, if he is of <5>opinion that the Anglo-Indian community needs representation in the Legislative <5>Assembly of the State and is not adequately represented therein, nominate one <5>member of that community to the Assembly. <7>334. Reservation of seats and special representation to <4>• First chamber representation quotas <7>cease after seventy years <5>Notwithstanding anything in the foregoing provisions of this Part, the provisions of <5>this Constitution relating to- <6>a.<5> the reservation of seats for the Scheduled Castes and the Scheduled Tribes <5>in the House of the People and in the Legislative Assemblies of the States; <5>and <6>b.<5> the representation of the Anglo-Indian community in the House of the <5>People and in the Legislative Assemblies of the States by nomination, <5>shall cease to have effect on the expiration of a period of seventy years from the <5>commencement of this Constitution: <5>Provided that nothing in this article shall affect any representation in the House of <5>the People or in the Legislative Assembly of a State until the dissolution of the then <5>existing House or Assembly, as the case may be. <4>• Civil service recruitment <7>335. Claims of Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes to <7>services and posts <5>The claims of the members of the Scheduled Castes and the Scheduled Tribes shall <5>be taken into consideration, consistently with the maintenance of efficiency of <5>administration, in the making of appointments to services and posts in connection <5>with the affairs of the Union or of a State. <5>Provided that nothing in this article shall prevent in making of any provision in <5>favour of the members of the Scheduled Castes and the Scheduled Tribes for <5>relaxation in qualifying marks in any examination or lowering the standards of <5>evaluation, for reservation in matters of promotion to any class or classes of services <5>or posts in connection with the affairs of the Union or of a State. <7>336. Special provision for Anglo-Indian community in <7>certain services <4>• Telecommunications <6>1.<5> During the first two years after the commencement of this Constitution, <5>appointments of members of the Anglo-Indian community to posts in the <5>railway, customs, postal and telegraph services of the Union shall be made on <5>the same basis as immediately before the fifteenth day of August, 1947. <5>During every succeeding period of two years, the number of posts reserved for <5>the members of the said community in the said services shall, as nearly as <5>possible, be less by ten per cent, than the numbers so reserved during the <5>immediately preceding period of two years: <5>Provided that at the end of ten years from the commencement of this <5>Constitution all such reservations shall cease. <6>2.<5> Nothing in clause (1) shall bar the appointment of members of the Anglo-Indian <5>community to posts other than, or in addition to, those reserved for the <5>community under that clause if such members are found qualified for <5>appointment on merit as compared with the members of other communities. <7>337. Special provision with respect to educational grants <7>for the benefit of Anglo-Indian community <5>During the first three financial years after the commencement of this Constitution, <5>the same grants, if any, shall be made by the Union and by each State for the benefit <5>of the Anglo-Indian community in respect of education as were made in the financial <5>year ending on the thirty-first day of March, 1948. <5>During every succeeding period of three years the grants may be less by ten per cent, <5>than those for the immediately preceding period of three years: <5>Provided that at the end of ten years from the commencement of this Constitution <5>such grants, to the extent to which they are a special concession to the Anglo-Indian <5>community, shall cease: <5>Provided further that no educational institution shall be entitled to receive any grant <5>under this article unless at least forty per cent, of the annual admissions therein are <5>made available to members of communities other than the Anglo-Indian community. <7>338. National Commission for Scheduled Castes <6>1.<5> There shall be a Commission for the Scheduled Castes to be known as the <5>National Commission for the Scheduled Castes. <6>2. <5>Subject to the provisions of any law made in this behalf by Parliament, the <5>Commission shall consist of a Chairperson, Vice-Chairperson and three other <5>Members and the conditions of service and tenure of office of the Chairperson, <5>Vice-Chairperson and other Members so appointed shall be such as the <5>President may by rule determine. <6>3. <5>The Chairperson, Vice-Chairperson and other Members of the Commission shall <5>be appointed by the President by warrant under his hand and seal. <6>4. <5>The Commission shall have the power to regulate its own procedure. <6>5. <5>It shall be the duty of the Commission- <6>a.<5> to investigate and monitor all matters relating to the safeguards provided <5>for the Scheduled Castes under this Constitution or under any other law for <5>the time being in force or under any order of the Government and to <5>evaluate the working of such safeguards; <6>b.<5> to inquire into specific complaints with respect to the deprivation of rights <5>and safeguards of the Scheduled Castes; <6>c. <5>to participate and advise on the planning process of socio-economic <5>development: of the Scheduled Castes and to evaluate the progress of their <5>development under the Union and any State; <6>d.<5> to present to the President, annually and at such other times as the <5>Commission may deem fit, reports upon the working of those safeguards; <6>e.<5> to make in such reports recommendations as to the measures that should <5>be taken by the Union or any State for the effective implementation of <5>those safeguards and other measures for the protection, welfare and <5>socio-economic development of the Scheduled Castes; and <6>f. <5>to discharge such other functions in relation to the protection, welfare and <5>development and advancement of the scheduled Castes as the President <5>may, subject to the provisions of any law made by Parliament, by rule <5>specify. <6>6. <5>The President shall cause all such reports to be laid before each House of <5>Parliament along with a memorandum explaining the action taken or proposed <5>to be taken on the recommendations relating to the Union and the reasons for <5>the non-acceptance, if any, of any of such recommendations. <6>7. <5>Where any such report, or any part thereof, relates to any matter with which <5>any State Government is concerned, a copy of such report shall be forwarded to <5>the Governor of the State who shall cause it to be laid before the Legislature of <5>the State along with a memorandum explaining the action taken or proposed to <5>be taken on the recommendations relating to the State and the reasons for the <5>non-acceptance, if any, of any of such recommendations. <6>8. <5>The Commission shall, while investigating any matter referred to in sub-clause <5>(a) or inquiring into any complaint referred to in sub-clause (b) of clause (5), have <5>all the powers of a civil court trying a suit and in particular in respect of the <5>following matters, namely:- <6>a.<5> summoning and enforcing the attendance of any person from any part of <5>India and examining him on oath; <6>b.<5> requiring the discovery and production of any document; <6>c. <5>receiving evidence on affidavits; <6>d.<5> requisitioning any public record or copy thereof from any court or office; <6>e.<5> issuing commissions for the examination of witnesses and documents; <6>f. <5>any other matter which the President may, by rule, determine. <6>9.<5> The Union and every State Government shall consult the Commission on all <5>major policy matters affecting Scheduled Castes. <6>10.<5> In this article, references to the Scheduled Castes shall be construed as <5>including references to such other backward classes as the President may, on <5>receipt of the report of a Commission appointed under clause (1) of article 340, <5>by order specify and also to the Anglo-Indian community. <7>338A. National Commission for Scheduled Tribes <6>1. <5>There shall be a Commission for the Scheduled Tribes to be known as the <5>National Commission for the Scheduled Tribes. <6>2. <5>Subject to the provisions of any law made in this behalf by Parliament, the <5>Commission shall consist of a Chairperson, Vice-Chairperson and three other <5>Members and the conditions of service and tenure of office of the Chairperson, <5>Vice-Chairperson and other Members so appointed shall be such as the <5>President may by rule determine. <6>3. <5>The Chairperson, Vice-Chairperson and other Members of the Commission shall <5>be appointed by the President by warrant under his hand and seal. <6>4. <5>The Commission shall have the power to regulate its own procedure. <6>5. <5>It shall be the duty of the Commission- <6>a.<5> to investigate and monitor all matters relating to the safeguards provided <5>for the Scheduled Tribes under this Constitution or under any other law for <5>the time being in force or under any order of the Government and to <5>evaluate the working of such safeguards; <6>b.<5> to inquire into specific complaints with respect to the deprivation of rights <5>and safeguards of the Scheduled Tribes; <6>c. <5>to participate and advise on the planning process of socio-economic <5>development of the Scheduled Tribes and to evaluate the progress of their <5>development under the Union and any State; <6>d.<5> to present to the President, annually and at such other times as the <5>Commission may deem fit, reports upon the working of those safeguards; <6>e.<5> to make in such reports recommendations as to the measures that should <5>be taken by the Union or any State for the effective implementation of <5>those safeguards and other measures for the protection, welfare and <5>socio-economic development of the Scheduled Tribes;
