and <6>f. <5>to discharge such other functions in relation to the protection, welfare and <5>development and advancement of the Scheduled Tribes as the President <5>may, subject to the provisions of any law made by Parliament, by rule <5>specify. <6>6. <5>The President shall cause all such reports to be laid before each House of <5>Parliament along with a memorandum explaining the action taken or proposed <5>to be taken on the recommendations relating to the Union and the reasons for <5>the non-acceptance, if any, of any of such recommendations. <6>7. <5>Where any such report, or any part thereof, relates to any matter with which <5>any State Government is concerned, a copy of such report shall be forwarded to <5>the Governor of the State who shall cause it to be laid before the Legislature of <5>the State along with a memorandum explaining the action taken or proposed to <5>be taken on the recommendations relating to the State and the reasons for the <5>non-acceptance, if any, of any of such recommendations. <6>8. <5>The Commission shall, while investigating any matter referred to in sub-clause <5>(a) or inquiring into any complaint referred to in sub-clause (b) of clause (5), have <5>all the powers of a civil court trying a suit and in particular in respect of the <5>following matters, namely:- <6>a.<5> summoning and enforcing the attendance of any person from any part of <5>India and examining him on oath; <6>b.<5> requiring the discovery and production of any document; <6>c. <5>receiving evidence on affidavits; <6>d.<5> requisitioning any public record or copy thereof from any court or office; <6>e.<5> issuing commissions for the examination of witnesses and documents; <6>f. <5>any other matter which the President may, by rule, determine. <6>9. <5>The Union and every State Government shall consult the Commission on all <5>major policy matters affecting Scheduled Tribes. <7>339. Control of the Union over the administration of <7>Scheduled Areas and the welfare of Scheduled Tribes <6>1.<5> The President may at any time and shall, at the expiration of ten years from the <5>commencement of this Constitution by order appoint a Commission to report on <5>the administration of the Scheduled Areas and the welfare of the Scheduled <5>Tribes in the States. <5>The order may define the composition, powers and procedure of the <5>Commission and may contain such incidental or ancillary provisions as the <5>President may consider necessary or desirable. <6>2.<5> The executive power of the Union shall extend to the giving of directions to a <5>State as to the drawing up and execution of schemes specified in the direction to <5>be essential for the welfare of the Scheduled Tribes in the State. <7>340. Appointment of a Commission to investigate the <7>conditions of backward classes <6>1.<5> The President may by order appoint a Commission consisting of such persons as <5>he thinks fit to investigate the conditions of socially and educationally backward <5>classes within the territory of India and the difficulties under which they labour <5>and to make recommendations as to the steps that should be taken by the Union <5>or any State to remove such difficulties and to improve their condition and as to <5>the grants that should be made for the purpose by the Union or any State and <5>the conditions subject to which such grants should be made, and the order <5>appointing such Commission shall define the procedure to be followed by the <5>Commission. <6>2.<5> A Commission so appointed shall investigate the matters referred to them and <5>present to the President a report setting out the facts as found by them and <5>making such recommendations as they think proper. <6>3.<5> The President shall cause a copy of the report so presented together with a <5>memorandum explaining the action taken thereon to be laid before each House <5>of Parliament. <7>341. Scheduled Castes <6>1.<5> The President may with respect to any State or Union territory, and where it is a <5>State, after consultation with the Governor thereof, by public notification, <5>specify the castes, races or tribes or parts of or groups within castes, races or <5>tribes which shall for the purposes of this Constitution be deemed to be <5>Scheduled Castes in relation to that State or Union territory, as the case may be. <6>2.<5> Parliament may by law include in or exclude from the list of Scheduled Castes <5>specified in a notification issued under clause (1) any caste, race or tribe or part <5>of or group within any caste, race or tribe, but save as aforesaid a notification <5>issued under the said clause shall not be varied by any subsequent notification. <7>342. Scheduled Tribes <6>1.<5> The President may with respect to any State or Union territory, and where it is a <5>State, after consultation with the Governor thereof, by public notification, <5>specify the tribes or tribal communities or parts of or groups within tribes or <5>tribal communities which shall for the purposes of this Constitution be deemed <5>to be Scheduled Tribes in relation to that State or Union territory, as the case <5>may be. <6>2.<5> Parliament may by law include in or exclude from the list of Scheduled Tribes <5>specified in a notification issued under clause (1) any tribe or tribal community <5>or part of or group within any tribe or tribal community, but save as aforesaid a <5>notification issued under the said clause shall not be varied by any subsequent <5>notification. <9>PART XVII: OFFICIAL LANGUAGE <7>CHAPTER I: LANGUAGE OF THE UNION <4>• Official or national languages <7>343. Official language of the Union <6>1.<5> The official language of the Union shall be Hindi in Devanagari script. <5>The form of numerals to be used for the official purposes of the Union shall be <5>the international form of Indian numerals. <6>2.<5> Notwithstanding anything in clause (1), for a period of fifteen years from the <5>commencement of this Constitution, the English language shall continue to be <5>used for all the official purposes of the Union for which it was being used <5>immediately before such commencement: <5>Provided that the President may, during the said period, by order authorise the <5>use of the Hindi language in addition to the English language and of the <5>Devanagari form of numerals in addition to the international form of Indian <5>numerals for any of the official purposes of the Union. <6>3.<5> Notwithstanding anything in this article, Parliament may by law provide for the <5>use, after the said period of fifteen years, of- <6>a.<5> the English language, or <6>b.<5> the Devanagari form of numerals, <5>for such purposes as may be specified in the law. <4>• Official or national languages <7>344. Commission and Committee of Parliament on official <7>language <6>1.<5> The President shall, at the expiration of five years from the commencement of <5>this Constitution and thereafter at the expiration of ten years from such <5>commencement, by order constitute a Commission which shall consist of a <5>Chairman and such other members representing the different languages <5>specified in the Eighth Schedule as the President may appoint, and the order <5>shall define the procedure to be followed by the Commission. <6>2.<5> It shall be the duty of the Commission to make recommendations to the <5>President as to- <6>a.<5> the progressive use of the Hindi language for the official purposes of the <5>Union; <6>b.<5> restrictions on the use of the English language for all or any of the official <5>purposes of the Union; <6>c. <5>the language to be used for all or any of the purposes mentioned in article <5>348; <6>d.<5> the form of numerals to be used for any one or more specified purposes of <5>the Union; <6>e.<5> any other matter referred to the Commission by the President as regards <5>the official language of the Union and the language for communication <5>between the Union and a State or between one State and another and their <5>use. <6>3.<5> In making their recommendations under clause (2), the Commission shall have <5>due regard to the industrial, cultural and scientific advancement of India, and the <5>just claims and the interests of persons belonging to the non-Hindi speaking <5>areas in regard to the public services. <6>4.<5> There shall be constituted a Committee consisting of thirty members, of whom <5>twenty shall be members of the House of the People and ten shall be members <5>of the Council of States to be elected respectively by the members of the House <5>of the People and the members of the Council of States in accordance with the <5>system of proportional representation by means of the single transferable vote. <6>5.<5> It shall be the duty of the Committee to examine the recommendations of the <5>Commission constituted under clause (1) and to report to the President their <5>opinion thereon. <6>6.<5> Notwithstanding anything in article 343, the President may, after consideration <5>of the report referred to in clause (5), issue directions in accordance with the <5>whole or any part of that report. <7>CHAPTER II: REGIONAL LANGUAGES <4>• Official or national languages <7>345. Official language or languages of a State <5>Subject to the provisions of articles 346 and 347, the Legislature of a State may by <5>law adopt any one or more of the languages in use in the State or Hindi as the <5>Language or Languages to be used for all or any of the official purposes of that State: <5>Provided that, until the Legislature of the State otherwise provides by law, the <5>English language shall continue to be used for those official purposes within the <5>State for which it was being used immediately before the commencement of this <5>Constitution. <4>• Official or national languages <7>346. Official language for communication between one <7>State and another or between a State and the Union <5>The language for the time being authorised for use in the Union for official purposes <5>shall be the official language for communication between one State and another <5>State and between a State and the Union: <5>Provided that if two or more States agree that the Hindi language should be the <5>official language for communication between such States, that language may be used <5>for such communication. <4>• Official or national languages <7>347. Special provision relating to language spoken by a <7>section of the population of a State <5>On a demand being made in that behalf the President may, if he is satisfied that a <5>substantial proportion of the population of a State desire the use of any language <5>spoken by them to be recognised by that state, direct that such language shall also be <5>officially recognised throughout that State or any part thereof for such purpose as he <5>may specify. <7>CHAPTER III: LANGUAGE OF THE SUPREME COURT, <7>HIGH COURTS, ETC <4>• Official or national languages <7>348. Language to be used in the Supreme Court and in the <7>High Courts and for Acts, Bills, etc <6>1. <5>Notwithstanding anything in the foregoing provisions of this Part, until <5>Parliament by law otherwise provides- <6>a.<5> all proceedings in the Supreme Court and in every High Court, <6>b.<5> the authoritative texts- <6>i. <5>of all Bills to be introduced or amendments thereto to be moved in <5>either House of Parliament or in the House or either House of the <5>Legislature of a State. <6>ii. <5>of all Acts passed by Parliament or the Legislature of a State and of all <5>Ordinances promulgated by the President or the Governor of a State, <5>and <6>iii. <5>of all orders, rules, regulations and bye-laws issued under this <5>Constitution or under any law made by Parliament or the Legislature <5>of a State, <5>shall be in the English language. <6>2. <5>Notwithstanding anything in sub-clause (a) of clause (1), the Governor of a State <5>may, with the previous consent of the President, authorise the use of the Hindi <5>language, or any other language used for any official purposes of the State, in <5>proceedings in the High Court having its principal seat in that State: <5>Provided that nothing in this clause shall apply to any judgment, decree or order <5>passed or made by such High Court. <6>3. <5>Notwithstanding anything in sub-clause (b) of clause (1), where the Legislature <5>of a State has prescribed any language other than the English language for use in <5>Bills introduced in, or Acts passed by, the Legislature of the State or in <5>Ordinances promulgated by the Governor of the State or in any order, rule, <5>regulation or bye-law referred to in paragraph <5>(iii) of that sub-clause, a <5>translation of the same in the English language published under the authority of <5>the Governor of the State in the Official Gazette of that State shall be deemed to <5>be the authoritative text thereof in the English language under this article. <7>349. Special procedure for enactment of certain laws <7>relating to language <5>During the period of fifteen years from the commencement of this Constitution, no <5>Bill or amendment making provision for the language to be used for any of the <5>purposes mentioned in clause (1) of article 348 shall be introduced or moved in <5>either House of Parliament without the previous sanction of the President, and the <5>President shall not give his sanction to the introduction of any such Bill or the <5>moving of any such amendment except after he has taken into consideration the <5>recommendations of the Commission constituted under clause (1) of article 344 and <5>the report of the Committee constituted under clause (4) of that article. <7>CHAPTER IV: SPECIAL DIRECTIVES <4>• Protection of language use <7>350. Language to be used in representations for redress of <7>grievances <5>Every person shall be entitled to submit a representation for the redress of any <5>grievance to any officer or authority of the Union or a State in any of the languages <5>used in the Union or in the State, as the case may be. <4>• Protection of language use <7>350A. Facilities for instruction in mother-tongue at <7>primary stage <5>It shall be the endeavour of every State and of every local authority within the State <5>to provide adequate facilities for instruction in the mother-tongue at the primary <5>stage of education to children belonging to linguistic minority groups; and the <5>President may issue such directions to any State as he considers necessary or proper <5>for securing the provision of such facilities. <7>350B. Special Officer for linguistic minorities <6>1.<5> There shall be a Special Officer for linguistic minorities to be appointed by the <5>President. <6>2.<5> It shall be the duty of the Special Officer to investigate all matters relating to the <5>safeguards provided for linguistic minorities under this Constitution and report <5>to the President upon those matters at such intervals as the President may <5>direct, and the President shall cause all such reports to be laid before each <5>House of Parliament, and sent to the Government of the States concerned. <7>351. Directive for development of the Hindi language <5>It shall be the duty of the Union to promote the spread of the Hindi language, to <5>develop it so that it may serve as a medium of expression for all the elements of the <5>composite culture of India and to secure its enrichment by assimilating without <5>interfering with its genius, the forms, style and expressions used in Hindustani and in <5>the other languages of India specified in the Eighth Schedule, and by drawing, <5>wherever necessary or desirable, for its vocabulary, primarily on Sanskrit and <5>secondarily on other languages. <9>PART XVIII: EMERGENCY PROVISIONS <4>• Emergency provisions <7>352. Proclamation of Emergency <6>1.<5> If the President is satisfied that a grave emergency exists whereby the security <5>of India or of any part of the territory thereof is threatened, whether by war or <5>external aggression or armed rebellion, he may, by proclamation, make a <5>declaration to that effect in respect of the whole of India or of such part of the <5>territory thereof as may be specified in the proclamation. <7>Explanation <5>A proclamation of Emergency declaring that the security of India or any part of the <5>territory thereof is threatened by war or by external aggression or by armed <5>rebellion may be made before the actual occurrence of war or of any such aggression <5>or rebellion, if the President is satisfied that there is imminent danger thereof. <6>2. <5>A Proclamation issued under clause (1) may be varied or revoked by a <5>subsequent Proclamation. <6>3. <5>The President shall not issue a Proclamation under clause (1) or a Proclamation <5>varying such Proclamation unless the decision of the Union cabinet (that is to <5>say, the Council consisting of the Prime Minister and other Ministers of Cabinet <5>rank appointed under article 75) that such a Proclamation may be issued has <5>been communicated to him in writing. <6>4. <5>Every Proclamation issued under this article shall be laid before each House of <5>Parliament and shall, except where it is a Proclamation revoking a previous <5>Proclamation, cease to operate at the expiration of one month unless before the <5>expiration of that period it has been approved by resolutions of both Houses of <5>Parliament: <5>Provided that if any such Proclamation (not being a Proclamation revoking a <5>previous Proclamation) is issued at a time when the House of the People has <5>been dissolved, or the dissolution of the House of the People takes place during <5>the period of one month referred to in this clause, and if a resolution approving <5>the Proclamation has been passed by the Council of States, but no resolution <5>with respect to such Proclamation has been passed by the House of the People <5>before the expiration of that period, the Proclamation shall cease to operate at <5>the expiration of thirty days from the date on which the House of the People <5>first sits after its reconstitution, unless before the expiration of the said period <5>of thirty days a resolution approving the Proclamation has been also passed by <5>the House of the People. <6>5. <5>A Proclamation so approved shall, unless revoked, cease to operate on the <5>expiration of a period of six months from the date of the passing of the second of <5>the resolutions approving the Proclamation under clause (4): <5>Provided that if and so often as a resolution approving the continuance in force <5>of such a Proclamation is passed by both Houses of Parliament the Proclamation <5>shall, unless revoked, continue in force for a further period of six months from <5>the date on which it would otherwise have ceased to operate under this clause: <5>Provided further that if the dissolution of the House of the People takes place <5>during any such period of six months and a resolution approving the continuance <5>in force of such Proclamation has been passed by the Council of States but no <5>resolution with respect to the continuance in force of such Proclamation has <5>been passed by the house of the people during the said period, the proclamation <5>shall cease to operate at the expiration of thirty days from the date on which the <5>House of the People first sits after its reconstitution unless before the <5>expiration of the said period of thirty days, a resolution approving the <5>continuance in force of the Proclamation has been also passed by the House of <5>the People. <6>6. <5>For the purposes of clauses (4) and (5), a resolution may be passed by either <5>House of Parliament only by a majority of the total membership of that House <5>and by a majority of not less than two-thirds of the members of that House <5>present and voting. <6>7. <5>Notwithstanding anything contained in the foregoing clauses, the President <5>shall revoke a Proclamation issued under clause (1) or a Proclamation varying <5>such Proclamation if the House of the People passes a resolution disapproving, <5>or, as the case may be, disapproving the continuance in force of, such <5>Proclamation. <6>8.<5> Where a notice in writing signed by not less than one-tenth of the total number <5>of members of the House of the People has been given, of their intention to <5>move a resolution for disapproving, or, as the case may be, for disapproving the <5>continuance in force of, a Proclamation issued under clause <5>(1) or a <5>Proclamation varying such Proclamation,- <6>a.<5> to the Speaker, if the House is in session; or <6>b.<5> to the President, if the House is not in session, <5>a special sitting of the House shall be held within fourteen days from the date on <5>which such notice is received by the Speaker, or, as the case may be, by the <5>President, for the purpose of considering such resolution. <6>9.<5> The power conferred on the President by this article shall include the power to <5>issue different Proclamations on different grounds, being war or external <5>aggression or armed rebellion or imminent danger of war or external aggression <5>or armed rebellion, whether or not there is a Proclamation already issued by the <5>President under clause (1) and such Proclamation is in operation. <4>• Emergency provisions <7>353. Effect of Proclamation of Emergency <5>While a Proclamation of Emergency is in operation, then- <6>a.<5> notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, the executive power of the <5>Union shall extend to the giving of directions to any State as to the manner <5>in which the executive power thereof is to be exercised; <6>b.<5> the power of Parliament to make laws with respect to any matter shall <5>include power to make laws conferring powers and imposing duties, or <5>authorising the conferring of powers and the imposition of duties, upon the <5>Union or officers and authorities of the Union as respects that matter, <5>notwithstanding that it is one which is not enumerated in the Union List: <5>Provided that where a Proclamation of Emergency is in operation only in any part of <5>the territory of India,- <6>i. <5>the executive power of the Union to give directions under clause (a), and <6>ii. <5>the power of Parliament to make laws under clause (b), <5>shall also extend to any State other than a State in which or in any part of which the <5>Proclamation of Emergency is in operation if and in so far as the security of India or <5>any part of the territory thereof is threatened by activities in or in relation to the <5>part of the territory of India in which the Proclamation of Emergency is in operation. <4>• Emergency provisions <7>354. Application of provisions relating to distribution of <7>revenues while a Proclamation of Emergency is in <7>operation <6>1.<5> The President may, while a Proclamation of Emergency is in operation, by order <5>direct that all or any of the provisions of articles 268 to 279 shall for such period, <5>not extending in any case beyond the expiration of the financial year in which <5>such Proclamation ceases to operate, as may be specified in the order, have <5>effect subject to such exceptions or modifications as he thinks fit. <6>2.<5> Every order made under clause (1) shall, as soon as may be after it is made, be <5>laid before each House of Parliament. <4>• Emergency provisions <7>355. Duty of the Union to protect States against external <7>aggression and internal disturbance <5>It shall be the duty of the Union to protect every State against external aggression <5>and internal disturbance and to ensure that the government of every State is carried <5>on in accordance with the provisions of this Constitution. <4>• Emergency provisions <7>356. Provisions in case of failure of constitutional <7>machinery in States <6>1. <5>If the President, on receipt of a report from the Governor of a State or <5>otherwise, is satisfied that a situation has arisen in which the government of the <5>State cannot be carried on in accordance with the provisions of this <5>Constitution, the President may by Proclamation- <6>a.<5> assume to himself all or any of the functions of the Government of the State <5>and all or any of the powers vested in or exercisable by the Governor or any <5>body or authority in the State other than the Legislature of the State. <6>b.<5> declare that the powers of the Legislature of the State shall be exercisable <5>by or under the authority of Parliament; <6>c. <5>make such incidental and consequential provisions as appear to the <5>President to be necessary or desirable for giving effect to the objects of the <5>Proclamation, including provisions for suspending in whole or in part the <5>operation of any provisions of this Constitution relating to any body or <5>authority in the State: <5>Provided that nothing in this clause shall authorise the President to assume to <5>himself any of the powers vested in or exercisable by a High Court, or to <5>suspend in whole or in part the operation of any provision of this Constitution <5>relating to High Courts. <6>2. <5>Any such Proclamation may be revoked or varied by a subsequent Proclamation. <6>3. <5>Every Proclamation under this article shall be laid before each House of <5>Parliament and shall, except where it is a Proclamation revoking a previous <5>Proclamation, cease to operate at the expiration of two months unless before <5>the expiration of that period it has been approved by resolutions of both Houses <5>of Parliament: <5>Provided that if any such Proclamation (not being a Proclamation revoking a <5>previous Proclamation) is issued at a time when the House of the People is <5>dissolved or the dissolution of the House of the People takes place during the <5>period of two months referred to in this clause, and if a resolution approving the <5>Proclamation has been passed by the Council of States, but no resolution with <5>respect to such Proclamation has been passed by the House of the People <5>before the expiration of that period, the Proclamation shall cease to operate at <5>the expiration of thirty days from the date on which the House of the People <5>first sits after its reconstitution unless before the expiration of the said period of <5>thirty days a resolution approving the Proclamation has been also passed by the <5>House of the People. <6>4. <5>A Proclamation so approved shall, unless revoked, cease to operate on the <5>expiration of a period of six months from the date of issue of the Proclamation: <5>Provided that if and so often as a resolution approving the continuance in force <5>of such a Proclamation is passed by both Houses of Parliament, the <5>Proclamation shall, unless revoked, continue in force for a further period of six <5>months from the date on which under this clause it would otherwise have <5>ceased to operate, but no such Proclamation shall in any case remain in force for <5>more than three years: <5>Provided further that if the dissolution of the House of the People takes place <5>during any such period of six months and a resolution approving the continuance <5>in force of such Proclamation has been passed by the Council of States, but no <5>resolution with respect to the continuance in force of such Proclamation has <5>been passed by the House of the People during the said period, the <5>Proclamation shall cease to operate at the expiration of thirty days from the <5>date on which the House of the People first sits after its reconstitution unless <5>before the expiration of the said period of thirty days a resolution approving the <5>continuance in force of the Proclamation has been also passed by the House of <5>the People: <5>Provided also that in the case of the Proclamation issued under clause (1) on the <5>11th day of May, 1987 with respect to the State of Punjab, the reference in the <5>first proviso to this clause to "three years" shall be construed as a reference to <5>five years. <6>5. <5>Notwithstanding anything contained in clause (4), a resolution with respect to <5>the continuance in force of a Proclamation approved under clause (3) for any <5>period beyond the expiration of one year from the date of issue of such <5>Proclamation shall not be passed by either House of Parliament unless- <6>a.<5> a Proclamation of Emergency is in operation, in the whole of India or, as the <5>case may be, in the whole or any part of the State, at the time of the passing <5>of such resolution, and <6>b.<5> the Election Commission certifies that the continuance in force of the <5>Proclamation approved under clause (3) during the period specified in such <5>resolution is necessary on account of difficulties in holding general <5>elections to the Legislative Assembly of the State concerned. <5>Provided that nothing in this clause shall apply to the Proclamation issued under <5>clause (1) on the 11th day of May, 1987 with respect to the State of Punjab. <4>• Emergency provisions <7>357. Exercise of legislative powers under Proclamation <7>issued under article 356 <6>1.<5> Where by a Proclamation issued under clause (1) of article 356, it has been <5>declared that the powers of the Legislature of the State shall be exercisable by <5>or under the authority of Parliament, it shall be competent- <6>a.<5> for Parliament to confer on the President the power of the Legislature of <5>the State to make laws, and to authorise the President to delegate, subject <5>to such conditions as he may think fit to impose, the power so conferred to <5>any other authority to be specified by him in that behalf; <6>b.<5> for Parliament, or for the President or other authority in whom such power <5>to make laws is vested under sub-clause (a), to make laws conferring <5>powers and imposing duties, or authorising the conferring of powers and <5>the imposition of duties, upon the Union or officers and authorities thereof; <6>c. <5>for the President to authorise when the House of the People is not in <5>session expenditure from the Consolidated Fund of the State pending the <5>sanction of such expenditure by Parliament. <6>2.<5> Any law made in exercise of the power of the Legislature of the State by <5>Parliament or the President or other authority referred to in sub-clause (a) of <5>clause (1) which Parliament or the President or such other authority would not, <5>but for the issue of a Proclamation under article 356, have been competent to <5>make shall, after the Proclamation has ceased to operate, continue in force until <5>altered or repealed or amended by a competent Legislature or other authority. <4>• Emergency provisions <7>358. Suspension of provisions of article 19 during <7>emergencies <6>1.<5> While a Proclamation of Emergency declaring that the security of India or any <5>part of the territory thereof is threatened by war or by external aggression is in <5>operation, nothing in article 19 shall restrict the power of the State as defined in <5>Part III to make any law or to take any executive action which the State would <5>but for the provisions contained in that Part be competent to make or to take, <5>but any law so made shall, to the extent of the incompetency, cease to have <5>effect as soon as the Proclamation ceases to operate, except as respects things <5>done or omitted to be done before the law so ceases to have effect: <5>Provided that where such Proclamation of Emergency is in operation only in any <5>part of the territory of India, any such law may be made, or any such executive <5>action may be taken, under this article in relation to or in any State or Union <5>territory in which or in any part of which the Proclamation of Emergency is not <5>in operation, if and in so far as the security of India or any part of the territory <5>thereof is threatened by activities in or in relation to the part of the territory of <5>India in which the Proclamation of Emergency is in operation. <6>2.<5> Nothing in clause (1) shall apply- <6>a.<5> to any law which does not contain a recital to the effect that such law is in <5>relation to the Proclamation of Emergency in operation when it is made; or <6>b.<5> to any executive action taken otherwise than under a law containing such a <5>recital. <4>• Emergency provisions <7>359. Suspension of the enforcement of the rights conferred <7>by Part III during emergencies <6>1.<5> Where a Proclamation of Emergency is in operation, the President may by order <5>declare that the right to move any court for the enforcement of such of the <5>rights conferred by Part III (except articles 20 and 21) as may be mentioned in <5>the order and all proceedings pending in any court for the enforcement of the <5>rights so mentioned shall remain suspended for the period during which the <5>Proclamation is in force or for such shorter period as may be specified in the <5>order. <6>1A. <5>While an order made under clause (1) mentioning any of the rights conferred by <5>Part III (except articles 20 and 21) is in operation, nothing in that Part conferring <5>those rights shall restrict the power of the State as defined in the said Part to <5>make any law or to take any executive action which the State would but for the <5>provisions contained in that Part be competent to make or to take, but any law <5>so made shall, to the extent of the incompetency, cease to have effect as soon as <5>the order aforesaid ceases to operate, except as respects things done or omitted <5>to be done before the law so ceases to have effect: <5>Provided that where a Proclamation of Emergency is in operation only in any <5>part of the territory of India, any such law may be made, or any such executive <5>action may be taken, under this article in relation to or in any State or Union <5>territory in which or in any part of which the Proclamation of Emergency is not <5>in operation, if and in so far as the security of India or any part of the territory <5>thereof is threatened by activities in or in relation to the part of the territory of <5>India in which the Proclamation of Emergency is in operation. <6>1B. <5>Nothing in clause (1A) shall apply- <6>a.<5> to any law which does not contain a recital to the effect that such law is in <5>relation to the Proclamation of Emergency in operation when it is made; or <6>b.<5> to any executive action taken otherwise than under a law containing such a <5>recital. <6>2. <5>An order made as aforesaid may extend to the whole or any part of the territory <5>of India: <5>Provided that where a Proclamation of Emergency is in operation only in a part <5>of the territory of India, any such order shall not extend to any other part of the <5>territory of India unless the President, being satisfied that the security of India <5>or any part of the territory thereof is threatened by activities in or in relation to <5>the part of the territory of India in which the Proclamation of Emergency is in <5>operation, considers such extension to be necessary. <6>3. <5>Every order made under clause (1) shall, as soon as may be after it is made, be <5>laid before each House of Parliament. <7>359A. Application of this Part to the State of Punjab <5>Repealed by the Constitution <5>(Sixty-third Amendment) Act, <5>1989 s. <5>3(w.e.f. <5>6-1-1990). <4>• Emergency provisions <7>360. Provisions as to financial emergency <6>1.<5> If the President is satisfied that a situation has arisen whereby the financial <5>stability or credit of India or of any part of the territory thereof is threatened, he <5>may by a Proclamation make a declaration to that effect. <6>2.<5> A Proclamation issued under clause (1)- <6>a.<5> may be revoked or varied by a subsequent Proclamation; <6>b.<5> shall be laid before each House of Parliament; <6>c. <5>shall cease to operate at the expiration of two months, unless before the <5>expiration of that period it has been approved by resolutions of both <5>Houses of Parliament: <5>Provided that if any such Proclamation is issued at a time when the House of the <5>People has been dissolved or the dissolution of the House of the People takes <5>place during the period of two months referred to in sub-clause (c), and if a <5>resolution approving the Proclamation has been passed by the Council of States, <5>but no resolution with respect to such Proclamation has been passed by the <5>House of the People before the expiration of that period, the Proclamation shall <5>cease to operate at the expiration of thirty days from the date on which the <5>House of the People first sits after its reconstitution unless before the <5>expiration of the said period of thirty days a resolution approving the <5>Proclamation has been also passed by the House of the People. <6>3. <5>During the period any such Proclamation as is mentioned in clause (1) is in <5>operation, the executive authority of the Union shall extend to the giving of <5>directions to any State to observe such canons of financial propriety as may be <5>specified in the directions, and to the giving of such other directions as the <5>President may deem necessary and adequate for the purpose. <6>4. <5>Notwithstanding anything in this constitution- <6>a.<5> any such direction may include- <6>i. <5>a provision requiring the reduction of salaries and allowances of all or <5>any class of persons serving in connection with the affairs of a State; <6>ii. <5>a provision requiring all Money Bills or other Bills to which the <5>provisions of article 207 apply to be reserved for the consideration of <5>the President after they are passed by the Legislature of the State; <6>b.<5> it shall be competent for the President during the period any Proclamation <5>issued under this article is in operation to issue directions for the reduction <5>of salaries and allowances of all or any class of persons serving in <5>connection with the affairs of the Union including the Judges of the <5>Supreme Court and the High Courts. <9>PART XIX: MISCELLANEOUS <4>• Head of state immunity <7>361. Protection of President and Governors and <7>Rajpramukhs <6>1.<5> The President, or the Governor or Rajpramukh of a State, shall not be <5>answerable to any court for the exercise and performance of the powers and <5>duties of his office or for any act done or purporting to be done by him in the <5>exercise and performance of those powers and duties: <5>Provided that the conduct of the President may be brought under review by any <5>court, tribunal or body appointed or designated by either House of Parliament <5>for the investigation of a charge under article 61: <5>Provided further that nothing in this clause shall be construed as restricting the <5>right of any person to bring appropriate proceedings against the Government of <5>India or the Government of a State. <6>2.<5> No criminal proceedings whatsoever shall be instituted or continued against the <5>President, or the Governor of a State, in any court during his term of office. <6>3.<5> No process for the arrest or imprisonment of the President, or the Governor of a <5>State, shall issue from any court during his term of office. <6>4.<5> No civil proceedings in which relief is claimed against the President, or the <5>Governor of a State, shall be instituted during his term of office in any court in <5>respect of any act done or purporting to be done by him in his personal capacity, <5>whether before or after he entered upon his office as President, or as Governor <5>of such State, until the expiration of two months next after notice in writing has <5>been delivered to the President or the Governor, as the case may be, or left at <5>his office stating the nature of the proceedings, the cause of action therefor, the <5>name, description and place of residence of the party by whom such proceedings <5>are to be instituted and the relief which he claims. <7>361A. Protection of publication of proceedings of <7>Parliament and State Legislatures <6>1.<5> No person shall be liable to any proceedings, civil or criminal, in any court in <5>respect of the publication in a newspaper of a substantially true report of any <5>proceedings of either House of Parliament or the Legislative Assembly, or, as the <5>case may be, either House of the Legislature, of a State, unless the publication is <5>proved to have been made with malice: <5>Provided that nothing in this clause shall apply to the publication of any report <5>of the proceedings of a secret sitting of either House of Parliament or the <5>Legislative Assembly, or, as the case may be, either House of the Legislature, of a <5>State. <4>• Telecommunications <6>2.<5> Clause (1) shall apply in relation to reports or matters broadcast by means of <5>wireless telegraphy as part of any programme or service provided by means of a <5>broadcasting station as it applies in relation to reports or matters published in a <5>newspaper. <7>Explanation <5>In this article, "newspaper" includes a news agency report containing material for <5>publication in a newspaper. <7>361B. Disqualification for appointment on remunerative <7>political post <5>A member of a House belonging to any political party who is disqualified for being a <5>member of the House under paragraph 2 of the Tenth Schedule shall also be <5>disqualified to hold any remunerative political post for duration of the period <5>commencing from the date of his disqualification till the date on which the term of <5>his office as such member would expire or till the date on which he contests an <5>election to a House and is declared elected, whichever is earlier. <7>Explanation <5>For the purposes of this article,- <6>a.<5> the expression “House” has the meaning assigned to it in clause (a) of <5>paragraph 1 of the Tenth Schedule; <6>b.<5> the expression “remunerative political post” means any office— <6>i. <5>under the Government of India or the Government of a State where <5>the salary or remuneration for such office is paid out of the public <5>revenue of the Government of India or the Government of the State, as <5>the case may be; or <6>ii. <5>under a body, whether incorporated or not, which is wholly or partially <5>owned by the Government of India or the Government of a State and <5>the salary or remuneration for such office is paid by such body, <5>except where such salary or remuneration paid is compensatory in nature. <7>362. Rights and privileges of Rulers of Indian States <5>Rep. by the Constitution (Twenty-sixth Amendment) Act, 1971, s. 2. <7>363. Bar to interference by courts in disputes arising out of <7>certain treaties, agreements, etc <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution but subject to the provisions of <5>article <5>143, neither the Supreme Court nor any other court shall have <5>jurisdiction in any dispute arising out of any provision of a treaty, agreement, <5>covenant, engagement, sanad or other similar instrument which was entered <5>into or executed before the commencement of this Constitution by any Ruler of <5>an Indian State and to which the Government of the Dominion of India or any of <5>its predecessor Governments was a party and which has or has been continued <5>in operation after such commencement, or in any dispute in respect of any right <5>accruing under or any liability or obligation arising out of any of the provisions of <5>this Constitution relating to any such treaty, agreement, covenant, engagement, <5>sanad, or other similar instrument. <6>2.<5> In this article- <6>a.<5> "Indian State" means any territory recognised before the commencement <5>of this Constitution by His Majesty or the Government of the Dominion of <5>India as being such a State: and <6>b.<5> "Ruler" includes the Prince, Chief or other person recognised before such <5>commencement by His Majesty or the Government of the Dominion of <5>India as the Ruler of any Indian State. <7>363A. Recognition granted to Rulers of Indian States to <7>cease and Privy purses to be abolished <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution or in any law for the time being in <5>force- <6>a.<5> the Prince, Chief or other person who, at any time before the <5>commencement of the Constitution (Twenty-sixth Amendment) Act, 1971, <5>was recognised by the President as the Ruler of an Indian State or any <5>person who, at any time before such commencement, was recognised by <5>the President as the successor of such Ruler shall, on and from such <5>commencement, cease to be recognised as such Ruler or the successor of <5>such Ruler; <6>b.<5> on and from the commencement of the Constitution <5>(Twenty-sixth <5>Amendment) Act, 1971, privy purse is abolished and all rights, liabilities and <5>obligations in respect of privy purse are extinguished and accordingly the <5>Ruler or, as the case may be, the successor of such Ruler, referred to in <5>clause (a) or any other person shall not be paid any sum as privy purse. <7>364. Special provisions as to major ports and aerodromes <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, the President may by public <5>notification direct that as from such date as may be specified in the notification- <6>a.<5> any law made by Parliament or by the Legislature of a State shall not apply <5>to any major port or aerodrome or shall apply thereto subject to such <5>exceptions or modifications as may be specified in the notification, or <6>b.<5> any existing law shall cease to have effect in any major port or aerodrome <5>except as respects things done or omitted to be done before the said date, <5>or shall in its application to such port or aerodrome have effect subject to <5>such exceptions or modifications as may be specified in the notification. <6>2.<5> In this article- <6>a.<5> "major port" means a port declared to be a major port by or under any law <5>made by Parliament or any existing law and includes all areas for the time <5>being included within the limits of such port; <6>b.<5> "aerodrome" means aerodrome as defined for the purposes of the <5>enactments relating to airways, aircraft and air navigation. <7>365. Effect of failure to comply with, or to give effect to, <7>directions given by the Union <5>Where any State has failed to comply with, or to give effect to, any directions given in <5>the exercise of the executive power of the Union under any of the provisions of this <5>Constitution, it shall be lawful for the President to hold that a situation has arisen in <5>which the Government of the State cannot be carried on in accordance with the <5>provisions of this Constitution. <7>366. Definitions <5>In this Constitution, unless the context otherwise requires, the following expressions <5>have the meanings hereby respectively assigned to them, that is to say- <6>1. <5>"agricultural income" means agricultural income as defined for the <5>purposes of the enactments relating to Indian income-tax; <6>2. <5>"an Anglo-Indian" means a person whose father or any of whose other male <5>progenitors in the male line is or was of European descent but who is <5>domiciled within the territory of India and is or was born within such <5>territory of parents habitually resident therein and not established there <5>for temporary purposes only; <6>3. <5>"article" means an article of this Constitution; <6>4. <5>"borrow" includes the raising of money by the grant of annuities, and "loan" <5>shall be construed accordingly; <6>5. <5>"clause" means a clause of the article in which the expression occurs; <6>6. <5>"corporation tax" means any tax on income, so far as that tax is payable by <5>companies and is a tax in the case of which the following conditions are <5>fulfilled:- <6>a.<5> that it is not chargeable in respect of agricultural income; <6>b.<5> that no deduction in respect of the tax paid by the companies is, by any <5>enactments which may apply to the tax, authorised to be made from <5>dividends payable by the companies to individuals; <6>c. <5>that no provision exists for taking the tax so paid into account in <5>computing for the purposes of Indian income-tax the total income of <5>individuals receiving such dividends, or in computing the Indian <5>income-tax payable by, or refundable to, such individuals; <6>7. <5>"corresponding Province", "corresponding Indian State" or "corresponding <5>State" means in cases of doubt such Province, Indian State or State as may <5>be determined by the President to be the corresponding Province, the <5>corresponding Indian State or the corresponding State, as the case may be, <5>for the particular purpose in question; <6>8. <5>"debt" includes any liability in respect of any obligation to repay capital <5>sums by way of annuities and any liability under any guarantee, and "debt <5>charges" shall be construed accordingly; <6>9. <5>"estate duty" means a duty to be assessed on or by reference to the <5>principal value, ascertained in accordance with such rules as may be <5>prescribed by or under laws made by Parliament or the Legislature of a <5>State relating to the duty, of all property passing upon death or deemed, <5>under the provisions of the said laws, so to pass; <6>10. <5>"existing law" means any law, Ordinance, order, bye-law, rule or regulation <5>passed or made before the commencement of this Constitution by any <5>Legislature, authority or person having power to make such a law, <5>Ordinance, order, bye-law, rule or regulation; <6>11. <5>"Federal Court" means the Federal Court constituted under the <5>Government of India Act, 1935; <6>12. <5>"goods" includes all materials, commodities, and articles; <6>13. <5>"guarantee" includes any obligation undertaken before the commencement <5>of this Constitution to make payments in the event of the profits of an <5>undertaking falling short of a specified amount; <6>14. <5>"High Court" means any Court which is deemed for the purposes of this <5>Constitution to be a High Court for any State and includes- <6>a.<5> any Court in the territory of India constituted or reconstituted under <5>this Constitution as a High Court, and <6>b.<5> any other Court in the territory of India which may be declared by <5>Parliament by law to be a High Court for all or any of the purposes of <5>this Constitution; <6>15. <5>"Indian State" means any territory which the Government of the Dominion <5>of India recognised as such a State; <6>16. <5>"Part" means a Part of this Constitution; <6>17. <5>"pension" means a pension, whether contributory or not, of any kind <5>whatsoever payable to or in respect of any person, and includes retired pay <5>so payable; a gratuity so payable and any sum or sums so payable by way of <5>the return, with or without interest thereon or any other addition thereto, <5>of subscriptions to a provident fund; <6>18. <5>"Proclamation of Emergency" means a Proclamation issued under clause (1) <5>of article 352; <6>19. <5>"public notification" means a notification in the Gazette of India, or, as the <5>case may be, the Official Gazette of a State; <6>20. <5>"railway" does not include- <6>a.<5> a tramway wholly within a municipal area, or <6>b.<5> any other line of communication wholly situate in one State and <5>declared by Parliament by law not to be a railway; <6>21. <5>[omitted by the Constitution (Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956, s. 29 and <5>Sch.] <6>22. <5>"Ruler" means the Prince, Chief or other person who, at any time before the <5>commencement of the Constitution (Twenty-sixth Amendment) Act, 1971, <5>was recognised by the President as the Ruler of an Indian State or any <5>person who, at any time before such commencement, was recognised by <5>the President as the successor of such Ruler; <6>23. <5>"Schedule" means a Schedule to this Constitution; <6>24.<5> "Scheduled Castes" means such castes, races or tribes or parts of or groups <5>within such castes, races or tribes as are deemed under article 341 to be <5>Scheduled Castes for the purposes of this Constitution; <6>25.<5> "Scheduled Tribes" means such tribes or tribal communities or parts of or <5>groups within such tribes or tribal communities as are deemed under article <5>342 to be Scheduled Tribes for the purposes of this constitution; <6>26.<5> "securities" includes stock <6>27.<5> "sub-clause" means a sub-clause of the clause in which the expression <5>occurs; <6>28.<5> "taxation" includes the imposition of any tax or impost, whether general or <5>local or special, and "tax" shall be construed accordingly; <6>29.<5> "tax on income" includes a tax in the nature of an excess profits tax; <6>29A.<5> "tax on the sale or purchase of goods" includes- <6>a.<5> a tax on the transfer, otherwise than in pursuance of a contract, of <5>property in any goods for cash, deferred payment or other valuable <5>consideration; <6>b.<5> a tax on the transfer of property in goods (whether as goods or in some <5>other form) involved in the execution of a works contract; <6>c. <5>a tax on the delivery of goods on hire-purchase or any system of <5>payment by installments; <6>d.<5> a tax on the transfer of the right to use any goods for any purpose <5>(whether or not for a specified period) for cash, deferred payment or <5>other valuable consideration; <6>e.<5> a tax on the supply of goods by any unincorporated association or body <5>of persons to a member thereof for cash, deferred payment or other <5>valuable consideration; <6>f. <5>a tax on the supply, by way of or as part of any service or in any other <5>manner whatsoever, of goods, being food or any other article for <5>human consumption or any drink (whether or not intoxicating), where <5>such supply or service is for cash, deferred payment or other valuable <5>consideration, <5>and such transfer, delivery or supply of any goods shall be deemed to be a <5>sale of those goods by the person making the transfer, delivery or supply <5>and a purchase of those goods by the person to whom such transfer, <5>delivery or supply is made; <6>30.<5> "Union territory" means any Union territory specified in the First Schedule <5>and includes any other territory comprised within the territory of India but <5>not specified in that Schedule. <7>367. Interpretation <6>1.<5> Unless the context otherwise requires, the General Clauses Act, 1897, shall, <5>subject to any adaptations and modifications that may be made therein under <5>article 372, apply for the interpretation of this Constitution as it applies for the <5>interpretation of an Act of the Legislature of the Dominion of India. <6>2.<5> Any reference in this Constitution to Acts or laws of, or made by, Parliament, or <5>to Acts or laws of, or made by, the Legislature of a State, shall be construed as <5>including a reference to an Ordinance made by the President or, to an <5>Ordinance made by a Governor, as the case may be. <6>3.<5> For the purposes of this Constitution "foreign State" means any State other than <5>India: <5>Provided that, subject to the provisions of any law made by Parliament, the <5>President may by order declare any State not to be a foreign State for such <5>purposes as may be specified in the order. <9>PART XX: AMENDMENT OF THE <9>CONSTITUTION <7>368. Power of Parliament to amend the Constitution and <4>• Constitution amendment procedure <7>procedure therefor <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, Parliament may in exercise of its <5>constituent power amend by way of addition, variation or repeal any provision <5>of this Constitution in accordance with the procedure laid down in this article. <6>2.<5> An amendment of this Constitution may be initiated only by the introduction of <5>a Bill for the purpose in either House of Parliament, and when the Bill is passed <5>in each House by a majority of the total membership of that House and by a <5>majority of not less than two-thirds of the members of that House present and <5>voting, it shall be presented to the President who shall give his assent to the Bill <5>and thereupon the Constitution shall stand amended in accordance with the <5>terms of the Bill: <5>Provided that if such amendment seeks to make any change in- <6>a.<5> article 54, article 55, article 73, article 162 or article 241, or <6>b.<5> Chapter IV of Part V, Chapter V of Part VI, or Chapter I of Part XI, or <6>c. <5>any of the Lists in the Seventh Schedule, or <6>d.<5> the representation of States in Parliament, or <6>e.<5> the provisions of this article, <5>the amendment shall also require to be ratified by the Legislatures of not less <5>than one half of the States by resolutions to that effect passed by those <5>Legislatures before the Bill making provision for such amendment is presented <5>to the President for assent. <6>3.<5> Nothing in article 13 shall apply to any amendment made under this article. <6>4.<5> No amendment of this Constitution (including the provisions of Part III) made or <5>purporting to have been made under this article whether before or after the <5>commencement of section 55 of the Constitution (Forty-second Amendment) <5>Act, 1976 shall be called in question in any court on any ground. <6>5.<5> For the removal of doubts, it is hereby declared that there shall be no limitation <5>whatever on the constituent power of Parliament to amend by way of addition, <5>variation or repeal the provisions of this Constitution under this article. <9>PART XXI: TEMPORARY, TRANSITIONAL <9>AND SPECIAL PROVISIONS <4>• Transitional provisions <7>369. Temporary power to Parliament to make laws with <7>respect to certain matters in the State List as if they were <7>matters in the Concurrent List <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, Parliament shall, during a period of <5>five years from the commencement of this Constitution, have power to make laws <5>with respect to the following matters as if they were enumerated in the Concurrent <5>List, namely:- <6>a.<5> trade and commerce within a State List, and the production, supply and <5>distribution of, cotton and woollen textiles, raw cotton (including ginned <5>cotton and unginned cotton or kapas), cotton seed, paper (including <5>newsprint), food-stuffs (including edible oilseeds and oil), cattle fodder <5>(including oil-cakes and other concentrates), coal <5>(including coke and <5>derivatives of coal), iron, steel and mica; <6>b.<5> offences against laws with respect to any of the matters mentioned in <5>clause (a), jurisdiction and powers of all courts except the Supreme Court <5>with respect to any of those matters, and fees in respect of any of those <5>matters but not including fees taken in any court, <5>but any law made by Parliament, which Parliament would not but for the provisions <5>of this article have been competent to make, shall, to the extent of the incompetency, <5>cease to have effect on the expiration of the said period, except as respects things <5>done or omitted to be done before the expiration thereof. <7>370. Temporary provisions with respect to the State of <7>Jammu and Kashmir <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,- <6>a.<5> the provisions of article 238 shall not apply in relation to the State of <5>Jammu and Kashmir; <6>b.<5> the power of Parliament to make laws for the said State shall be limited to- <6>i. <5>those matters in the Union List and the Concurrent List which, in <5>consultation with the Government of the State, are declared by the <5>President to correspond to matters specified in the Instrument of <5>Accession governing the accession of the State to the Dominion of <5>India as the matters with respect to which the Dominion Legislature <5>may make laws for that State; and <6>ii. <5>such other matters in the said Lists, as, with the concurrence of the <5>Government of the State, the President may by order specify. <5>Explanation: For the purposes of this article, the Government of the <5>State means the person for the time being recognised by the President <5>as the Maharaja of Jammu and Kashmir acting on the advice of the <5>Council of Ministers for the time being in office under the Maharaja's <5>Proclamation dated the fifth day of March, 1948; <6>c. <5>the provisions of article 1 and of this article shall apply in relation to that <5>State; <6>d.<5> such of the other provisions of this Constitution shall apply in relation to <5>that State subject to such exceptions and modifications as the President <5>may by order specify: <5>Provided that no such order which relates to the matters specified in the <5>Instrument of Accession of the State referred to in paragraph (i) of sub-clause (b) <5>shall be issued except in consultation with the Government of the State: <5>Provided further that no such order which relates to matters other than those <5>referred to in the last preceding proviso shall be issued except with the <5>concurrence of that Government. <6>2. <5>If the concurrence of the Government of the State referred to in paragraph (ii) of <5>sub-clause (b) of clause (1) or in the second proviso to sub-clause (d) of that <5>clause be given before the Constituent Assembly for the purpose of framing the <5>Constitution of the State is convened, it shall be placed before such Assembly <5>for such decision as it may take thereon. <6>3. <5>Notwithstanding anything in the foregoing provisions of this article, the <5>President may, by public notification, declare that this article shall cease to be <5>operative or shall be operative only with such exceptions and modifications and <5>from such date as he may specify: <5>Provided that the recommendation of the Constituent Assembly of the State <5>referred to in clause (2) shall be necessary before the President issues such a <5>notification. <7>371. Special provision with respect to the States of <7>Maharashtra and Gujarat <6>1. <5>[omitted by s. 2, ibid., (w.e.f. 1-7-1974).] <6>2.<5> Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, the President may by order made <5>with respect to the State of Maharashtra or Gujarat, provide for any special <5>responsibility of the Governor for- <4>• Right to culture <6>a.<5> the establishment of separate development boards for Vidarbha, <4>• Indigenous right to representation <4>• Indigenous right to self governance <5>Marathwada, and the rest of Maharashtra or, as the case may be, <5>Saurashtra, Kutch and the rest of Gujarat with the provision that a report <5>on the working of each of these boards will be placed each year before the <5>State Legislative Assembly; <6>b.<5> the equitable allocation of funds for developmental expenditure over the <5>said areas, subject to the requirements of the State as a whole; and <6>c. <5>an equitable arrangement providing adequate facilities for technical <5>education and vocational training, and adequate opportunities for <5>employment in services under the control of the State Government, in <5>respect of all the said areas, subject to the requirements of the State as a <5>whole. <7>371A. Special provision with respect to the State of <7>Nagaland <6>1. <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,- <6>a. <5>no Act of Parliament in respect of- <6>i. <5>religious or social practices of the Nagas, <6>ii. <5>Naga customary law and procedure, <6>iii. <5>administration of civil and criminal justice involving decisions <5>according to Naga customary law, <6>iv.<5> ownership and transfer of land and its resources, <5>shall apply to the State of Nagaland unless the Legislative Assembly of <5>Nagaland by a resolution so decides; <6>b. <5>the Governor of Nagaland shall have special responsibility with respect to <5>law and order in the State of Nagaland for so long as in his opinion internal <5>disturbances occurring in the Naga Hills-Tuensang Area immediately <5>before the formation of that State continue therein or in any part thereof <5>and in the discharge of his functions in relation thereto the Governor shall, <5>after consulting the Council of Ministers, exercise his individual judgment <5>as to the action to be taken: <5>Provided that if any question arises whether any matter is or is not a matter <5>as respects which the Governor is under this sub-clause required to act in <5>the exercise of his individual judgment, the decision of the Governor in his <5>discretion shall be final, and the validity of anything done by the Governor <5>shall not be called in question on the ground that he ought or ought not to <5>have acted in the exercise of his individual judgment: <5>Provided further that if the President on receipt of a report from the <5>Governor or otherwise is satisfied that it is no longer necessary for the <5>Governor to have special responsibility with respect to law and order in the <5>State of Nagaland, he may by order direct that the Governor shall cease to <5>have such responsibility with effect from such date as may be specified in <5>the order; <6>c. <5>in making his recommendation with respect to any demand for a grant, the <5>Governor of Nagaland shall ensure that any money provided by the <5>Government of India out of the Consolidated Fund of India for any specific <5>service or purpose is included in the demand for a grant relating to that <5>service or purpose and not in any other demand; <6>d. <5>as from such date as the Governor of Nagaland may by public notification in <5>this behalf specify, there shall be established a regional council for the <5>Tuensang district consisting of thirty-five members and the Governor shall <5>in his discretion make rules providing for- <6>i. <5>the composition of the regional council and the manner in which the <5>members of the regional council shall be chosen: <5>Provided that the Deputy Commissioner of the Tuensang district shall <5>be the Chairman ex-officio of the regional council and the <5>Vice-Chairman of the regional council shall be elected by the members <5>thereof from amongst themselves; <6>ii. <5>the qualifications for being chosen as, and for being, members of the <5>regional council; <6>iii. <5>the term of office of, and the salaries and allowances, if any, to be paid <5>to members of, the regional council; <6>iv.<5> the procedure and conduct of business of the regional council; <6>v.<5> the appointment of officers and staff of the regional council and their <5>conditions of services; and <6>vi.<5> any other matter in respect of which it is necessary to make rules for <5>the constitution and proper functioning of the regional council. <6>2. <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, for a period of ten years from the <5>date of the formation of the State of Nagaland or for such further period as the <5>Governor may, on the recommendation of the regional council, by public <5>notification specify in this behalf,- <6>a.<5> the administration of the Tuensang district shall be carried on by the <5>Governor; <6>b. <5>where any money is provided by the Government of India to the <5>Government of Nagaland to meet the requirements of the State of <5>Nagaland as a whole, the Governor shall in his discretion arrange for an <5>equitable allocation of that money between the Tuensang district and the <5>rest of the State; <6>c. <5>no Act of the Legislature of Nagaland shall apply to Tuensang district unless <5>the Governor, on the recommendation of the regional council, by public <5>notification so directs and the Governor in giving such direction with <5>respect to any such Act may direct that the Act shall in its application to the <5>Tuensang district or any part thereof have effect subject to such exceptions <5>or modifications as the Governor may specify on the recommendation of <5>the regional council: <5>Provided that any direction given under this sub-clause may be given so as <5>to have retrospective effect; <6>d. <5>the Governor may make regulations for the peace, progress and good <5>government of the Tuensang district and any regulations so made may <5>repeal or amend with retrospective effect, if necessary, any Act of <5>Parliament or any other law which is for the time being applicable to that <5>district; <6>e. <6>i. <5>one of the members representing the Tuensang district in the <5>Legislative Assembly of Nagaland shall be appointed Minister for <5>Tuensang affairs by the Governor on the advice of the Chief Minister <5>and the Chief Minister in tendering his advice shall act on the <5>recommendation of the majority of the members as aforesaid; <6>ii. <5>the Minister for Tuensang affairs shall deal with, and have direct <5>access to the Governor on, all matters relating to the Tuensang district <5>but he shall keep the Chief Minister informed about the same; <6>f. <5>notwithstanding anything in the foregoing provisions of this clause, the <5>final decision on all matters relating to the Tuensang district shall be made <5>by the Governor in his discretion; <6>g. <5>in articles 54 and 55 and clause (4) of article 80, references to the elected <5>members of the Legislative Assembly of a State or to each such member <5>shall include references to the members or member of the Legislative <5>Assembly of Nagaland elected by the regional council established under <5>this article; <6>h. <5>in article 170- <6>i. <5>clause (1) shall, in relation to the Legislative Assembly of Nagaland, <5>have effect as if for the word "sixty", the words "forty-six" had been <5>substituted; <6>ii. <5>in the said clause, the reference to direct election from territorial <5>constituencies in the state shall include election by the members of the <5>regional council established under this article; <6>iii. <5>in clauses (2) and (3), references to territorial constituencies shall <5>mean references to territorial constituencies in the Kohima and <5>Mokokchung districts. <6>3.<5> If any difficulty arises in giving effect to any of the foregoing provisions of this <5>article, the President may by order do anything (including any adaptation or <5>modification of any other article) which appears to him to be necessary for the <5>purpose of removing that difficulty: <5>Provided that no such order shall be made after the expiration of three years <5>from the date of the formation of the State of Nagaland. <7>Explanation <5>In this article, the Kohima, Mokokchung and Tuensang districts shall have the same <5>meanings as in the State of Nagaland Act, 1962. <7>371B. Special provision with respect to the State of Assam <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, the President may, by order made <5>with respect to the State of Assam, provide for the constitution and functions of a <5>committee of the Legislative Assembly of the State consisting of members of that <5>Assembly elected from the tribal areas specified in Part I of the table appended to <5>paragraph 20 of the Sixth Schedule and such number of other members of that <5>Assembly as may be specified in the order and for the modifications to be made in <5>the rules of procedure of that Assembly for the constitution and proper functioning <5>of such committee. <7>371C. Special provision with respect to the State of <7>Manipur <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, the President may, by order <5>made with respect to the State of Manipur, provide for the constitution and <5>functions of a committee of the Legislative Assembly of the State consisting of <5>members of that Assembly elected from the Hill Areas of that State, for the <5>modifications to be made in the rules of business of the Government and in the <5>rules of procedure of the Legislative Assembly of the State and for any special <5>responsibility of the Governor in order to secure the proper functioning of such <5>committee. <6>2.<5> The Governor shall annually, or whenever so required by the President, make a <5>report to the President regarding the administration of the Hill Areas in the <5>State of Manipur and the executive power of the Union shall extend to the giving <5>of directions to the State as to the administration of the said areas. <7>Explanation <5>In this article, the expression "Hill Areas" means such areas as the President may, by <5>order, declare to be Hill Areas. <7>371D. Special provisions with respect to the State of <7>Andhra Pradesh <6>1. <5>The President may by order made with respect to the State of Andhra Pradesh <5>provide, having regard to the requirements of the State as a whole, for equitable <5>opportunities and facilities for the people belonging to different parts of the <5>State, in the matter of public employment and in the matter of education, and <5>different provisions may be made for various parts of the State. <6>2. <5>An order made under clause (1) may, in particular,- <6>a. <5>require the State Government to organise any class or classes of posts in a <5>civil service of, or any class or classes of civil posts under, the State into <5>different local cadres for different parts of the State and allot in accordance <5>with such principles and procedure as may be specified in the order the <5>persons holding such posts to the local cadres so organised; <6>b. <5>specify any part or parts of the State which shall be regarded as the local <5>area- <6>i. <5>for direct recruitment to posts in any local cadre (whether organised in <5>pursuance of an order under this article or constituted otherwise) <5>under the State Government; <6>ii. <5>for direct recruitment to posts in any cadre under any local authority <5>within the State; and <6>iii. <5>for the purposes of admission to any University within the state or to <5>any other educational institution which is subject to the control of the <5>State Government; <6>c. <5>specify the extent to which, the manner in which and the conditions subject <5>to which, preference or reservation shall be given or made- <6>i. <5>in the matter of direct recruitment to posts in any such cadre referred <5>to in sub-clause (b) as may be specified in this behalf in the order, <6>ii. <5>in the matter of admission to any such University or other educational <5>institution referred to in sub-clause (b) as may be specified in this <5>behalf in the order, <5>to or in favour of candidates who have resided or studied for any period <5>specified in the order in the local area in respect of such cadre, University <5>or other educational institution, as the case may be. <4>• Establishment of administrative courts <6>3. <5>The President may, by order, provide for the constitution of an Administrative <5>Tribunal for the State of Andhra Pradesh to exercise such jurisdiction, powers <5>and authority including any jurisdiction, power and authority which immediately <5>before the commencement of the Constitution (Thirty-second Amendment) Act, <5>1973, was exercisable by any court (other than the Supreme Court) or by any <5>tribunal or other authority as may be specified in the order with respect to the <5>following matters, namely:- <6>a.<5> appointment, allotment or promotion to such class or classes of posts in any <5>civil service of the State, or to such class or classes of civil posts under the <5>State, or to such class or classes of posts under the control of any local <5>authority within the State, as may be specified in the order; <6>b.<5> Seniority of persons appointed, allotted or promoted to such class or <5>classes of posts in any civil service of the State, or to such class or classes of <5>civil posts under the State, or to such class or classes of posts under the <5>control of any local authority within the State, as may be specified in the <5>order; <6>c. <5>such other conditions of service of persons appointed, allotted or promoted <5>to such class or classes of posts in any civil service of the State or to such <5>class or classes of civil posts under the State or to such class or classes of <5>posts under the control of any local authority within the State, as may be <5>specified in the order. <6>4. <5>An order made under clause (3) may- <6>a.<5> authorise the Administrative Tribunal to receive representations for the <5>redress of grievances relating to any matter within its jurisdiction as the <5>President may specify in the order and to make such orders thereon as the <5>Administrative Tribunal deems fit; <6>b.<5> contain such provisions with respect to the powers and authorities and <5>procedure of the Administrative Tribunal (including provisions with respect <5>to the powers of the Administrative Tribunal to punish for contempt of <5>itself) as the President may deem necessary; <6>c. <5>provide for the transfer to the Administrative Tribunal of such classes of <5>proceedings, being proceedings relating to matters within its jurisdiction <5>and pending before any court (other than the Supreme Court) or tribunal or <5>other authority immediately before the commencement of such order, as <5>may be specified in the order; <6>d.<5> contain such supplemental, incidental and consequential provisions <5>(including provisions as to fees and as to limitation, evidence or for the <5>application of any law for the time being in force subject to any exceptions <5>or modifications) as the President may deem necessary. <6>5. <5>The order of the Administrative Tribunal finally disposing of any case shall <5>become effective upon its confirmation by the State Government or on the <5>expiry of three months from the date on which the order is made, whichever is <5>earlier: <5>Provided that the State Government may, by special order made in writing and <5>for reasons to be specified therein, modify or annul any order of the <5>Administrative Tribunal before it becomes effective and in such a case, the order <5>of the Administrative Tribunal shall have effect only in such modified form or be <5>of no effect, as the case may be. <6>6. <5>Every special order made by the State Government under the proviso to clause <5>(5) shall be laid, as soon as may be after it is made, before both Houses of the <5>State Legislature. <6>7. <5>The High Court for the State shall not have any powers of superintendence over <5>the Administrative Tribunal and no court (other than the Supreme Court) or <5>tribunal shall exercise any jurisdiction, power or authority in respect of any <5>matter subject to the jurisdiction, power or authority of, or in relation to the <5>Administrative Tribunal. <6>8. <5>If the President is satisfied that the continued existence of the Administrative <5>Tribunal is not necessary, the President may by order abolish the Administrative <5>Tribunal and make such provisions in such order as he may deem fit for the <5>transfer and disposal of cases pending before the Tribunal immediately before <5>such abolition. <6>9. <5>Notwithstanding any judgment, decree or order of any court, tribunal or other <5>authority,- <6>a.<5> no appointment, posting, promotion or transfer of any person- <6>i. <5>made before the 1st day of November, 1956, to any post under the <5>Government of, or any local authority within, the State of Hyderabad <5>as it existed before that date; or <6>ii. <5>made before the commencement of the Constitution (Thirty-second <5>Amendment) Act, 1973, to any post under the Government of, or any <5>local or other authority within, the State of Andhra Pradesh; and <6>b.<5> no action taken or thing done by or before any person referred to in <5>sub-clause (a), <5>shall be deemed to be illegal or void or ever to have become illegal or void <5>merely on the ground that the appointment, posting, promotion or transfer of <5>such person was not made in accordance with any law, then in force, providing <5>for any requirement as to residence within the State of Hyderabad or, as the <5>case may be, within any part of the State of Andhra Pradesh, in respect of such <5>appointment, posting, promotion or transfer. <6>10. <5>The provisions of this article and of any order made by the President thereunder <5>shall have effect notwithstanding anything in any other provision of this <5>Constitution or in any other law for the time being in force. <7>371E. Establishment of Central University in Andhra <7>Pradesh <5>Parliament may by law provide for the establishment of a University in the State of <5>Andhra Pradesh. <7>371F.
