Special provisions with respect to the State of Sikkim <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,- <6>a. <5>the Legislative Assembly of the State of Sikkim shall consist of not less than <5>thirty members; <6>b. <5>as from the date of commencement of the Constitution (Thirty-sixth <5>Amendment) Act, 1975 (hereafter in this article referred to as the <5>appointed day)- <6>i. <5>the Assembly for Sikkim formed as a result of the elections held in <5>Sikkim in April, 1974 with thirty-two members elected in the said <5>elections (hereinafter referred to as the sitting members) shall be <5>deemed to be the Legislative Assembly of the State of Sikkim duly <5>constituted under this Constitution; <6>ii. <5>the sitting members shall be deemed to be the members of the <5>Legislative Assembly of the State of Sikkim duly elected under this <5>Constitution; and <6>iii. <5>the said Legislative Assembly of the State of Sikkim shall exercise the <5>powers and perform the functions of the Legislative Assembly of a <5>State under this Constitution; <6>c. <5>in the case of the Assembly deemed to be the Legislative Assembly of the <5>State of Sikkim under clause (b), the references to the period of five years in <5>clause (1) of article 172 shall be construed as references to a period of four <5>years and the said period of four years shall be deemed to commence from <5>the appointed day; <6>d. <5>until other provisions are made by Parliament by law, there shall be allotted <5>to the State of Sikkim one seat in the House of the People and the State of <5>Sikkim shall form one parliamentary constituency to be called the <5>parliamentary constituency for Sikkim; <6>e. <5>the representative of the State of Sikkim in the House of the People in <5>existence on the appointed day shall be elected by the members of the <5>Legislative Assembly of the State of Sikkim; <6>f. <5>Parliament may, for the purpose of protecting the rights and interests of <5>the different sections of the population of Sikkim make provision for the <5>number of seats in the Legislative Assembly of the State of Sikkim which <5>may be filled by candidates belonging to such sections and for the <5>delimitation of the assembly constituencies from which candidates <5>belonging to such sections alone may stand for election to the Legislative <5>Assembly of the State of Sikkim; <6>g. <5>the Governor of Sikkim shall have special responsibility for peace and for an <5>equitable arrangement for ensuring the social and economic advancement <5>of different sections of the population of Sikkim and in the discharge of his <5>special responsibility under this clause, the Governor of Sikkim shall, <5>subject to such directions as the President may, from time to time, deem fit <5>to issue, act in his discretion; <6>h. <5>all property and assets (whether within or outside the territories comprised <5>in the State of Sikkim) which immediately before the appointed day were <5>vested in the Government of Sikkim or in any other authority or in any <5>person for the purposes of the Government of Sikkim shall, as from the <5>appointed day, vest in the Government of the State of Sikkim; <6>i. <5>the High Court functioning as such immediately before the appointed day <5>in the territories comprised in the State of Sikkim shall, on and from the <5>appointed day, be deemed to be the High Court for the State of Sikkim; <6>j. <5>all courts of civil, criminal and revenue jurisdiction, all authorities and all <5>officers judicial, executive and ministerial, throughout the territory of the <5>State of Sikkim shall continue on and from the appointed day to exercise <5>their respective functions subject to the provisions of this Constitution; <6>k. <5>all laws in force immediately before the appointed day in the territories <5>comprised in the State of Sikkim or any part thereof shall continue to be in <5>force therein until amended or repealed by a competent Legislature or <5>other competent authority; <6>l. <5>for the purpose of facilitating the application of any such law as is referred <5>to in clause <6>k. <5>in relation to the administration of the State of Sikkim and for the purpose <5>of bringing the provisions of any such law into accord with the provisions of <5>this Constitution, the President may, within two years from the appointed <5>day, by order, make such adaptations and modifications of the law, whether <5>by way of repeal or amendment, as may be necessary or expedient, and <5>thereupon, every such law shall have effect subject to the adaptations and <5>modifications so made, and any such adaptation or modification shall not be <5>questioned in any court of law; <6>m. <5>neither the Supreme Court nor any other court shall have jurisdiction in <5>respect of any dispute or other matter arising out of any treaty, agreement, <5>engagement or other similar instrument relating to Sikkim which was <5>entered into or executed before the appointed day and to which the <5>Government of India or any of its predecessor Governments was a party, <5>but nothing in this clause shall be construed to derogate from the <5>provisions of article 143; <6>n. <5>the President may, by public notification, extend with such restrictions or <5>modifications as he thinks fit to the State of Sikkim any enactment which is <5>in force in a State in India at the date of the notification; <6>o.<5> if any difficulty arises in giving effect to any of the foregoing provisions of <5>this article, the President may, by order, do anything <5>(including any <5>adaptation or modification of any other article) which appears to him to be <5>necessary for the purpose of removing that difficulty: <5>Provided that no such order shall be made after the expiry of two years <5>from the appointed day; <6>p.<5> all things done and all actions taken in or in relation to the State of Sikkim <5>or the territories comprised therein during the period commencing on the <5>appointed day and ending immediately before the date on which the <5>Constitution (Thirty-sixth Amendment) Act, 1975, receives the assent of <5>the President shall, in so far as they are in conformity with the provisions of <5>this Constitution as amended by the Constitution <5>(Thirty-sixth <5>Amendment) Act, 1975, be deemed for all purposes to have been validly <5>done or taken under this Constitution as so amended. <4>• Right to culture <7>371G. Special provision with respect to the State of <4>• Indigenous right to self governance <7>Mizoram <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,- <6>a.<5> no Act of Parliament in respect of- <6>i. <5>religious or social practices of the Mizos. <6>ii. <5>Mizo customary law and procedure. <6>iii. <5>administration of civil and criminal justice involving decisions <5>according to Mizo customary law, <6>iv.<5> ownership and transfer of land, <5>shall apply to the State of Mizoram unless the Legislative Assembly of the <5>State of Mizoram by a resolution so decides: <5>Provided that nothing in this clause shall apply to any Central Act in force in <5>the Union territory of Mizoram immediately before the commencement of <5>the Constitution (Fifty-third Amendment) Act, 1986; <6>b.<5> the Legislative Assembly of the State of Mizoram shall consist of not less <5>than forty members. <7>371H. Special provision with respect to the State of <7>Arunachal Pradesh <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,- <6>a.<5> the governor of Arunachal Pradesh shall have special responsibility with <5>respect to law and order in the State of Arunachal Pradesh and in the <5>discharge of his functions in relation thereto, the Governor shall, after <5>consulting the Council of Ministers, exercise his individual judgment as to <5>the action to be taken: <5>Provided that if any question arises whether any matter is or is not a matter <5>as respects which the Governor is under this clause required to act in the <5>exercise of his individual judgment, the decision of the Governor in his <5>discretion shall be final, and the validity of anything done by the Governor <5>shall not be called in question on the ground that he ought or ought not to <5>have acted in the exercise of his individual judgment: <5>Provided further that if the President on receipt of a report from the <5>Governor or otherwise is satisfied that it is no longer necessary for the <5>Governor to have special responsibility with respect to law and order in the <5>State of Arunachal Pradesh, he may by order direct that the Governor shall <5>cease to have such responsibility with effect from such date as may be <5>specified in the order; <6>b.<5> the Legislative Assembly of the State of Arunachal Pradesh shall consist of <5>not less than thirty members. <7>371I. Special provision with respect to the State of Goa <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, the Legislative Assembly of the State <5>of Goa shall consist of not less than thirty members. <7>371J. Special provisions with respect to State of Karnataka <6>1.<5> The President may, by order made with respect to the State of Karnataka, <5>provide for any special responsibility of the Government for- <6>a.<5> establishment of a separate development board for Hyderabad-Karnataka <5>region with the provision that a report on the working of the board will be <5>placed each year before the State Legislative Assembly; <6>b.<5> equitable allocation of funds for developmental expenditure over the said <5>region, subject to the requirements of the State as a whole; and <6>c. <5>equitable opportunities and facilities for the people belonging to the said <5>region, in matters of public employment, education and vocational training, <5>subject to the requirements of the State as a whole. <6>2.<5> An order made under sub-clause (c) of clause (1) may provide for- <6>a.<5> reservation of a proportion of seats in educational and vocational training <5>institutions in the Hyderabad-Karnataka region for students who belong to <5>that region by birth or by domicile; and <6>b.<5> identification of posts or classes of posts under the State Government and <5>in any body or organisation under the control of the State Government in <5>the Hyderabad-Karnataka region and reservation of a proportion of such <5>posts for persons who belong to that region by birth or by domicile and for <5>appointment thereto by direct recruitment or by promotion or in any other <5>manner as may be specified in the order. <7>372. Continuance in force of existing laws and their <7>adaptation <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding the repeal by this Constitution of the enactments referred to <5>in article 395 but subject to the other provisions of this Constitution, all the law <5>in force in the territory of India immediately before the commencement of this <5>Constitution shall continue in force therein until altered or repealed or amended <5>by a competent Legislature or other competent authority. <6>2.<5> For the purpose of bringing the provisions of any law in force in the territory of <5>India into accord with the provisions of this Constitution, the President may by <5>order make such adaptations and modifications of such law, whether by way of <5>repeal or amendment, as may be necessary or expedient, and provide, that the <5>law shall, as from such date as may be specified in the order, have effect subject <5>to the adaptations and modifications so made, and any such adaptation or <5>modification shall not be questioned in any court of law. <6>3.<5> Nothing in clause (2) shall be deemed- <6>a.<5> to empower the President to make any adaptation or modification of any <5>law after the expiration of three years from the commencement of this <5>Constitution; or <6>b.<5> to prevent any competent Legislature or other competent authority from <5>repealing or amending any law adapted or modified by the President under <5>the said clause. <7>Explanation I <5>The expression "law in force" in this article shall include a law passed or made by a <5>Legislature or other competent authority in the territory of India before the <5>commencement of this Constitution and not previously repealed, notwithstanding <5>that it or parts of it may not be then in operation either at all or in particular areas. <7>Explanation II <5>Any law passed or made by a Legislature or other competent authority in the <5>territory of India which immediately before the commencement of this Constitution <5>had extra-territorial effect as well as effect in the territory of India shall, subject to <5>any such adaptations and modifications as aforesaid, continue to have such <5>extra-territorial effect. <7>Explanation III <5>Nothing in this article shall be construed as continuing any temporary law in force <5>beyond the date fixed for its expiration or the date on which it would have expired if <5>this Constitution had not come into force. <7>Explanation IV <5>An Ordinance promulgated by the Governor of a Province under section 88 of the <5>Government of India Act, 1935, and in force immediately before the commencement <5>of this Constitution shall, unless withdrawn by the Governor of the corresponding <5>State earlier, cease to operate at the expiration of six weeks from the first meeting <5>after such commencement of the Legislative Assembly of that State functioning <5>under clause (1) of article 382, and nothing in this article shall be construed as <5>continuing any such Ordinance in force beyond the said period. <7>372A. Power of the President to adapt laws <6>1.<5> For the purposes of bringing the provisions of any law in force in India or in any <5>part thereof, immediately before the commencement of the Constitution <5>(Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956, into accord with the provisions of this <5>Constitution as amended by that Act, the President may by order made before <5>the first day of November, 1957, make such adaptations and modifications of <5>the law, whether by way of repeal or amendment, as may be necessary or <5>expedient, and provide that the law shall, as from such date as may be specified <5>in the order, have effect subject to the adaptations and modifications so made, <5>and any such adaptation or modification shall not be questioned in any court of <5>law. <6>2.<5> Nothing in clause (1) shall be deemed to prevent a competent Legislature or <5>other competent authority from repealing or amending any law adapted or <5>modified by the President under the said clause. <7>373. Power of President to make order in respect of <7>persons under preventive detention in certain cases <5>Until provision is made by Parliament under clause (7) of article 22, or until the <5>expiration of one year from the commencement of this Constitution, whichever is <5>earlier the said article shall have effect as if for any reference to Parliament in <5>clauses (4) and (7) thereof there were substituted a reference to the President and <5>for any reference to an law made by Parliament in those clauses there were <5>substituted a reference to an order made by the President. <7>374. Provisions as to Judges of the Federal Court and <7>proceedings pending in the Federal Court or before His <7>Majesty in Council <6>1.<5> The Judges of the Federal Court holding office immediately before the <5>commencement of this Constitution shall, unless they have elected otherwise, <5>become on such commencement the Judges of the Supreme Court and shall <5>thereupon be entitled to such salaries and allowances and to such rights in <5>respect of leave of absence and pension as are provided for under article 125 in <5>respect of the Judges of the Supreme Court. <6>2.<5> All suits, appeals and proceedings, civil or criminal, pending in the Federal Court <5>at the commencement of this Constitution shall stand removed to the Supreme <5>Court, and the Supreme Court shall have jurisdiction to hear and determine the <5>same, and the judgments and orders of the Federal Court delivered or made <5>before the commencement of this Constitution shall have the same force and <5>effect as if they had been delivered or made by the Supreme Court. <6>3.<5> Nothing in this Constitution shall operate to invalidate the exercise of <5>jurisdiction by His Majesty in Council to dispose of appeals and petitions from, <5>or in respect of, any judgment, decree or order of any court within the territory <5>of India in so far as the exercise of such jurisdiction is authorised by law, and any <5>order of His Majesty in Council made on any such appeal or petition after the <5>commencement of this Constitution shall for all purposes have effect as if it <5>were an order or decree made by the Supreme Court in the exercise of the <5>jurisdiction conferred on such Court by this Constitution. <6>4.<5> On and from the commencement of this Constitution the jurisdiction of the <5>authority functioning as the Privy Council in a State specified in Part B of the <5>First Schedule to entertain and dispose of appeals and petitions from or in <5>respect of any judgment, decree or order of any court within that State shall <5>cease, and all appeals and other proceedings pending before the said authority <5>at such commencement shall be transferred to, and disposed of by, the Supreme <5>Court. <6>5.<5> Further provision may be made by Parliament by law to give effect to the <5>provisions of this article. <7>375. Courts, authorities and officers to continue to <7>function subject to the provisions of the Constitution <5>All courts of civil, criminal and revenue jurisdiction, all authorities and all officers, <5>judicial, executive and ministerial, throughout the territory of India, shall continue to <5>exercise their respective functions subject to the provisions of this Constitution. <7>376. Provisions as to Judges of High Courts <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in clause (2) of article 217, the Judges of a High Court <5>in any Province holding office immediately before the commencement of this <5>Constitution shall, unless they have elected otherwise, become on such <5>commencement the Judges of the High Court in the corresponding State, and <5>shall thereupon be entitled to such salaries and allowances and to such rights in <5>respect of leave of absence and pension as are provided for under article 221 in <5>respect of the Judges of such High Court. Any such Judge shall, notwithstanding <5>that he is not a citizen of India, be eligible for appointment as Chief Justice of <5>such High Court, or as Chief Justice or other Judge of any other High Court. <6>2.<5> The judges of a High Court in any Indian State corresponding to any State <5>specified in Part B of the First Schedule holding office immediately before the <5>commencement of this Constitution shall, unless they have elected otherwise, <5>become on such commencement the Judges of the High Court in the State so <5>specified and shall, notwithstanding anything in clauses (1) and (2) of article 217 <5>but subject to the proviso to clause (1) of that article, continue to hold office <5>until the expiration of such period as the President may by order determine. <6>3.<5> In this article, the expression "Judge" does not include an acting Judge or an <5>additional Judge. <7>377. Provisions as to Comptroller and Auditor-General of <7>India <5>The Auditor-General of India holding office immediately before the commencement <5>of this Constitution shall, unless he has elected otherwise, become on such <5>commencement the Comptroller and Auditor-General of India and shall thereupon <5>be entitled to such salaries and to such rights in respect of leave of absence and <5>pension as are provided for under clause (3) of article 148 in respect of the <5>Comptroller and Auditor-General of India and be entitled to continue to hold office <5>until the expiration of his term of office as determined under the provisions which <5>were applicable to him immediately before such commencement. <7>378. Provisions as to Public Service Commissions <6>1.<5> The members of the Public Service Commission for the Dominion of India <5>holding office immediately before the commencement of this Constitution shall, <5>unless they have elected otherwise, become on such commencement the <5>members of the Public Service Commission for the Union and shall, <5>notwithstanding anything in clauses (1) and (2) of article 316 but subject to the <5>proviso to clause (2) of that article, continue to hold office until the expiration of <5>their term of office as determined under the rules which were applicable <5>immediately before such commencement to such members. <6>2.<5> The members of a Public Service Commission of a Province or of a Public Service <5>Commission serving the needs of a group of Provinces holding office <5>immediately before the commencement of this Constitution shall, unless they <5>have elected otherwise, become on such commencement the members of the <5>Public Service Commission for the corresponding State or the members of the <5>Joint State Public Service Commission serving the needs of the corresponding <5>States, as the case may be, and shall, notwithstanding anything in clauses (1) and <5>(2) of article 316 but subject to the proviso to clause (2) of that article, continue <5>to hold office until the expiration of their term of office as determined under the <5>rules which were applicable immediately before such commencement to such <5>members. <7>378A. Special provisions as to duration of Andhra Pradesh <7>Legislative Assembly <5>Notwithstanding anything contained in article 172, the Legislative Assembly of the <5>State of Andhra Pradesh as constituted under the provisions of sections 28 and 29 of <5>the States Reorganisation Act, 1956, shall, unless sooner dissolved, continue for a <5>period of five years from the date referred to in the said section 29 and no longer and <5>the expiration of the said period shall operate as a dissolution of that Legislative <5>Assembly. <7>379-391. Rep. by the Constitution (Seventh Amendment) <7>Act, 1956, s. 29 and Sch <7>392. Power of the President to remove difficulties <6>1.<5> The President may, for the purpose of removing any difficulties, particularly in <5>relation to the transition from the provisions of the Government of India Act, <5>1935, to the provisions of this Constitution, by order direct that this <5>Constitution shall, during such period as may be specified in the order, have <5>effect subject to such adaptations, whether by way of modification, addition or <5>omission, as he may deem to be necessary or expedient: <5>Provided that no such order shall be made after the first meeting of Parliament <5>duly constituted under Chapter II of Part V. <6>2.<5> Every order made under clause (1) shall be laid before Parliament. <6>3.<5> The powers conferred on the President by this article, by article 324, by clause <5>(3) of article 367 and by article 391 shall, before the commencement of this <5>Constitution, be exercisable by the Governor-General of the Dominion of India. <9>PART XXII: SHORT TITLE, <9>COMMENCEMENT, AUTHORITATIVE TEXT <9>IN HINDI AND REPEALS <7>393. Short title <5>This Constitution may be called the Constitution of India. <7>394. Commencement <5>This article and articles 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 60, 324, 366, 367, 379, 380, 388, 391, 392 and <5>393 shall come into force at once, and the remaining provisions of this Constitution <5>shall come into force on the twenty-sixth day of January, 1950, which day is referred <5>to in this Constitution as the commencement of this Constitution. <7>394A. Authoritative text in the Hindi language <6>1.<5> The President shall cause to be published under his authority,- <6>a.<5> the translation of this Constitution in the Hindi language, signed by the <5>members of the Constituent Assembly, with such modifications as may be <5>necessary to bring it in conformity with the language, style and terminology <5>adopted in the authoritative texts of Central Acts in the Hindi language, <5>and incorporating therein all the amendments of this Constitution made <5>before such publication; and <6>b.<5> the translation in the Hindi language of every amendment of this <5>Constitution made in the English language. <6>2.<5> The translation of this Constitution and of every amendment thereof published <5>under clause (1) shall be construed to have the same meaning as the original <5>thereof and if any difficulty arises in so construing any part of such translation, <5>the President shall cause the same to be revised suitably. <6>3.<5> The translation of this Constitution and of every amendment thereof published <5>under this article shall be deemed to be, for all purposes, the authoritative text <5>thereof in the Hindi language. <7>395. Repeals <5>The Indian Independence Act, 1947, and the Government of India Act, 1935, <5>together with all enactments amending or supplementing the latter Act, but not <5>including the Abolition of Privy Council Jurisdiction Act, 1949, are hereby repealed. <9>FIRST SCHEDULE: (Articles 1 and 4) <7>I.
