<7>PART A: PROVISIONS AS TO THE PRESIDENT AND THE <7>GOVERNORS OF STATES <6>1.<5> There shall be paid to the President and to the Governors of the States the <5>following emoluments per mensem, that is to say:- <6>•<5> The President - 10,000 rupees. <6>•<5> The Governor of a State - 5,500 rupees. <6>2.<5> There shall also be paid to the President and to the Governors of the States such <5>allowances as were payable respectively to the Governor-General of the <5>Dominion of India and to the Governors of the corresponding Provinces <5>immediately before the commencement of this Constitution. <6>3.<5> The President and the Governors of the States throughout their respective <5>terms of office shall be entitled to the same privileges to which the <5>Governor-General and the Governors of the corresponding Provinces were <5>respectively entitled immediately before the commencement of this <5>Constitution. <6>4.<5> While the Vice-President or any other person is discharging the functions of, or <5>is acting as, President, or any person is discharging the functions of the <5>Governor, he shall be entitled to the same emoluments, allowances and <5>privileges as the President or the Governor whose functions he discharges or for <5>whom he acts, as the case may be. <7>PART B <5>[omitted by s. 29 and Sch., ibid.] <7>PART C: PROVISIONS AS TO THE SPEAKER AND THE <7>DEPUTY SPEAKER OF THE HOUSE OF THE PEOPLE AND <7>THE CHAIRMAN AND THE DEPUTY CHAIRMAN OF THE <7>COUNCIL OF STATES AND THE SPEAKER AND THE <7>DEPUTY SPEAKER OF THE LEGISLATIVE ASSEMBLY AND <7>THE CHAIRMAN AND THE DEPUTY CHAIRMAN OF THE <7>LEGISLATIVE COUNCIL OF A STATE <6>7.<5> There shall be paid to the Speaker of the House of the People and the Chairman <5>of the Council of States such salaries and allowances as were payable to the <5>Speaker of the Constituent Assembly of the Dominion of India immediately <5>before the commencement of this Constitution, and there shall be paid to the <5>Deputy Speaker of the House of the People and to the Deputy Chairman of the <5>Council of States such salaries and allowances as were payable to the Deputy <5>Speaker of the Constituent Assembly of the Dominion of India immediately <5>before such commencement. <6>8.<5> There shall be paid to the Speaker and the Deputy Speaker of the Legislative <5>Assembly and to the Chairman and the Deputy Chairman of the Legislative <5>Council of a State such salaries and allowances as were payable respectively to <5>the Speaker and the Deputy Speaker of the Legislative Assembly and the <5>President and the Deputy President of the Legislative Council of the <5>corresponding Province immediately before the commencement of this <5>Constitution and, where the corresponding Province had no Legislative Council <5>immediately before such commencement, there shall be paid to the Chairman <5>and the Deputy Chairman of the Legislative Council of the State such salaries <5>and allowances as the Governor of the State may determine. <7>PART D: PROVISIONS AS TO THE JUDGES OF THE <7>SUPREME COURT AND OF THE HIGH COURTS <6>9. 1.<5> There shall be paid to the Judges of the Supreme Court, in respect of time spent <5>on actual service, salary at the following rates per mensem, that is to say:- <6>•<5> The Chief Justice - 10,000 rupees. <6>•<5> Any Other Judge - 9,000 rupees. <5>Provided that if a Judge of the Supreme Court at the time of his appointment is <5>in receipt of a pension (other than a disability or wound pension) in respect of <5>any previous service under the Government of India or any of its predecessor <5>Governments or under the Government of a State or any of its predecessor <5>Governments, his salary in respect of service in the Supreme Court shall be <5>reduced- <6>a.<5> by the amount of that pension, and <6>b.<5> if he has, before such appointment, received in lieu of a portion of the <5>pension due to him in respect of such previous service the commuted value <5>thereof, by the amount of that portion of the pension, and <6>c. <5>If he has, before such appointment, received a retirement gratuity in <5>respect of such previous service, by the pension equivalent of that gratuity. <6>2. <5>Every Judge of the Supreme Court shall be entitled without payment of rent to <5>the use of an official residence. <6>3. <5>Nothing in sub-paragraph (2) of this paragraph shall apply to a Judge who, <5>immediately before the commencement of this Constitution,- <6>a.<5> was holding office as the Chief Justice of the Federal Court and has become <5>on such commencement the Chief Justice of the Supreme Court under <5>clause (1) of article 374, or <6>b.<5> was holding office as any other Judge of the Federal Court and has on such <5>commencement become a Judge (other than the Chief Justice) of the <5>Supreme Court under the said clause, <5>during the period he holds office as such Chief Justice or other Judge, and every <5>Judge who so becomes the Chief Justice or other Judge of the Supreme Court <5>shall, in respect of time spent on actual service as such Chief Justice or other <5>Judge, as the case may be, be entitled to receive in addition to the salary <5>specified in sub-paragraph (1) of this paragraph as special pay an amount <5>equivalent to the difference between the salary so specified and the salary <5>which he was drawing immediately before such commencement. <6>4. <5>Every Judge of the Supreme Court shall receive such reasonable allowances to <5>reimburse him for expenses incurred in travelling on duty within the territory of <5>India and shall be afforded such reasonable facilities in connection with <5>travelling as the President may from time to time prescribe. <6>5. <5>The rights in respect of leave of absence (including leave allowances) and <5>pension of the Judges of the Supreme Court shall be governed by the provisions <5>which, immediately before the commencement of this Constitution, were <5>applicable to the Judges of the Federal Court. <6>10. 1.<5> There shall be paid to the Judges of High Courts, in respect of time spent on <5>actual service, salary at the following rates per mensem, that is to say,- <6>•<5> The Chief Justice - 9,000 rupees. <6>•<5> Any other Judge - 8,000 rupees. <5>Provided that if a Judge of a High Court at the time of his appointment is in <5>receipt of a pension (other than a disability or wound pension) in respect of any <5>previous service under the Government of India or any of its predecessor <5>Governments or under the Government of a State or any of its predecessor <5>Governments, his salary in respect of service in the High Court shall be reduced- <6>a.<5> by the amount of that pension, and <6>b.<5> if he has, before such appointment, received in lieu of a portion of the <5>pension due to him in respect of such previous service the commuted value <5>thereof, by the amount of that portion of the pension, and <6>c. <5>if he has, before such appointment, received a retirement gratuity in <5>respect of such previous service, by the pension equivalent of that gratuity. <6>2. <5>Every person who immediately before the commencement of this Constitution- <6>a.<5> was holding office as the Chief Justice of a High Court in any Province and <5>has on such commencement become the Chief Justice of the High Court in <5>the corresponding State under clause (1) of Article 376, or <6>b.<5> was holding office as any other Judge of a High Court in any Province and <5>has on such commencement become a Judge (other than the Chief Justice) <5>of the High Court in the corresponding State under the said clause, <5>shall, if he was immediately before such commencement drawing a salary at a <5>rate higher than that specified in sub-paragraph (1) of this paragraph, be entitled <5>to receive in respect of time spent on actual service as such Chief Justice or <5>other Judge, as the case may be, in addition to the salary specified in the said <5>sub-paragraph as special pay an amount equivalent to the difference between <5>the salary so specified and the salary which he was drawing immediately before <5>such commencement. <6>3. <5>Any person who, immediately before the commencement of the Constitution <5>(Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956, was holding office as the Chief Justice of the <5>High Court of a State specified in Part B of the First Schedule and has on such <5>commencement become the Chief Justice of the High Court of a State specified <5>in the said Schedule as amended by the said Act, shall, if he was immediately <5>before such commencement drawing any amount as allowance in addition to his <5>salary, be entitled to receive in respect of time spent on actual service as such <5>Chief Justice, the same amount as allowance in addition to the salary specified in <5>sub-paragraph (1) of this paragraph. <6>11. <5>In this Part, unless the context otherwise requires,- <6>a.<5> the expression "Chief Justice" includes an acting Chief Justice, and a <5>"Judge" includes an ad hoc Judge; <6>b.<5> "actual service" includes- <6>i. <5>time spent by a Judge on duty as a Judge or in the performance of such <5>other functions as he may at the request of the President undertake to <5>discharge; <6>ii. <5>vacations, excluding any time during which the Judge is absent on <5>leave; and <6>iii. <5>joining time on transfer from a High Court to the Supreme Court or <5>from one High Court to another. <7>PART E: PROVISIONS AS TO THE COMPTROLLER AND <7>AUDITOR-GENERAL OF INDIA <6>12. 1.<5> There shall be paid to the Comptroller and Auditor-General of India a salary <5>at the rate of four thousand rupees per mensem. <6>2.<5> The person who was holding office immediately before the commencement of <5>this Constitution as Auditor-General of India and has become on such <5>commencement the Comptroller and Auditor-General of India under article 377 <5>shall in addition to the salary specified in sub-paragraph (1) of this paragraph be <5>entitled to receive as special pay an amount equivalent to the difference <5>between the salary so specified and the salary which he was drawing as <5>Auditor-General of India immediately before such commencement. <6>3.<5> The rights in respect of leave of absence and pension and the other conditions of <5>service of the Comptroller and Auditor-General of India shall be governed or <5>shall continue to be governed, as the case may be, by the provisions which were <5>applicable to the Auditor-General of India immediately before the <5>commencement of this Constitution and all references in those provisions to the <5>Governor-General shall be construed as references to the President. <9>THIRD SCHEDULE: Forms of Oaths or <9>Affirmations (Articles 75(4), 99, 124(6), <9>148(2), 164(3), 188 and 219) <4>• Oaths to abide by constitution <7>I. Form of oath of office for a Minister for the Union <5>"I, A.B., do Swear in the name of God/Solemnly Affirm that I will bear true faith and <5>allegiance to the Constitution of India as by law established, that I will uphold the <5>sovereignty and integrity of India, that I will faithfully and conscientiously discharge <5>my duties as a Minister for the Union and that I will do right to all manner of people <5>in accordance with the Constitution and the law, without fear or favour, affection or <5>ill- will." <7>II. Form of oath of secrecy for a Minister for the Union <5>"I, A.B., do Swear in the name of God/Solemnly Affirm that I will not directly or <5>indirectly communicate or reveal to any person or persons any matter which shall be <5>brought under my consideration or shall become known to me as a Minister for the <5>Union except as may be required for the due discharge of my duties as such <5>Minister." <7>III. <7>A. Form of oath or affirmation to be made by a candidate <7>for election to Parliament <5>"I, A.B., having been nominated as a candidate to fill a seat in the Council of <5>States (or the House of the People) do Swear in the name of God/Solemnly <5>Affirm that I will bear true faith and allegiance to the Constitution of India as by <5>law established and that I will uphold the sovereignty and integrity of India." <7>B. Form of oath or affirmation to be made by a member of <7>Parliament <5>"I, A.B., having been elected (or nominated) a member of the Council of States (or the <5>House of the People) do Swear in the name of God/Solemnly Affirm that I will bear <5>true faith and allegiance to the Constitution of India as by law established, that I will <5>uphold the sovereignty and integrity of India and that I will faithfully discharge the <5>duty upon which I am about to enter." <7>IV. Form of oath or affirmation to be made by the Judges of <7>the Supreme Court and the Comptroller and <7>Auditor-General of India <5>"I, A.B., having been appointed Chief Justice (or a Judge) of the Supreme Court of <5>India (or Comptroller and Auditor-General of India) do Swear in the name of <5>God/Solemnly Affirm that I will bear true faith and allegiance to the Constitution of <5>India as by law established, that I will uphold the sovereignty and integrity of India, <5>that I will duly and faithfully and to the best of my ability, knowledge and judgment <5>perform the duties of my office without fear or favour, affection or ill-will and that I <5>will uphold the Constitution and the laws." <7>V. Form of oath of office for a Minister for a State <5>"I, A.B., do Swear in the name of God/Solemnly Affirm that I will bear true faith and <5>allegiance to the Constitution of India as by law established, that I will uphold the <5>sovereignty and integrity of India, that I will faithfully and conscientiously discharge <5>my duties as a Minister for the State of and that I will do right to all manner of people <5>in accordance with the Constitution and the law without fear or favour, affection or <5>ill-will." <7>VI. Form of oath of secrecy for a Minister for a State <5>"I, A.B., do Swear in the name of God/Solemnly Affirm that I will not directly or <5>indirectly communicate or reveal to any person or persons any matter which shall be <5>brought under my consideration or shall become known to me as a Minister for the <5>State of except as may be required for the due discharge of my duties as such <5>Minister." <7>VII. <7>A. Form of oath or affirmation to be made by a candidate <7>for election to the Legislature of a State <5>"I, A.B., having been nominated as a candidate to fill a seat in the Legislative <5>Assembly (or Legislative Council), do Swear in the name of God/Solemnly Affirm <5>that I will bear true faith and allegiance to the Constitution of India as by law <5>established and that I will uphold the sovereignty and integrity of India." <7>B. Form of oath or affirmation to be made by a member of <7>the Legislature of a State <5>"I, A.B., having been elected (or nominated) a member of the Legislative Assembly (or <5>Legislative Council), do Swear in the name of God/Solemnly Affirm that I will bear <5>true faith and allegiance to the Constitution of India as by law established, that I will <5>uphold the sovereignty and integrity of India and that I will faithfully discharge the <5>duty upon which I am about to enter." <7>VIII. Form of oath or affirmation to be made by the Judges <7>of a High Court <5>"I, A.B., having been appointed Chief Justice (or a Judge) of the High Court at (or of) <5>do swear in the name of God solemnly affirm that I will bear true faith and allegiance <5>to the Constitution of India as by law established, that I will uphold the sovereignty <5>and integrity of India, that, I will duly and faithfully and to the best of my ability, <5>knowledge and judgment perform the duties of my office without fear or favour, <5>affection or ill-will and that I will uphold the Constitution and the laws." <9>FOURTH SCHEDULE: Allocation of Seats in <9>the Council of States (Articles 4(1) and 80(2)) <5>To each State or Union territory specified in the first column of the following table, <5>there shall be allotted the number of seats specified in the second column thereof <5>opposite to that State or that Union Territory, as the case may be. <6>1. <5>Andhra Pradesh - 18 <6>2. <5>Assam - 7 <6>3. <5>Bihar - 22 <6>4. <5>Goa - 1 <6>5. <5>Gujarat - 11 <6>6. <5>Haryana - 5 <6>7. <5>Kerala - 9 <6>8. <5>Madhya Pradesh - 16 <6>9. <5>Tamil Nadu - 18 <6>10. <5>Maharashtra - 19 <6>11. <5>Karnataka - 12 <6>12. <5>Orissa - 10 <6>13. <5>Punjab - 7 <6>14. <5>Rajasthan - 10 <6>15. <5>Uttar Pradesh - 34 <6>16. <5>West Bengal - 16 <6>17. <5>Jammu and Kashmir - 4 <6>18. <5>Nagaland - 1 <6>19. <5>Himachal Pradesh - 3 <6>20. <5>Manipur - 1 <6>21. <5>Tripura - 1 <6>22. <5>Meghalaya - 1 <6>23. <5>Sikkim - 1 <6>24. <5>Mizoram - 1 <6>25. <5>Arunachal Pradesh - 1 <6>26. <5>Delhi - 3 <6>27. <5>Pondicherry - 1 <5>TOTAL 233 <9>FIFTH SCHEDULE: Provisions as to the <9>Administration and Control of Scheduled <9>Areas and Scheduled Tribes (Article 244 (1)) <4>• Right to culture <4>• Indigenous right to self governance <7>PART A: GENERAL <7>1. Interpretation <5>In this Schedule, unless the context otherwise requires, the expression "State" does <5>not include the States of Assam, Meghalaya, Tripura and Mizoram. <7>2. Executive power of a State in Scheduled Areas <5>Subject to the provisions of this Schedule, the executive power of a State extends to <5>the Scheduled Areas therein. <7>3. Report by the Governor to the President regarding the <7>administration of Scheduled Areas <5>The Governor of each State having Scheduled Areas therein shall annually, or <5>whenever so required by the President, make a report to the President regarding the <5>administration of the Scheduled Areas in that State and the executive power of the <5>Union shall extend to the giving of directions to the State as to the administration of <5>the said areas. <7>PART B: ADMINISTRATION AND CONTROL OF <7>SCHEDULED AREAS AND SCHEDULED TRIBES <7>4. Tribes Advisory Council <6>1.<5> There shall be established in each State having Scheduled Areas therein and, if <5>the President so directs, also in any State having Scheduled Tribes but not <5>Scheduled Areas therein, a Tribes Advisory Council consisting of not more than <5>twenty members of whom, as nearly as may be, three-fourths shall be the <5>representatives of the Scheduled Tribes in the Legislative Assembly of the State: <5>Provided that if the number of representatives of the Scheduled Tribes in the <5>Legislative Assembly of the State is less than the number of seats in the Tribes <5>Advisory Council to be filled by such representatives, the remaining seats shall <5>be filled by other members of those tribes. <6>2.<5> It shall be the duty of the Tribes Advisory Council to advise on such matters <5>pertaining to the welfare and advancement of the Scheduled Tribes in the State <5>as may be referred to them by the Governor <6>3.<5> The Governor may make rules prescribing or regulating, as the case may be,- <6>a.<5> the number of members of the Council, the mode of their appointment and <5>the appointment of the Chairman of the Council and of the officers and <5>servants thereof; <6>b.<5> the conduct of its meetings and its procedure in general; and <6>c. <5>all other incidental matters. <7>5. Law applicable to Scheduled Areas <6>1. <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution the Governor may by public <5>notification direct that any particular Act of Parliament or of the Legislature of <5>the State shall not apply to a Scheduled Area or any part thereof in the State or <5>shall apply to a Scheduled Area or any part thereof in the State subject to such <5>exceptions and modifications as he may specify in the notification and any <5>direction given under this sub-paragraph may be given so as to have <5>retrospective effect. <6>2. <5>The Governor may make regulations for the peace and good government of any <5>area in a State which is for the time being a Scheduled Area. <5>In particular and without prejudice to the generality of the foregoing power, <5>such regulations may- <6>a.<5> prohibit or restrict the transfer of land by or among members of the <5>Scheduled Tribes in such area; <6>b.<5> regulate the allotment of land to members of the Scheduled Tribes in such <5>area; <6>c. <5>regulate the carrying on of business as money-lender by persons who lend <5>money to members of the Scheduled Tribes in such area. <6>3. <5>In making any such regulation as is referred to in sub-paragraph (2) of this <5>paragraph, the Governor may repeal or amend any Act of Parliament or of the <5>Legislature of the State or any existing law which is for the time being applicable <5>to the area in question. <6>4. <5>All regulations made under this paragraph shall be submitted forthwith to the <5>President and, until assented to by him, shall have no effect. <6>5. <5>No regulation shall be made under this paragraph unless the Governor making <5>the regulation has, in the case where there is a Tribes Advisory Council for the <5>State, consulted such Council. <7>PART C: SCHEDULED AREAS <7>6. Scheduled Areas <6>1.<5> In this Constitution, the expression "Scheduled Areas" means such areas as the <5>President may by order566 declare to be Scheduled Areas. <6>2.<5> The President may at any time by order- <6>a.<5> direct that the whole or any specified part of a Scheduled Area shall cease <5>to be a Scheduled Area or a part of such an area; <6>aa.<5> increase the area of any Scheduled Area in a State after consultation with <5>the Governor of that State; <6>b.<5> alter, but only by way of rectification of boundaries, any Scheduled Area; <6>c. <5>on any alternation of the boundaries of a State or on the admission into the <5>Union or the establishment of a new State, declare any territory not <5>previously included in any State to be, or to form part of, a Scheduled Area; <6>d.<5> rescind, in relation to any State or States, any order or orders made under <5>this paragraph, and in consultation with the Governor of the State <5>concerned, make fresh orders redefining the areas which are to be <5>Scheduled Areas, <5>and any such order may contain such incidental and consequential provisions as <5>appear to the President to be necessary and proper, but save as aforesaid, the <5>order made under subparagraph (1) of this paragraph shall not be varied by any <5>subsequent order. <7>PART D: AMENDMENT OF THE SCHEDULE <7>7. Amendment of the Schedule <6>1.<5> Parliament may from time to time by law amend by way of addition, variation or <5>repeal any of the provisions of this Schedule and, when the Schedule is so <5>amended, any reference to this Schedule in this Constitution shall be construed <5>as a reference to such Schedule as so amended. <6>2.<5> No such law as is mentioned in sub-paragraph (1) of this paragraph shall be <5>deemed to be an amendment of this Constitution for the purposes of article 368. <9>SIXTH SCHEDULE: Provisions as to the <9>Administration of Tribal Areas in the States of <9>Assam, Meghalaya, Tripura and Mizoram <9>(Articles 244 (2) and 275 (1)) <7>1. Autonomous districts and autonomous regions <6>1.<5> Subject to the provisions of this paragraph, the tribal areas in each item of <5>571572Parts I, II and IIA and in Part III of the table appended to paragraph 20 of <5>this Schedule shall be an autonomous district. <6>2.<5> If there are different Scheduled Tribes in an autonomous district, the Governor <5>may, by public notification, divide the area or areas inhabited by them into <5>autonomous regions. <6>3.<5> The Governor may, by public notification,- <6>a.<5> include, any area in 573any of the Parts of the said table, <6>b.<5> exclude any area from 574any of the Parts of the said table, <6>c. <5>create a new autonomous district, <6>d.<5> increase the area of any autonomous district, <6>e.<5> diminish the area of any autonomous district, <6>f. <5>unite two or more autonomous districts or parts thereof so as to form one <5>autonomous district, <6>ff.<5> alter the name of any autonomous district, <6>g.<5> define the boundaries of any autonomous district: <5>Provided that no order shall be made by the Governor under clauses (c), (d), (e) <5>and (f) of this sub-paragraph except after consideration of the report of a <5>Commission appointed under sub-paragraph <5>(1) of paragraph <5>14 of this <5>Schedule: <5>Provided further that any order made by the Governor under this <5>sub-paragraph may contain such incidental and consequential provisions <5>(including any amendment of paragraph 20 and of any item in any of the Parts of <5>the said table) as appear to the Governor to be necessary for giving effect to the <5>provisions of the order. <7>2. Constitution of District Councils and Regional Councils <6>1. <5>There shall be a District Council for each autonomous district consisting of not <5>more than thirty members, of whom not more than four persons shall be <5>nominated by the Governor and the rest shall be elected on the basis of adult <5>suffrage. <6>2. <5>There shall be a separate Regional Council for each area constituted an <5>autonomous region under sub-paragraph (2) of paragraph 1 of this Schedule. <6>3. <5>Each District Council and each Regional Council shall be a body corporate by the <5>name respectively of "the District Council of (name of district)" and "the <5>Regional Council of (name of region)", shall have perpetual succession and a <5>common seal and shall by the said name sue and be sued. <6>4. <5>Subject to the provisions of this Schedule, the administration of an autonomous <5>district shall, in so far as it is not vested under this Schedule in any Regional <5>Council within such district, be vested in the District Council for such district <5>and the administration of an autonomous region shall be vested in the Regional <5>Council for such region. <6>5. <5>In an autonomous district with Regional Councils, the District Council shall have <5>only such powers with respect to the areas under the authority of the Regional <5>Council as may be delegated to it by the Regional Council in addition to the <5>powers conferred on it by this Schedule with respect to such areas. <6>6. <5>The Governor shall make rules for the first constitution of District Councils and <5>Regional Councils in consultation with the existing tribal Councils or other <5>representative tribal organisations within the autonomous districts or regions <5>concerned, and such rules shall provide for- <6>a.<5> the composition of the District Councils and Regional Councils and the <5>allocation of seats therein; <6>b.<5> the delimitation of territorial constituencies for the purpose of elections to <5>those Councils; <6>c. <5>the qualifications for voting at such elections and the preparation of <5>electoral rolls therefor; <6>d.<5> the qualifications for being elected at such elections as members of such <5>Councils: <6>e.<5> the term of office of members of 579Regional Councils; <6>f. <5>any other matter relating to or connected with elections or nominations to <5>such Councils; <6>g.<5> the procedure and the conduct of business 580(including the power to act <5>notwithstanding any vacancy) in the District and Regional Councils; <6>h.<5> the appointment of officers and staff of the District and Regional Councils. <6>6A. <5>The elected members of the District Council shall hold office for a term of five <5>years from the date appointed for the first meeting of the Council after the <5>general elections to the Council, unless the District Council is sooner dissolved <5>under Paragraph 16 and a nominated member shall hold office at the pleasure of <5>the Governor: <5>Provided that the said period of five years may, while a Proclamation of <5>Emergency is in operation or if circumstances exist which, in the opinion of the <5>Governor, render the holding of elections impracticable, be extended by the <5>Governor for a period not exceeding one year at a time and in any case where a <5>Proclamation of Emergency is in operation not extending beyond a period of six <5>months after the Proclamation has ceased to operate: <5>Provided further that a member elected to fill a casual vacancy shall hold office <5>only for the remainder of the term of office of the member whom he replaces. <6>7. <5>The District or the Regional Council may after its first constitution make rules <5>with the approval of the Governor with regard to the matters specified in <5>subparagraph (6) of this paragraph and may also make rules 583with like <5>approval regulating- <6>a.<5> the formation of subordinate local Councils or Boards and their procedure <5>and the conduct of their business; and <6>b.<5> generally all matters relating to the transaction of business pertaining to <5>the administration of the district or region, as the case may be: <5>Provided that until rules are made by the District or the Regional Council under <5>this subparagraph the rules made by the Governor under sub-paragraph (6) of <5>this paragraph shall have effect in respect of elections to, the officers and staff <5>of, and the procedure and the conduct of business in, each such Council. <7>3. Powers of the District Councils and Regional Councils to <7>make laws <6>1. <5>The Regional Council for an autonomous region in respect of all areas within <5>such region and the District Council for an autonomous district in respect of all <5>areas within the district except those which are under the authority of Regional <5>Councils, if any, within the district shall have power to make laws with respect <5>to- <6>a. <5>the allotment, occupation or use, or the setting apart, of land, other than <5>any land which is a reserved forest for the purposes of agriculture or <5>grazing or for residential or other non-agricultural purposes or for any <5>other purpose likely to promote the interests of the inhabitants of any <5>village or town: <5>Provided that nothing in such laws shall prevent the compulsory acquisition <5>of any land, whether occupied or unoccupied, for public purposes 586by <5>the Government of the State concerned in accordance with the law for the <5>time being in force authorising such acquisition; <6>b. <5>the management of any forest not being a reserved forest; <6>c. <5>the use of any canal or water-course for the purpose of agriculture; <6>d. <5>the regulation of the practice of jhum or other forms of shifting cultivation; <6>e. <5>the establishment of village or town committees or councils and their <5>powers; <6>f. <5>any other matter relating to village or town administration, including village <5>or town police and public health and sanitation; <6>g. <5>the appointment or succession of Chiefs or headmen; <6>h. <5>the inheritance of property; <6>i. <5>marriage and divorce; <6>j. <5>social customs. <6>2. <5>In this paragraph, a "reserved forest" means any area which is a reserved forest <5>under the Assam Forest Regulation, 1891, or under any other law for the time <5>being in force in the area in question. <6>3. <5>All laws made under this paragraph shall be submitted forthwith to the <5>Governor and, until assented to by him, shall have no effect. <7>4. Administration of justice in autonomous districts and <7>autonomous regions <6>1. <5>The Regional Council for an autonomous region in respect of areas within such <5>region and the District Council for an autonomous district in respect of areas <5>within the district other than those which are under the authority of the <5>Regional Councils, if any, within the district may constitute village councils or <5>courts for the trial of suits and cases between the parties all of whom belong to <5>Scheduled Tribes within such areas, other than suits and cases to which the <5>provisions of sub-paragraph (1) of paragraph 5 of this Schedule apply, to the <5>exclusion of any court in the State, and may appoint suitable persons to be <5>members of such village councils or presiding officers of such courts, and may <5>also appoint such officers as may be necessary for the administration of the laws <5>made under paragraph 3 of this Schedule. <6>2. <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, the Regional Council for an <5>autonomous region or any court constituted in that behalf by the Regional <5>Council or, if in respect of any area within an autonomous district there is no <5>Regional Council, the District Council for such district, or any court constituted <5>in that behalf by the District Council, shall exercise the powers of a court of <5>appeal in respect of all suits and cases triable by a village council or court <5>constituted under sub-paragraph (1) of this paragraph within such region or <5>area, as the case may be, other than those to which the provisions of <5>sub-paragraph (1) of paragraph 5 of this Schedule apply, and no other court <5>except the High Court and the Supreme Court shall have jurisdiction over such <5>suits or cases. <6>3. <5>The High Court shall have and exercise such jurisdiction over the suits and cases <5>to which the provisions of sub-paragraph (2) of this paragraph apply as the <5>Governor may from time to time by order specify. <6>4. <5>A Regional Council or District Council, as the case may be, may with the <5>previous approval of the Governor make rules regulating- <6>a.<5> the constitution of village councils and courts and the powers to be <5>exercised by them under this paragraph; <6>b.<5> the procedure to be followed by village councils or courts in the trial of suits <5>and cases under sub-paragraph (1) of this paragraph; <6>c. <5>the procedure to be followed by the Regional or District Council or any <5>court constituted by such Council in appeals and other proceedings under <5>sub-paragraph (2) of this paragraph; <6>d.<5> the enforcement of decisions and orders of such Councils and courts; <6>e.<5> all other ancillary matters for the carrying out of the provisions of <5>sub-paragraphs (1) and (2) of this paragraph. <6>5. <5>On and from such date as the President may, 590after consulting the <5>Government of the State concerned, by notification appoint in this behalf, this <5>paragraph shall have effect in relation to such autonomous district or region as <5>may be specified in the notification, as if- <6>a. <5>in sub-paragraph (1), for the words "between the parties all of whom belong <5>to Scheduled Tribes within such areas, other than suits and cases to which <5>the provisions of sub-paragraph (1) of paragraph 5 of this Schedule apply", <5>the words "not being suits and cases of the nature referred to in <5>sub-paragraph (1) of paragraph (5) of this Schedule, which the Governor <5>may specify in this behalf," had been substituted; <6>b. <5>sub-paragraphs (2) and (3) had been omitted; <6>c. <5>in sub-paragraph (4)- <6>i. <5>for the words "A Regional Council or District Council, as the case may <5>be, may with the previous approval of the Governor make rules <5>regulating", the words "The Governor may make rules regulating" had <5>been substituted; and <6>ii. <5>for clause (a), the following clause had been substituted, namely:- <5>"(a) the constitution of village councils and courts, the powers to be <5>exercised by them under this paragraph and the courts to which <5>appeals from the decisions of village councils and courts shall lie;"; <6>iii. <5>for clause (c), the following clause had been substituted, namely:- <5>"(c) the transfer of appeals and other proceedings pending before the <5>Regional or District Council or any court constituted by such Council <5>immediately before the date appointed by the President under <5>sub-paragraph (5);"; and <6>iv.<5> in clause (e), for the words, brackets and figures "sub-paragraphs (1) <5>and (2)", the word, brackets and figure "sub-paragraph (1)" had been <5>substituted. <7>5. Conferment of powers under the Code of Civil <7>Procedure, 1908, and the Code of Criminal Procedure, <7>1898, on the Regional and District Councils and on certain <7>courts and officers for the trial of certain suits, cases and <7>offences <6>1.<5> The Governor may, for the trial of suits or cases arising out of any law in force in <5>any autonomous district or region being a law specified in that behalf by the <5>Governor, or for the trial of offences punishable with death, transportation for <5>life, or imprisonment for a term of not less than five years under the Indian Penal <5>Code or under any other law for the time being applicable to such district or <5>region, confer on the District Council or the Regional Council having authority <5>over such district or region or on courts constituted by such District Council or <5>on any officer appointed in that behalf by the Governor, such powers under the <5>Code of Civil Procedure, 1908, or as the case may be, the Code of Criminal <5>Procedure, 1898, as he deems appropriate, and thereupon the said Council, <5>court or officer shall try the suits, cases or offences in exercise of the powers so <5>conferred. <6>2.<5> The Governor may withdraw or modify any of the powers conferred on a <5>District Council, Regional Council, court or officer under sub-paragraph (1) of <5>this paragraph. <6>3.<5> Save as expressly provided in this paragraph, the Code of Civil Procedure, 1908, <5>and the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898593, shall not apply to the trial of any <5>suits, cases or offences in an autonomous district or in any autonomous region <5>to which the provisions of this paragraph apply. <6>4.<5> On and from the date appointed by the President under sub-paragraph (5) of <5>paragraph 4 in relation to any autonomous district or autonomous region, <5>nothing contained in this paragraph shall, in its application to that district or <5>region, be deemed to authorise the Governor to confer on the District Council <5>or Regional Council or on courts constituted by the District Council any of the <5>powers referred to in sub-paragraph (1) of this paragraph. <7>6. Powers of the District Council to establish primary <7>schools, etc <6>1.<5> The District Council for an autonomous district may establish, construct, or <5>manage primary schools, dispensaries, markets, <5>596cattle pounds, ferries, <5>fisheries, roads, road transport and waterways in the district and may, with the <5>previous approval of the Governor, make regulations for the regulation and <5>control thereof and, in particular, may prescribe the language and the manner in <5>which primary education shall be imparted in the primary schools in the district. <6>2.<5> The Governor may, with the consent of any District Council, entrust either <5>conditionally or unconditionally to that Council or to its officers functions in <5>relation to agriculture, animal husbandry, community projects, co-operative <5>societies, social welfare, village planning or any other matter to which the <5>executive power of the State extends. <7>7. District and Regional Funds <6>1.<5> There shall be constituted for each autonomous district, a District Fund and for <5>each autonomous region, a Regional Fund to which shall be credited all moneys <5>received respectively by the District Council for that district and the Regional <5>Council for that region in the course of the administration of such district or <5>region, as the case may be, in accordance with the provisions of this <5>Constitution. <6>2.<5> The Governor may make rules for the management of the District Fund, or, as <5>the case may be, the Regional Fund and for the procedure to be followed in <5>respect of payment of money into the said Fund, the withdrawal of moneys <5>therefrom, the custody of moneys therein and any other matter connected with <5>or ancillary to the matters aforesaid. <6>3.<5> The accounts of the District Council or, as the case may be, the Regional Council <5>shall be kept in such form as the Comptroller and Auditor-General of India may, <5>with the approval of the President, prescribe. <6>4.<5> The Comptroller and Auditor-General shall cause the accounts of the District <5>and Regional Councils to be audited in such manner as he may think fit, and the <5>reports of the Comptroller and Auditor-General relating to such accounts shall <5>be submitted to the Governor who shall cause them to be laid before the <5>Council. <7>8. Powers to assess and collect land revenue and to impose <7>taxes <6>1. <5>The Regional Council for an autonomous region in respect of all lands within <5>such region and the District Council for an autonomous district in respect of all <5>lands within the district except those which are in the areas under the authority <5>of Regional Councils, if any, within the district, shall have the power to assess <5>and collect revenue in respect of such lands in accordance with the principles for <5>the time being followed 599by the Government of the State in assessing lands <5>for the purpose of land revenue in the State generally. <6>2. <5>The Regional Council for an autonomous region in respect of areas within such <5>region and the District Council for an autonomous district in respect of all areas <5>in the district except those which are under the authority of Regional Councils, if <5>any, within the district, shall have power to levy and collect taxes on lands and <5>buildings, and tolls on persons resident within such areas. <6>3. <5>The District Council for an autonomous district shall have the power to levy and <5>collect all or any of the following taxes within such district, that is to say- <6>a.<5> taxes on professions, trades, callings and employments; <6>b.<5> taxes on animals, vehicles and boats; <6>c. <5>taxes on the entry of goods into a market for sale therein, and tolls on <5>passengers and goods carried in ferries; and <6>d.<5> taxes for the maintenance of schools, dispensaries or roads. <6>4. <5>A Regional Council or District Council, as the case may be, may make regulations <5>to provide for the levy and collection of any of the taxes specified in <5>sub-paragraphs (2) and (3) of this paragraph 600and every such regulation shall <5>be submitted forthwith to the Governor and, until assented to by him, shall have <5>no effect. <7>9. Licences or leases for the purpose of prospecting for, or <7>extraction of, minerals <6>1.<5> Such share of the royalties accruing each year from licences or leases for the <5>purpose of prospecting for, or the extraction of, minerals granted by the <5>Government of the State in respect of any area within an autonomous district as <5>may be agreed upon between the Government of the State and the District <5>Council of such district shall be made over to that District Council. <6>2.<5> If any dispute arises as to the share of such royalties to be made over to a <5>District Council, it shall be referred to the Governor for determination and the <5>amount determined by the Governor in his discretion shall be deemed to be the <5>amount payable under subparagraph (1) of this paragraph to the District Council <5>and the decision of the Governor shall be final. <7>10. Power of District Council to make regulations for the <7>control of moneylending and trading by non-tribals <6>1. <5>The District Council of an autonomous district may make regulations for the <5>regulation and control of money-lending or trading within the district by <5>persons other than Scheduled Tribes resident in the district. <6>2. <5>In particular and without prejudice to the generality of the foregoing power, <5>such regulations may- <6>a.<5> prescribe that no one except the holder of a licence issued in that behalf <5>shall carry on the business of money-lending; <6>b.<5> prescribe the maximum rate of interest which may be charged or be <5>recovered by a money-lender; <6>c. <5>provide for the maintenance of accounts by money-lenders and for the <5>inspection of such accounts by officers appointed in that behalf by the <5>District Council; <6>d.<5> prescribe that no person who is not a member of the Scheduled Tribes <5>resident in the district shall carry on wholesale or retail business in any <5>commodity except under a licence issued in that behalf by the District <5>Council: <5>Provided that no regulations may be made under this paragraph unless they are <5>passed by a majority of not less than three-fourths of the total membership of <5>the District Council: <5>Provided further that it shall not be competent under any such regulations to <5>refuse the grant of a licence to a money-lender or a trader who has been <5>carrying on business within the district since before the time of the making of <5>such regulations. <6>3. <5>All regulations made under this paragraph shall be submitted forthwith to the <5>Governor and, until assented to by him, shall have no effect. <7>11. Publication of laws, rules and regulations made under <7>the Schedule <5>All laws, rules and regulations made under this Schedule by a District Council or a <5>Regional Council shall be published forthwith in the Official Gazette of the State and <5>shall on such publication have the force of law. <7>12. Application of Acts of Parliament and of the Legislature <7>of the State of Assam to autonomous districts and <7>autonomous regions in the state of Assam <6>1.<5> Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,- <6>a.<5> no Act of the Legislature of the State of Assam in respect of any of the <5>matters specified in paragraph 3 of this Schedule as matters with respect to <5>which a District Council or a Regional Council may make laws, and no Act of <5>the Legislature of the State of Assam prohibiting or restricting the <5>consumption of any non-distilled alcoholic liquor shall apply to any <5>autonomous district or autonomous region 609in that State unless in either <5>case the District Council for such district or having jurisdiction over such <5>region by public notification so directs, and the District Council in giving <5>such direction with respect to any Act may direct that the Act shall in its <5>application to such district or region or any part thereof have effect subject <5>to such exceptions or modifications as it thinks fit; <6>b.<5> the Governor may, by public notification, direct that any Act of Parliament <5>or of the Legislature of the State of Assam to which the provisions of clause <5>(a) of this subparagraph do not apply, shall not apply to an autonomous <5>district or an autonomous region in that State, or shall apply to such district <5>or region or any part thereof subject to such exceptions or modifications as <5>he may specify in the notification. <6>2.<5> Any direction given under sub-paragraph (1) of this paragraph may be given so <5>as to have retrospective effect. <7>12A. Application of Acts of Parliament and of the <7>Legislature of the State of Meghalaya to autonomous <7>districts and autonomous regions in the State of <7>Meghalaya <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,- <6>a.<5> if any provision of a law made by a District or Regional Council in the State <5>of Meghalaya with respect to any matter specified in sub-paragraph (1) of <5>paragraph 3 of this Schedule or if any provision of any regulation made by a <5>District Council or a Regional Council in that State under paragraph 8 or <5>paragraph 10 of this Schedule, is repugnant to any provision of a law made <5>by the Legislature of the State of Meghalaya with respect to that matter, <5>then, the law or regulation made by the District Council or, as the case may <5>be, the Regional Council whether made before or after the law made by the <5>Legislature of the State of Meghalaya, shall, to the extent of repugnancy, be <5>void and the law made by the Legislature of the State of Meghalaya shall <5>prevail; <6>b.<5> the President may, with respect to any Act of Parliament, by notification, <5>direct that it shall not apply to an autonomous district or an autonomous <5>region in the State of Meghalaya, or shall apply to such district or region or <5>any part thereof subject to such exceptions or modifications as he may <5>specify in the notification and any such direction may be given so as to have <5>retrospective effect. <7>12AA. Application of Acts of Parliament and of the <7>Legislature of the State of Tripura to the autonomous <7>district and autonomous regions in the State of Tripura <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,- <6>a. <5>no Act of the Legislature of the State of Tripura in respect of any of the <5>matters specified in paragraph 3 of this Schedule as matters with respect to <5>which a District Council or a Regional Council may make laws, and no Act of <5>the Legislature of the State of Tripura prohibiting or restricting the <5>consumption of any non-distilled alcoholic liquor shall apply to the <5>autonomous district or an autonomous region in that State unless, in either <5>case, the District Council for that district or having jurisdiction over such <5>region by public notification so directs, and the District Council in giving <5>such direction with respect to any Act may direct that the Act shall, in its <5>application to that district or such region or any part thereof, have effect <5>subject to such exceptions or modifications as it thinks fit; <6>b. <5>the Governor may, by public notification, direct that any Act of the <5>Legislature of the State of Tripura to which the provisions of clause (a) of <5>the sub-paragraph do not apply, shall not apply to the autonomous district <5>or an autonomous region in that State, or shall apply to that district or such <5>region, or any part thereof, subject to such exceptions or modifications, as <5>he may specify in the notification; <6>c. <5>the President may, with respect to any Act of Parliament, by notification, <5>direct that it shall not apply to the autonomous district or an autonomous <5>region in the State of Tripura, or shall apply to such district or region or any <5>part thereof, subject to such exceptions or modifications as he may specify <5>in the notification and any such direction may be given so as to have <5>retrospective effect. <7>12B. Application of Acts of Parliament and of the <7>Legislature of the State of Mizoram to autonomous <7>districts and autonomous regions in the State of Mizoram <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,- <6>a.<5> no Act of the Legislature of the State of Mizoram in respect of any of the <5>matters specified in paragraph 3 of this Schedule as matters with respect to <5>which a District Council or a Regional Council may make laws, and no Act of <5>the Legislature of the State of Mizoram prohibiting or restricting the <5>consumption of any non-distilled alcoholic liquor shall apply to any <5>autonomous district or autonomous region in that State unless, in either <5>case, the District Council for such district or having jurisdiction over such <5>region, by public notification, so directs, and the District Council, in giving <5>such direction with respect to any Act, may direct that the Act shall, in its <5>application to such district or region or any part thereof, have effect subject <5>to such exceptions or modifications as it thinks fit; <6>b.<5> the Governor may, by public notification, direct that any Act of the <5>Legislature of the State of Mizoram to which the provisions of clause (a) of <5>this sub-paragraph do not apply, shall not apply to an autonomous district <5>or an autonomous region in that State, or shall apply to such district or <5>region, or any part thereof, subject to such exceptions or modifications, as <5>he may specify in the notification; <6>c. <5>the President may, with respect to any Act of Parliament, by notification, <5>direct that it shall not apply to an autonomous district or an autonomous <5>region in the State of Mizoram, or shall apply to such district or region or <5>any part thereof, subject to such exceptions or modifications as he may <5>specify in the notification and any such direction may be given so as to have <5>retrospective effect. <7>13. Estimated receipts and expenditure pertaining to <7>autonomous districts to be shown separately in the annual <7>financial statement <5>The estimated receipts and expenditure pertaining to an autonomous district which <5>are to be credited to, or is to be made from, the Consolidated Fund of the State shall <5>be first placed before the District Council for discussion and then after such <5>discussion be shown separately in the annual financial statement of the State to be <5>laid before the Legislature of the State under article 202. <7>14. Appointment of Commission to inquire into and report <7>on the administration of autonomous districts and <7>autonomous regions <6>1. <5>The Governor may at any time appoint a Commission to examine and report on <5>any matter specified by him relating to the administration of the autonomous <5>districts and autonomous regions in the State, including matters specified in <5>clauses (c), (d), (e) and (f) of sub-paragraph (3) of paragraph 1 of this Schedule, or <5>may appoint a Commission to inquire into and report from time to time on the <5>administration of autonomous districts and autonomous regions in the State <5>generally and in particular on- <6>a.<5> the provision of educational and medical facilities and communications in <5>such districts and regions; <6>b.<5> the need for any new or special legislation in respect of such districts and <5>regions; and <6>c. <5>the administration of the laws, rules and regulations made by the District <5>and Regional Councils, <5>and define the procedure to be followed by such Commission. <6>2. <5>The report of every such Commission with the recommendations of the <5>Governor with respect thereto shall be laid before the Legislature of the State <5>by the Minister concerned together with an explanatory memorandum <5>regarding the action proposed to be taken thereon by the Government of the <5>State. <6>3. <5>In allocating the business of the Government of the State among his Ministers <5>the Governor may place one of his Ministers specially in charge of the welfare of <5>the autonomous districts and autonomous regions in the State. <7>15. Annulment or suspension of acts and resolutions of <7>District and Regional Councils <6>1.<5> If at any time the Governor is satisfied that an act or resolution of a District or a <5>Regional Council is likely to endanger the safety of India 618or is likely to be <5>prejudicial to public order, he may annul or suspend such act or resolution and <5>take such steps as he may consider necessary (including the suspension of the <5>Council and the assumption to himself of all or any of the powers vested in or <5>exercisable by the Council) to prevent the commission or continuance of such <5>act, or the giving of effect to such resolution. <6>2.<5> Any order made by the Governor under sub-paragraph (1) of this paragraph <5>together with the reasons therefor shall be laid before the Legislature of the <5>State as soon as possible and the order shall, unless revoked by the Legislature <5>of the State, continue in force for a period of twelve months from the date on <5>which it was so made: <5>Provided that if and so often as a resolution approving the continuance in force <5>of such order is passed by the Legislature of the State, the order shall unless <5>cancelled by the Governor continue in force for a further period of twelve <5>months from the date on which under this paragraph it would otherwise have <5>ceased to operate. <7>16. Dissolution of a District or a Regional Council <6>1. <5>The Governor may on the recommendation of a Commission appointed under <5>paragraph 14 of this Schedule by public notification order the dissolution of a <5>district or a Regional Council, and- <6>a.<5> direct that a fresh general election shall be held immediately for the <5>reconstitution of the Council, or <6>b.<5> subject to the previous approval of the Legislature of the State assume the <5>administration of the area under the authority of such Council himself or <5>place the administration of such area under the Commission appointed <5>under the said paragraph or any other body considered suitable by him for <5>a period not exceeding twelve months: <5>Provided that when an order under clause (a) of this paragraph has been made, <5>the Governor may take the action referred to in clause (b) of this paragraph with <5>regard to the administration of the area in question pending the reconstitution <5>of the Council on fresh general election: <5>Provided further that no action shall be taken under clause (b) of this paragraph <5>without giving the District or the Regional Council, as the case may be, an <5>opportunity of placing its views before the Legislature of the State. <6>2. <5>If at any time the Governor is satisfied that a situation has arisen in which the <5>administration of an autonomous district or region cannot be carried on in <5>accordance with the provisions of this Schedule, he may, by public notification <5>assume to himself all or any of the functions or powers vested in or exercisable <5>by the District Council or, as the case may be, the Regional Council and declare <5>that such functions or powers shall be exercisable by such person or authority as <5>he may specify in this behalf, for a period not exceeding six months: <5>Provided that the Governor may by a further order or orders extend the <5>operation of the initial order by a period not exceeding six months on each <5>occasion. <6>3. <5>Every order made under sub-paragraph (2) of this paragraph with the reasons <5>therefor shall be laid before the Legislature of the State and shall cease to <5>operate at the expiration of thirty days from the date on which the State <5>Legislature first sits after the issue of the order, unless, before the expiry of that <5>period it has been approved by the State Legislature. <7>17. Exclusion of areas from autonomous districts in <7>forming constituencies in such districts <5>For the purposes of elections to the Legislative Assembly of Assam or Meghalaya or <5>Tripura or Mizoram, the Governor may by order declare that any area within an <5>autonomous district 625in the State of Assam or Meghalaya or Tripura or Mizoram, <5>as the case may be, shall not form part of any constituency to fill a seat or seats in the <5>Assembly reserved for any such district but shall form part of a constituency to fill a <5>seat or seats in the Assembly not so reserved to be specified in the order. <7>18. omitted by s. 71(i) and Eighth Sch., ibid. (w.e.f. <7>21-1-1972) <4>• Transitional provisions <7>19. Transitional provisions <6>1.<5> As soon as possible after the commencement of this Constitution the Governor <5>shall take steps for the constitution of a District Council for each autonomous <5>district in the State under this Schedule and, until a District Council is so <5>constituted for an autonomous district, the administration of such district shall <5>be vested in the Governor and the following provisions shall apply to the <5>administration of the areas within such district instead of the foregoing <5>provisions of this Schedule, namely:- <6>a.<5> no Act of Parliament or of the Legislature of the State shall apply to any <5>such area unless the Governor by public notification so directs; and the <5>Governor in giving such a direction with respect to any Act may direct that <5>the Act shall, in its application to the area or to any specified part thereof, <5>have effect subject to such exceptions or modifications as he thinks fit; <6>b.<5> the Governor may make regulations for the peace and good government of <5>any such area and any regulations so made may repeal or amend any Act of <5>Parliament or of the Legislature of the State or any existing law which is for <5>the time being applicable to such area. <6>2.<5> Any direction given by the Governor under clause (a) of sub-paragraph (1) of this <5>paragraph may be given so as to have retrospective effect. <6>3.<5> All regulations made under clause (b) of sub-paragraph (1) of this paragraph <5>shall be submitted forthwith to the President and, until assented to by him, shall <5>have no effect. <7>20. Tribal areas <6>1.<5> The areas specified in Parts I, II, IIA and III of the table below shall respectively <5>be the tribal areas within the State of Assam, the State of Meghalaya, the State <5>of Tripura and the State of Mizoram. <6>2.<5> Any reference in Part I, Part II or Part III of the table below to any district shall <5>be construed as a reference to the territories comprised within the autonomous <5>district of that name existing immediately before the day appointed under <5>clause (b) of section 2 of the North-Eastern Areas (Reorganisation) Act, 1971: <5>Provided that for the purposes of clauses (e) and (f) of sub-paragraph (1) of <5>paragraph 3, paragraph 4, paragraph 5, paragraph 6, sub-paragraph (2), clauses <5>(a), (b) and (d) of subparagraph (3) and sub-paragraph (4) of paragraph 8 and <5>clause (d) of sub-paragraph (2) of paragraph 10 of this Schedule, no part of the <5>area comprised within the municipality of Shillong shall be deemed to be within <5>the Khasi Hills District. <6>3.<5> The reference in Part IIA in the table below to the "Tripura Tribal Areas District" <5>shall be construed as a reference to the territory comprising the tribal areas <5>specified in the First Schedule to the Tripura Tribal Areas Autonomous District <5>Council Act, 1979. <7>TABLE <7>PART 1 <6>1.<5> The North Cachar Hills District. <6>2. <5>636The Karbi Anglong District. <7>PART 2 <6>1.<5> Khasi Hills District. <6>2.<5> Jaintia Hills District. <6>3.<5> The Garo Hills District. <7>PART 2A <5>Tripura Tribal Areas District. <7>PART 3 <6>1.<5> The Chakma District. <6>2.<5> The Mara District. <6>3.<5> The Lai District. <7>20A. Dissolution of the Mizo District Council <6>1. <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Schedule, the District Council of the Mizo <5>District existing immediately before the prescribed date (hereinafter referred to <5>as the Mizo District Council) shall stand dissolved and cease to exist. <6>2. <5>The Administrator of the Union territory of Mizoram may, by one or more <5>orders, provide for all or any of the following matters, namely:- <6>a.<5> the transfer, in whole or in part, of the assets, rights and liabilities of the <5>Mizo District Council (including the rights and liabilities under any contract <5>made by it) to the Union or to any other authority; <6>b.<5> the substitution of the Union or any other authority for the Mizo District <5>Council, or the addition of the Union or any other authority, as a party to <5>any legal proceedings to which the Mizo District Council is a party; <6>c. <5>the transfer or re-employment of any employees of the Mizo District <5>Council to or by the Union or any other authority, the terms and conditions <5>of service applicable to such employees after such transfer or <5>re-employment; <6>d.<5> the continuance of any laws, made by the Mizo District Council and in force <5>immediately before its dissolution, subject to such adaptations and <5>modifications, whether by way of repeal or amendment, as the <5>Administrator may make in this behalf, until such laws are altered, repealed <5>or amended by a competent Legislature or other competent authority; <6>e.<5> such incidental, consequential and supplementary matters as the <5>Administrator considers necessary. <7>Explanation <5>In this paragraph and in paragraph 20B of this Schedule, the expression "prescribed <5>date" means the date on which the Legislative Assembly of the Union territory of <5>Mizoram is duly constituted under and in accordance with the provisions of the <5>Government of Union Territories Act, 1963. <7>20B. Autonomous regions in the Union territory of <7>Mizoram to be autonomous districts and transitory <7>provisions consequent thereto <6>1. <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Schedule,- <6>a.<5> every autonomous region existing immediately before the prescribed date <5>in the Union territory of Mizoram shall, on and from that date, be an <5>autonomous district in that Union territory (hereafter referred to as the <5>corresponding new district) and the Administrator thereof may, by one or <5>more orders, direct that such consequential amendments as are necessary <5>to give effect to the provisions of this clause shall be made in paragraph 20 <5>of this Schedule (including Part III of the table appended to that paragraph) <5>and thereupon the said paragraph and the said part III shall be deemed to <5>have been amended accordingly; <6>b.<5> every Regional Council of an autonomous region in the Union territory of <5>Mizoram existing immediately before the prescribed date <5>(hereafter <5>referred to as the existing Regional Council) shall, on and from that date <5>and until a District Council is duly constituted for the corresponding new <5>district, be deemed to be the District Council of that district (hereafter <5>referred to as the corresponding new District Council). <6>2. <5>Every member whether elected or nominated of an existing Regional Council <5>shall be deemed to have been elected or, as the case may be, nominated to the <5>corresponding new District Council and shall hold office until a District Council <5>is duly constituted for the corresponding new district under this Schedule. <6>3. <5>Until rules are made under sub-paragraph (7) of paragraph 2 and sub-paragraph <5>(4) of paragraph 4 of this Schedule by the corresponding new District Council, <5>the rules made under the said provisions by the existing Regional Council and in <5>force immediately before the prescribed date shall have effect in relation to the <5>corresponding new District Council subject to such adaptations and <5>modifications as may be made therein by the Administrator of the Union <5>territory of Mizoram. <6>4. <5>The Administrator of the Union territory of Mizoram may, by one or more <5>orders, provide for all or any of the following matters, namely:- <6>a.<5> the transfer in whole or in part of the assets, rights and liabilities of the <5>existing Regional Council (including the rights and liabilities under any <5>contract made by it) to the corresponding new District Council; <6>b.<5> the substitution of the corresponding new District Council for the existing <5>Regional Council as a party to the legal proceedings to which the existing <5>Regional Council is a party; <6>c. <5>the transfer or re-employment of any employees of the existing Regional <5>Council to or by the corresponding new District Council, the terms and <5>conditions of service applicable to such employees after such transfer or <5>re-employment; <6>d.<5> the continuance of any laws made by the existing Regional Council and in <5>force immediately before the prescribed date, subject to such adaptations <5>and modifications, whether by way of repeal or amendment, as the <5>Administrator may make in this behalf until such laws are altered, repealed <5>or amended by a competent Legislature or other competent authority; <6>e.<5> such incidental, consequential and supplementary matters as the <5>Administrator considers necessary. <7>20C. Interpretation <5>Subject to any provision made in this behalf, the provisions of this Schedule shall, in <5>their application to the Union territory of Mizoram, have effect- <6>1. <5>as if references to the Governor and Government of the State were <5>references to the Administrator of the Union territory appointed under <5>article 239, references to State (except in the expression "Government of <5>the State") were references to the Union territory of Mizoram and <5>references to the State Legislature were references to the Legislative <5>Assembly of the Union territory of Mizoram; <6>2. <5>as if- <6>a.<5> in sub-paragraph (5) of paragraph 4, the provision for consultation with <5>the Government of the State concerned had been omitted; <6>b.<5> in sub-paragraph (2) of paragraph 6, for the words "to which the <5>executive power of the State extends", the words "with respect to <5>which the Legislative Assembly of the Union territory of Mizoram has <5>power to make laws" had been substituted; <6>c. <5>in paragraph 13, the words and figures "under article 202" had been <5>omitted. <7>21. Amendment of the Schedule <6>1.<5> Parliament may from time to time by law amend by way of addition, variation or <5>repeal any of the provisions of this Schedule and, when the Schedule is so <5>amended, any reference to this Schedule in this Constitution shall be construed <5>as a reference to such Schedule as so amended. <6>2.<5> No such law as is mentioned in sub-paragraph (1) of this paragraph shall be <5>deemed to be an amendment of this Constitution for the purposes of article 368. <9>SEVENTH SCHEDULE: (Article 246) <7>List I: Union List <6>1.<5> Defence of India and every part III of <5>1955), in contravention of the second proviso to clause (1) of article 31A shall, to the <5>extent of the contravention, be void. <9>TENTH SCHEDULE: Provisions as to <9>disqualification on ground of defection <9>(Articles 102(2) and 191(2)) <7>1. Interpretation <5>In this Schedule, unless the context otherwise requires,- <6>a.<5> "House" means either House of Parliament or the Legislative Assembly or, <5>as the case may be, either House of the Legislature of a State; <6>b.<5> "legislature party", in relation to a member of a House belonging to any <5>political party in accordance with the provisions of paragraph <5>2 or <5>paragraph 4, means the group consisting of all the members of that House <5>for the time being belonging to that political party in accordance with the <5>said provisions; <6>c. <5>"original political party", in relation to a member of a House, means the <5>political party to which he belongs for the purposes of sub-paragraph (1) of <5>paragraph 2; <6>d.<5> "paragraph" means a paragraph of this Schedule. <7>2. Disqualification on ground of defection <6>1.<5> Subject to the provisions of paragraphs 4 and 5, a member of a House belonging <5>to any political party shall be disqualified for being a member of the House- <6>a.<5> if he has voluntarily given up his membership of such political party; or <6>b.<5> if he votes or abstains from voting in such House contrary to any direction <5>issued by the political party to which he belongs or by any person or <5>authority authorised by it in this behalf, without obtaining, in either case, <5>the prior permission of such political party, person or authority and such <5>voting or abstention has not been condoned by such political party, person <5>or authority within fifteen days from the date of such voting or abstention. <7>Explanation <5>For the purposes of this sub-paragraph,- <6>a.<5> an elected member of a House shall be deemed to belong to the political <5>party, if any, by which he was set up as a candidate for election as such <5>member; <6>b.<5> a nominated member of a House shall,- <6>i. <5>where he is a member of any political party on the date of his <5>nomination as such member, be deemed to belong to such political <5>party; <6>ii. <5>in any other case, be deemed to belong to the political party of which <5>he becomes, or, as the case may be, first becomes, a member before <5>the expiry of six months from the date on which he takes his seat after <5>complying with the requirements of article 99 or, as the case may be, <5>article 188. <6>2. <5>An elected member of a House who has been elected as such otherwise than as a <5>candidate set up by any political party shall be disqualified for being a member of <5>the House if he joins any political party after such election. <6>3. <5>A nominated member of a House shall be disqualified for being a member of the <5>House if he joins any political party after the expiry of six months from the date <5>on which he takes his seat after complying with the requirements of article 99 <5>or, as the case may be, article 188. <6>4. <5>Notwithstanding anything contained in the foregoing provisions of this <5>paragraph, a person who, on the commencement of the Constitution <5>(Fifty-second Amendment) Act, 1985, is a member of a House (whether elected <5>or nominated as such) shall,- <6>i. <5>where he was a member of a political party immediately before such <5>commencement, be deemed, for the purposes of sub-paragraph (1) of this <5>paragraph, to have been elected as a member of such House as a candidate <5>set up by such political party; <6>ii. <5>in any other case, be deemed to be an elected member of the House who <5>has been elected as such otherwise than as a candidate set up by any <5>political party for the purposes of sub-paragraph (2) of this paragraph or, as <5>the case may be, be deemed to be a nominated member of the House for <5>the purposes of sub-paragraph (3) of this paragraph. <7>3. Disqualification on ground of defection not to apply in <7>case of split <5>[Repealed] <7>4. Disqualification on ground of defection not to apply in <7>case of merger <6>1.<5> A member of a House shall not be disqualified under sub-paragraph (1) of <5>paragraph 2 where his original political party merges with another political party <5>and he claims that he and any other members of his original political party- <6>a.<5> have become members of such other political party or, as the case may be, <5>of a new political party formed by such merger; or <6>b.<5> have not accepted the merger and opted to function as a separate group, <5>and from the time of such merger, such other political party or new political <5>party or group, as the case may be, shall be deemed to be the political party to <5>which he belongs for the purposes of sub-paragraph (1) of paragraph 2 and to be <5>his original political party for the purposes of this sub-paragraph. <6>2.<5> For the purposes of sub-paragraph (1) of this paragraph, the merger of the <5>original political party of a member of a House shall be deemed to have taken <5>place if, and only if, not less than two-thirds of the members of the legislature <5>party concerned have agreed to such merger. <7>5. Exemption <5>Notwithstanding anything contained in this Schedule, a person who has been elected <5>to the office of the Speaker or the Deputy Speaker of the House of the People or the <5>Deputy Chairman of the Council of States or the Chairman or the Deputy Chairman <5>of the Legislative Council of a State or the Speaker or the Deputy Speaker of the <5>Legislative Assembly of a State, shall not be disqualified under this Schedule,- <6>a.<5> if he, by reason of his election to such office, voluntarily gives up the <5>membership of the political party to which he belonged immediately before <5>such election and does not, so long as he continues to hold such office <5>thereafter, rejoin that political party or become a member of another <5>political party; or <6>b.<5> if he, having given up by reason of his election to such office his <5>membership of the political party to which he belonged immediately before <5>such election, rejoins such political party after he ceases to hold such office. <7>6. Decision on questions as to disqualification on ground of <7>defection <6>1.<5> If any question arises as to whether a member of a House has become subject to <5>disqualification under this Schedule, the question shall be referred for the <5>decision of the Chairman or, as the case may be, the Speaker of such House and <5>his decision shall be final: <5>Provided that where the question which has arisen is as to whether the <5>Chairman or the Speaker of a House has become subject to such disqualification, <5>the question shall be referred for the decision of such member of the House as <5>the House may elect in this behalf and his decision shall be final. <6>2.<5> All proceedings under sub-paragraph (1) of this paragraph in relation to any <5>question as to disqualification of a member of a House under this Schedule shall <5>be deemed to be proceedings in Parliament within the meaning of article 122 or, <5>as the case may be, proceedings in the Legislature of a State within the meaning <5>of article 212. <7>7. Bar of jurisdiction of courts <5>Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, no court shall have any jurisdiction in <5>respect of any matter connected with the disqualification of a member of a House <5>under this Schedule. <7>8. Rules <6>1.<5> Subject to the provisions of sub-paragraph (2) of this paragraph, the Chairman <5>or the Speaker of a House may make rules for giving effect to the provisions of <5>this Schedule, and in particular, and without prejudice to the generality of the <5>foregoing, such rules may provide for- <6>a.<5> the maintenance of registers or other records as to the political parties, if <5>any, to which different members of the House belong; <6>b.<5> the report which the leader of a legislature party in relation to a member of <5>a House shall furnish with regard to any condonation of the nature referred <5>to in clause (b) of subparagraph (1) of paragraph 2 in respect of such <5>member, the time within which and the authority to whom such report shall <5>be furnished; <6>c. <5>the reports which a political party shall furnish with regard to admission to <5>such political party of any members of the House and the officer of the <5>House to whom such reports shall be furnished; and <6>d.<5> the procedure for deciding any question referred to in sub-paragraph (1) of <5>paragraph 6 including the procedure for any inquiry which may be made for <5>the purpose of deciding such question. <6>2.<5> The rules made by the Chairman or the Speaker of a House under sub-paragraph <5>(1) of this paragraph shall be laid as soon as may be after they are made before <5>the House for a total period of thirty days which may be comprised in one <5>session or in two or more successive sessions and shall take effect upon the <5>expiry of the said period of thirty days unless they are sooner approved with or <5>without modifications or disapproved by the House and where they are so <5>approved, they shall take effect on such approval in the form in which they were <5>laid or in such modified form, as the case may be, and where they are so <5>disapproved, they shall be of no effect. <6>3.<5> The Chairman or the Speaker of a House may, without prejudice to the <5>provisions of article 105 or, as the case may be, article 194, and to any other <5>power which he may have under this Constitution direct that any wilful <5>contravention by any person of the rules made under this paragraph may be <5>dealt with in the same manner as a breach of privilege of the House. <9>ELEVENTH SCHEDULE: (Article 243G) <6>1. <5>Agriculture, including agricultural extension. <6>2. <5>Land
